# ## PROLOGUE

---

## **HERMENEUTICAL ORDERING: TONAL CONSIDERATIONS**

*What should be in my head, tonally, as I decide which event goes where?*

These are purely feel‑based constraints for sequencing every event under a single apocalyptic sky.

### Global Feel While Placing Any Event

For each placement, ask: "If this were the only thing the reader saw right now, what would they feel, and how will that feeling mutate once the surrounding events are known?"

Keep a constant background sense of *inevitable but not yet arrived judgment*: events should feel like fragments drifting toward a catastrophe the reader intuits but cannot fully map. The ordering should amplify this intuition without ever needing to state it.

### Local Emotional Honesty vs. Global Dread

Let each event keep its own mood intact: joy as joy, terror as terror, banality as banality. When deciding where it goes, the question is not "How do I darken this?" but "What do I put before and after it so that its native feeling is still true, yet uneasy in context?"

Guard against flattening: if the internal meter says, "This scene now feels *less* joyful than the text itself," move it until the joy is restored, even if that increases dread elsewhere. The blood‑red sky comes from the whole arrangement, not from repainting each star.

### Pattern Pressure Without Visible Machinery

As neighbors are chosen for any event, think in terms of *emerging pattern*, not formula: "If the reader has already seen these three rises and collapses, how does placing this next one tilt their sense of the world's moral physics?"

Let recognition do the work. The arrangement is not meant to shout "this always goes bad," but to ensure that the reader, on their own, begins to fear the *kind* of thing they see starting again, even when the moment itself is beautiful.

### Temporal Dislocation as Emotional Tool

When something is moved "out of time," the guiding question is: "Does seeing this *now*, instead of 'when it happened,' intensify the reader's unease without lying about the scene's own feeling?"

Use non‑chronology as emotional shuffling: not solving a puzzle for cleverness' sake, but arranging so that memory, not plot, becomes the primary carrier of dread. The reader's prior experiences in the book should echo loudly whenever a new event is dropped in.

### Breath, Contrast, and Load‑Bearing Points

As a run of events is placed, attend to *breath*: "Is the reader being allowed to fully inhale this joy or horror before being asked to hold something heavier?" The aim is not comfort, but full saturation; no emotion should be half‑felt because of a rush to the next.

Reserve the sharpest contrasts for points meant to feel load‑bearing in the moral architecture. When the gut says, "Putting *that* after *this* feels almost too much," those are the joints where the blood‑red sky thickens.

### Memory, Echo, and Haunting

When choosing where to drop a small or obscure event, ask: "What earlier feeling do I want this to wake back up?" The placement's job is to ring a bell in the reader's memory, not to make a point in the abstract.

Think in terms of *haunting rather than foreshadowing*: the order should make readers feel followed by what they have already seen. If an event, as placed, sends a faint chill backward through the book, it is doing the right kind of work.

---

## **PROLOGUE**

*Sections 1–11: The Three-Thread Collapse*

(As per your existing design: the interwoven strands converging toward incarnation, each marked by its own shadow of violence and expectation.)

PART FIVE: THE DESERT TESTIMONY
Holiness codes and wandering years, fire and leprosy, grumbling and rebellion: the pattern of proximity to glory that consumes what it sanctifies, where every privilege is shadowed by plague.

PART SIX: THE INHERITANCE OF BLOOD
Conquest and allotment, Jericho's fall and Ai's ambush, extermination and covenant: the pattern of promised land gained through genocide commanded, where every acre is paid for in corpses.

PART SEVEN: WHEN THERE WAS NO KING
The rhythm of apostasy and deliverance, each judge a darker savior: the pattern of rescue through violence that cannot hold, where every deliverer is also destroyer, and the spiral descends.

"Must you take a wife from the uncircumcised Philistines?"
"Get her for me, for she is right in my eyes"
"His father and mother did not know it was from the Lord"
"For he was seeking an opportunity against the Philistines"
Samson goes down to Timnah
A young lion roars against him
Spirit of the Lord rushes upon him
He tears the lion in pieces as one tears a young goat
"He had nothing in his hand"
He does not tell his father or mother
Later, he turns aside to see the carcass
A swarm of bees and honey in the body
He scrapes honey into his hands
He eats as he goes
He gives some to his parents
He does not tell them
His father goes down to the woman
Samson makes a feast
Thirty companions given to him
Samson's riddle: "Out of the eater came something to eat"
"Out of the strong came something sweet"
Three days; they cannot solve it
Seventh day: they say to Samson's wife, "Entice your husband"
"Lest we burn you and your father's house"
"Have you invited us here to impoverish us?"
Samson's wife weeps before him
"You only hate me; you do not love me"
Seven days of the feast she weeps
On the seventh day he tells her
She tells her people
Seventh day, before the sun sets
"What is sweeter than honey?"
"What is stronger than a lion?"
"If you had not plowed with my heifer, you would not have found out my riddle"
Spirit of the Lord rushes upon him
He goes down to Ashkelon
He strikes down thirty men
He takes their spoil
He gives the garments to those who had told the riddle
His anger burns
He goes up to his father's house
His wife is given to his companion
Later, at wheat harvest, Samson visits his wife
He takes a young goat
Her father: "I gave her to your companion"
"Is not her younger sister more beautiful?"
Samson: "This time I shall be innocent regarding the Philistines when I do them harm"
He catches 300 foxes
He takes torches
He ties the foxes tail to tail
He puts a torch between each pair of tails
He lets them go into the standing grain
He burns up the shocks, the standing grain, the olive orchards
Philistines: "Who has done this?"
"Samson, because his father-in-law gave his wife to his companion"
Philistines go up and burn her and her father
Samson: "If this is what you do, I swear I will be avenged"
He strikes them hip and thigh with a great blow
He goes down and stays in the cleft of the rock of Etam
Philistines encamp in Judah
They spread out against Lehi
Men of Judah: "Why have you come up against us?"
"We have come to bind Samson"
3,000 men of Judah go to the rock
"Do you not know the Philistines rule over us?"
"What have you done to us?"
Samson: "As they did to me, so have I done to them"
"We have come to bind you and give you into their hands"
Samson: "Swear to me that you will not attack me yourselves"
They bind him with two new ropes
They bring him up from the rock
He comes to Lehi
Philistines shout
Spirit of the Lord rushes upon him
Ropes on his arms become as flax burned with fire
Bonds melt off his hands
He finds a fresh jawbone of a donkey
He reaches out and takes it
He strikes 1,000 men with it
"With the jawbone of a donkey, heaps upon heaps"
"With the jawbone of a donkey have I struck down a thousand men"
He throws away the jawbone
Ramath-lehi: "Hill of the Jawbone"
He is very thirsty
He calls upon the Lord
"You have given this great salvation"
"Shall I now die of thirst?"
God splits open the hollow place at Lehi
Water comes out
He drinks, his spirit returns
En-hakkore: "Spring of the One Who Called"
He judges Israel twenty years
Samson goes to Gaza
He sees a prostitute
He goes in to her
Gazites are told, "Samson has come here"
They surround the place
They lie in wait all night at the gate
"As soon as the light of the morning comes, we will kill him"
Samson lies till midnight
At midnight he arises
He takes hold of the doors of the city gate
He pulls them up, bar and all
He puts them on his shoulders
He carries them to the top of the hill at Hebron
Samson loves a woman in the Valley of Sorek
Her name is Delilah
Lords of the Philistines come to her
"Entice him, and see where his great strength lies"
"That we may bind him and subdue him"
"We will each give you 1,100 pieces of silver"
Delilah: "Please tell me where your great strength lies"
"And how you might be bound"
Samson: "If they bind me with seven fresh bowstrings"
"I shall become weak and be like any other man"
Lords bring seven fresh bowstrings
She binds him
Men lie in ambush in an inner chamber
"The Philistines are upon you, Samson!"
He snaps the bowstrings as a thread snaps
His strength is not known
Delilah: "You have mocked me and told me lies"
"Please tell me how you might be bound"
Samson: "If they bind me with new ropes"
She takes new ropes and binds him
"The Philistines are upon you!"
He snaps the ropes off his arms like a thread
Delilah: "Until now you have mocked me"
"Tell me how you might be bound"
Samson: "If you weave the seven locks of my head with the web"
She weaves it tight with the pin
"The Philistines are upon you!"
He awakes and pulls away the pin, the loom, and the web
"How can you say, 'I love you,' when your heart is not with me?"
"You have mocked me these three times"
She presses him hard day after day
His soul is vexed to death
He tells her all his heart
"A razor has never come upon my head"
"For I have been a Nazirite to God from my mother's womb"
"If my head is shaved, then my strength will leave me"
Delilah sees he has told her all his heart
She sends word to the lords
"Come up again, for he has told me all his heart"
Lords come up with the money
She makes him sleep on her knees
She calls a man
He shaves off the seven locks
She begins to torment him
His strength leaves him
"The Philistines are upon you!"
He awakes: "I will go out as at other times and shake myself free"
"He did not know that the Lord had left him"
Philistines seize him
They gouge out his eyes
They bring him down to Gaza
They bind him with bronze shackles
He grinds at the mill in the prison
"But the hair of his head began to grow again"
Lords gather to offer a great sacrifice to Dagon
"Our god has given Samson our enemy into our hand"
They praise their god
Their hearts are merry
"Call Samson, that he may entertain us"
They call Samson from prison
He entertains them
They make him stand between the pillars
About 3,000 men and women on the roof
Samson says to the boy who holds his hand
"Let me feel the pillars on which the house rests"
Samson calls to the Lord
"O Lord God, please remember me"
"Please strengthen me only this once, O God"
"That I may be avenged on the Philistines for my two eyes"
He grasps the two middle pillars
One with his right hand, one with his left
"Let me die with the Philistines"
He bows with all his strength
The house falls upon the lords
The house falls upon all the people
"The dead whom he killed at his death were more than those he had killed during his life"
His brothers and all his family come down
They take him and bury him between Zorah and Eshtaol
He has judged Israel twenty years
Micah and the Levite
Micah makes an ephod and household gods
A Levite sojourns with him
"You shall be to me a father and a priest"
Five Danites spy out the land
They come to Micah's house
They recognize the voice of the Levite
They take Micah's idol and the ephod
600 Danites come with weapons
The Levite goes with them
Micah and his neighbors pursue
"What is the matter with you?"
"You take away my gods and my priest and go away"
"What have I left?"
Danites: "Do not let your voice be heard"
"Lest angry fellows fall upon you"
Micah sees they are too strong
He turns and goes home
Danites set up Micah's carved image
Laish captured and burned
They rebuild the city and dwell there
Levite and his concubine
The Levite takes a concubine from Bethlehem
She is unfaithful
She goes away to her father's house
Four months
Her husband goes after her to speak kindly
Her father makes him stay
Fifth day: they set out late
They pass by Jebus
The servant: "Let us turn aside to this city of the Jebusites"
The Levite: "We will not turn aside into a foreign city"
"We will pass on to Gibeah"
They come to Gibeah of Benjamin
They sit down in the open square
No one takes them into his house
An old man from the hill country of Ephraim
"Where are you going, and where do you come from?"
The Levite tells his journey
The old man: "Peace be to you; I will care for all your wants"
"Only, do not spend the night in the square"
He brings them into his house
They are making their hearts merry
Worthless fellows surround the house
They pound on the door
"Bring out the man who came into your house, that we may know him"
Old man goes out to them
"No, my brothers, do not act so wickedly"
"Do not do this vile thing"
"Here are my virgin daughter and his concubine"
"Let me bring them out now"
"Violate them and do with them what seems good to you"
"But against this man do not do this outrageous thing"
Men will not listen
The man seizes his concubine
He puts her out to them
They know her and abuse her all night
At dawn they let her go
As morning appears, the woman comes back
She falls down at the door
She lies there until it is light
Her master rises in the morning
He opens the doors to go out
There is his concubine, fallen at the door
Her hands on the threshold
"Get up, let us be going"
There is no answer
He puts her on the donkey
He goes to his home
He takes a knife
He lays hold of his concubine
He divides her, limb by limb, into twelve pieces
He sends her throughout all the territory of Israel
"Such a thing has never happened since the day the Israelites came up"
All Israel assembles at Mizpah
400,000 men on foot who draw the sword
Benjaminites hear that Israel has come up
Israel: "Tell us, how did this evil happen?"
The Levite recounts the events
"I took hold of my concubine and cut her in pieces"
"They have committed abomination and outrage in Israel"
"Give your advice and counsel"
All the people arise as one
"We will not any of us go to his tent"
"We will go up against Gibeah by lot"
Tribes send men through Benjamin
"What evil is this that has taken place?"
"Give up the men, the worthless fellows in Gibeah"
"That we may put them to death"
"That we may purge evil from Israel"
Benjaminites will not listen
Benjaminites gather from the cities to Gibeah
26,000 men who draw the sword
700 chosen men from Gibeah
"Every one could sling a stone and not miss"
Israel has 400,000 men who draw the sword
Israel goes to Bethel
"Who shall go up first to fight?"
The Lord: "Judah shall go up first"
Morning: Israel encamps against Gibeah
Men of Benjamin come out
They strike down 22,000 Israelites
People weep before the Lord
"Shall we again draw near to fight?"
The Lord: "Go up against them"
Second day: Benjamin strikes down 18,000 Israelites
All Israel weeps and fasts
They offer burnt offerings and peace offerings
"Shall I go out once more to fight?"
The Lord: "Go up, for tomorrow I will give them into your hand"
Israel sets men in ambush
Third day: Israel draws up against Gibeah
Benjamin comes out
They are drawn away from the city
They begin to strike and kill
About thirty men of Israel fall
"We are defeating them as before"
Israel: "Let us flee and draw them away"
All the men of Israel rise from their place
Israel turns and forms a line
Men in ambush rush upon Gibeah
They strike all the city with the sword
Smoke of the city goes up to heaven
Men of Israel turn
Men of Benjamin are dismayed
"They saw that disaster was close upon them"
They flee toward the wilderness
The battle overtakes them
Those who came out of the cities are destroyed
Israel surrounds Benjamin
They pursue them and tread them down
18,000 men of Benjamin fall
"All of them men of valor"
They turn and flee toward the wilderness to the rock of Rimmon
5,000 more cut down on the highways
They pursue hard after them to Gidom
2,000 more struck down
25,000 men of Benjamin fall that day
"All of them men of valor"
600 men turn and flee to the rock of Rimmon
They remain four months
Israel turns back against the people of Benjamin
They strike them with the sword
Men, beasts, all that is found
"Also all the towns that they found they set on fire"
The men of Israel have sworn at Mizpah
"No one of us shall give his daughter in marriage to Benjamin"
The people come to Bethel
They sit there until evening before God
They weep bitterly
"O Lord, God of Israel, why has this happened?"
"That today there should be one tribe lacking in Israel?"
Next day: they build an altar
They offer burnt offerings and peace offerings
"Which of all the tribes did not come up to the Lord?"
"For they had taken a great oath concerning anyone who did not come up"
"He shall surely be put to death"
They have compassion on Benjamin
"How shall we provide wives for those who are left?"
"Since the women are destroyed out of Benjamin?"
"There must be an inheritance for the survivors"
"That a tribe not be blotted out from Israel"
"Yet we cannot give them wives of our daughters"
"Who is there that did not come up to Mizpah?"
"It was found that none of Jabesh-gilead had come"
12,000 of the bravest men sent
"Go and strike the inhabitants of Jabesh-gilead with the sword"
"Also the women and the little ones"
"Every male and every woman that has lain with a male you shall devote to destruction"
They find 400 young virgins
"Who had not known a man by lying with him"
They bring them to the camp at Shiloh
The congregation sends word of peace to Benjamin at the rock of Rimmon
Benjamin returns
They give them the women of Jabesh-gilead
"But they were not enough"
"What shall we do for wives for those who are left?"
"Behold, there is the yearly feast of the Lord at Shiloh"
They command the people of Benjamin
"Go and lie in ambush in the vineyards"
"When the daughters of Shiloh come out to dance"
"Each of you catch his wife from the daughters of Shiloh"
People of Benjamin do so
They catch their wives
They return to their inheritance
They rebuild the towns and dwell in them
The people of Israel depart
Each to his tribe and family
Each to his inheritance
"In those days there was no king in Israel"
"Everyone did what was right in his own eyes"
PART EIGHT: THE ANOINTED AND THE MADFrom Ruth's gleaning to David's throne, through Saul's torment and Jonathan's death: the pattern of kingship as divine madness, where the chosen become the cursed, and every coronation promises eventual corpses.
Famine in the days of the judges
Elimelech goes to sojourn in Moab
Elimelech, Naomi, Mahlon, and Chilion
They remain there
Elimelech dies
Naomi is left with her two sons
They take Moabite wives
Orpah and Ruth
They live there about ten years
Mahlon and Chilion die
Naomi is left without her two sons and her husband
She hears the Lord has visited his people
She sets out to return
Her two daughters-in-law with her
Naomi: "Go, return each of you to her mother's house"
"May the Lord deal kindly with you"
She kisses them
They weep aloud
"No, we will return with you"
Naomi: "Turn back, my daughters"
"Why will you go with me?"
"Have I yet sons in my womb?"
"It is exceedingly bitter to me for your sake"
"The hand of the Lord has gone out against me"
They weep again
Orpah kisses her mother-in-law
Ruth clings to her
"See, your sister-in-law has gone back"
Ruth: "Do not urge me to leave you"
"Where you go I will go"
"Your people shall be my people"
"Your God my God"
"Where you die I will die"
"May the Lord do so to me and more if anything but death parts me from you"
They come to Bethlehem at the beginning of barley harvest
The whole town is stirred
"Is this Naomi?"
"Do not call me Naomi; call me Mara"
"For the Almighty has dealt very bitterly with me"
"I went away full, and the Lord has brought me back empty"
Ruth goes to glean in the field
She happens to come to the part belonging to Boaz
Boaz comes from Bethlehem
"The Lord be with you"
Reapers: "The Lord bless you"
Boaz notices Ruth
"Whose young woman is this?"
"She is the young Moabite woman"
Boaz speaks to Ruth
"Do not go to glean in another field"
"Keep close to my young women"
Ruth falls on her face
"Why have I found favor in your eyes?"
"I am a foreigner"
Boaz: "All that you have done for your mother-in-law has been fully told to me"
"The Lord repay you for what you have done"
"A full reward be given you by the Lord"
"Under whose wings you have come to take refuge"
At mealtime: "Come here and eat"
She sits beside the reapers
He passes her roasted grain
She eats and is satisfied
She has some left over
Boaz instructs his young men
"Let her glean even among the sheaves"
"Pull out some from the bundles for her"
She gleans until evening
She beats out what she has gleaned
About an ephah of barley
She brings it to Naomi
Naomi: "Where did you glean today?"
"Blessed be the man who took notice of you"
"The man's name is Boaz"
Naomi: "May he be blessed by the Lord"
"The man is a close relative of ours, one of our redeemers"
Ruth gleans in his field until the end of barley and wheat harvest
Naomi: "Should I not seek rest for you?"
"Is not Boaz our relative?"
"He will be winnowing barley tonight at the threshing floor"
"Wash and anoint yourself"
"Put on your cloak"
"When he lies down, observe the place"
"Then go and uncover his feet and lie down"
Ruth: "All that you say I will do"
She goes down to the threshing floor
Boaz eats and drinks
His heart is merry
He goes to lie down at the end of the heap of grain
She comes softly
She uncovers his feet
She lies down
At midnight the man is startled
He turns over
A woman is lying at his feet
"Who are you?"
"I am Ruth, your servant"
"Spread your wings over your servant"
"For you are a redeemer"
Boaz: "May you be blessed by the Lord"
"You have made this last kindness greater than the first"
"You have not gone after young men"
"Do not fear"
"I will do for you all that you ask"
"All my fellow townsmen know you are a worthy woman"
"Now it is true that I am a redeemer"
"Yet there is a redeemer nearer than I"
"Remain tonight"
"In the morning, if he will redeem you, good"
"But if he is not willing, as the Lord lives, I will redeem you"
She lies at his feet until the morning
She rises before one could recognize another
Boaz: "Let it not be known that the woman came to the threshing floor"
He measures out six measures of barley
He loads it on her
She goes into the city
Naomi: "How did you fare, my daughter?"
Ruth tells her all
"He gave me these six measures"
"He said, 'You must not go back empty-handed to your mother-in-law'"
Naomi: "Wait until you learn how the matter turns out"
"The man will not rest but will settle the matter today"
Boaz goes up to the gate
He sits down there
The redeemer passes by
"Turn aside, friend; sit down here"
He turns aside and sits down
Boaz takes ten men of the elders
"Sit down here"
They sit down
Boaz speaks to the redeemer
"Naomi is selling the parcel of land that belonged to Elimelech"
"If you will redeem it, redeem it"
"But if you will not, tell me, that I may know"
"For there is no one besides you to redeem it"
"And I come after you"
The redeemer: "I will redeem it"
Boaz: "The day you buy the field from Naomi"
"You also acquire Ruth the Moabite"
"In order to perpetuate the name of the dead in his inheritance"
"Then I cannot redeem it"
"Lest I impair my own inheritance"
"Take my right of redemption yourself"
"For I cannot redeem it"
The custom of drawing off the sandal
The man draws off his sandal
Boaz to the elders: "You are witnesses"
"I have bought all that was Elimelech's"
"Also Ruth the Moabite I have bought to be my wife"
Elders and all the people: "We are witnesses"
"May the Lord make the woman like Rachel and Leah"
"May you act worthily in Ephrathah"
Boaz takes Ruth
She becomes his wife
He goes in to her
The Lord gives her conception
She bears a son
Women say to Naomi: "Blessed be the Lord"
"Who has not left you without a redeemer"
"May his name be renowned in Israel"
"He shall be to you a restorer of life"
Naomi takes the child
She lays him on her lap
She becomes his nurse
Women: "A son has been born to Naomi"
They name him Obed
Obed, father of Jesse
Jesse, father of David
Elkanah has two wives
Hannah and Peninnah
Peninnah has children
Hannah has no children
Elkanah goes up year by year to worship at Shiloh
Hophni and Phinehas, priests of the Lord, are there
When the day comes, Elkanah offers sacrifice
He gives portions to Peninnah and her children
To Hannah he gives a double portion
"Because he loved her"
"Though the Lord had closed her womb"
Her rival used to provoke her grievously
"To irritate her, because the Lord had closed her womb"
So it went on year by year
Whenever she went up to the house of the Lord
"She used to provoke her"
Hannah weeps and will not eat
Elkanah: "Hannah, why do you weep?"
"Why do you not eat?"
"Why is your heart sad?"
"Am I not more to you than ten sons?"
Hannah rises after they have eaten and drunk
Eli the priest is sitting on the seat beside the doorpost
Hannah is deeply distressed
She prays to the Lord
She weeps bitterly
She vows a vow
"O Lord of hosts, if you will look on the affliction of your servant"
"And remember me and not forget your servant"
"But will give to your servant a son"
"Then I will give him to the Lord all the days of his life"
"And no razor shall touch his head"
She continues praying before the Lord
Eli observes her mouth
Hannah is speaking in her heart
Only her lips move
Her voice is not heard
Eli thinks she is drunk
"How long will you go on being drunk?"
"Put your wine away from you"
Hannah: "No, my lord"
"I am a woman troubled in spirit"
"I have drunk neither wine nor strong drink"
"I have been pouring out my soul before the Lord"
"Do not regard your servant as a worthless woman"
"All along I have been speaking out of my great anxiety and vexation"
Eli: "Go in peace"
"The God of Israel grant your petition"
"Let your servant find favor in your eyes"
She goes her way and eats
Her face is no longer sad
They rise early and worship
They return to their house at Ramah
Elkanah knows Hannah
The Lord remembers her
In due time Hannah conceives
She bears a son
She calls his name Samuel
"For I have asked for him from the Lord"
Elkanah goes up with all his house to offer sacrifice
Hannah does not go up
"As soon as the child is weaned, I will bring him"
"That he may appear in the presence of the Lord"
"And dwell there forever"
Elkanah: "Do what seems best to you"
"Only, may the Lord establish his word"
The woman remains and nurses her son
Until she weans him
When she has weaned him, she takes him up
A three-year-old bull
An ephah of flour
A skin of wine
She brings him to the house of the Lord at Shiloh
The child is young
They slaughter the bull
They bring the child to Eli
"Oh, my lord! As you live, my lord"
"I am the woman who was standing here in your presence, praying"
"For this child I prayed"
"The Lord has granted my petition"
"Therefore I have lent him to the Lord"
"As long as he lives, he is lent to the Lord"
They worship the Lord there
Hannah's prayer
"My heart exults in the Lord"
"My horn is exalted in the Lord"
"There is none holy like the Lord"
"There is no rock like our God"
"The bows of the mighty are broken"
"But the feeble bind on strength"
"Those who were full have hired themselves out for bread"
"But those who were hungry have ceased to hunger"
"The barren has borne seven"
"But she who has many children is forlorn"
"The Lord kills and brings to life"
"He brings down to Sheol and raises up"
"The Lord makes poor and makes rich"
"He brings low and he exalts"
"He raises up the poor from the dust"
"He lifts the needy from the ash heap"
Elkanah returns home to Ramah
The boy ministers to the Lord in the presence of Eli
The sons of Eli are worthless men
They do not know the Lord
The custom of the priests with the people
When any man offered sacrifice
The priest's servant would come with a three-pronged fork
He would thrust it into the pan or kettle
"All that the fork brought up the priest would take"
This is what they did at Shiloh
Before the fat was burned
The priest's servant would come
"Give meat for the priest to roast"
"He will not accept boiled meat from you but only raw"
If the man said, "Let them burn the fat first"
"Then take as much as you wish"
He would say, "No, you must give it now"
"If not, I will take it by force"
The sin of the young men was very great
"For the men treated the offering of the Lord with contempt"
Samuel ministers before the Lord
A boy clothed with a linen ephod
His mother makes him a little robe
She takes it to him each year
When she comes up with her husband to offer the sacrifice
Eli blesses Elkanah and his wife
"May the Lord give you children by this woman"
"For the petition she asked of the Lord"
They return to their home
The Lord visits Hannah
She conceives and bears three sons and two daughters
The boy Samuel grows in the presence of the Lord
Eli is very old
He hears all his sons are doing to Israel
"How they lie with the women who serve at the entrance"
"Why do you do such things?"
"I hear of your evil dealings from all these people"
"No, my sons; it is no good report"
"If someone sins against a man, God will mediate"
"But if someone sins against the Lord, who can intercede?"
They do not listen to their father
"For it was the will of the Lord to put them to death"
Samuel continues to grow in stature and in favor
A man of God comes to Eli
"Thus says the Lord: Did I indeed reveal myself to your father's house?"
"Did I choose him out of all the tribes to be my priest?"
"Why then do you scorn my sacrifices?"
"Why do you honor your sons above me?"
"Therefore the Lord declares: Far be it from me"
"For those who honor me I will honor"
"Those who despise me shall be lightly esteemed"
"Behold, the days are coming when I will cut off your strength"
"I will raise up for myself a faithful priest"
"Everyone who is left in your house shall come to implore him for a piece of silver"
"This that shall come upon your two sons shall be the sign"
"They shall both die on the same day"
Samuel ministers to the Lord under Eli
The word of the Lord is rare in those days
There is no frequent vision
Eli is lying down in his own place
His eyes have begun to grow dim
He cannot see
The lamp of God has not yet gone out
Samuel is lying down in the temple
Where the ark of God is
The Lord calls: "Samuel! Samuel!"
"Here I am"
He runs to Eli
"Here I am, for you called me"
"I did not call; lie down again"
He goes and lies down
The Lord calls again: "Samuel!"
Samuel goes to Eli
"Here I am, for you called me"
"I did not call, my son; lie down again"
"Now Samuel did not yet know the Lord"
"The word of the Lord had not yet been revealed to him"
The Lord calls Samuel the third time
He gets up and goes to Eli
"Here I am, for you called me"
Eli perceives the Lord is calling the boy
"Go, lie down, and if he calls you, you shall say"
"'Speak, Lord, for your servant hears'"
Samuel goes and lies down
The Lord comes and stands
Calling as at other times: "Samuel! Samuel!"
"Speak, for your servant hears"
The Lord says to Samuel
"Behold, I am about to do a thing in Israel"
"At which the two ears of everyone who hears will tingle"
"I declare against Eli all that I have spoken concerning his house"
"From beginning to end"
"I declare to him that I am about to punish his house forever"
"For the iniquity that he knew"
"Because his sons were blaspheming God, and he did not restrain them"
"I swear to the house of Eli"
"The iniquity of Eli's house shall not be atoned for by sacrifice or offering forever"
Samuel lies until morning
He opens the doors of the house of the Lord
Samuel is afraid to tell the vision to Eli
Eli calls Samuel
"What was it he told you?"
"Do not hide it from me"
"May God do so to you and more also if you hide anything"
Samuel tells him everything
He hides nothing
"It is the Lord"
"Let him do what seems good to him"
Samuel grows
The Lord is with him
He lets none of his words fall to the ground
All Israel from Dan to Beersheba knows Samuel is established as a prophet
The Lord continues to appear at Shiloh
The word of Samuel comes to all Israel
Israel goes out to battle against the Philistines
They encamp beside Ebenezer
The Philistines encamp at Aphek
The Philistines draw up in line against Israel
The battle spreads
Israel is defeated
About 4,000 men fall
The people come to the camp
Elders of Israel: "Why has the Lord defeated us today?"
"Let us bring the ark of the covenant"
"That it may come among us and save us"
They send to Shiloh
They bring from there the ark of the covenant
The two sons of Eli, Hophni and Phinehas, are with the ark
When the ark comes into the camp
All Israel gives a mighty shout
The earth resounds
Philistines hear the sound of the shouting
"What does this great shouting mean?"
They learn the ark has come
The Philistines are afraid
"A god has come into the camp"
"Woe to us! Who can deliver us from these mighty gods?"
"These are the gods who struck the Egyptians with every sort of plague"
"Take courage, and be men, O Philistines"
"Lest you become slaves to the Hebrews"
"Fight"
The Philistines fight
Israel is defeated
Every man flees to his home
Very great slaughter
30,000 foot soldiers of Israel fall
The ark of God is captured
The two sons of Eli, Hophni and Phinehas, die
A man of Benjamin runs from the battle line
He comes to Shiloh the same day
His clothes torn and earth on his head
Eli is sitting on his seat by the road watching
"For his heart trembles for the ark"
The man comes into the city and tells the news
All the city cries out
Eli hears the sound of the outcry
"What is this uproar?"
The man hurries and tells Eli
Eli is ninety-eight years old
His eyes are set so that he cannot see
The man says to Eli
"I am he who has come from the battle"
"I fled from the battle today"
"How did it go, my son?"
"Israel has fled before the Philistines"
"There has been a great defeat among the people"
"Your two sons also, Hophni and Phinehas, are dead"
"The ark of God has been captured"
When he mentions the ark
Eli falls over backward from his seat by the side of the gate
His neck is broken
He dies
"For the man was old and heavy"
He has judged Israel forty years
His daughter-in-law, the wife of Phinehas, is pregnant
About to give birth
When she hears the news
That the ark is captured
That her father-in-law and her husband are dead
She bows and gives birth
"For her pains come upon her"
About the time of her death the women attending her say
"Do not be afraid, for you have borne a son"
She does not answer or pay attention
She names the child Ichabod
"The glory has departed from Israel"
"Because the ark of God has been captured"
"And because of her father-in-law and her husband"
"The glory has departed from Israel"
"For the ark of God has been captured"
The Philistines capture the ark
They bring it from Ebenezer to Ashdod
They bring it into the house of Dagon
They set it up beside Dagon
When the people of Ashdod rise early the next day
Dagon has fallen face downward before the ark
They take Dagon and put him back
Next morning: Dagon has fallen face downward again
The head of Dagon and both his hands are lying cut off
Only the trunk of Dagon is left
The hand of the Lord is heavy against the people of Ashdod
He terrifies and afflicts them with tumors
Ashdod and its territory
The men of Ashdod see what is happening
"The ark of the God of Israel must not remain with us"
"For his hand is hard against us and against Dagon"
They send and gather all the lords of the Philistines
"What shall we do with the ark?"
"Let the ark be brought around to Gath"
They bring it to Gath
The hand of the Lord is against the city
Very great panic
He afflicts the men with tumors, both young and old
They send the ark to Ekron
As it comes to Ekron
The people cry out
"They have brought around the ark to us, to kill us and our people"
They send and gather all the lords
"Send away the ark of the God of Israel"
"Let it return to its own place"
"That it may not kill us and our people"
There is a deathly panic
The hand of God is very heavy there
The men who do not die are stricken with tumors
The cry of the city goes up to heaven
The ark is in the country of the Philistines seven months
The Philistines call for the priests and diviners
"What shall we do with the ark?"
"Tell us how we should send it to its place"
"Do not send it empty"
"By all means return him a guilt offering"
"Then you will be healed"
"What is the guilt offering we shall return?"
"Five golden tumors and five golden mice"
"According to the number of the lords of the Philistines"
"For the same plague was on all of you"
"Why should you harden your hearts as the Egyptians hardened their hearts?"
"Now then, take and prepare a new cart"
"And two milk cows on which there has never come a yoke"
"Yoke the cows to the cart"
"But take their calves home, away from them"
"Take the ark and place it on the cart"
"Put in a box at its side the figures of gold"
"Send it off and let it go its way"
"And watch. If it goes up on the way to its own land"
"Then it is he who has done us this great harm"
"But if not, then we shall know it is not his hand that struck us"
"It happened to us by coincidence"
The men do so
They take two milk cows
They yoke them to the cart
They shut up their calves at home
They put the ark on the cart
The box with the golden mice and images of tumors
The cows go straight toward Beth-shemesh
They go along the highway, lowing as they go
They turn neither to the right nor to the left
Lords of the Philistines follow them
As far as the border of Beth-shemesh
People of Beth-shemesh are reaping wheat harvest
They lift up their eyes
They see the ark
They rejoice to see it
The cart comes into the field of Joshua
It stops there
A great stone is there
They split up the wood of the cart
They offer the cows as a burnt offering to the Lord
The Levites take down the ark
They take down the box
They set them upon the great stone
Men of Beth-shemesh offer burnt offerings
They sacrifice sacrifices to the Lord
The five lords of the Philistines see it
They return to Ekron
These are the golden tumors the Philistines return
One for each of the cities of the Philistines
The golden mice, according to the number of all the cities
The great stone beside which they set down the ark
"Is a witness to this day in the field of Joshua"
The Lord strikes some of the men of Beth-shemesh
"Because they looked upon the ark"
He strikes seventy men
The people mourn
"Because the Lord had struck the people with a great blow"
Men of Beth-shemesh: "Who is able to stand before the Lord, this holy God?"
"To whom shall he go up away from us?"
They send messengers to Kiriath-jearim
"The Philistines have returned the ark"
"Come down and take it up to you"
The men of Kiriath-jearim come
They bring up the ark
They bring it to the house of Abinadab on the hill
They consecrate Eleazar to have charge of the ark
From the day the ark lodges at Kiriath-jearim
A long time passes
Twenty years
All the house of Israel laments after the Lord
Samuel says to Israel
"If you are returning to the Lord with all your heart"
"Put away the foreign gods and the Ashtaroth"
"Direct your heart to the Lord and serve him only"
"He will deliver you out of the hand of the Philistines"
People of Israel put away the Baals and the Ashtaroth
They serve the Lord only
Samuel: "Gather all Israel at Mizpah"
"I will pray to the Lord for you"
They gather at Mizpah
They draw water and pour it out before the Lord
They fast that day
"We have sinned against the Lord"
Samuel judges Israel at Mizpah
Philistines hear Israel has gathered
Lords of the Philistines go up against Israel
People of Israel hear and are afraid
"Do not cease to cry out to the Lord for us"
"That he may save us from the hand of the Philistines"
Samuel takes a nursing lamb
He offers it as a whole burnt offering
He cries out to the Lord
The Lord answers him
As Samuel is offering up the burnt offering
The Philistines draw near
The Lord thunders with a mighty sound
He throws them into confusion
They are routed before Israel
Men of Israel go out from Mizpah
They pursue the Philistines
They strike them down
Samuel takes a stone
He sets it up between Mizpah and Shen
He calls its name Ebenezer
"For he said, 'Till now the Lord has helped us'"
Philistines are subdued
They do not again enter the territory of Israel
The hand of the Lord is against the Philistines all the days of Samuel
Cities the Philistines had taken are restored
There is peace between Israel and the Amorites
Samuel judges Israel all the days of his life
He goes on a circuit year by year
Bethel, Gilgal, and Mizpah
He judges Israel in all these places
He returns to Ramah
His home is there
He judges Israel there
He builds an altar to the Lord
Samuel grows old
He makes his sons judges over Israel
Name of his firstborn son: Joel
Name of his second: Abijah
They are judges in Beersheba
His sons do not walk in his ways
They turn aside after gain
They take bribes
They pervert justice
All the elders of Israel gather
They come to Samuel at Ramah
"Behold, you are old"
"Your sons do not walk in your ways"
"Appoint for us a king to judge us like all the nations"
It displeases Samuel
"When they said, 'Give us a king to judge us'"
Samuel prays to the Lord
The Lord says to Samuel
"Obey the voice of the people in all that they say"
"For they have not rejected you, but they have rejected me"
"From being king over them"
"According to all the deeds they have done"
"From the day I brought them up out of Egypt until this day"
"Forsaking me and serving other gods"
"So they are also doing to you"
"Obey their voice"
"Only you shall solemnly warn them"
"Show them the ways of the king who shall reign over them"
Samuel tells the people the words of the Lord
"These will be the ways of the king"
"He will take your sons and appoint them to his chariots"
"He will appoint for himself commanders"
"Some to plow his ground and reap his harvest"
"To make his implements of war"
"He will take your daughters to be perfumers, cooks, and bakers"
"He will take the best of your fields and vineyards"
"He will give them to his servants"
"He will take the tenth of your grain and of your vineyards"
"He will take your male servants and female servants"
"The best of your young men and your donkeys"
"He will take the tenth of your flocks"
"You shall be his slaves"
"In that day you will cry out because of your king"
"But the Lord will not answer you in that day"
The people refuse to obey Samuel
"No! But there shall be a king over us"
"That we also may be like all the nations"
"That our king may judge us"
"And go out before us and fight our battles"
Samuel hears all the words of the people
He repeats them in the ears of the Lord
The Lord: "Obey their voice and make them a king"
Samuel: "Go every man to his city"
There is a man of Benjamin
His name is Kish
A mighty man of valor
He has a son
His name is Saul
A handsome young man
There is not a man among the people more handsome
From his shoulders upward he is taller than any of the people
The donkeys of Kish are lost
Kish says to Saul: "Take one of the young men"
"Arise, go and look for the donkeys"
They pass through the hill country of Ephraim
They pass through the land of Shalishah
They do not find them
They pass through the land of Shaalim
They are not there
They pass through the land of Benjamin
They do not find them
They come to the land of Zuph
Saul says to his servant
"Come, let us go back"
"Lest my father cease to care about the donkeys and become anxious"
The servant: "Behold, there is a man of God in this city"
"All that he says comes true"
"Perhaps he can tell us the way we should go"
"What can we bring the man?"
"The bread in our sacks is gone"
"There is no present to bring"
The servant: "Here, I have with me a quarter of a shekel of silver"
"I will give it to the man of God to tell us our way"
"He who is now called a prophet was formerly called a seer"
"Come, let us go to the seer"
As they go up the hill to the city
They meet young women coming out to draw water
"Is the seer here?"
"He is; behold, he is just ahead of you"
"Hurry now, for he has come today to the city"
"Because the people have a sacrifice today on the high place"
They go up to the city
As they enter the city, they meet Samuel coming out
The day before Saul came
The Lord had revealed to Samuel
"Tomorrow about this time I will send to you a man from Benjamin"
"You shall anoint him to be prince over my people Israel"
"He shall save my people from the hand of the Philistines"
"For I have seen my people"
"Because their cry has come to me"
When Samuel sees Saul
The Lord tells him
"Here is the man of whom I spoke"
"He it is who shall restrain my people"
Saul approaches Samuel in the gate
"Tell me where is the house of the seer"
Samuel: "I am the seer"
"Go up before me to the high place"
"You shall eat with me today"
"In the morning I will let you go"
"I will tell you all that is on your mind"
"As for your donkeys that were lost three days ago"
"Do not set your mind on them, for they have been found"
"For whom is all that is desirable in Israel?"
"Is it not for you and for all your father's house?"
Saul: "Am I not a Benjaminite?"
"From the least of the tribes of Israel?"
"Is not my clan the humblest of all the clans?"
"Why then have you spoken to me in this way?"
Samuel takes Saul and his young man
He brings them into the hall
He gives them a place at the head of those invited
About thirty persons
Samuel says to the cook
"Bring the portion I gave you"
The cook takes up the leg and what was on it
He sets it before Saul
Samuel: "See, what was kept is set before you"
"Eat, because it was kept for you until the hour appointed"
Saul eats with Samuel that day
They come down from the high place
He speaks with Saul on the roof
They arise early
About the break of dawn
Samuel calls to Saul on the roof
"Up, that I may send you on your way"
Saul arose
Both he and Samuel go out into the street
As they are going down to the outskirts of the city
Samuel: "Tell the servant to pass on before us"
"But you, stand here a while"
"That I may make known to you the word of God"
Samuel takes a flask of oil
He pours it on Saul's head
He kisses him
"Has not the Lord anointed you to be prince over his people Israel?"
"You shall reign over the people of the Lord"
"You will save them from the hand of their surrounding enemies"
"This shall be the sign to you that the Lord has anointed you"
Samuel tells him the signs
"When you depart from me today"
"You will meet two men by Rachel's tomb"
"They will say to you, 'The donkeys have been found'"
"Then you shall go on from there"
"You will come to the oak of Tabor"
"Three men going up to God at Bethel will meet you"
"One carrying three young goats, another three loaves, another a skin of wine"
"They will greet you and give you two loaves"
"You shall accept them"
"After that you shall come to Gibeath-elohim"
"Where there is a garrison of the Philistines"
"When you come to the city"
"You will meet a group of prophets"
"Prophesying, with harp, tambourine, flute, and lyre before them"
"Then the Spirit of the Lord will rush upon you"
"You will prophesy with them"
"You will be turned into another man"
"When these signs meet you"
"Do what your hand finds to do"
"For God is with you"
"Go down before me to Gilgal"
"I am coming down to you to offer burnt offerings"
"Seven days you shall wait"
"Until I come to you and show you what you shall do"
When Saul turns his back to leave Samuel
God gives him another heart
All these signs come to pass that day
When they come to Gibeah
A group of prophets meets him
The Spirit of God rushes upon him
He prophesies among them
All who knew him previously see him prophesying
"What has come over the son of Kish?"
"Is Saul also among the prophets?"
A man of the place answers
"And who is their father?"
"Is Saul also among the prophets?" becomes a proverb
He finishes prophesying
He comes to the high place
Saul's uncle: "Where did you go?"
"To seek the donkeys"
"When we saw they were not to be found, we went to Samuel"
"Please tell me what Samuel said"
Saul: "He told us plainly that the donkeys had been found"
"But about the matter of the kingdom"
"He did not tell him anything"
Samuel summons the people to the Lord at Mizpah
He says to the people of Israel
"Thus says the Lord, the God of Israel"
"I brought up Israel out of Egypt"
"I delivered you from the hand of the Egyptians"
"From the hand of all the kingdoms that were oppressing you"
"But today you have rejected your God"
"Who saves you from all your calamities and distresses"
"You have said to him, 'Set a king over us'"
"Now present yourselves before the Lord"
"By your tribes and by your thousands"
Samuel brings all the tribes near
The tribe of Benjamin is taken by lot
He brings the tribe of Benjamin near by its clans
The clan of the Matrites is taken
Saul the son of Kish is taken
They seek him, but he cannot be found
They inquire again of the Lord
"Is there a man still to come?"
The Lord: "Behold, he has hidden himself among the baggage"
They run and take him from there
When he stands among the people
He is taller than any of the people from his shoulders upward
Samuel: "Do you see him whom the Lord has chosen?"
"There is none like him among all the people"
All the people shout
"Long live the king!"
Samuel tells the people the rights and duties of the kingship
He writes them in a book
He lays it up before the Lord
Samuel sends all the people away
Each one to his home
Saul also goes to his home at Gibeah
Men of valor go with him
"Whose hearts God had touched"
Some worthless fellows: "How can this man save us?"
They despise him
They bring him no present
He holds his peace
Nahash the Ammonite goes up
He besieges Jabesh-gilead
All the men of Jabesh say to Nahash
"Make a treaty with us, and we will serve you"
Nahash: "On this condition I will make a treaty"
"That I gouge out all your right eyes"
"Thus put disgrace on all Israel"
Elders of Jabesh: "Give us seven days' respite"
"That we may send messengers through all Israel"
"If there is no one to save us, we will give ourselves up to you"
Messengers come to Gibeah of Saul
They tell the news in the ears of the people
All the people weep aloud
Saul is coming from the field behind the oxen
"What is wrong with the people, that they are weeping?"
They tell him the news of the men of Jabesh
The Spirit of God rushes upon Saul
His anger is greatly kindled
He takes a yoke of oxen
He cuts them in pieces
He sends them throughout Israel by messengers
"Whoever does not come out after Saul and Samuel"
"So shall it be done to his oxen!"
The dread of the Lord falls upon the people
They come out as one man
He musters them at Bezek
300,000 from Israel
30,000 from Judah
They say to the messengers
"Thus shall you say to the men of Jabesh-gilead"
"'Tomorrow, by the time the sun is hot, you shall have deliverance'"
The messengers come and tell the men of Jabesh
They are glad
Men of Jabesh say to Nahash
"Tomorrow we will give ourselves up to you"
"Then you may do to us whatever seems good to you"
The next day Saul puts the people in three companies
They come into the midst of the camp in the morning watch
They strike down the Ammonites until the heat of the day
Those who survive are scattered
"So that no two of them are left together"
The people say to Samuel
"Who is it that said, 'Shall Saul reign over us?'"
"Bring the men, that we may put them to death"
Saul: "Not a man shall be put to death this day"
"For today the Lord has worked salvation in Israel"
Samuel: "Come, let us go to Gilgal"
"And there renew the kingdom"
All the people go to Gilgal
They make Saul king before the Lord
They sacrifice peace offerings before the Lord
There Saul and all the men of Israel rejoice greatly
Samuel addresses all Israel
"Behold, I have obeyed your voice"
"I have made a king over you"
"Behold, the king walks before you"
"I am old and gray"
"My sons are with you"
"I have walked before you from my youth until this day"
"Here I am; testify against me"
"Whose ox have I taken?"
"Whose donkey have I taken?"
"Whom have I defrauded?"
"Whom have I oppressed?"
"From whose hand have I taken a bribe to blind my eyes?"
"Testify against me and I will restore it to you"
"You have not defrauded us or oppressed us"
"You have not taken anything from any man's hand"
"The Lord is witness against you"
"His anointed is witness this day"
"That you have not found anything in my hand"
"He is witness"
Samuel recounts Israel's history
"It is the Lord who appointed Moses and Aaron"
"Who brought your fathers up out of Egypt"
"They forgot the Lord their God"
"He sold them into the hand of Sisera"
"Into the hand of the Philistines"
"Into the hand of the king of Moab"
"They cried to the Lord and said"
"'We have sinned, because we have forsaken the Lord'"
"'Deliver us out of the hand of our enemies'"
"The Lord sent Jerubbaal and Barak"
"Jephthah and Samuel, and delivered you"
"When you saw that Nahash was coming against you"
"You said to me, 'No, but a king shall reign over us'"
"When the Lord your God was your king"
"Behold, here is the king you have chosen"
"Behold, the Lord has set a king over you"
"If you will fear the Lord and serve him"
"And obey his voice"
"And not rebel against the commandment of the Lord"
"Then both you and the king will follow the Lord"
"But if you will not obey the voice of the Lord"
"Then the hand of the Lord will be against you and your king"
"Now therefore stand still and see this great thing"
"It is wheat harvest today"
"I will call upon the Lord"
"That he may send thunder and rain"
"You shall know and see that your wickedness is great"
"In asking for yourselves a king"
Samuel calls upon the Lord
The Lord sends thunder and rain that day
All the people greatly fear the Lord and Samuel
All the people say to Samuel
"Pray for your servants to the Lord your God"
"That we may not die"
"For we have added to all our sins this evil, to ask for ourselves a king"
Samuel: "Do not be afraid"
"You have done all this evil"
"Yet do not turn aside from following the Lord"
"Serve the Lord with all your heart"
"The Lord will not forsake his people"
"For his great name's sake"
"It has pleased the Lord to make you a people for himself"
"Moreover, as for me, far be it from me that I should sin against the Lord"
"By ceasing to pray for you"
"I will instruct you in the good and the right way"
"Only fear the Lord and serve him faithfully with all your heart"
"For consider what great things he has done for you"
"But if you still do wickedly"
"You shall be swept away, both you and your king"
Saul is one year old when he begins to reign
When he has reigned two years over Israel
Saul chooses 3,000 men of Israel
2,000 with Saul at Michmash
1,000 with Jonathan at Gibeah
He sends the rest home
Jonathan defeats the garrison of the Philistines at Geba
The Philistines hear of it
Saul blows the trumpet throughout the land
"Let the Hebrews hear"
All Israel hears: "Saul has defeated the garrison"
"Also Israel has become a stench to the Philistines"
The people are called out to join Saul at Gilgal
Philistines gather to fight
30,000 chariots
6,000 horsemen
Troops like the sand on the seashore
They encamp at Michmash
When the men of Israel see they are in trouble
They hide in caves, holes, rocks, tombs, cisterns
Some Hebrews cross the Jordan to Gad and Gilead
Saul is still at Gilgal
All the people follow him trembling
He waits seven days
The time appointed by Samuel
But Samuel does not come to Gilgal
The people are scattering from him
Saul: "Bring the burnt offering and the peace offerings"
He offers the burnt offering
As soon as he finishes offering the burnt offering
Samuel arrives
Saul goes out to meet him and greet him
Samuel: "What have you done?"
Saul: "When I saw that the people were scattering"
"You did not come within the days appointed"
"The Philistines had mustered at Michmash"
"I said, 'Now the Philistines will come down against me at Gilgal'"
"'I have not sought the favor of the Lord'"
"So I forced myself, and offered the burnt offering"
Samuel: "You have done foolishly"
"You have not kept the command of the Lord your God"
"If you had kept it, the Lord would have established your kingdom over Israel forever"
"But now your kingdom shall not continue"
"The Lord has sought out a man after his own heart"
"The Lord has commanded him to be prince over his people"
"Because you have not kept what the Lord commanded you"
Samuel rises and goes
Saul goes up from Gilgal to Gibeah of Benjamin
Saul numbers the people present with him
About 600 men
Saul, Jonathan, and the people are staying in Geba
Philistines encamp at Michmash
Raiders come out of the camp in three companies
One company turns toward Ophrah
One toward Beth-horon
One toward the border that looks down on the Valley of Zeboim
There is no blacksmith in all the land of Israel
"For the Philistines said, 'Lest the Hebrews make swords or spears'"
Every one of the Israelites goes down to the Philistines
To sharpen his plowshare, mattock, axe, or sickle
On the day of the battle
There is neither sword nor spear in the hand of any of the people
Except for Saul and Jonathan
Garrison of the Philistines goes out to the pass of Michmash
Jonathan says to his armor-bearer
"Come, let us go over to the garrison of these uncircumcised"
"It may be that the Lord will work for us"
"For nothing can hinder the Lord from saving by many or by few"
"Do all that is in your heart"
"I am with you heart and soul"
Jonathan: "We will cross over to the men"
"We will show ourselves to them"
"If they say, 'Wait until we come to you'"
"Then we will stand still"
"But if they say, 'Come up to us'"
"Then we will go up"
"For the Lord has given them into our hand"
"This shall be the sign to us"
They show themselves to the garrison
"Look, Hebrews are coming out of the holes"
"Come up to us, and we will show you a thing"
Jonathan to his armor-bearer: "Come up after me"
"For the Lord has given them into the hand of Israel"
Jonathan climbs up on his hands and feet
His armor-bearer after him
They fall before Jonathan
His armor-bearer kills them after him
About twenty men in the first strike
There is a panic in the camp
In the field
Among all the people
The garrison and the raiders also tremble
The earth quakes
It becomes a very great panic
Watchmen of Saul look
The multitude is dispersing here and there
Saul: "Count and see who has gone from us"
They count
Jonathan and his armor-bearer are not there
Saul says to Ahijah: "Bring the ark of God here"
"For the ark was at that time with the people of Israel"
While Saul is talking to the priest
The tumult in the camp of the Philistines increases
Saul: "Withdraw your hand"
Saul and all the people rally
They go to the battle
Every Philistine's sword is against his fellow
Very great confusion
Hebrews who had been with the Philistines join Israel
Israelites who had hidden hear the Philistines are fleeing
They too follow hard after them
The Lord saves Israel that day
The battle passes beyond Beth-aven
Men of Israel are hard pressed that day
Saul has laid an oath on the people
"Cursed be the man who eats food until it is evening"
"And I am avenged on my enemies"
None of the people tastes food
They all enter the forest
There is honey on the ground
When the people enter the forest
The honey is dropping
But no one puts his hand to his mouth
"For the people fear the oath"
Jonathan has not heard his father charge the people
He puts out the tip of the staff
He dips it in the honeycomb
He puts his hand to his mouth
His eyes become bright
One of the people: "Your father strictly charged the people with an oath"
"'Cursed be the man who eats food this day'"
"So the people are faint"
Jonathan: "My father has troubled the land"
"See how my eyes have become bright"
"Because I tasted a little of this honey"
"How much better if the people had eaten freely"
"Of the spoil of their enemies that they found"
"The defeat among the Philistines would have been much greater"
They strike down the Philistines
From Michmash to Aijalon
The people are very faint
They pounce on the spoil
They take sheep, oxen, and calves
They slaughter them on the ground
The people eat them with the blood
"Behold, the people are sinning against the Lord"
"By eating with the blood"
Saul: "You have dealt treacherously"
"Roll a great stone to me here"
"Disperse yourselves among the people"
"Say to them, 'Let every man bring his ox or his sheep'"
"'Slaughter them here and eat'"
"'Do not sin against the Lord by eating with the blood'"
Every man brings his ox that night
They slaughter them there
Saul builds an altar to the Lord
It is the first altar he built
Saul: "Let us go down after the Philistines by night"
"Let us plunder them until the morning light"
"Let us not leave a man of them"
"Do whatever seems good to you"
The priest: "Let us draw near to God here"
Saul inquires of God
"Shall I go down after the Philistines?"
"Will you give them into the hand of Israel?"
He does not answer him that day
Saul: "Come here, all you leaders of the people"
"Know and see how this sin has arisen today"
"As the Lord lives who saves Israel"
"Though it be in Jonathan my son"
"He shall surely die"
Not one of the people answers
He says to all Israel
"You shall be on one side"
"I and Jonathan my son will be on the other"
"Do what seems good to you"
Saul: "O Lord God of Israel"
"Why have you not answered your servant this day?"
"If this guilt is in me or in Jonathan"
"Give Urim"
"But if this guilt is in your people Israel"
"Give Thummim"
Jonathan and Saul are taken
The people are cleared
"Cast the lot between me and my son Jonathan"
Jonathan is taken
Saul: "Tell me what you have done"
Jonathan: "I tasted a little honey"
"With the tip of the staff in my hand"
"Here I am; I will die"
Saul: "God do so to me and more also"
"You shall surely die, Jonathan"
The people say to Saul
"Shall Jonathan die"
"Who has worked this great salvation in Israel?"
"Far from it!"
"As the Lord lives, there shall not one hair of his head fall"
"For he has worked with God this day"
The people ransom Jonathan
He does not die
Saul goes up from pursuing the Philistines
The Philistines go to their own place
Saul takes the kingship over Israel
He fights against all his enemies on every side
Moab, Ammonites, Edom, the kings of Zobah, Philistines
Wherever he turns he puts them to the worse
He does valiantly
He strikes the Amalekites
He delivers Israel out of the hands of those who plundered them
The sons of Saul: Jonathan, Ishvi, and Malchi-shua
His two daughters: Merab the firstborn, Michal the younger
Name of Saul's wife: Ahinoam
Name of the commander of his army: Abner
There is hard fighting against the Philistines all the days of Saul
When Saul sees any strong man
Or any valiant man
He attaches him to himself
Samuel says to Saul
"The Lord sent me to anoint you king"
"Now listen to the words of the Lord"
"Thus says the Lord of hosts"
"I have noted what Amalek did to Israel"
"How he set himself against him on the way"

"Devote to destruction all that they have"
"Do not spare them"
"But kill both man and woman, child and infant"
"Ox and sheep, camel and donkey"

He numbers them in Telaim
200,000 men on foot
10,000 from Judah

He lies in wait in the valley

"Lest I destroy you with them"

Saul defeats the Amalekites
From Havilah as far as Shur
He takes Agag the king alive
He devotes to destruction all the people with the sword
Saul and the people spare Agag
The best of the sheep, oxen, fattened calves, lambs
"All that was good"
They are unwilling to devote them to destruction
All that is despised and worthless they devote to destruction
The word of the Lord comes to Samuel
"I regret that I have made Saul king"
"For he has turned back from following me"
"He has not performed my commandments"
Samuel is angry
He cries to the Lord all night
Samuel rises early to meet Saul
Samuel is told
"Saul came to Carmel"
"He set up a monument for himself"
"He has gone on down to Gilgal"
Samuel comes to Saul
Saul: "Blessed be you to the Lord"
"I have performed the commandment of the Lord"
Samuel: "What then is this bleating of the sheep in my ears?"
"And the lowing of the oxen that I hear?"
Saul: "They have brought them from the Amalekites"
"For the people spared the best of the sheep and of the oxen"
"To sacrifice to the Lord your God"
"The rest we have devoted to destruction"
Samuel: "Stop!"
"I will tell you what the Lord said to me this night"
"Say on"
"Though you are little in your own eyes"
"Are you not the head of the tribes of Israel?"
"The Lord anointed you king over Israel"
"The Lord sent you on a mission"
"'Go, devote to destruction the sinners, the Amalekites'"
"Why then did you not obey the voice of the Lord?"
"Why did you pounce on the spoil?"
"And do what was evil in the sight of the Lord?"
Saul: "I have obeyed the voice of the Lord"
"I have gone on the mission on which the Lord sent me"
"I have brought Agag the king of Amalek"
"I have devoted the Amalekites to destruction"
"But the people took of the spoil"
"Sheep and oxen, the best of the things devoted to destruction"
"To sacrifice to the Lord your God in Gilgal"
Samuel: "Has the Lord as great delight in burnt offerings and sacrifices"
"As in obeying the voice of the Lord?"
"Behold, to obey is better than sacrifice"
"To listen than the fat of rams"
"For rebellion is as the sin of divination"
"And presumption is as iniquity and idolatry"
"Because you have rejected the word of the Lord"
"He has also rejected you from being king"
Saul: "I have sinned"
"For I have transgressed the commandment of the Lord and your words"
"Because I feared the people and obeyed their voice"
"Now therefore, please pardon my sin"
"Return with me that I may bow before the Lord"
Samuel: "I will not return with you"
"For you have rejected the word of the Lord"
"The Lord has rejected you from being king over Israel"
As Samuel turns to go away
Saul seizes the skirt of his robe
It tears
Samuel: "The Lord has torn the kingdom of Israel from you this day"
"He has given it to a neighbor of yours, who is better than you"
"The Glory of Israel will not lie or have regret"
"For he is not a man, that he should have regret"
Saul: "I have sinned"
"Yet honor me now before the elders of my people and before Israel"

"So shall your mother be childless among women"
Samuel hacks Agag to pieces before the Lord in Gilgal
Samuel goes to Ramah
Saul goes up to his house in Gibeah
Samuel does not see Saul again until the day of his death
Samuel grieves over Saul
The Lord regrets that he has made Saul king over Israel
The Lord says to Samuel
"How long will you grieve over Saul?"
"I have rejected him from being king"
"Fill your horn with oil"
"I will send you to Jesse the Bethlehemite"
"For I have provided for myself a king among his sons"

"If Saul hears it, he will kill me"
The Lord: "Take a heifer with you"
"Say, 'I have come to sacrifice to the Lord'"
"Invite Jesse to the sacrifice"
"I will show you what you shall do"
"You shall anoint for me him whom I declare to you"
Samuel does what the Lord commands
He comes to Bethlehem

He consecrates Jesse and his sons
He invites them to the sacrifice
When they come, he looks on Eliab
"Surely the Lord's anointed is before him"

"For I have rejected him"
"The Lord sees not as man sees"
"Man looks on the outward appearance"

He makes him pass before Samuel
"Neither has the Lord chosen this one"
Jesse makes Shammah pass by
"Neither has the Lord chosen this one"

Samuel: "The Lord has not chosen these"
"Are all your sons here?"
"There remains yet the youngest"

He sends and brings him in
He is ruddy
With beautiful eyes and handsome

"For this is he"
Samuel takes the horn of oil
He anoints him in the midst of his brothers
The Spirit of the Lord rushes upon David from that day forward
Samuel rises and goes to Ramah
The Spirit of the Lord departs from Saul
A harmful spirit from the Lord torments him

"When the harmful spirit is upon you"
"He will play it, and you will be well"

"A man of valor, a man of war"
"Prudent in speech, and a man of good presence"

He enters his service

"Let David remain in my service"
"For he has found favor in my sight"
Whenever the harmful spirit is upon Saul
David takes the lyre and plays it
Saul is refreshed and well
The harmful spirit departs from him
Philistines gather their armies for battle
They are gathered at Socoh
They encamp between Socoh and Azekah
Saul and the men of Israel are gathered
They encamp in the Valley of Elah
They draw up in line of battle against the Philistines
Philistines stand on the mountain on one side
Israel stands on the mountain on the other side
A valley between them
A champion comes out from the camp of the Philistines
Named Goliath of Gath
His height is six cubits and a span
He has a helmet of bronze on his head
He is armed with a coat of mail
The weight of the coat is five thousand shekels of bronze
He has bronze armor on his legs
A javelin of bronze slung between his shoulders
The shaft of his spear is like a weaver's beam
His spear's head weighs six hundred shekels of iron
A shield-bearer goes before him
He stands and shouts to the ranks of Israel
"Why have you come out to draw up for battle?"
"Am I not a Philistine, and are you not servants of Saul?"
"Choose a man for yourselves"
"Let him come down to me"
"If he is able to fight with me and kill me"
"Then we will be your servants"
"But if I prevail against him and kill him"
"Then you shall be our servants and serve us"
"I defy the ranks of Israel this day"
"Give me a man, that we may fight together"
When Saul and all Israel hear these words
They are dismayed and greatly afraid
David is the son of an Ephrathite of Bethlehem
The man's name is Jesse
He has eight sons
In the days of Saul the man is already old
The three oldest sons of Jesse have followed Saul
Eliab the firstborn, Abinadab the second, Shammah the third
David is the youngest
The three oldest follow Saul
David goes back and forth from Saul to feed his father's sheep
For forty days the Philistine comes forward
Morning and evening he takes his stand
Jesse says to David
"Take for your brothers an ephah of this parched grain"
"These ten loaves"
"Carry them quickly to the camp to your brothers"
"Also take these ten cheeses to the commander"
"See if your brothers are well"
"Bring some token from them"
Saul and they and all the men of Israel are in the Valley of Elah
Fighting with the Philistines
David rises early in the morning
He leaves the sheep with a keeper
He takes the provisions and goes
He comes to the encampment
The army is going out to the battle line
Shouting the war cry
Israel and the Philistines draw up for battle
Army against army
David leaves the things in charge of the keeper of the baggage
He runs to the ranks
He greets his brothers
As he talks with them

He speaks the same words as before
David hears him
All the men of Israel flee from him
They are much afraid
"Have you seen this man who has come up?"
"Surely he has come up to defy Israel"
"The king will enrich the man who kills him"
"Will give him his daughter"
"Make his father's house free in Israel"
David asks the men who stand by him

"And takes away the reproach from Israel?"
"For who is this uncircumcised Philistine"
"That he should defy the armies of the living God?"
The people answer him in the same way
"So shall it be done to the man who kills him"
When the words David speaks are heard
They repeat them before Saul
Saul sends for him
David says to Saul
"Let no man's heart fail because of him"
"Your servant will go and fight with this Philistine"
Saul: "You are not able to go against this Philistine"
"You are but a youth"
"He has been a man of war from his youth"

"When there came a lion, or a bear"
"And took a lamb from the flock"
"I went after him and struck him"
"I delivered it out of his mouth"
"When he arose against me"
"I caught him by his beard"
"I struck him and killed him"
"Your servant has struck down both lions and bears"
"This uncircumcised Philistine shall be like one of them"
"For he has defied the armies of the living God"
"The Lord who delivered me from the paw of the lion"
"And from the paw of the bear"
"Will deliver me from the hand of this Philistine"
Saul: "Go, and the Lord be with you"
Saul clothes David with his armor
He puts a helmet of bronze on his head
He clothes him with a coat of mail
David straps his sword over his armor

"For he had not tested them"
David: "I cannot go with these"
"For I have not tested them"
David takes them off
He takes his staff in his hand
He chooses five smooth stones from the brook
He puts them in his shepherd's pouch
His sling is in his hand
He approaches the Philistine
The Philistine moves forward
Comes near to David
The man who carried his shield goes before him
When the Philistine looks and sees David
He disdains him
"For he was but a youth"
"Ruddy and handsome in appearance"
The Philistine: "Am I a dog"
"That you come to me with sticks?"

"Come to me"
"I will give your flesh to the birds and to the beasts"
David: "You come to me with a sword, spear, and javelin"
"But I come to you in the name of the Lord of hosts"
"The God of the armies of Israel, whom you have defied"
"This day the Lord will deliver you into my hand"
"I will strike you down"
"I will take your head from you"
"I will give the dead bodies of the host of the Philistines this day"
"To the birds and to the wild beasts"
"That all the earth may know that there is a God in Israel"
"That all this assembly may know"
"That the Lord saves not with sword and spear"
"For the battle is the Lord's"
"He will give you into our hand"
When the Philistine arises and comes and draws near
David runs quickly toward the battle line
David puts his hand in his bag
He takes out a stone
He slings it
It strikes the Philistine on his forehead
The stone sinks into his forehead
He falls on his face to the ground
David prevails over the Philistine with a sling and with a stone
He strikes the Philistine and kills him
There is no sword in the hand of David
David runs and stands over the Philistine
He takes his sword
He draws it out of its sheath
He kills him
He cuts off his head with it
When the Philistines see that their champion is dead
They flee
Men of Israel and Judah rise with a shout
They pursue the Philistines
As far as Gath and the gates of Ekron

As far as Gath and Ekron
The people of Israel come back from chasing the Philistines
They plunder their camp
David takes the head of the Philistine
He brings it to Jerusalem
He puts his armor in his tent
As soon as Saul sees David go out against the Philistine
He says to Abner, commander of the army
"Abner, whose son is this youth?"

The king: "Inquire whose son the boy is"
As soon as David returns from striking down the Philistine
Abner takes him
He brings him before Saul
With the head of the Philistine in his hand
Saul: "Whose son are you, young man?"
David: "I am the son of your servant Jesse the Bethlehemite"
As soon as he has finished speaking to Saul
The soul of Jonathan is knit to the soul of David
Jonathan loves him as his own soul
Saul takes him that day
He will not let him return to his father's house
Jonathan makes a covenant with David
Because he loves him as his own soul
Jonathan strips himself of the robe he is wearing
He gives it to David
His armor, his sword, his bow, his belt
David goes out
Wherever Saul sends him, he succeeds
Saul sets him over the men of war
This is good in the sight of all the people
Also in the sight of Saul's servants
As they are coming home
When David returns from striking down the Philistine
The women come out of all the cities of Israel
Singing and dancing to meet King Saul
With tambourines, with songs of joy, with musical instruments
The women sing to one another as they celebrate
"Saul has struck down his thousands"
"David his ten thousands"
Saul is very angry
This saying displeases him
"They have ascribed to David ten thousands"
"To me they have ascribed thousands"
"What more can he have but the kingdom?"
Saul eyes David from that day on
The next day a harmful spirit from God rushes upon Saul
He raves within his house
David is playing the lyre, as he does day by day
Saul has his spear in his hand

Because the Lord is with him
But has departed from Saul

It pleases David well to be the king's son-in-law

His name is highly esteemed

To all his servants
That they should kill David
Jonathan, Saul's son, delights much in David

"Saul my father seeks to kill you"

When they see the company of the prophets prophesying
Samuel standing as head over them

They also prophesy
When it is told Saul

They also prophesy
Saul sends messengers again the third time
They also prophesy
Then he himself goes to Ramah

He goes there to Naioth in Ramah
The Spirit of God comes upon him also
He goes on and prophesies
Until he comes to Naioth in Ramah
He also strips off his clothes
He also prophesies before Samuel
He lies naked all that day and all that night
"Is Saul also among the prophets?"
David flees from Naioth in Ramah
He comes and says before Jonathan
"What have I done?"

"What is my sin before your father"
"That he seeks my life?"
Jonathan: "Far from it! You shall not die"
"My father does nothing great or small without disclosing it to me"
"Why should my father hide this from me?"
"It is not so"
David vows again
"Your father knows well that I have found favor in your eyes"
"He thinks, 'Let not Jonathan know this'"
"Lest he be grieved"
"But truly, as the Lord lives and as your soul lives"
"There is but a step between me and death"
Jonathan: "Whatever you say, I will do for you"
David: "Behold, tomorrow is the new moon"
"I should not fail to sit at table with the king"

"If your father misses me at all"
"Then say, 'David earnestly asked leave of me'"
"'To run to Bethlehem his city'"
