"'For there is a yearly sacrifice there for all the clan'"
"If he says, 'Good!' it will be well with your servant"
"But if he is angry, know that harm is determined by him"
"Deal kindly with your servant"
"For you have brought your servant into a covenant of the Lord with you"
"But if there is guilt in me, kill me yourself"
"Why should you bring me to your father?"
Jonathan: "Far be it from you!"
"If I knew that harm was determined by my father"
"Would I not tell you?"
David: "Who will tell me if your father answers you roughly?"
Jonathan: "Come, let us go out into the field"
They go out into the field
Jonathan says to David
"The Lord, the God of Israel, be witness!"
"When I have sounded out my father about this time tomorrow"
"If he is well disposed toward David"
"Shall I not then send and disclose it to you?"
"But should it please my father to do you harm"
"The Lord do so to Jonathan and more also"
"If I do not disclose it to you and send you away"
"That you may go in safety"
"May the Lord be with you, as he has been with my father"
"If I am still alive, show me the steadfast love of the Lord"
"That I may not die"
"Do not cut off your steadfast love from my house forever"
"When the Lord cuts off every one of the enemies of David"
Jonathan makes a covenant with the house of David
"May the Lord take vengeance on David's enemies"
Jonathan makes David swear again by his love for him
"For he loved him as he loved his own soul"
Jonathan: "Tomorrow is the new moon"
"You will be missed, because your seat will be empty"
"On the third day go down quickly"
"Go to the place where you hid yourself"
"Remain beside the stone heap"
"I will shoot three arrows to the side of it"
"As though I shot at a mark"
"I will send the boy, saying, 'Go, find the arrows'"
"If I say to the boy, 'Look, the arrows are on this side of you, take them'"
"Then you are to come, for, as the Lord lives, it is safe"
"There is no danger"
"But if I say to the youth, 'Look, the arrows are beyond you'"
"Then go, for the Lord has sent you away"
"As for the matter of which you and I have spoken"
"Behold, the Lord is between you and me forever"
David hides himself in the field
When the new moon comes
The king sits down to eat food
The king sits on his seat, as at other times
On the seat by the wall
Jonathan sits opposite
Abner sits by Saul's side
David's place is empty
Saul does not say anything that day
He thinks, "Something has happened to him"
"He is not clean; surely he is not clean"
On the second day, the day after the new moon
David's place is empty
Saul says to Jonathan
"Why has not the son of Jesse come to the meal?"
"Either yesterday or today?"
Jonathan: "David earnestly asked leave of me to go to Bethlehem"
"He said, 'Let me go'"
"'Our clan holds a sacrifice in the city'"
"'My brother has commanded me to be there'"
"'If I have found favor in your eyes'"
"'Let me get away and see my brothers'"
"'That is why he has not come to the king's table'"
Saul's anger is kindled against Jonathan
"You son of a perverse, rebellious woman"
"Do I not know that you have chosen the son of Jesse"
"To your own shame"
"And to the shame of your mother's nakedness?"
"For as long as the son of Jesse lives on the earth"
"Neither you nor your kingdom shall be established"
"Now send and bring him to me"
"For he shall surely die"
Jonathan: "Why should he be put to death?"
"What has he done?"
Saul hurls his spear at him to strike him
Jonathan knows that his father is determined to put David to death
Jonathan rises from the table in fierce anger
He eats no food the second day of the month
"For he is grieved for David"
"Because his father has disgraced him"
In the morning Jonathan goes out into the field
To the appointment with David
A little boy is with him
He says to his boy, "Run and find the arrows that I shoot"
As the boy runs, he shoots an arrow beyond him
When the boy comes to the place of the arrow
Jonathan cries after the boy
"Is not the arrow beyond you?"
Jonathan cries after the boy
"Hurry! Be quick! Do not stay!"
Jonathan's boy gathers up the arrows
He comes to his master
The boy knows nothing
Only Jonathan and David know the matter
Jonathan gives his weapons to his boy
"Go and carry them to the city"
As soon as the boy has gone
David rises from beside the stone heap
He falls on his face to the ground
He bows three times
They kiss one another
They weep with one another
David weeps the most
Jonathan: "Go in peace"
"Because we have sworn both of us in the name of the Lord"
"'The Lord shall be between me and you'"
"'And between my offspring and your offspring, forever'"
David rises and departs
Jonathan goes into the city
David comes to Nob, to Ahimelech the priest
Ahimelech comes to meet David trembling
"Why are you alone?"
"No one with you?"
David: "The king has charged me with a matter"
"'Let no one know anything of the matter'"
"I have made an appointment with the young men"
"Now then, what do you have on hand?"
"Give me five loaves of bread, or whatever is here"
The priest: "I have no common bread on hand"
"But there is holy bread"
"If the young men have kept themselves from women"
David: "Truly women have been kept from us"
"As always when I go on an expedition"
"The vessels of the young men are holy"
"Even when it is an ordinary journey"
"How much more today will their vessels be holy?"
The priest gives him the holy bread
"For there was no bread there but the bread of the Presence"
"Which is removed from before the Lord"
"To be replaced by hot bread on the day it is taken away"
Now a certain man of the servants of Saul is there that day
Detained before the Lord
His name is Doeg the Edomite
The chief of Saul's herdsmen
David says to Ahimelech
"Is there not here a spear or sword on hand?"
"I have brought neither my sword nor my weapons with me"
"Because the king's business required haste"
The priest: "The sword of Goliath the Philistine"
"Whom you struck down in the Valley of Elah"
"Behold, it is here wrapped in a cloth behind the ephod"
"If you will take that, take it"
"For there is none but that here"
David: "There is none like that; give it to me"
David rises and flees that day from Saul
He goes to Achish the king of Gath
The servants of Achish say to him
"Is not this David the king of the land?"
"Did they not sing to one another of him in dances"
"'Saul has struck down his thousands'"
"'David his ten thousands'?"
David takes these words to heart
He is much afraid of Achish the king of Gath
He changes his behavior before them
He pretends to be insane in their hands
He makes marks on the doors of the gate
He lets his spittle run down his beard
Achish says to his servants
"Behold, you see the man is mad"
"Why then have you brought him to me?"
"Do I lack madmen"
"That you have brought this fellow to behave as a madman in my presence?"
"Shall this fellow come into my house?"
David departs from there
He escapes to the cave of Adullam
When his brothers and all his father's house hear it
They go down there to him
Everyone who is in distress gathers to him
Everyone who is in debt
Everyone who is bitter in soul
He becomes commander over them
There are with him about four hundred men
David goes from there to Mizpeh of Moab
He says to the king of Moab
"Please let my father and my mother stay with you"
"Till I know what God will do for me"
He leaves them with the king of Moab
They stay with him all the time David is in the stronghold
The prophet Gad says to David
"Do not remain in the stronghold"
"Depart, and go into the land of Judah"
David departs
He goes into the forest of Hereth
Saul hears that David is discovered
And the men who are with him
Saul is sitting at Gibeah under the tamarisk tree on the height
His spear in his hand
All his servants are standing about him
Saul says to his servants who stand about him
"Hear now, people of Benjamin"
"Will the son of Jesse give every one of you fields and vineyards?"
"Will he make you all commanders of thousands and commanders of hundreds?"
"That all of you have conspired against me?"
"No one discloses to me when my son makes a covenant with the son of Jesse"
"None of you is sorry for me"
"Or discloses to me that my son has stirred up my servant against me"
"To lie in wait, as at this day"
Doeg the Edomite, who stands by the servants of Saul, answers
"I saw the son of Jesse coming to Nob"
"To Ahimelech the son of Ahitub"
"He inquired of the Lord for him"
"Gave him provisions"
"Gave him the sword of Goliath the Philistine"
The king sends to summon Ahimelech the priest
All his father's house, the priests who are at Nob
All of them come to the king
Saul: "Hear now, son of Ahitub"
"Here I am, my lord"
"Why have you conspired against me"
"You and the son of Jesse"
"In that you have given him bread and a sword"
"Have inquired of God for him"
"So that he has risen against me, to lie in wait, as at this day"
Ahimelech: "Who among all your servants is so faithful as David?"
"Who is the king's son-in-law"
"Who turns aside to do your bidding"
"Who is honored in your house?"
"Is today the first time I have inquired of God for him?"
"No! Let not the king impute anything to his servant"
"Or to all the house of my father"
"For your servant has known nothing of all this"
"Much or little"
The king: "You shall surely die, Ahimelech"
"You and all your father's house"
The king says to the guard who stands about him
"Turn and kill the priests of the Lord"
"Because their hand also is with David"
"They knew that he fled and did not disclose it to me"
The servants of the king will not put out their hand
To strike the priests of the Lord
The king says to Doeg
"You turn and strike the priests"
Doeg the Edomite turns and strikes the priests
He kills on that day eighty-five persons who wore the linen ephod
Nob, the city of the priests, he puts to the sword
Both man and woman, child and infant
Ox, donkey, and sheep, he puts to the sword
One of the sons of Ahimelech escapes
His name is Abiathar
He flees after David
Abiathar tells David that Saul has killed the priests
David: "I knew on that day, when Doeg the Edomite was there"
"That he would surely tell Saul"
"I have occasioned the death of all the persons of your father's house"
"Stay with me; do not be afraid"
"For he who seeks my life seeks your life"
"With me you shall be in safekeeping"
They tell David
"Behold, the Philistines are fighting against Keilah"
"They are robbing the threshing floors"
David inquires of the Lord
"Shall I go and attack these Philistines?"
The Lord: "Go and attack the Philistines and save Keilah"
David's men: "Behold, we are afraid here in Judah"
"How much more then if we go to Keilah against the armies?"
David inquires of the Lord again
The Lord: "Arise, go down to Keilah"
"For I will give the Philistines into your hand"
David and his men go to Keilah
They fight with the Philistines
They bring away their livestock
They strike them with a great blow
David saves the inhabitants of Keilah
When Abiathar flees to David at Keilah
He comes down with an ephod in his hand
It is told Saul that David has come to Keilah
Saul: "God has given him into my hand"
"For he has shut himself in by entering a town that has gates and bars"
Saul summons all the people to war
To go down to Keilah, to besiege David and his men
David knows that Saul is plotting harm against him
He says to Abiathar: "Bring the ephod here"
David: "O Lord, the God of Israel"
"Your servant has surely heard that Saul seeks to come to Keilah"
"To destroy the city on my account"
"Will the men of Keilah surrender me into his hand?"
"Will Saul come down, as your servant has heard?"
"O Lord, the God of Israel, please tell your servant"
The Lord: "He will come down"
"Will the men of Keilah surrender me and my men into the hand of Saul?"
The Lord: "They will surrender you"
David and his men, about six hundred, arise
They depart from Keilah
They go wherever they can go
When Saul is told that David has escaped from Keilah
He gives up the expedition
David remains in the strongholds in the wilderness
In the hill country of the wilderness of Ziph
Saul seeks him every day
God does not give him into his hand
David sees that Saul has come out to seek his life
David is in the wilderness of Ziph at Horesh
Jonathan, Saul's son, rises
He goes to David at Horesh
He strengthens his hand in God
"Do not fear"
"For the hand of Saul my father shall not find you"
"You shall be king over Israel"
"I shall be next to you"
"Saul my father also knows this"
The two of them make a covenant before the Lord
David remains at Horesh
Jonathan goes home
The Ziphites go up to Saul at Gibeah
"Is not David hiding among us in the strongholds at Horesh?"
"On the hill of Hachilah, which is south of Jeshimon?"
"Now, O king, come down"
"Whenever your soul desires to come down"
"Our part shall be to surrender him into the king's hand"
Saul: "May you be blessed by the Lord"
"For you have had compassion on me"
"Go, make yet more sure"
"Know and see the place where his foot is"
"Who has seen him there"
"For it is told me that he is very cunning"
"See therefore and take note of all the lurking places"
"Come back to me with sure information"
"Then I will go with you"
"If he is in the land, I will search him out"
"Among all the thousands of Judah"
They arise and go to Ziph ahead of Saul
David and his men are in the wilderness of Maon
In the Arabah to the south of Jeshimon
Saul and his men go to seek him
David is told
He goes down to the rock
He remains in the wilderness of Maon
When Saul hears that
He pursues after David in the wilderness of Maon
Saul goes on one side of the mountain
David and his men on the other side
David is hurrying to get away from Saul
As Saul and his men are closing in on David and his men to capture them
A messenger comes to Saul
"Hurry and come"
"For the Philistines have made a raid against the land"
Saul returns from pursuing after David
He goes against the Philistines
That place is called the Rock of Escape
David goes up from there
He dwells in the strongholds of Engedi
When Saul returns from following the Philistines
He is told
"Behold, David is in the wilderness of Engedi"
Saul takes three thousand chosen men out of all Israel
He goes to seek David and his men
In front of the Wildgoats' Rocks
He comes to the sheepfolds by the way
A cave is there
Saul goes in to relieve himself
David and his men are sitting in the innermost parts of the cave
The men of David say to him
"Here is the day of which the Lord said to you"
"'Behold, I will give your enemy into your hand'"
"'You shall do to him as it shall seem good to you'"
David rises and stealthily cuts off a corner of Saul's robe
Afterward David's heart strikes him
"Because he had cut off a corner of Saul's robe"
He says to his men
"The Lord forbid that I should do this thing to my lord"
"The Lord's anointed"
"To put out my hand against him"
"Seeing he is the Lord's anointed"
David persuades his men with these words
He does not permit them to attack Saul
Saul rises up and leaves the cave
He goes on his way
Afterward David also rises
He goes out of the cave
He calls after Saul
"My lord the king!"
When Saul looks behind him
David bows with his face to the earth
He prostrates himself
David: "Why do you listen to the words of men who say"
"'Behold, David seeks your harm'?"
"Behold, this day your eyes have seen"
"How the Lord gave you today into my hand in the cave"
"Some told me to kill you"
"But I spared you"
"I said, 'I will not put out my hand against my lord'"
"'For he is the Lord's anointed'"
"See, my father, see the corner of your robe in my hand"
"For by the fact that I cut off the corner of your robe"
"And did not kill you"
"You may know and see that there is no wrong or treason in my hands"
"I have not sinned against you"
"Though you hunt my life to take it"
"May the Lord judge between me and you"
"May the Lord avenge me against you"
"But my hand shall not be against you"
"As the proverb of the ancients says"
"'Out of the wicked comes wickedness'"
"But my hand shall not be against you"
"After whom has the king of Israel come out?"
"After whom do you pursue?"
"After a dead dog! After a flea!"
"May the Lord therefore be judge"
"And give sentence between me and you"
"May he see to it and plead my cause"
"And deliver me from your hand"
As soon as David finishes speaking these words to Saul
Saul: "Is this your voice, my son David?"
Saul lifts up his voice and weeps
"You are more righteous than I"
"For you have repaid me good"
"Whereas I have repaid you evil"
"You have declared this day how you have dealt well with me"
"In that you did not kill me when the Lord put me into your hands"
"For if a man finds his enemy"
"Will he let him go away safe?"
"So may the Lord reward you with good"
"For what you have done to me this day"
"Now, behold, I know that you shall surely be king"
"The kingdom of Israel shall be established in your hand"
"Swear to me therefore by the Lord"
"That you will not cut off my offspring after me"
"That you will not destroy my name out of my father's house"
David swears this to Saul
Saul goes home
David and his men go up to the stronghold
Samuel dies
All Israel assembles and mourns for him
They bury him in his house at Ramah
David is in the wilderness of Maon
There is a man in Maon whose business is in Carmel
The man is very rich
He has three thousand sheep and a thousand goats
He is shearing his sheep in Carmel
The name of the man is Nabal
The name of his wife is Abigail
The woman is discerning and beautiful
The man is harsh and badly behaved
He is a Calebite
David hears in the wilderness that Nabal is shearing his sheep
David sends ten young men
"Go up to Carmel, and go to Nabal"
"Greet him in my name"
"Thus you shall greet him: 'Peace be to you'"
"'Peace be to your house, and peace be to all that you have'"
"I hear that you have shearers"
"Now your shepherds have been with us"
"We did them no harm"
"They missed nothing all the time they were in Carmel"
"Ask your young men, and they will tell you"
"Therefore let my young men find favor in your eyes"
"For we come on a feast day"
"Please give whatever you have at hand to your servants"
"And to your son David"
When David's young men come, they say all this to Nabal
In the name of David
Then they wait
Nabal answers David's servants
"Who is David?"
"Who is the son of Jesse?"
"There are many servants these days who are breaking away from their masters"
"Shall I take my bread and my water"
"And my meat that I have killed for my shearers"
"And give it to men who come from I do not know where?"
David's young men turn away
They come back and tell him all this
David says to his men
"Every man strap on his sword"
Every man straps on his sword
David also straps on his sword
About four hundred men go up after David
Two hundred remain with the baggage
One of the young men tells Abigail, Nabal's wife
"Behold, David sent messengers out of the wilderness to greet our master"
"He railed at them"
"Yet the men were very good to us"
"We suffered no harm"
"We did not miss anything when we were in the fields"
"They were a wall to us both by night and by day"
"All the while we were with them keeping the sheep"
"Now therefore know this and consider what you should do"
"For harm is determined against our master and against all his house"
"For he is such a worthless man that one cannot speak to him"
Abigail makes haste
She takes two hundred loaves and two skins of wine
Five sheep already prepared
Five seahs of parched grain
A hundred clusters of raisins
Two hundred cakes of figs
She lays them on donkeys
She says to her young men, "Go on before me"
"Behold, I come after you"
She does not tell her husband Nabal
As she rides on the donkey and comes down under cover of the mountain
Behold, David and his men come down toward her
She meets them
David has just said
"Surely in vain have I guarded all that this fellow has in the wilderness"
"So that nothing was missed of all that belonged to him"
"He has returned me evil for good"
"God do so to the enemies of David and more also"
"If by morning I leave so much as one male of all who belong to him"
When Abigail sees David
She hurries and gets down from the donkey
She falls before David on her face
She bows to the ground
She falls at his feet
"On me alone, my lord, be the guilt"
"Please let your servant speak in your ears"
"Hear the words of your servant"
"Let not my lord regard this worthless fellow, Nabal"
"For as his name is, so is he"
"Nabal is his name, and folly is with him"
"But I your servant did not see the young men of my lord"
"Whom you sent"
"Now then, my lord, as the Lord lives, and as your soul lives"
"Because the Lord has restrained you from bloodguilt"
"And from saving with your own hand"
"Now then let your enemies and those who seek to do evil to my lord"
"Be as Nabal"
"And now let this present that your servant has brought to my lord"
"Be given to the young men who follow my lord"
"Please forgive the trespass of your servant"
"For the Lord will certainly make my lord a sure house"
"Because my lord is fighting the battles of the Lord"
"And evil shall not be found in you so long as you live"
"If men rise up to pursue you and to seek your life"
"The life of my lord shall be bound in the bundle of the living"
"In the care of the Lord your God"
"And the lives of your enemies he shall sling out"
"As from the hollow of a sling"
"When the Lord has done to my lord according to all the good"
"And has appointed you prince over Israel"
"My lord shall have no cause of grief or pangs of conscience"
"For having shed blood without cause"
"Or for my lord working salvation with his own hand"
"And when the Lord has dealt well with my lord"
"Then remember your servant"
David says to Abigail
"Blessed be the Lord, the God of Israel, who sent you this day to meet me"
"Blessed be your discretion"
"Blessed be you, who have kept me this day from bloodguilt"
"And from working salvation with my own hand"
"For as surely as the Lord, the God of Israel, lives"
"Who has restrained me from hurting you"
"Unless you had hurried and come to meet me"
"Truly by morning there had not been left to Nabal so much as one male"
David receives from her hand what she has brought him
"Go up in peace to your house"
"See, I have obeyed your voice"
"I have granted your petition"
Abigail comes to Nabal
Behold, he is holding a feast in his house
Like the feast of a king
Nabal's heart is merry within him
For he is very drunk
She tells him nothing at all until the morning light
In the morning, when the wine has gone out of Nabal
His wife tells him these things
His heart dies within him
He becomes as a stone
About ten days later the Lord strikes Nabal
He dies
When David hears that Nabal is dead
"Blessed be the Lord who has avenged the insult I received"
"Who has kept back his servant from wrongdoing"
"The Lord has returned the evil of Nabal on his own head"
David sends and speaks to Abigail
To take her as his wife
When the servants of David come to Abigail at Carmel
They say, "David has sent us to you to take you to him as his wife"
She rises and bows with her face to the ground
"Behold, your handmaid is a servant to wash the feet of the servants"
Abigail hurries and rises
She rides on a donkey
With five young women attending her
She follows the messengers of David
She becomes his wife
David also takes Ahinoam of Jezreel
Both of them become his wives
Saul has given Michal his daughter, David's wife, to Palti
The Ziphites come to Saul at Gibeah
"Is not David hiding himself on the hill of Hachilah?"
Saul arises and goes down to the wilderness of Ziph
With three thousand chosen men of Israel
To seek David
Saul encamps on the hill of Hachilah
David remains in the wilderness
When he sees that Saul comes after him into the wilderness
David sends out spies
He learns that Saul has indeed come
David rises and comes to the place where Saul has encamped
David sees the place where Saul lay
With Abner the son of Ner, the commander of his army
Saul is lying within the encampment
The army is encamped around him
David says to Ahimelech the Hittite
And to Joab's brother Abishai the son of Zeruiah
"Who will go down with me into the camp to Saul?"
Abishai: "I will go down with you"
David and Abishai go to the army by night
There lay Saul sleeping within the encampment
His spear stuck in the ground at his head
Abner and the army lying around him
Abishai says to David
"God has given your enemy into your hand this day"
"Now please let me pin him to the earth with one stroke of the spear"
"I will not strike him twice"
David: "Do not destroy him"
"For who can put out his hand against the Lord's anointed"
"And be guiltless?"
"As the Lord lives, the Lord will strike him"
"Or his day will come to die"
"Or he will go down into battle and perish"
"The Lord forbid that I should put out my hand"
"Against the Lord's anointed"
"But take now the spear that is at his head"
"And the jar of water"
"And let us go"
David takes the spear and the jar of water from Saul's head
They go away
No man sees it or knows it
Nor does any awake
For they are all asleep
Because a deep sleep from the Lord has fallen upon them
David goes over to the other side
He stands far off on the top of the hill
A great space is between them
David calls to the army
To Abner the son of Ner
"Will you not answer, Abner?"
Abner: "Who are you who calls to the king?"
David: "Are you not a man?"
"Who is like you in Israel?"
"Why then have you not kept watch over your lord the king?"
"For one of the people came in to destroy the king"
"This thing that you have done is not good"
"As the Lord lives, you deserve to die"
"Because you have not kept watch over your lord"
"The Lord's anointed"
"And now see where the king's spear is"
"And the jar of water that was at his head"
Saul recognizes David's voice
"Is this your voice, my son David?"
David: "It is my voice, my lord, O king"
"Why does my lord pursue after his servant?"
"For what have I done?"
"What evil is on my hands?"
"Now therefore let my lord the king hear the words of his servant"
"If it is the Lord who has stirred you up against me"
"May he accept an offering"
"But if it is men, may they be cursed before the Lord"
"For they have driven me out this day"
"That I should have no share in the heritage of the Lord"
"Saying, 'Go, serve other gods'"
"Now therefore, let not my blood fall to the earth"
"Away from the presence of the Lord"
"For the king of Israel has come out to seek a single flea"
"Like one who hunts a partridge in the mountains"
Saul: "I have sinned"
"Return, my son David"
"For I will no more do you harm"
"Because my life was precious in your eyes this day"
"Behold, I have acted foolishly"
"I have made a great mistake"
David: "Here is the spear, O king"
"Let one of the young men come over and take it"
"The Lord rewards every man for his righteousness and his faithfulness"
"For the Lord gave you into my hand today"
"I would not put out my hand against the Lord's anointed"
"Behold, as your life was precious this day in my sight"
"So may my life be precious in the sight of the Lord"
"May he deliver me out of all tribulation"
Saul: "Blessed be you, my son David"
"You will do many things and will succeed in them"
David goes his way
Saul returns to his place
David says in his heart
"Now I shall perish one day by the hand of Saul"
"There is nothing better for me than that I should escape"
"To the land of the Philistines"
"Then Saul will despair of seeking me any longer within the borders"
"And I shall escape out of his hand"
David arises and goes over
He and the six hundred men who are with him
To Achish the son of Maoch, king of Gath
David lived with Achish at Gath
He and his men, every man with his household
David with his two wives
Ahinoam of Jezreel, and Abigail of Carmel
When it is told Saul that David has fled to Gath
He no longer seeks him
David says to Achish
"If I have found favor in your eyes"
"Let a place be given me in one of the country towns"
"That I may dwell there"
"For why should your servant dwell in the royal city with you?"
Achish gives him Ziklag that day
Therefore Ziklag has belonged to the kings of Judah to this day
The number of the days David lived in the country of the Philistines
Was a year and four months
David and his men go up and make raids
Against the Geshurites, the Girzites, and the Amalekites
For these were the inhabitants of the land from of old
David strikes the land
He leaves neither man nor woman alive
He takes away the sheep, oxen, donkeys, camels, and garments
He returns and comes to Achish
When Achish asks, "Where have you made a raid today?"
David says, "Against the Negeb of Judah"
Or, "Against the Negeb of the Jerahmeelites"
Or, "Against the Negeb of the Kenites"
David leaves neither man nor woman alive to bring news to Gath
Thinking, "Lest they should tell about us"
Such was his custom all the while he lived in the country of the Philistines
Achish trusts David
Thinking, "He has made himself an utter stench to his people Israel"
"Therefore he shall always be my servant"
The Philistines gather all their forces for war
To fight against Israel
Achish says to David
"Understand that you and your men are to go out with me in the army"
David: "Very well, you shall know what your servant can do"
Achish: "Very well, I will make you my bodyguard for life"
Samuel has died
All Israel has mourned for him and buried him in Ramah
Saul has put the mediums and the necromancers out of the land
The Philistines assemble
They come and encamp at Shunem
Saul gathers all Israel
They encamp at Gilboa
When Saul sees the army of the Philistines
He is afraid
His heart trembles greatly
When Saul inquires of the Lord
The Lord does not answer him
Either by dreams, or by Urim, or by prophets
Saul says to his servants
"Seek out for me a woman who is a medium"
"That I may go to her and inquire of her"
His servants: "Behold, there is a medium at En-dor"
Saul disguises himself
He puts on other garments
He goes, he and two men with him
They come to the woman by night
"Divine for me by a spirit"
"Bring up for me whomever I shall name to you"
The woman: "Surely you know what Saul has done"
"How he has cut off the mediums and the necromancers from the land"
"Why then are you laying a trap for my life"
"To bring about my death?"
Saul swears to her by the Lord
"As the Lord lives, no punishment shall come upon you"
The woman: "Whom shall I bring up for you?"
"Bring up Samuel for me"
When the woman sees Samuel
She cries out with a loud voice
The woman: "Why have you deceived me?"
"You are Saul"
The king: "Do not be afraid"
"What do you see?"
The woman: "I see a god coming up out of the earth"
"What is his appearance?"
"An old man is coming up"
"He is wrapped in a robe"
Saul knows that it is Samuel
He bows with his face to the ground
He prostrates himself
Samuel: "Why have you disturbed me by bringing me up?"
Saul: "I am in great distress"
"For the Philistines are warring against me"
"God has turned away from me"
"He answers me no more, either by prophets or by dreams"
"Therefore I have summoned you to tell me what I shall do"
Samuel: "Why then do you ask me"
"Since the Lord has turned from you and become your enemy?"
"The Lord has done to you as he spoke by me"
"For the Lord has torn the kingdom out of your hand"
"He has given it to your neighbor, David"
"Because you did not obey the voice of the Lord"
"And did not carry out his fierce wrath against Amalek"
"Therefore the Lord has done this thing to you this day"
"Moreover, the Lord will give Israel also with you"
"Into the hand of the Philistines"
"Tomorrow you and your sons shall be with me"
"The Lord will give the army of Israel also into the hand of the Philistines"
Saul falls at once full length on the ground
Filled with fear because of the words of Samuel
There is no strength in him
For he has eaten nothing all day and all night
The woman comes to Saul
She sees that he is terrified
"Behold, your servant has obeyed you"
"I have taken my life in my hand"
"I have listened to what you have said to me"
"Now therefore, you also obey your servant"
"Let me set a morsel of bread before you"
"Eat, that you may have strength when you go on your way"
He refuses: "I will not eat"
His servants, together with the woman, urge him
He listens to their words
He arises from the earth
He sits on the bed
The woman has a fattened calf in the house
She quickly kills it
She takes flour and kneads it
She bakes unleavened bread
She puts it before Saul and his servants
They eat
They rise and go away that night
The Philistines gather all their forces at Aphek
The Israelites are encamped by the spring that is in Jezreel
As the lords of the Philistines are passing on by hundreds and by thousands
David and his men are passing on in the rear with Achish
The commanders of the Philistines: "What are these Hebrews doing here?"
Achish: "Is this not David, the servant of Saul, king of Israel?"
"Who has been with me now for days and years"
"Since he deserted to me I have found no fault in him to this day"
The commanders of the Philistines are angry with him
"Send the man back"
"That he may return to the place to which you have assigned him"
"He shall not go down with us to battle"
"Lest in the battle he become an adversary to us"
"For how could this fellow reconcile himself to his lord?"
"Would it not be with the heads of the men here?"
"Is not this David, of whom they sing to one another in dances"
"'Saul has struck down his thousands'"
"'And David his ten thousands'?"
Achish calls David
"As the Lord lives, you have been honest"
"Your going out and your coming in with me in the camp has been blameless"
"For to this day I have found nothing wrong in you"
"From the day of your coming to me to this day"
"Nevertheless, the lords do not approve of you"
"So go back now; and go peaceably"
"That you may not displease the lords of the Philistines"
David: "But what have I done?"
"What have you found in your servant from the day I entered your service"
"Until now, that I may not go and fight"
"Against the enemies of my lord the king?"
Achish: "I know that you are as blameless in my sight as an angel of God"
"Nevertheless, the commanders of the Philistines have said"
"'He shall not go up with us to the battle'"
"Now then rise early in the morning with the servants of your lord"
"As soon as you have light, depart"
David sets out with his men early in the morning
To return to the land of the Philistines
The Philistines go up to Jezreel
When David and his men came to Ziklag on the third day
The Amalekites have made a raid against the Negeb and against Ziklag
They have overcome Ziklag and burned it with fire
They have taken captive the women and all who were in it
Both small and great
They kill no one
But carry them off and go their way
When David and his men come to the city
They find it burned with fire
Their wives and sons and daughters taken captive
David and the people who are with him raise their voices and weep
Until they have no more strength to weep
David's two wives also have been taken captive
Ahinoam of Jezreel and Abigail the widow of Nabal of Carmel
David is greatly distressed
For the people speak of stoning him
Because all the people are bitter in soul
Each for his sons and daughters
But David strengthens himself in the Lord his God
David says to Abiathar the priest
"Bring me the ephod"
Abiathar brings the ephod to David
David inquires of the Lord
"Shall I pursue after this band?"
"Shall I overtake them?"
The Lord: "Pursue, for you shall surely overtake"
"And shall surely rescue"
David sets out, and the six hundred men who are with him
They come to the brook Besor
There those stay behind who are left behind
David and four hundred men continue the pursuit
Two hundred stay behind, too exhausted to cross the brook
They find an Egyptian in the open country
They bring him to David
They give him bread and he eats
They give him water to drink
They give him a piece of a cake of figs
Two clusters of raisins
When he has eaten, his spirit revives
For he has not eaten bread or drunk water for three days and three nights
David: "To whom do you belong?"
"Where are you from?"
"I am a young man of Egypt, servant to an Amalekite"
"My master left me behind"
"Because I fell sick three days ago"
"We had made a raid against the Negeb of the Cherethites"
"Against that which belongs to Judah"
"Against the Negeb of Caleb"
"We burned Ziklag with fire"
David: "Will you take me down to this band?"
"Swear to me by God that you will not kill me"
"Or deliver me into the hands of my master"
"And I will take you down to this band"
He takes him down
Behold, they are spread abroad over all the land
Eating and drinking and dancing
Because of all the great spoil they have taken
From the land of the Philistines and from the land of Judah
David strikes them down from twilight until the evening of the next day
Not a man of them escapes
Except four hundred young men
Who mount camels and flee
David recovers all that the Amalekites have taken
David rescues his two wives
Nothing is missing
Whether small or great, sons or daughters, spoil or anything
David brings back all
David also captures all the flocks and herds
They drive the livestock before him
"This is David's spoil"
David comes to the two hundred men
Who have been too exhausted to follow David
Who had been left at the brook Besor
They go out to meet David and to meet the people
When David comes near to the people he greets them
Then all the wicked and worthless fellows among the men who have gone with David say
"Because they did not go with us"
"We will not give them any of the spoil that we have recovered"
"Except that each man may lead away his wife and children"
"And depart"
David: "You shall not do so, my brothers"
"With what the Lord has given us"
"He has preserved us"
"He has given into our hand the band that came against us"
"Who would listen to you in this matter?"
"For as his share is who goes down into the battle"
"So shall his share be who stays by the baggage"
"They shall share alike"
And he makes it a statute and a rule for Israel
From that day forward to this day
When David comes to Ziklag
He sends part of the spoil to his friends, the elders of Judah
"Here is a present for you from the spoil of the enemies of the Lord"
The Philistines fight against Israel
The men of Israel flee before the Philistines
They fall slain on Mount Gilboa
The Philistines overtake Saul and his sons
The Philistines strike down Jonathan
Abinadab
Malchi-shua, the sons of Saul
The battle presses hard against Saul
The archers find him
He is badly wounded by the archers
Saul says to his armor-bearer
"Draw your sword, and thrust me through with it"
"Lest these uncircumcised come and thrust me through"
"And mistreat me"
His armor-bearer will not
For he fears greatly
Therefore Saul takes his own sword
He falls upon it
When his armor-bearer sees that Saul is dead
He also falls upon his sword
He dies with him
Thus Saul dies
His three sons
His armor-bearer
All his men, on the same day together
When the men of Israel who are on the other side of the valley
And those beyond the Jordan
See that the men of Israel have fled
And that Saul and his sons are dead
They abandon their cities and flee
The Philistines come and dwell in them
The next day, when the Philistines come to strip the slain
They find Saul and his three sons fallen on Mount Gilboa
They cut off his head
They strip off his armor
They send messengers throughout the land of the Philistines
To carry the good news to the house of their idols
And to the people
They put his armor in the temple of Ashtaroth
They fasten his body to the wall of Beth-shan
When the inhabitants of Jabesh-gilead hear what the Philistines have done
All the valiant men arise
They go all night
They take the body of Saul and the bodies of his sons from the wall
They come to Jabesh and burn them there
They take their bones
They bury them under the tamarisk tree in Jabesh
They fast seven days
After the death of Saul
When David has returned from striking down the Amalekites
David remains two days in Ziklag
On the third day, behold, a man comes from Saul's camp
His clothes are torn and earth is on his head
When he comes to David, he falls to the ground
He prostrates himself
David: "Where do you come from?"
"I have escaped from the camp of Israel"
"How did it go? Tell me"
"The people have fled from the battle"
"Many of the people also have fallen and are dead"
"Saul and his son Jonathan also are dead"
David: "How do you know that Saul and his son Jonathan are dead?"
The young man: "By chance I happened to be on Mount Gilboa"
"There was Saul leaning on his spear"
"The chariots and the horsemen were close upon him"
"When he looked behind him, he saw me, and called to me"
"I answered, 'Here I am'"
"He said to me, 'Who are you?'"
"I answered, 'I am an Amalekite'"
"He said to me, 'Stand beside me and kill me'"
"'For anguish has seized me, and yet my life still lingers'"
"So I stood beside him and killed him"
"Because I was sure that he could not live"
"I took the crown that was on his head"
"And the armlet that was on his arm"
"I have brought them here to my lord"
David takes hold of his clothes
He tears them
All the men who are with him do likewise
They mourn and weep and fast until evening
For Saul and for Jonathan his son
For the people of the Lord and for the house of Israel
Because they have fallen by the sword
David says to the young man who told him
"Where do you come from?"
"I am the son of a sojourner, an Amalekite"
David: "How is it you were not afraid"
"To put out your hand to destroy the Lord's anointed?"
David calls one of the young men
"Go, execute him"
He strikes him down so that he dies
David: "Your blood be on your head"
"For your own mouth has testified against you"
"'I have killed the Lord's anointed'"
David laments with this lamentation over Saul and Jonathan
He orders that the people of Judah be taught The Song of the Bow
"Your glory, O Israel, is slain on your high places"
"How the mighty have fallen"
"Tell it not in Gath"
"Publish it not in the streets of Ashkelon"
"Lest the daughters of the Philistines rejoice"
"Lest the daughters of the uncircumcised exult"
"You mountains of Gilboa"
"Let there be no dew or rain upon you"
"Nor fields of offerings"
"For there the shield of the mighty was defiled"
"The shield of Saul, not anointed with oil"
"From the blood of the slain, from the fat of the mighty"
"The bow of Jonathan turned not back"
"The sword of Saul returned not empty"
"Saul and Jonathan, beloved and lovely"
"In life and in death they were not divided"
"They were swifter than eagles"
"They were stronger than lions"
"You daughters of Israel, weep over Saul"
"Who clothed you luxuriously in scarlet"
"Who put ornaments of gold on your apparel"
"How the mighty have fallen in the midst of the battle"
"Jonathan lies slain on your high places"
"I am distressed for you, my brother Jonathan"
"Very pleasant have you been to me"
"Your love to me was extraordinary"
"Surpassing the love of women"
"How the mighty have fallen"
"And the weapons of war perished"
After this David inquires of the Lord
"Shall I go up into any of the cities of Judah?"
The Lord: "Go up"
David: "To which shall I go up?"
"To Hebron"
David goes up there
His two wives also, Ahinoam of Jezreel and Abigail the widow of Nabal
David brings up his men who are with him
Everyone with his household
They dwell in the towns of Hebron
The men of Judah come
They anoint David king over the house of Judah
They tell David
"It was the men of Jabesh-gilead who buried Saul"
David sends messengers to the men of Jabesh-gilead
"May you be blessed by the Lord"
"Because you showed this loyalty to Saul your lord"
"And buried him"
"Now may the Lord show steadfast love and faithfulness to you"
"And I will do good to you because you have done this thing"
"Now therefore let your hands be strong"
"Be valiant"
"For Saul your lord is dead"
"The house of Judah has anointed me king over them"
Abner the son of Ner, commander of Saul's army
Takes Ish-bosheth the son of Saul
He brings him over to Mahanaim
He makes him king over Gilead, Ashurites, Jezreel, Ephraim, Benjamin
Over all Israel
Ish-bosheth, Saul's son, is forty years old when he begins to reign
He reigns two years
The house of Judah follows David
The time that David is king in Hebron over the house of Judah
Is seven years and six months
Abner and the servants of Ish-bosheth go out from Mahanaim to Gibeon
Joab the son of Zeruiah and the servants of David go out
They meet them at the pool of Gibeon
They sit down, one on one side of the pool
The other on the other side
Abner: "Let the young men arise and compete before us"
Joab: "Let them arise"
They arise and pass over by number
Twelve for Benjamin and Ish-bosheth
Twelve of the servants of David
Each catches his opponent by the head
He thrusts his sword in his opponent's side
They fall down together
That place is called Helkath-hazzurim
The battle is very fierce that day
Abner and the men of Israel are beaten before the servants of David
The three sons of Zeruiah are there
Joab, Abishai, and Asahel
Asahel is as swift of foot as a wild gazelle
Asahel pursues Abner
He turns neither to the right hand nor to the left from following Abner
Abner looks behind him
"Is it you, Asahel?"
"It is I"
Abner: "Turn aside to your right hand or to your left"
"Seize one of the young men and take his spoil"
Asahel will not turn aside from following him
Abner says again to Asahel
"Turn aside from following me"
"Why should I strike you to the ground?"
"How then could I lift up my face to your brother Joab?"
He refuses to turn aside
Abner strikes him in the stomach with the butt of his spear
The spear comes out at his back
He falls there and dies where he is
All who come to the place where Asahel has fallen and died, stand still
Joab and Abishai pursue Abner
As the sun is going down they come to the hill of Ammah
The Benjaminites gather themselves together behind Abner
They form a single group
They take their stand on the top of a hill
Abner calls to Joab
"Shall the sword devour forever?"
"Do you not know that the end will be bitter?"
"How long will it be before you tell your people to turn from the pursuit?"
Joab: "As God lives, if you had not spoken"
"Surely the men would not have given up the pursuit until the morning"
Joab blows the trumpet
All the men stop
They pursue Israel no more
They do not fight anymore
Abner and his men go all that night through the Arabah
They cross the Jordan
They march the whole morning
They come to Mahanaim
Joab returns from the pursuit of Abner
When he has gathered all the people together
There are missing from David's servants nineteen men besides Asahel
The servants of David have struck down of Benjamin
360 of Abner's men
They take up Asahel
They bury him in the tomb of his father
Which is at Bethlehem
Joab and his men march all night
The day breaks upon them at Hebron
There is a long war between the house of Saul and the house of David
David grows stronger and stronger
The house of Saul becomes weaker and weaker
Sons are born to David at Hebron
His firstborn is Amnon, of Ahinoam of Jezreel
His second, Chileab, of Abigail the widow of Nabal
The third, Absalom the son of Maacah
The fourth, Adonijah the son of Haggith
The fifth, Shephatiah the son of Abital
The sixth, Ithream, of Eglah, David's wife
These are born to David in Hebron
While there is war between the house of Saul and the house of David
Abner is making himself strong in the house of Saul
Saul has a concubine whose name is Rizpah
Ish-bosheth says to Abner
"Why have you gone in to my father's concubine?"
Abner is very angry over the words of Ish-bosheth
"Am I a dog's head of Judah?"
"To this day I keep showing steadfast love to the house of Saul"
"To his brothers, and to his friends"
"I have not given you into the hand of David"
"Yet you charge me today with a fault concerning a woman"
"God do so to Abner and more also"
"If I do not accomplish for David what the Lord has sworn to him"
"To transfer the kingdom from the house of Saul"
"To set up the throne of David over Israel and over Judah"
"From Dan to Beersheba"
Ish-bosheth cannot answer Abner another word
Because he fears him
Abner sends messengers to David on his behalf
"To whom does the land belong?"
"Make your covenant with me"
"Behold, my hand shall be with you to bring over all Israel"
David: "Good; I will make a covenant with you"
"But one thing I require of you"
"You shall not see my face unless you first bring Michal, Saul's daughter"
"When you come to see my face"
David sends messengers to Ish-bosheth, Saul's son
"Give me my wife Michal, for whom I paid the bride-price of a hundred foreskins"
Ish-bosheth sends and takes her from her husband Paltiel
Her husband goes with her, weeping after her all the way to Bahurim
Abner: "Go, return"
He returns
Abner confers with the elders of Israel
"For some time past you have been seeking David as king over you"
"Now then bring it about"
"For the Lord has promised David"
"'By the hand of my servant David I will save my people Israel'"
"'From the hand of the Philistines, and from the hand of all their enemies'"
Abner also speaks to Benjamin
Abner goes to tell David at Hebron all that Israel and Benjamin think good to do
When Abner comes with twenty men to David at Hebron
David makes a feast for Abner and the men who are with him
Abner says to David
"I will arise and go and will gather all Israel to my lord the king"
"That they may make a covenant with you"
"You may reign over all that your heart desires"
David sends Abner away
He goes in peace
Just then the servants of David arrive with Joab from a raid
Bringing much spoil with them
Abner is not with David at Hebron
For David has sent him away, and he has gone in peace
When Joab and all the army with him arrive
It is told Joab
"Abner the son of Ner came to the king"
"He has let him go, and he has gone in peace"
Joab goes to the king
"What have you done?"
"Behold, Abner came to you"
"Why is it that you have sent him away, so that he is gone?"
"You know that Abner the son of Ner came to deceive you"
"To know your going out and your coming in"
"To know all that you are doing"
When Joab comes out from David's presence
He sends messengers after Abner
They bring him back from the cistern of Sirah
David does not know about it
When Abner returns to Hebron
Joab takes him aside into the midst of the gate to speak with him privately
There he strikes him in the stomach
He dies, for the blood of Asahel his brother
Afterward, when David hears of it
"I and my kingdom are forever guiltless before the Lord"
"For the blood of Abner the son of Ner"
"May it fall upon the head of Joab"
"And upon all his father's house"
"May the house of Joab never be without one who has a discharge"
"Or who is leprous, or who holds a spindle"
"Or who falls by the sword, or who lacks bread"
Joab and Abishai his brother kill Abner
Because he has put their brother Asahel to death
David says to Joab and to all the people who are with him
"Tear your clothes and put on sackcloth"
"Mourn before Abner"
King David follows the bier
They bury Abner at Hebron
The king lifts up his voice and weeps at the grave of Abner
All the people weep
The king laments for Abner
"Should Abner die as a fool dies?"
"Your hands were not bound; your feet were not fettered"
"As one falls before the wicked you have fallen"
All the people weep again over him
All the people come to persuade David to eat bread
While it is yet day
David swears
"God do so to me and more also"
"If I taste bread or anything else till the sun goes down"
All the people take notice of it
It pleases them
As everything that the king does pleases all the people
All the people and all Israel understand that day
That it has not been the king's will to put to death Abner
The king says to his servants
"Do you not know that a prince and a great man has fallen this day in Israel?"
"And I am this day weak, though anointed king"
"These men, the sons of Zeruiah, are more severe than I"
"The Lord repay the evildoer according to his wickedness"
When Ish-bosheth, Saul's son, hears that Abner has died at Hebron
His courage fails
All Israel is dismayed
Saul's son has two men who are captains of raiding bands
The name of the one is Baanah
The name of the other Rechab
Sons of Rimmon a man of Benjamin from Beeroth
For Beeroth also is counted as part of Benjamin
The Beerothites fled to Gittaim
They have been sojourners there to this day
Jonathan, the son of Saul, has a son who is crippled in his feet
He is five years old when the news about Saul and Jonathan comes from Jezreel
His nurse takes him up and flees
As she flees in her haste, he falls and becomes lame
His name is Mephibosheth
The sons of Rimmon the Beerothite, Rechab and Baanah, set out
About the heat of the day they come to the house of Ish-bosheth
As he is taking his noonday rest
They come into the midst of the house
As if to get wheat
They strike him in the stomach
Rechab and Baanah his brother escape
When they come into the house, as he lies on his bed in his bedroom
They strike him and put him to death
They behead him
They take his head
They go by the way of the Arabah all night
They bring the head of Ish-bosheth to David at Hebron
"Here is the head of Ish-bosheth, the son of Saul, your enemy"
"Who sought your life"
"The Lord has avenged my lord the king this day"
"On Saul and on his offspring"
David answers Rechab and Baanah
"As the Lord lives, who has redeemed my life out of every adversity"
"When one told me, 'Behold, Saul is dead'"
"Thinking to bring good news"
"I seized him and killed him at Ziklag"
"Which was the reward I gave him for his news"
"How much more, when wicked men have killed a righteous man"
"In his own house on his bed"
"Shall I not now require his blood at your hand"
"And destroy you from the earth?"
David commands his young men
They kill them
They cut off their hands and feet
They hang them beside the pool at Hebron
They take the head of Ish-bosheth
They bury it in the tomb of Abner at Hebron
All the tribes of Israel come to David at Hebron
"Behold, we are your bone and flesh"
"In times past, when Saul was king over us"
"It was you who led out and brought in Israel"
"The Lord said to you, 'You shall be shepherd of my people Israel'"
"'You shall be prince over Israel'"
All the elders of Israel come to the king at Hebron
King David makes a covenant with them at Hebron before the Lord
They anoint David king over Israel
David is thirty years old when he begins to reign
He reigns forty years
At Hebron he reigns over Judah seven years and six months
At Jerusalem he reigns over all Israel and Judah thirty-three years
The king and his men go to Jerusalem against the Jebusites
The inhabitants of the land
They say to David, "You will not come in here"
"But the blind and the lame will ward you off"
Thinking, "David cannot come in here"
Nevertheless, David takes the stronghold of Zion
That is, the city of David
David says on that day
"Whoever would strike the Jebusites, let him get up the water shaft"
"To attack 'the lame and the blind'"
"Who are hated by David's soul"
Therefore it is said, "The blind and the lame shall not come into the house"
David dwells in the stronghold
He calls it the city of David
David builds the city all around from the Millo inward
David becomes greater and greater
For the Lord, the God of hosts, is with him
Hiram king of Tyre sends messengers to David
Cedar trees, also carpenters and masons
They build David a house
David knows that the Lord has established him king over Israel
That he has exalted his kingdom for the sake of his people Israel
David takes more concubines and wives from Jerusalem
After he comes from Hebron
More sons and daughters are born to David
These are the names of those born to him in Jerusalem
Shammua, Shobab, Nathan, Solomon
Ibhar, Elishua, Nepheg, Japhia
Elishama, Eliada, and Eliphelet
When the Philistines hear that David has been anointed king over Israel
All the Philistines go up to search for David
David hears of it
He goes down to the stronghold
The Philistines come and spread out in the Valley of Rephaim
David inquires of the Lord
"Shall I go up against the Philistines?"
"Will you give them into my hand?"
The Lord: "Go up, for I will certainly give the Philistines into your hand"
David comes to Baal-perazim
David defeats them there
"The Lord has broken through my enemies before me"
"Like a breaking flood"
Therefore the name of that place is called Baal-perazim
The Philistines leave their idols there
David and his men carry them away
The Philistines come up yet again
They spread out in the Valley of Rephaim
When David inquires of the Lord
"You shall not go up"
"Go around to their rear"
"Come against them opposite the balsam trees"
"When you hear the sound of marching in the tops of the balsam trees"
"Then rouse yourself"
"For then the Lord has gone out before you"
"To strike down the army of the Philistines"
David does as the Lord commands him
He strikes down the Philistines from Geba to Gezer
David again gathers all the chosen men of Israel
Thirty thousand
David arises and goes with all the people who are with him
From Baale-judah to bring up from there the ark of God
Which is called by the name of the Lord of hosts
Who sits enthroned on the cherubim
They carry the ark of God on a new cart
They bring it out of the house of Abinadab
Which is on the hill
Uzzah and Ahio, the sons of Abinadab, are driving the new cart
They bring it out of the house of Abinadab with the ark of God
Ahio goes before the ark
David and all the house of Israel are celebrating before the Lord
With songs and lyres and harps and tambourines and castanets and cymbals
When they come to the threshing floor of Nacon
Uzzah puts out his hand to the ark of God
He takes hold of it
For the oxen stumble
The anger of the Lord is kindled against Uzzah
God strikes him down there because of his error
He dies there beside the ark of God
David is angry because the Lord has broken out against Uzzah
That place is called Perez-uzzah to this day
David is afraid of the Lord that day
"How can the ark of the Lord come to me?"
David is not willing to take the ark of the Lord into the city of David
David takes it aside to the house of Obed-edom the Gittite
The ark of the Lord remains in the house of Obed-edom the Gittite
Three months
The Lord blesses Obed-edom and all his household
It is told King David
"The Lord has blessed the household of Obed-edom"
"And all that belongs to him, because of the ark of God"
David goes and brings up the ark of God
From the house of Obed-edom to the city of David with rejoicing
When those who bear the ark of the Lord have gone six steps
He sacrifices an ox and a fattened animal
David dances before the Lord with all his might
David is wearing a linen ephod
David and all the house of Israel bring up the ark of the Lord
With shouting and with the sound of the horn
As the ark of the Lord comes into the city of David
Michal the daughter of Saul looks out of the window
She sees King David leaping and dancing before the Lord
She despises him in her heart
They bring in the ark of the Lord
They set it in its place, inside the tent that David has pitched for it
David offers burnt offerings and peace offerings before the Lord
When David finishes offering the burnt offerings and peace offerings
He blesses the people in the name of the Lord of hosts
He distributes among all the people, the whole multitude of Israel
Both men and women, a cake of bread, a portion of meat, a cake of raisins
All the people depart, each to his house
David returns to bless his household
Michal the daughter of Saul comes out to meet David
"How the king of Israel honored himself today"
"Uncovering himself today before the eyes of his servants' female servants"
"As one of the vulgar fellows shamelessly uncovers himself"
David says to Michal
"It was before the Lord, who chose me above your father"
"And above all his house, to appoint me as prince over Israel"
"The people of the Lord, and I will celebrate before the Lord"
"I will make myself yet more contemptible than this"
"I will be abased in your eyes"
"But by the female servants of whom you have spoken"
"By them I shall be held in honor"
Michal the daughter of Saul has no child to the day of her death
The king dwells in his house
The Lord has given him rest from all his surrounding enemies
The king says to Nathan the prophet
"See now, I dwell in a house of cedar"
"But the ark of God dwells in a tent"
Nathan says to the king
"Go, do all that is in your heart"
"For the Lord is with you"
That same night the word of the Lord comes to Nathan
"Go and tell my servant David"
"'Thus says the Lord: Would you build me a house to dwell in?'"
"I have not lived in a house since the day I brought up the people of Israel"
"From Egypt to this day"
"But I have been moving about in a tent for my dwelling"
"In all places where I have moved with all the people of Israel"
"Did I speak a word with any of the judges of Israel"
"Whom I commanded to shepherd my people Israel"
"'Why have you not built me a house of cedar?'"
"Now, therefore, thus you shall say to my servant David"
"'Thus says the Lord of hosts'"
"'I took you from the pasture, from following the sheep'"
"'That you should be prince over my people Israel'"
"'I have been with you wherever you went'"
"'I have cut off all your enemies from before you'"
"'I will make for you a great name'"
"'Like the name of the great ones of the earth'"
"'I will appoint a place for my people Israel'"
"'I will plant them, so that they may dwell in their own place'"
"'And be disturbed no more'"
"'Violent men shall afflict them no more, as formerly'"
"'From the time that I appointed judges over my people Israel'"
"'I will give you rest from all your enemies'"
"'Moreover, the Lord declares to you'"
"'That the Lord will make you a house'"
"'When your days are fulfilled and you lie down with your fathers'"
"'I will raise up your offspring after you'"
"'Who shall come from your body'"
"'I will establish his kingdom'"
"'He shall build a house for my name'"
"'I will establish the throne of his kingdom forever'"
"'I will be to him a father, and he shall be to me a son'"
"'When he commits iniquity, I will discipline him'"
"'With the rod of men, with the stripes of the sons of men'"
"'But my steadfast love will not depart from him'"
"'As I took it from Saul, whom I put away from before you'"
"'Your house and your kingdom shall be made sure forever before me'"
"'Your throne shall be established forever'"
Nathan speaks to David according to all these words
According to all this vision
King David goes in and sits before the Lord
"Who am I, O Lord God, and what is my house"
"That you have brought me thus far?"
"Yet this was a small thing in your eyes, O Lord God"
"You have spoken also of your servant's house for a great while to come"
"Is this instruction for mankind, O Lord God?"
"What more can David say to you?"
"For you know your servant, O Lord God"
"Because of your promise, and according to your own heart"
"You have brought about all this greatness"
"To make your servant know it"
"Therefore you are great, O Lord God"
"For there is none like you"
"There is no God besides you"
"According to all that we have heard with our ears"
"Who is like your people Israel"
"The one nation on earth whom God went to redeem"
"To be his people, making himself a name"
"Doing for them great and awesome things"
"By driving out before your people, whom you redeemed for yourself"
"Nations and their gods?"
"You established for yourself your people Israel to be your people forever"
"And you, O Lord, became their God"
"Now, O Lord God, confirm forever the word"
"That you have spoken concerning your servant and concerning his house"
"Do as you have spoken"
"Your name will be magnified forever"
"'The Lord of hosts is God over Israel'"
"And the house of your servant David will be established before you"
"For you, O Lord of hosts, the God of Israel, have made this revelation"
"'I will build you a house'"
"Therefore your servant has found courage to pray this prayer to you"
"Now, O Lord God, you are God"
"Your words are true"
"You have promised this good thing to your servant"
"Now therefore may it please you to bless the house of your servant"
"So that it may continue forever before you"
"For you, O Lord God, have spoken"
"With your blessing shall the house of your servant be blessed forever"
After this David defeats the Philistines
He subdues them
David takes Metheg-ammah out of the hand of the Philistines
He defeats Moab
He measures them with a line
Making them lie down on the ground
Two lines he measures to be put to death
One full line to be spared
The Moabites become servants to David
They bring tribute
David also defeats Hadadezer the son of Rehob, king of Zobah
As he went to restore his power at the river Euphrates
David takes from him 1,700 horsemen
And 20,000 foot soldiers
David hamstrings all the chariot horses
But leaves enough for 100 chariots
When the Syrians of Damascus come to help Hadadezer
David strikes down 22,000 men of the Syrians
David puts garrisons in Aram of Damascus
The Syrians become servants to David
They bring tribute
The Lord gives victory to David wherever he goes
David takes the shields of gold that are carried by the servants of Hadadezer
He brings them to Jerusalem
From Betah and from Berothai, cities of Hadadezer
King David takes very much bronze
When Toi king of Hamath hears that David has defeated the whole army of Hadadezer
Toi sends his son Joram to King David
To ask about his health and to bless him
Because he has fought against Hadadezer and defeated him
For Hadadezer has often been at war with Toi
Joram brings with him articles of silver, of gold, and of bronze
King David dedicates these also to the Lord
Together with the silver and gold that he dedicates from all the nations
From Edom, Moab, the Ammonites, the Philistines, Amalek
From the spoil of Hadadezer the son of Rehob, king of Zobah
David makes a name for himself
When he returns, he strikes down 18,000 Edomites in the Valley of Salt
He puts garrisons in Edom
Throughout all Edom he puts garrisons
All the Edomites become David's servants
The Lord gives victory to David wherever he goes
David reigns over all Israel
David administers justice and equity to all his people
Joab the son of Zeruiah is over the army
Jehoshaphat the son of Ahilud is recorder
Zadok the son of Ahitub and Ahimelech the son of Abiathar are priests
Seraiah is secretary
Benaiah the son of Jehoiada is over the Cherethites and the Pelethites
David's sons are priests
David says, "Is there still anyone left of the house of Saul"
"That I may show him kindness for Jonathan's sake?"
There is a servant of the house of Saul whose name is Ziba
They call him to David
The king: "Are you Ziba?"
"I am your servant"
The king: "Is there not still someone of the house of Saul"
"That I may show the kindness of God to him?"
Ziba: "There is still a son of Jonathan"
"He is crippled in his feet"
The king: "Where is he?"
Ziba: "He is in the house of Machir the son of Ammiel, at Lo-debar"
King David sends and brings him from the house of Machir
When Mephibosheth the son of Jonathan, son of Saul, comes to David
He falls on his face and prostrates himself
David: "Mephibosheth!"
"Behold, I am your servant"
David: "Do not fear"
"For I will show you kindness for the sake of your father Jonathan"
"I will restore to you all the land of Saul your father"
"You shall eat at my table always"
He prostrates himself
"What is your servant, that you should show regard for a dead dog such as I?"
The king calls Ziba, Saul's servant
"All that belonged to Saul and to all his house I have given"
"To your master's grandson"
"You and your sons and your servants shall till the land for him"
"Shall bring in the produce, that your master's grandson may have bread to eat"
"But Mephibosheth your master's grandson shall always eat at my table"
Ziba has fifteen sons and twenty servants
Ziba: "According to all that my lord the king commands his servant"
"So will your servant do"
Mephibosheth eats at David's table, like one of the king's sons
Mephibosheth has a young son, whose name is Mica
All who dwell in Ziba's house become Mephibosheth's servants
Mephibosheth dwells in Jerusalem
For he eats always at the king's table
He is lame in both his feet
After this the king of the Ammonites dies
Hanun his son reigns in his place
David says, "I will deal loyally with Hanun the son of Nahash"
"As his father dealt loyally with me"
David sends by his servants to console him concerning his father
When David's servants come into the land of the Ammonites
The princes of the Ammonites say to Hanun their lord
"Do you think, because David has sent comforters to you"
"That he is honoring your father?"
"Has not David sent his servants to you"
"To search the city and to spy it out and to overthrow it?"
Hanun takes David's servants
He shaves off half the beard of each
He cuts off their garments in the middle, at their hips
He sends them away
When it is told David
He sends to meet them
For the men are greatly ashamed
The king: "Remain at Jericho until your beards have grown"
"Then return"
When the Ammonites see that they have become a stench to David
The Ammonites send and hire the Syrians of Beth-rehob
And the Syrians of Zobah, 20,000 foot soldiers
The king of Maacah, 1,000 men
The men of Tob, 12,000 men
When David hears of it, he sends Joab and all the host of the mighty men
The Ammonites come out and draw up in battle array
At the entrance of the gate
The Syrians of Zobah and of Rehob
And the men of Tob and Maacah, are by themselves in the open country
When Joab sees that the battle is set against him both in front and in the rear
He chooses some of the best men of Israel
He arrays them against the Syrians
The rest of his men he puts in the charge of Abishai his brother
He arrays them against the Ammonites
"If the Syrians are too strong for me"
"Then you shall help me"
"But if the Ammonites are too strong for you"
"Then I will come and help you"
"Be of good courage, and let us be courageous for our people"
"And for the cities of our God"
"May the Lord do what seems good to him"
Joab and the people who are with him draw near to battle against the Syrians
They flee before him
When the Ammonites see that the Syrians flee
They likewise flee before Abishai
They enter the city
Joab returns from fighting against the Ammonites
He comes to Jerusalem
When the Syrians see that they have been defeated by Israel
They gather themselves together
Hadadezer sends and brings out the Syrians who are beyond the Euphrates
They come to Helam
Shobach the commander of the army of Hadadezer at their head
When it is told David
He gathers all Israel together
He crosses the Jordan
He comes to Helam
The Syrians array themselves against David
They fight with him
The Syrians flee before Israel
David kills of the Syrians the men of 700 chariots
And 40,000 horsemen
He strikes down Shobach the commander of their army
He dies there
When all the kings who are servants of Hadadezer see
That they have been defeated by Israel
They make peace with Israel and become subject to them
The Syrians are afraid to save the Ammonites anymore
In the spring of the year, the time when kings go out to battle
David sends Joab, and his servants with him, and all Israel
They ravage the Ammonites
They besiege Rabbah
David remains at Jerusalem
Late one afternoon, David arises from his couch
He is walking on the roof of the king's house
From the roof he sees a woman bathing
The woman is very beautiful
David sends and inquires about the woman
"Is not this Bathsheba, the daughter of Eliam?"
"The wife of Uriah the Hittite?"
David sends messengers and takes her
She comes to him
He lies with her
(Now she is purifying herself from her uncleanness)
She returns to her house
The woman conceives
She sends and tells David, "I am pregnant"
David sends word to Joab, "Send me Uriah the Hittite"
Joab sends Uriah to David
When Uriah comes to him, David asks
How Joab is doing and how the people are doing
How the war is going
David says to Uriah, "Go down to your house"
"Wash your feet"
Uriah goes out of the king's house
There follows him a present from the king
Uriah sleeps at the door of the king's house
With all the servants of his lord
He does not go down to his house
When they tell David, "Uriah did not go down to his house"
David says to Uriah
"Have you not come from a journey?"
"Why did you not go down to your house?"
Uriah says to David
"The ark and Israel and Judah dwell in booths"
"My lord Joab and the servants of my lord are camping in the open field"
"Shall I then go to my house, to eat and to drink"
"And to lie with my wife?"
"As you live, and as your soul lives, I will not do this thing"
David says to Uriah, "Remain here today also"
"Tomorrow I will send you back"
Uriah remains in Jerusalem that day and the next
David invites him
He eats in his presence and drinks
David makes him drunk
In the evening he goes out to lie on his couch
With the servants of his lord
He does not go down to his house
In the morning David writes a letter to Joab
He sends it by the hand of Uriah
In the letter he writes
"Set Uriah in the forefront of the hardest fighting"
"Then draw back from him, that he may be struck down, and die"
As Joab is besieging the city
He assigns Uriah to the place where he knows there are valiant men
The men of the city come out and fight with Joab
Some of the servants of David among the people fall
Uriah the Hittite also dies
Joab sends and tells David all the news about the fighting
He instructs the messenger
"When you have finished telling all the news about the fighting to the king"
"Then, if the king's anger rises"
"And if he says to you, 'Why did you go so near the city to fight?'"
"'Did you not know that they would shoot from the wall?'"
"'Who killed Abimelech the son of Jerubbesheth?'"
"'Did not a woman cast an upper millstone on him from the wall'"
"'So that he died at Thebez?'"
"'Why did you go so near the wall?'"
"Then you shall say, 'Your servant Uriah the Hittite is dead also'"
The messenger goes
He comes and tells David all that Joab has sent him to tell
The messenger says to David
"The men gained an advantage over us"
"And came out against us in the field"
"But we drove them back to the entrance of the gate"
"Then the archers shot at your servants from the wall"
"Some of the king's servants are dead"
"Your servant Uriah the Hittite is dead also"
David says to the messenger
"Thus shall you say to Joab"
"'Do not let this matter displease you'"
"'For the sword devours now one and now another'"
"'Strengthen your attack against the city and overthrow it'"
"And encourage him"
When the wife of Uriah hears that Uriah her husband is dead
She mourns for her husband
When the mourning is over
David sends and brings her to his house
She becomes his wife
She bears him a son
The thing that David has done displeases the Lord
The Lord sends Nathan to David
He comes to him and says
"There were two men in a certain city"
"The one rich and the other poor"
"The rich man had very many flocks and herds"
"But the poor man had nothing but one little ewe lamb"
"Which he had bought"
"He brought it up, and it grew up with him and with his children"
"It used to eat of his morsel and drink from his cup"
"And lie in his arms, and it was like a daughter to him"
"Now there came a traveler to the rich man"
"He was unwilling to take one of his own flock or herd"
"To prepare for the guest who had come to him"
"But he took the poor man's lamb"
"And prepared it for the man who had come to him"
David's anger is greatly kindled against the man
"As the Lord lives, the man who has done this deserves to die"
"He shall restore the lamb fourfold"
"Because he did this thing, and because he had no pity"
Nathan says to David, "You are the man"
"Thus says the Lord, the God of Israel"
"'I anointed you king over Israel'"
"'I delivered you out of the hand of Saul'"
"'I gave you your master's house'"
"'Your master's wives into your arms'"
"'I gave you the house of Israel and of Judah'"
"'If this were too little, I would add to you as much more'"
"'Why have you despised the word of the Lord'"
"'To do what is evil in his sight?'"
"'You have struck down Uriah the Hittite with the sword'"
"'Have taken his wife to be your wife'"
"'Have killed him with the sword of the Ammonites'"
"'Now therefore the sword shall never depart from your house'"
"'Because you have despised me'"
"'Have taken the wife of Uriah the Hittite to be your wife'"
"'Thus says the Lord'"
"'Behold, I will raise up evil against you out of your own house'"
"'I will take your wives before your eyes'"
"'Give them to your neighbor'"
"'He shall lie with your wives in the sight of this sun'"
"'For you did it secretly'"
"'But I will do this thing before all Israel and before the sun'"
David says to Nathan, "I have sinned against the Lord"
Nathan says to David, "The Lord also has put away your sin"
"You shall not die"
"Nevertheless, because by this deed you have utterly scorned the Lord"
"The child who is born to you shall die"
Nathan goes to his house
The Lord afflicts the child that Uriah's wife bore to David
He becomes sick
David therefore seeks God on behalf of the child
David fasts
He goes in and lies all night on the ground
The elders of his house stand beside him
To raise him from the ground
He will not
Nor will he eat food with them
On the seventh day the child dies
The servants of David are afraid to tell him that the child is dead
"Behold, while the child was yet alive, we spoke to him"
"He did not listen to us"
"How then can we say to him the child is dead?"
"He may do himself some harm"
When David sees that his servants are whispering together
David understands that the child is dead
David says to his servants, "Is the child dead?"
"He is dead"
David arises from the earth
He washes and anoints himself
He changes his clothes
He goes into the house of the Lord
He worships
He then goes to his own house
