When he asks, they set food before him
He eats
His servants: "What is this thing that you have done?"
"You fasted and wept for the child while he was alive"
"But when the child died, you arose and ate food"
"While the child was still alive, I fasted and wept"
"For I said, 'Who knows whether the Lord will be gracious to me'"
"'That the child may live?'"
"But now he is dead"
"Why should I fast?"
"Can I bring him back again?"
"I shall go to him, but he will not return to me"
David comforts his wife, Bathsheba
He goes in to her
He lies with her
She bears a son
He calls his name Solomon
The Lord loves him
He sends a message by Nathan the prophet
He calls his name Jedidiah, because of the Lord
Joab fights against Rabbah of the Ammonites
He takes the royal city
Joab sends messengers to David
"I have fought against Rabbah"
"Moreover, I have taken the city of waters"
"Now then gather the rest of the people together"
"Encamp against the city and take it"
"Lest I take the city, and it be called by my name"
David gathers all the people together
He goes to Rabbah
He fights against it
He takes it
He takes the crown of their king from his head
The weight of it is a talent of gold
In it is a precious stone
It is placed on David's head
He brings out the spoil of the city, a very great amount
He brings out the people who are in it
He sets them to labor with saws and iron picks and iron axes
He makes them toil at the brick kilns
Thus he does to all the cities of the Ammonites
David and all the people return to Jerusalem
After this, Absalom the son of David has a beautiful sister
Whose name is Tamar
Amnon the son of David loves her
Amnon is so tormented that he makes himself ill
Because of his sister Tamar
For she is a virgin
It seems impossible to Amnon to do anything to her
Amnon has a friend, whose name is Jonadab
The son of Shimeah, David's brother
Jonadab is a very crafty man
"O son of the king, why are you so haggard morning after morning?"
"Will you not tell me?"
Amnon: "I love Tamar, my brother Absalom's sister"
Jonadab: "Lie down on your bed and pretend to be ill"
"When your father comes to see you, say to him"
"'Let my sister Tamar come and give me bread to eat'"
"'Let her prepare the food in my sight'"
"'That I may see it and eat it from her hand'"
Amnon lies down and pretends to be ill
When the king comes to see him
Amnon says to the king
"Please let my sister Tamar come"
"Let her make a couple of cakes in my sight"
"That I may eat from her hand"
David sends home to Tamar
"Go to your brother Amnon's house"
"Prepare food for him"
Tamar goes to her brother Amnon's house
Where he is lying down
She takes dough and kneads it
She makes cakes in his sight
She bakes the cakes
She takes the pan and empties it out before him
He refuses to eat
Amnon: "Send out everyone from me"
Everyone goes out from him
Amnon says to Tamar, "Bring the food into the chamber"
"That I may eat from your hand"
Tamar takes the cakes she has made
She brings them into the chamber to Amnon her brother
When she brings them near him to eat
He takes hold of her
"Come, lie with me, my sister"
"No, my brother, do not violate me"
"For such a thing is not done in Israel"
"Do not do this outrageous thing"
"As for me, where could I carry my shame?"
"And as for you, you would be as one of the outrageous fools in Israel"
"Now therefore, please speak to the king"
"For he will not withhold me from you"
He will not listen to her
Being stronger than she
He violates her
He lies with her
Amnon hates her with very great hatred
So that the hatred with which he hates her is greater
Than the love with which he had loved her
Amnon: "Get up! Go!"
"No, my brother, for this wrong in sending me away"
"Is greater than the other that you did to me"
He will not listen to her
He calls the young man who served him
"Put this woman out of my presence"
"Bolt the door after her"
(Now she is wearing a long robe with sleeves
For thus were the virgin daughters of the king dressed)
His servant puts her out
He bolts the door after her
Tamar puts ashes on her head
She tears the long robe that she wears
She lays her hand on her head
She goes away, crying aloud as she goes
Her brother Absalom says to her
"Has Amnon your brother been with you?"
"Now hold your peace, my sister"
"He is your brother; do not take this to heart"
Tamar dwells, a desolate woman, in her brother Absalom's house
When King David hears of all these things
He is very angry
Absalom speaks to Amnon neither good nor bad
For Absalom hates Amnon
Because he has violated his sister Tamar
After two full years Absalom has sheepshearers at Baal-hazor
Absalom invites all the king's sons
Absalom comes to the king
"Behold, your servant has sheepshearers"
"Please let the king and his servants go with your servant"
The king: "No, my son, let us not all go"
"Lest we be burdensome to you"
He presses him, but he will not go
He gives him his blessing
Absalom: "If not, please let my brother Amnon go with us"
The king: "Why should he go with you?"
Absalom presses him until he lets Amnon and all the king's sons go
Absalom makes a feast like a king's feast
Absalom commands his servants
"Mark when Amnon's heart is merry with wine"
"When I say to you, 'Strike Amnon,' then kill him"
"Do not fear; have not I commanded you?"
"Be courageous and be valiant"
The servants of Absalom do to Amnon as Absalom has commanded
All the king's sons arise
Each mounts his mule and flees
While they are on the way, news comes to David
"Absalom has struck down all the king's sons"
"Not one of them is left"
The king arises
He tears his garments
He lies on the earth
All his servants who are standing by tear their garments
Jonadab the son of Shimeah, David's brother, says
"Let not my lord suppose that they have killed all the young men, the king's sons"
"For Amnon alone is dead"
"For by the command of Absalom this has been determined"
"From the day he violated his sister Tamar"
"Now therefore let not my lord the king so take it to heart"
"As to suppose that all the king's sons are dead"
"For Amnon alone is dead"
Absalom has fled
The young man who kept the watch lifts up his eyes and looks
Behold, many people are coming from the road behind him by the side of the mountain
Jonadab says to the king
"Behold, the king's sons have come"
"As your servant said, so it has come about"
As soon as he has finished speaking
Behold, the king's sons come
They lift up their voice and weep
The king also and all his servants weep very bitterly
Absalom fled and went to Talmai the son of Ammihud, king of Geshur
David mourns for his son day after day
Absalom flees and goes to Geshur
He is there three years
The spirit of the king longs to go out to Absalom
Because he is comforted about Amnon, since he is dead
Joab the son of Zeruiah perceives that the king's heart goes out to Absalom
Joab sends to Tekoa and brings from there a wise woman
He says to her, "Pretend to be a mourner"
"Put on mourning garments"
"Do not anoint yourself with oil"
"But behave like a woman who has been mourning many days for the dead"
"Go to the king and speak thus to him"
Joab puts the words in her mouth
When the woman of Tekoa comes to the king
She falls on her face to the ground
She prostrates herself
"Save me, O king"
The king: "What is your trouble?"
"Alas, I am a widow; my husband is dead"
"Your servant had two sons"
"They quarreled with one another in the field"
"There was no one to separate them"
"One struck the other and killed him"
"Now the whole clan has risen against your servant"
"They say, 'Give up the man who struck his brother'"
"'That we may put him to death for the life of his brother'"
"'Thus they would destroy the heir also'"
"Thus they would quench my coal that is left"
"And leave to my husband neither name nor remnant on the face of the earth"
The king: "Go to your house, and I will give orders concerning you"
The woman of Tekoa: "On me be the guilt, my lord the king"
"And on my father's house"
"Let the king and his throne be guiltless"
The king: "If anyone says anything to you"
"Bring him to me, and he shall never touch you again"
"Please let the king invoke the Lord your God"
"That the avenger of blood kill no more"
"That my son be not destroyed"
"As the Lord lives, not one hair of your son shall fall to the ground"
"Please let your servant speak a word to my lord the king"
"Speak"
"Why then have you planned such a thing against the people of God?"
"For in giving this decision the king convicts himself"
"Inasmuch as the king does not bring his banished one home again"
"We must all die; we are like water spilled on the ground"
"Which cannot be gathered up again"
"But God will not take away life"
"He will devise plans so that the banished one will not remain an outcast"
"Now I have come to say this to my lord the king"
"Because the people have made me afraid"
"Your servant thought, 'I will speak to the king'"
"'It may be that the king will perform the request of his servant'"
"'For the king will hear and deliver his servant'"
"'From the hand of the man who would destroy me and my son together'"
"'From the heritage of God'"
"Your servant thought, 'The word of my lord the king will set me at rest'"
"For my lord the king is like the angel of God to discern good and evil"
"The Lord your God be with you"
The king answers the woman
"Do not hide from me anything I ask you"
The woman: "Let my lord the king speak"
"Is the hand of Joab with you in all this?"
The woman: "As surely as you live, my lord the king"
"One cannot turn to the right hand or to the left"
"From anything that my lord the king has said"
"It was your servant Joab who commanded me"
"It was he who put all these words in the mouth of your servant"
"In order to change the course of things your servant Joab did this"
"But my lord has wisdom like the wisdom of the angel of God"
"To know all things that are on the earth"
The king says to Joab, "Behold now, I grant this"
"Go, bring back the young man Absalom"
Joab falls on his face to the ground
He prostrates himself
He blesses the king
Joab: "Today your servant knows that I have found favor in your sight"
"My lord the king, in that the king has granted the request of his servant"
Joab arises and goes to Geshur
He brings Absalom to Jerusalem
The king: "Let him dwell apart in his own house"
"He is not to come into my presence"
Absalom dwells apart in his own house
He does not come into the king's presence
Now in all Israel there is no one so much to be praised for his handsome appearance
From the sole of his foot to the crown of his head there is no blemish in him
When he cuts the hair of his head
(For at the end of every year he used to cut it)
(When it was heavy on him, he cut it)
He weighs the hair of his head, two hundred shekels by the king's weight
There are born to Absalom three sons, and one daughter whose name is Tamar
She is a beautiful woman
Absalom dwells two full years in Jerusalem
Without coming into the king's presence
Absalom sends for Joab, to send him to the king
Joab will not come to him
He sends a second time, but Joab will not come
Absalom says to his servants
"See, Joab's field is next to mine"
"He has barley there; go and set it on fire"
Absalom's servants set the field on fire
Joab arises and goes to Absalom at his house
"Why have your servants set my field on fire?"
Absalom: "Behold, I sent word to you, 'Come here'"
"'That I may send you to the king, to ask'"
"'Why have I come from Geshur?'"
"'It would be better for me to be there still'"
"Now therefore let me go into the presence of the king"
"If there is guilt in me, let him put me to death"
Joab goes to the king and tells him
The king summons Absalom
He comes to the king
He bows himself on his face to the ground before the king
The king kisses Absalom
After this Absalom gets himself a chariot and horses
Fifty men to run before him
Absalom used to rise early
He would stand beside the way of the gate
When any man had a dispute to come before the king for judgment
Absalom would call to him
"From what city are you?"
When he says, "Your servant is of such and such a tribe in Israel"
Absalom: "See, your claims are good and right"
"But there is no man designated by the king to hear you"
"Oh that I were judge in the land"
"That every man with a dispute or cause might come to me"
"And I would give him justice"
Whenever a man came near to prostrate himself before him
He would put out his hand and take hold of him
He would kiss him
Thus Absalom did to all of Israel who came to the king for judgment
Absalom steals the hearts of the men of Israel
At the end of four years Absalom says to the king
"Please let me go and pay my vow, which I have vowed to the Lord, in Hebron"
"For your servant vowed a vow while I lived at Geshur in Syria"
"'If the Lord will indeed bring me back to Jerusalem'"
"'Then I will offer worship to the Lord'"
The king: "Go in peace"
He arises and goes to Hebron
Absalom sends secret messengers throughout all the tribes of Israel
"As soon as you hear the sound of the trumpet"
"Then say, 'Absalom is king at Hebron'"
With Absalom go two hundred men from Jerusalem
Who are invited guests
They go in their innocence and know nothing
While Absalom is offering the sacrifices
He sends for Ahithophel the Gilonite, David's counselor
From his city Giloh
The conspiracy grows strong
The people with Absalom keep increasing
A messenger comes to David
"The hearts of the men of Israel have gone after Absalom"
David says to all his servants who are with him at Jerusalem
"Arise, and let us flee"
"Or else there will be no escape for us from Absalom"
"Go quickly, lest he overtake us quickly"
"And bring down ruin on us and strike the city with the edge of the sword"
The king's servants: "Behold, your servants are ready to do whatever my lord chooses"
The king goes out
All his household after him
The king leaves ten concubines to keep the house
The king goes out
All the people after him
They halt at the last house
All his servants pass by him
All the Cherethites, all the Pelethites
All the six hundred Gittites who have followed him from Gath
Pass on before the king
The king says to Ittai the Gittite
"Why do you also go with us?"
"Go back and stay with the king"
"For you are a foreigner and also an exile from your home"
"You came only yesterday"
"Should I today make you wander about with us"
"Since I go I know not where?"
"Go back and take your brothers with you"
"May the Lord show steadfast love and faithfulness to you"
Ittai: "As the Lord lives, and as my lord the king lives"
"Wherever my lord the king shall be"
"Whether for death or for life, there also will your servant be"
David: "Go then, pass on"
Ittai the Gittite passes on with all his men
And all the little ones who are with him
All the land weeps aloud as all the people pass by
The king crosses the brook Kidron
All the people pass on toward the wilderness
Abiathar comes up
Behold, Zadok also comes
With all the Levites, bearing the ark of the covenant of God
They set down the ark of God
Until the people have all passed out of the city
The king says to Zadok
"Carry the ark of God back into the city"
"If I find favor in the eyes of the Lord"
"He will bring me back and let me see both it and his dwelling place"
"But if he says, 'I have no pleasure in you'"
"Behold, here I am, let him do to me what seems good to him"
The king also says to Zadok the priest
"Are you not a seer?"
"Go back to the city in peace"
"With your two sons, Ahimaaz your son, and Jonathan the son of Abiathar"
"See, I will wait at the fords of the wilderness"
"Until word comes from you to inform me"
Zadok and Abiathar carry the ark of God back to Jerusalem
They remain there
David goes up the ascent of the Mount of Olives
Weeping as he goes, barefoot and with his head covered
All the people who are with him cover their heads
They go up, weeping as they go
It is told David, "Ahithophel is among the conspirators with Absalom"
David: "O Lord, please turn the counsel of Ahithophel into foolishness"
When David comes to the summit
Where God is worshiped
Behold, Hushai the Archite comes to meet him
With his coat torn and dirt on his head
David says to him
"If you go on with me, you will be a burden to me"
"But if you return to the city and say to Absalom"
"'I will be your servant, O king'"
"'As I have been your father's servant in time past'"
"'So now I will be your servant'"
"Then you will defeat for me the counsel of Ahithophel"
"Are not Zadok and Abiathar the priests with you there?"
"So whatever you hear from the king's house, tell it to Zadok and Abiathar"
"Behold, their two sons are with them there"
"Ahimaaz, Zadok's son, and Jonathan, Abiathar's son"
"By them you shall send to me everything you hear"
Hushai, David's friend, comes into the city
Just as Absalom is entering Jerusalem
When David has passed a little beyond the summit
Ziba the servant of Mephibosheth meets him
With a couple of donkeys saddled
Bearing two hundred loaves of bread
A hundred bunches of raisins
A hundred of summer fruits
And a skin of wine
The king: "Why have you brought these?"
Ziba: "The donkeys are for the king's household to ride on"
"The bread and summer fruit for the young men to eat"
"The wine for those who faint in the wilderness to drink"
The king: "Where is your master's son?"
Ziba: "Behold, he remains in Jerusalem"
"For he said, 'Today the house of Israel will give me back'"
"'The kingdom of my father'"
The king: "Behold, all that belonged to Mephibosheth is now yours"
Ziba: "I pay homage; let me ever find favor in your sight, my lord the king"
When King David comes to Bahurim
There comes out a man of the family of the house of Saul
Whose name is Shimei, the son of Gera
He comes out cursing continually
He throws stones at David and at all the servants of King David
All the people and all the mighty men are on his right hand and on his left
Shimei says as he curses, "Get out, get out, you man of blood"
"You worthless man"
"The Lord has avenged on you all the blood of the house of Saul"
"In whose place you have reigned"
"The Lord has given the kingdom into the hand of your son Absalom"
"See, your evil is on you, for you are a man of blood"
Abishai the son of Zeruiah says to the king
"Why should this dead dog curse my lord the king?"
"Let me go over and take off his head"
The king: "What have I to do with you, you sons of Zeruiah?"
"If he is cursing because the Lord has said to him, 'Curse David'"
"Who then shall say, 'Why have you done so?'"
David says to Abishai and to all his servants
"Behold, my own son seeks my life"
"How much more now may this Benjaminite"
"Leave him alone, and let him curse"
"For the Lord has told him to"
"It may be that the Lord will look on the wrong done to me"
"That the Lord will repay me with good for his cursing today"
David and his men go on the road
While Shimei goes along on the hillside opposite him
Cursing as he goes and throwing stones at him
And flinging dust
The king, and all the people who are with him, arrive weary
At the Jordan
There he refreshes himself
Absalom, and all the people, the men of Israel, come to Jerusalem
Ahithophel with him
When Hushai the Archite, David's friend, comes to Absalom
Hushai says to Absalom, "Long live the king! Long live the king!"
Absalom: "Is this your loyalty to your friend?"
"Why did you not go with your friend?"
Hushai: "No, for whom the Lord and this people and all the men of Israel choose"
"His I will be, and with him I will remain"
"And again, whom should I serve?"
"Should it not be his son?"
"As I have served your father, so I will serve you"
Absalom says to Ahithophel
"Give your counsel"
"What shall we do?"
Ahithophel says to Absalom
"Go in to your father's concubines"
"Whom he has left to keep the house"
"When all Israel hears that you have made yourself a stench to your father"
"Then the hands of all who are with you will be strengthened"
They pitch a tent for Absalom on the roof
Absalom goes in to his father's concubines in the sight of all Israel
Now in those days the counsel that Ahithophel gives
Is as if one consulted the word of God
So is all the counsel of Ahithophel esteemed
Both by David and by Absalom
Ahithophel says to Absalom
"Let me choose twelve thousand men"
"I will arise and pursue David tonight"
"I will come upon him while he is weary and discouraged"
"I will throw him into a panic"
"All the people who are with him will flee"
"I will strike down only the king"
"I will bring all the people back to you as a bride comes home to her husband"
"You seek the life of only one man"
"All the people will be at peace"
The advice seems right to Absalom and all the elders of Israel
Absalom: "Call Hushai the Archite also"
"Let us hear what he has to say"
When Hushai comes to Absalom
Absalom tells him what Ahithophel has said
"Shall we do as he says?"
"If not, you speak"
Hushai says to Absalom
"This time the counsel that Ahithophel has given is not good"
Hushai says, "You know that your father and his men are mighty men"
"They are enraged, like a bear robbed of her cubs in the field"
"Besides, your father is expert in war"
"He will not spend the night with the people"
"Behold, even now he has hidden himself in one of the pits or in some other place"
"As soon as some of the people fall at the first attack"
"Whoever hears it will say, 'There has been a slaughter among the people'"
"Then even the valiant man, whose heart is like the heart of a lion"
"Will utterly melt with fear"
"For all Israel knows that your father is a mighty man"
"Those who are with him are valiant men"
"But my counsel is that all Israel be gathered to you"
"From Dan to Beersheba, as the sand by the sea for multitude"
"That you go to battle in person"
"So we shall come upon him in some place where he is to be found"
"We shall light upon him as the dew falls on the ground"
"Of him and all the men with him not one will be left"
"If he withdraws into a city"
"Then all Israel will bring ropes to that city"
"We shall drag it into the valley"
"Until not even a pebble is to be found there"
Absalom and all the men of Israel say
"The counsel of Hushai the Archite is better"
"Than the counsel of Ahithophel"
For the Lord has ordained to defeat the good counsel of Ahithophel
So that the Lord may bring harm upon Absalom
Hushai tells Zadok and Abiathar the priests
"Thus and so did Ahithophel counsel Absalom and the elders"
"Thus and so have I counseled"
"Now therefore send quickly and tell David"
"'Do not stay tonight at the fords of the wilderness'"
"'But by all means pass over'"
"'Lest the king and all the people who are with him be swallowed up'"
Jonathan and Ahimaaz are waiting at En-rogel
A female servant is to go and tell them
They are to go and tell King David
For they must not be seen entering the city
A young man sees them and tells Absalom
They both go away quickly
They come to the house of a man at Bahurim
Who has a well in his courtyard
They go down into it
The woman takes and spreads a covering over the well's mouth
She scatters grain on it
Nothing is known of it
When Absalom's servants come to the woman at the house
"Where are Ahimaaz and Jonathan?"
The woman: "They have gone over the brook of water"
When they have sought and do not find them
They return to Jerusalem
After they have gone, the men come up out of the well
They go and tell King David
"Arise, and go quickly over the water"
"For thus and so has Ahithophel counseled against you"
David arises, and all the people who are with him
They cross the Jordan
By daybreak not one is left who has not crossed the Jordan
When Ahithophel sees that his counsel is not followed
He saddles his donkey
He goes off home to his own city
He sets his house in order
He hangs himself
He dies and is buried in the tomb of his father
David comes to Mahanaim
Absalom crosses the Jordan with all the men of Israel
Absalom sets Amasa over the army instead of Joab
Amasa is the son of a man named Ithra the Ishmaelite
Who has married Abigal the daughter of Nahash
Sister of Zeruiah, Joab's mother
Israel and Absalom encamp in the land of Gilead
When David comes to Mahanaim
Shobi the son of Nahash from Rabbah of the Ammonites
Machir the son of Ammiel from Lo-debar
Barzillai the Gileadite from Rogelim
Bring beds, basins, and earthen vessels
Wheat, barley, flour, parched grain, beans and lentils
Honey and curds and sheep and cheese from the herd
For David and the people with him to eat
For they say, "The people are hungry and weary and thirsty in the wilderness"
David musters the men who are with him
He sets over them commanders of thousands and commanders of hundreds
David sends out the army
One third under the command of Joab
One third under the command of Abishai the son of Zeruiah, Joab's brother
One third under the command of Ittai the Gittite
The king says to the men
"I myself will also go out with you"
The men: "You shall not go out"
"For if we flee, they will not care about us"
"If half of us die, they will not care about us"
"But you are worth ten thousand of us"
"Therefore it is better that you send us help from the city"
The king: "Whatever seems best to you I will do"
The king stands at the side of the gate
While all the army marches out by hundreds and by thousands
The king commands Joab and Abishai and Ittai
"Deal gently for my sake with the young man Absalom"
All the people hear when the king gives orders to all the commanders
About Absalom
The army goes out into the field against Israel
The battle is fought in the forest of Ephraim
The men of Israel are defeated there by the servants of David
The loss there is great on that day
Twenty thousand men
The battle spreads over the face of all the country
The forest devours more people that day than the sword
Absalom happens to meet the servants of David
Absalom is riding on his mule
The mule goes under the thick branches of a great oak
His head catches fast in the oak
He is suspended between heaven and earth
While the mule that is under him goes on
A certain man sees it
He tells Joab, "Behold, I saw Absalom hanging in an oak"
Joab: "What, you saw him!"
"Why then did you not strike him there to the ground?"
"I would have been glad to give you ten pieces of silver and a belt"
The man: "Even if I felt in my hand the weight of a thousand pieces of silver"
"I would not reach out my hand against the king's son"
"For in our hearing the king commanded you and Abishai and Ittai"
"'For my sake protect the young man Absalom'"
"On the other hand, if I had dealt treacherously against his life"
"And there is nothing hidden from the king"
"Then you yourself would have stood aloof"
Joab: "I will not waste time like this with you"
He takes three javelins in his hand
He thrusts them into the heart of Absalom
While he is still alive in the oak
Ten young men, Joab's armor-bearers, surround Absalom
They strike him and kill him
Joab blows the trumpet
The troops come back from pursuing Israel
For Joab restrained them
They take Absalom
They cast him into a great pit in the forest
They raise over him a very great heap of stones
All Israel flees every one to his own home
Now Absalom in his lifetime has taken and set up for himself the pillar
Which is in the King's Valley
For he says, "I have no son to keep my name in remembrance"
He calls the pillar after his own name
It is called Absalom's monument to this day
Ahimaaz the son of Zadok says
"Let me run and carry news to the king"
"That the Lord has delivered him from the hand of his enemies"
Joab: "You are not to carry news today"
"You may carry news another day"
"But today you shall carry no news"
"Because the king's son is dead"
Joab says to the Cushite, "Go, tell the king what you have seen"
The Cushite bows before Joab, and runs
Ahimaaz the son of Zadok says again to Joab
"Come what may, let me also run after the Cushite"
Joab: "Why will you run, my son"
"Seeing that you will have no reward for the news?"
"Come what may, I will run"
"Run"
Ahimaaz runs by the way of the plain
He outstrips the Cushite
David is sitting between the two gates
The watchman goes up to the roof of the gate by the wall
He lifts up his eyes and looks
He sees a man running alone
The watchman calls out and tells the king
The king: "If he is alone, there is news in his mouth"
He comes nearer and nearer
The watchman sees another man running
The watchman calls to the gate
"See, another man running alone"
The king: "He also brings news"
The watchman: "I think the running of the first is like the running of Ahimaaz"
The king: "He is a good man and comes with good news"
Ahimaaz cries out to the king, "All is well"
He prostrates himself before the king with his face to the earth
"Blessed be the Lord your God"
"Who has delivered up the men who raised their hand against my lord the king"
The king: "Is it well with the young man Absalom?"
Ahimaaz: "When Joab sent your servant"
"I saw a great tumult, but I do not know what it was"
The king: "Turn aside and stand here"
He turns aside and stands still
The Cushite comes
The Cushite: "Good news for my lord the king"
"For the Lord has delivered you this day"
"From the hand of all who rose up against you"
The king: "Is it well with the young man Absalom?"
The Cushite: "May the enemies of my lord the king"
"And all who rise up against you for evil"
"Be like that young man"
The king is deeply moved
He goes up to the chamber over the gate
He weeps
As he goes, he says
"O my son Absalom, my son, my son Absalom"
"Would I had died instead of you"
"O Absalom, my son, my son"
It is told Joab, "Behold, the king is weeping and mourning for Absalom"
The victory that day is turned into mourning for all the people
For the people hear that day
"The king is grieving for his son"
The people steal into the city that day
As people steal in who are ashamed when they flee in battle
The king covers his face
The king cries with a loud voice
"O my son Absalom, O Absalom, my son, my son"
Joab comes into the house to the king
"You have today covered with shame the faces of all your servants"
"Who have this day saved your life"
"And the lives of your sons and your daughters"
"And the lives of your wives and your concubines"
"Because you love those who hate you"
"And hate those who love you"
"For you have made it clear today that commanders and servants are nothing"
"For today I know that if Absalom were alive and all of us were dead today"
"Then you would be pleased"
"Now therefore arise, go out and speak kindly to your servants"
"For I swear by the Lord, if you do not go"
"Not a man will stay with you this night"
"This will be worse for you than all the evil that has come upon you"
"From your youth until now"
The king arises and takes his seat in the gate
They tell all the people
"Behold, the king is sitting in the gate"
All the people come before the king
Now Israel has fled every man to his own home
All the people are arguing throughout all the tribes of Israel
"The king delivered us from the hand of our enemies"
"He saved us from the hand of the Philistines"
"Now he has fled out of the land from Absalom"
"But Absalom, whom we anointed over us, is dead in battle"
"Now therefore why do you say nothing about bringing the king back?"
King David sends this message to Zadok and Abiathar the priests
"Say to the elders of Judah"
"'Why should you be the last to bring the king back to his house?'"
"'The talk of all Israel has come to the king'"
"'You are my brothers; you are my bone and my flesh'"
"'Why then should you be the last to bring back the king?'"
"And say to Amasa"
"'Are you not my bone and my flesh?'"
"'God do so to me and more also'"
"'If you are not commander of my army from now on in place of Joab'"
He sways the heart of all the men of Judah as one man
They send word to the king
"Return, both you and all your servants"
The king comes back to the Jordan
Judah comes to Gilgal to meet the king
To bring the king over the Jordan
Shimei the son of Gera, the Benjaminite, from Bahurim
Hurries to come down with the men of Judah to meet King David
With him are a thousand men from Benjamin
Ziba the servant of the house of Saul, with his fifteen sons
And his twenty servants
They rush to the Jordan before the king
They cross the ford to bring over the king's household
To do his pleasure
Shimei the son of Gera falls down before the king
As he is about to cross the Jordan
He says to the king
"Let not my lord hold me guilty"
"Or remember how your servant did wrong on the day my lord the king left Jerusalem"
"Do not let the king take it to heart"
"For your servant knows that I have sinned"
"Therefore, behold, I have come this day"
"The first of all the house of Joseph to come down to meet my lord the king"
Abishai the son of Zeruiah answers
"Shall not Shimei be put to death for this"
"Because he cursed the Lord's anointed?"
David: "What have I to do with you, you sons of Zeruiah?"
"That you should this day be as an adversary to me?"
"Shall anyone be put to death in Israel this day?"
"For do I not know that I am this day king over Israel?"
The king says to Shimei, "You shall not die"
The king gives him his oath
Mephibosheth the son of Saul comes down to meet the king
He has neither taken care of his feet
Nor trimmed his beard
Nor washed his clothes
From the day the king departed until the day he came back in safety
When he comes to Jerusalem to meet the king
The king: "Why did you not go with me, Mephibosheth?"
"My lord, O king, my servant deceived me"
"For your servant said, 'I will saddle a donkey for myself'"
"'That I may ride on it and go with the king'"
"For your servant is lame"
"He has slandered your servant to my lord the king"
"But my lord the king is like the angel of God"
"Do therefore what seems good to you"
"For all my father's house were but men doomed to death before my lord the king"
"But you set your servant among those who eat at your table"
"What further right have I, then, to cry to the king?"
The king: "Why speak any more of your affairs?"
"I have decided: you and Ziba shall divide the land"
Mephibosheth: "Oh, let him take it all"
"Since my lord the king has come safely home"
Barzillai the Gileadite has come down from Rogelim
He goes on with the king to the Jordan
To escort him over the Jordan
Barzillai is a very aged man, eighty years old
He has provided the king with food while he stayed at Mahanaim
For he is a very wealthy man
The king says to Barzillai
"Come over with me, and I will provide for you with me in Jerusalem"
Barzillai: "How many years have I still to live"
"That I should go up with the king to Jerusalem?"
"I am this day eighty years old"
"Can I discern what is pleasant and what is not?"
"Can your servant taste what he eats or what he drinks?"
"Can I still listen to the voice of singing men and singing women?"
"Why then should your servant be an added burden to my lord the king?"
"Your servant will go a little way over the Jordan with the king"
"Why should the king repay me with such a reward?"
"Please let your servant return"
"That I may die in my own city near the grave of my father and my mother"
"But here is your servant Chimham"
"Let him go over with my lord the king"
"Do for him whatever seems good to you"
The king: "Chimham shall go over with me"
"I will do for him whatever seems good to you"
"Whatever you desire of me, I will do for you"
All the people go over the Jordan
The king goes over
The king kisses Barzillai and blesses him
He returns to his own home
The king goes on to Gilgal
Chimham goes on with him
All the people of Judah, and also half the people of Israel
Bring the king on his way
Behold, all the men of Israel come to the king
"Why have our brothers the men of Judah stolen you away"
"And brought the king and his household over the Jordan"
"And all David's men with him?"
All the men of Judah answer the men of Israel
"Because the king is our close relative"
"Why then are you angry over this matter?"
"Have we eaten at all at the king's expense?"
"Or has he given us any gift?"
The men of Israel answer the men of Judah
"We have ten shares in the king"
"In David also we have more than you"
"Why then did you despise us?"
"Were we not the first to speak of bringing back our king?"
The words of the men of Judah are fiercer than the words of the men of Israel
There happens to be there a worthless man, whose name is Sheba
The son of Bichri, a Benjaminite
He blows the trumpet
"We have no portion in David"
"We have no inheritance in the son of Jesse"
"Every man to his tents, O Israel"
All the men of Israel withdraw from David
They follow Sheba the son of Bichri
The men of Judah follow their king steadfastly
From the Jordan to Jerusalem
David comes to his house at Jerusalem
The king takes the ten concubines whom he has left to care for the house
He puts them in a house under guard
He provides for them
But does not go in to them
They are shut up until the day of their death
Living as if in widowhood
The king says to Amasa
"Call the men of Judah together to me within three days"
"And be here yourself"
Amasa goes to summon Judah
He delays beyond the set time that David has appointed him
David says to Abishai
"Now Sheba the son of Bichri will do us more harm than Absalom"
"Take your lord's servants and pursue him"
"Lest he get himself to fortified cities and escape from us"
Joab's men go out after him
The Cherethites and the Pelethites
All the mighty men
They go out from Jerusalem to pursue Sheba the son of Bichri
When they are at the great stone that is in Gibeon
Amasa comes to meet them
Joab is wearing a soldier's garment
Over it is a belt with a sword in its sheath fastened on his thigh
As he goes forward it falls out
Joab says to Amasa, "Is it well with you, my brother?"
Joab takes Amasa by the beard with his right hand to kiss him
Amasa does not observe the sword that is in Joab's hand
Joab strikes him with it in the stomach
He pours out his entrails to the ground
Without striking a second blow, he dies
Joab and Abishai his brother pursue Sheba the son of Bichri
One of Joab's young men takes his stand by Amasa
"Whoever favors Joab, and whoever is for David, let him follow Joab"
Amasa lies wallowing in his blood in the highway
When the man sees that all the people stop
He carries Amasa out of the highway into the field
He throws a garment over him
When he is taken out of the highway
All the people go on after Joab to pursue Sheba
Sheba passes through all the tribes of Israel to Abel of Beth-maacah
All the Bichrites assemble and follow him in
They come and besiege him in Abel of Beth-maacah
They cast up a mound against the city
It stands against the rampart
They are battering the wall to throw it down
A wise woman calls from the city
"Listen! Listen! Tell Joab, 'Come here, that I may speak to you'"
He comes near her
The woman: "Are you Joab?"
"I am"
"Listen to the words of your servant"
"I am listening"
"They used to say in former times"
"'Let them but ask counsel at Abel,' and so they settled a matter"
"I am one of those who are peaceable and faithful in Israel"
"You seek to destroy a city that is a mother in Israel"
"Why will you swallow up the heritage of the Lord?"
Joab: "Far be it from me, far be it"
"That I should swallow up or destroy"
"That is not true"
"A man of the hill country of Ephraim, called Sheba the son of Bichri"
"Has lifted up his hand against King David"
"Give up him alone, and I will withdraw from the city"
The woman: "Behold, his head shall be thrown to you over the wall"
The woman goes to all the people in her wisdom
They cut off the head of Sheba the son of Bichri
They throw it out to Joab
He blows the trumpet
They disperse from the city, every man to his home
Joab returns to Jerusalem to the king
Joab is in command of all the army of Israel
Benaiah the son of Jehoiada is in command of the Cherethites and the Pelethites
Adoram is in charge of the forced labor
Jehoshaphat the son of Ahilud is the recorder
Sheva is secretary
Zadok and Abiathar are priests
Ira the Jairite is also David's priest
Now there is a famine in the days of David for three years
Year after year
David seeks the face of the Lord
The Lord: "There is bloodguilt on Saul and on his house"
"Because he put the Gibeonites to death"
The king calls the Gibeonites and speaks to them
(Now the Gibeonites are not of the people of Israel
But of the remnant of the Amorites
Although the people of Israel have sworn to spare them
Saul has sought to strike them down in his zeal for the people of Israel and Judah)
David says to the Gibeonites
"What shall I do for you?"
"How shall I make atonement, that you may bless the heritage of the Lord?"
The Gibeonites: "It is not a matter of silver or gold between us and Saul"
"Or his house"
"Neither is it for us to put any man to death in Israel"
"What do you say that I shall do for you?"
"Let seven of his sons be given to us"
"So that we may hang them before the Lord at Gibeah of Saul"
"The chosen of the Lord"
The king: "I will give them"
The king spares Mephibosheth, the son of Saul's son Jonathan
Because of the oath of the Lord that was between them
Between David and Jonathan the son of Saul
The king takes the two sons of Rizpah the daughter of Aiah
Whom she bore to Saul, Armoni and Mephibosheth
The five sons of Merab the daughter of Saul
Whom she bore to Adriel the son of Barzillai the Meholathite
He gives them into the hands of the Gibeonites
They hang them on the mountain before the Lord
The seven of them perish together
They are put to death in the first days of harvest
At the beginning of barley harvest
Rizpah the daughter of Aiah takes sackcloth
She spreads it for herself on the rock
From the beginning of harvest until rain falls upon them from the heavens
She does not allow the birds of the air to come upon them by day
Or the beasts of the field by night
When David is told what Rizpah has done
David goes and takes the bones of Saul and the bones of his son Jonathan
From the men of Jabesh-gilead, who have stolen them from the public square of Beth-shan
Where the Philistines have hanged them, on the day the Philistines killed Saul on Gilboa
He brings up from there the bones of Saul and the bones of his son Jonathan
They gather the bones of those who were hanged
They bury the bones of Saul and his son Jonathan
In the land of Benjamin in Zela, in the tomb of Kish his father
They do all that the king commands
After that God heeds the plea for the land
There is war again between the Philistines and Israel
David goes down together with his servants
They fight against the Philistines
David grows weary
Ishbi-benob, one of the descendants of the giants
Whose spear weighs three hundred shekels of bronze
Is armed with a new sword
He thinks to kill David
Abishai the son of Zeruiah comes to his aid
He attacks the Philistine and kills him
Then David's men swear to him
"You shall no longer go out with us to battle"
"Lest you quench the lamp of Israel"
After this there is again war with the Philistines at Gob
Sibbecai the Hushathite strikes down Saph
Who is one of the descendants of the giants
There is again war with the Philistines at Gob
Elhanan the son of Jaare-oregim, the Bethlehemite
Strikes down Goliath the Gittite
The shaft of whose spear is like a weaver's beam
There is again war at Gath
There is a man of great stature
Who has six fingers on each hand, and six toes on each foot
Twenty-four in number
He also is descended from the giants
When he taunts Israel
Jonathan the son of Shimei, David's brother, strikes him down
These four are descended from the giants in Gath
They fall by the hand of David and by the hand of his servants
David speaks to the Lord the words of this song
On the day when the Lord delivers him from the hand of all his enemies
And from the hand of Saul
"The Lord is my rock and my fortress and my deliverer"
"My God, my rock, in whom I take refuge"
"My shield, and the horn of my salvation"
"My stronghold and my refuge, my savior"
"You save me from violence"
"I call upon the Lord, who is worthy to be praised"
"So I shall be saved from my enemies"
(The song continues)
These are the last words of David
The oracle of David, the son of Jesse
The oracle of the man who was raised on high
The anointed of the God of Jacob
The sweet psalmist of Israel
"The Spirit of the Lord speaks by me"
"His word is on my tongue"
"The God of Israel has spoken"
"The Rock of Israel has said to me"
"'When one rules justly over men'"
"'Ruling in the fear of God'"
"'He dawns on them like the morning light'"
"'Like the sun shining forth on a cloudless morning'"
"'Like rain that makes grass to sprout from the earth'"
"For does not my house stand so with God?"
"For he has made with me an everlasting covenant"
"Ordered in all things and secure"
"For will he not cause to prosper all my help and my desire?"
"But worthless men are all like thorns that are thrown away"
"For they cannot be taken with the hand"
"But the man who touches them arms himself with iron and the shaft of a spear"
"And they are utterly consumed with fire"
These are the names of the mighty men whom David has
Josheb-basshebeth a Tahchemonite
He is chief of the three
He wields his spear against eight hundred whom he kills at one time
Next to him among the three mighty men is Eleazar the son of Dodo
He is with David when they defy the Philistines
Who are gathered there for battle
The men of Israel withdraw
He rises and strikes down the Philistines until his hand is weary
His hand clings to the sword
The Lord brings about a great victory that day
The men return after him only to strip the slain
Next to him is Shammah, the son of Agee the Hararite
The Philistines gather at Lehi
Where there is a plot of ground full of lentils
The men flee from the Philistines
He takes his stand in the midst of the plot
He defends it and strikes down the Philistines
The Lord works a great victory
Three of the thirty chief men go down
They come about harvest time to David at the cave of Adullam
A band of Philistines is encamped in the Valley of Rephaim
David is then in the stronghold
The garrison of the Philistines is then at Bethlehem
David says longingly, "Oh, that someone would give me water to drink"
"From the well of Bethlehem that is by the gate"
The three mighty men break through the camp of the Philistines
They draw water out of the well of Bethlehem that is by the gate
They carry it and bring it to David
He will not drink of it
He pours it out to the Lord
"Far be it from me, O Lord, that I should do this"
"Shall I drink the blood of the men who went at the risk of their lives?"
Therefore he will not drink it
These things the three mighty men do
Abishai, the brother of Joab, is chief of the thirty
He wielded his spear against three hundred men and killed them
He won a name beside the three
He is the most renowned of the thirty
He becomes their commander
But he does not attain to the three
Benaiah the son of Jehoiada is a valiant man of Kabzeel
A doer of great deeds
He strikes down two ariels of Moab
He also goes down and strikes down a lion in a pit on a day when snow has fallen
He strikes down an Egyptian, a handsome man
The Egyptian has a spear in his hand
Benaiah goes down to him with a staff
He snatches the spear out of the Egyptian's hand
He kills him with his own spear
These things Benaiah the son of Jehoiada does
He wins a name beside the three mighty men
He is renowned among the thirty
But he does not attain to the three
David sets him over his bodyguard
(A list of the thirty follows, including Asahel, Uriah the Hittite, and others)
Again the anger of the Lord is kindled against Israel
He incites David against them, saying, "Go, number Israel and Judah"
The king says to Joab, the commander of the army, who is with him
"Go through all the tribes of Israel, from Dan to Beersheba"
"Number the people, that I may know the number of the people"
Joab: "May the Lord your God add to the people a hundred times as many as they are"
"While the eyes of my lord the king still see it"
"But why does my lord the king delight in this thing?"
The king's word prevails against Joab and the commanders of the army
Joab and the commanders of the army go out from the presence of the king
To number the people of Israel
They cross the Jordan
They begin from Aroer, and from the city that is in the middle of the valley
Toward Gad and on to Jazer
They come to Gilead, and to Kadesh in the land of the Hittites
They come to Dan, and from Dan they go around to Sidon
They come to the fortress of Tyre
And to all the cities of the Hivites and Canaanites
They go out to the Negeb of Judah at Beersheba
When they have gone through all the land
They come to Jerusalem at the end of nine months and twenty days
Joab gives the sum of the numbering of the people to the king
In Israel there are 800,000 valiant men who draw the sword
The men of Judah are 500,000
David's heart strikes him after he has numbered the people
David says to the Lord, "I have sinned greatly in what I have done"
"But now, O Lord, please take away the iniquity of your servant"
"For I have done very foolishly"
When David arises in the morning
The word of the Lord comes to the prophet Gad, David's seer
"Go and say to David"
"'Thus says the Lord: Three things I offer you'"
"'Choose one of them, that I may do it to you'"
Gad comes to David and tells him
"Shall three years of famine come to you in your land?"
"Or will you flee three months before your foes while they pursue you?"
"Or shall there be three days' pestilence in your land?"
"Now consider, and decide what answer I shall return to him who sent me"
David: "I am in great distress"
"Let us fall into the hand of the Lord"
"For his mercy is great"
"But let me not fall into the hand of man"
The Lord sends a pestilence on Israel from the morning until the appointed time
From Dan to Beersheba 70,000 men die
When the angel stretches out his hand toward Jerusalem to destroy it
The Lord relents from the calamity
He says to the angel who is working destruction among the people
"It is enough; now stay your hand"
The angel of the Lord is by the threshing floor of Araunah the Jebusite
David speaks to the Lord when he sees the angel who is striking the people
"Behold, I have sinned, and I have done wickedly"
"But these sheep, what have they done?"
"Please let your hand be against me and against my father's house"
Gad comes to David that day
"Go up, build an altar to the Lord on the threshing floor of Araunah"
David goes up at Gad's word, as the Lord commands
When Araunah looks down, he sees the king and his servants coming
Araunah goes out and prostrates himself before the king with his face to the ground
Araunah: "Why has my lord the king come to his servant?"
David: "To buy the threshing floor from you"
"In order to build an altar to the Lord"
"That the plague may be averted from the people"
Araunah: "Let my lord the king take and offer up what seems good to him"
"Here are the oxen for the burnt offering"
"And the threshing sledges and the yokes of the oxen for the wood"
"All this, O king, Araunah gives to the king"
"May the Lord your God accept you"
The king: "No, but I will buy it from you for a price"
"I will not offer burnt offerings to the Lord my God that cost me nothing"
David buys the threshing floor and the oxen for fifty shekels of silver
David builds there an altar to the Lord
He offers burnt offerings and peace offerings
The Lord heeds the plea for the land
The plague is averted from Israel
King David is old and advanced in years
Although they cover him with clothes, he cannot get warm
His servants say to him
"Let a young woman be sought for my lord the king"
"Let her wait on the king and be in his service"
"Let her lie in your arms, that my lord the king may be warm"
They seek for a beautiful young woman throughout all the territory of Israel
They find Abishag the Shunammite
They bring her to the king
The young woman is very beautiful
She becomes the king's servant and attends to him
The king knows her not
Now Adonijah the son of Haggith exalts himself
"I will be king"
He prepares for himself chariots and horsemen
And fifty men to run before him
His father has never at any time displeased him by asking
"Why have you done thus and so?"
He is also a very handsome man
He is born next after Absalom
He confers with Joab the son of Zeruiah
And with Abiathar the priest
They follow Adonijah and help him
Zadok the priest, Benaiah the son of Jehoiada
Nathan the prophet, Shimei, Rei, and David's mighty men
Are not with Adonijah
Adonijah sacrifices sheep, oxen, and fattened cattle
By the Serpent's Stone, which is beside En-rogel
He invites all his brothers, the king's sons
And all the royal officials of Judah
He does not invite Nathan the prophet
Or Benaiah or the mighty men or Solomon his brother
Nathan says to Bathsheba the mother of Solomon
"Have you not heard that Adonijah the son of Haggith has become king?"
"David our lord does not know it"
"Now therefore come, let me give you advice"
"That you may save your own life and the life of your son Solomon"
"Go in at once to King David"
"Say to him, 'Did you not, my lord the king, swear to your servant'"
"'Saying, "Solomon your son shall reign after me"'"
"'"And he shall sit on my throne"?'"
"'Why then is Adonijah king?'"
"Then while you are still speaking with the king"
"I also will come in after you and confirm your words"
Bathsheba goes to the king in his chamber
(The king is very old, and Abishag the Shunammite is attending to the king)
Bathsheba bows and prostrates herself before the king
The king: "What do you desire?"
"My lord, you swore to your servant by the Lord your God"
"'Solomon your son shall reign after me'"
"'"And he shall sit on my throne"'"
"And now, behold, Adonijah is king"
"Although you, my lord the king, do not know it"
"He has sacrificed oxen, fattened cattle, and sheep in abundance"
"He has invited all the sons of the king"
"Abiathar the priest, and Joab the commander of the army"
"But Solomon your servant he has not invited"
"And now, my lord the king, the eyes of all Israel are on you"
"To tell them who shall sit on the throne after you"
"Otherwise it will come to pass, when my lord the king sleeps with his fathers"
"That I and my son Solomon will be counted offenders"
While she is still speaking with the king
Nathan the prophet comes in
They tell the king, "Here is Nathan the prophet"
When he comes in before the king
He prostrates himself before the king with his face to the ground
Nathan: "My lord the king, have you said, 'Adonijah shall reign after me'"
"'"And he shall sit on my throne"?'"
"For he has gone down this day"
"He has sacrificed oxen, fattened cattle, and sheep in abundance"
"He has invited all the king's sons"
"Joab the commander of the army, and Abiathar the priest"
"Behold, they are eating and drinking before him"
"Saying, 'Long live King Adonijah!'"
"But me, your servant, and Zadok the priest"
"Benaiah the son of Jehoiada, and your servant Solomon"
"He has not invited"
"Has this thing been brought about by my lord the king"
"And you have not told your servants"
"Who should sit on the throne of my lord the king after him?"
King David answers
"Call Bathsheba to me"
She comes into the king's presence
She stands before the king
The king swears
"As the Lord lives, who has redeemed my soul out of every adversity"
"As I swore to you by the Lord, the God of Israel"
"'Solomon your son shall reign after me'"
"'"And he shall sit on my throne in my place"'"
"Even so will I do this day"
Bathsheba bows with her face to the ground
She prostrates herself before the king
"May my lord King David live forever"
King David: "Call to me Zadok the priest"
"Nathan the prophet, and Benaiah the son of Jehoiada"
They come before the king
The king says to them
"Take with you the servants of your lord"
"Have Solomon my son ride on my own mule"
"Bring him down to Gihon"
"Let Zadok the priest and Nathan the prophet"
"Anoint him there as king over Israel"
"Then blow the trumpet and say, 'Long live King Solomon!'"
"You shall then come up after him"
"He shall come and sit on my throne"
"For he shall be king in my place"
"I have appointed him to be ruler over Israel and over Judah"
Benaiah: "Amen!"
"May the Lord, the God of my lord the king, say so"
"As the Lord has been with my lord the king"
"Even so may he be with Solomon"
"And make his throne greater than the throne of my lord King David"
Zadok the priest, Nathan the prophet, and Benaiah
The Cherethites and the Pelethites go down
They have Solomon ride on King David's mule
They bring him to Gihon
Zadok the priest takes the horn of oil from the tent
He anoints Solomon
They blow the trumpet
All the people say, "Long live King Solomon!"
All the people go up after him
Playing on pipes, and rejoicing with great joy
So that the earth is split by their noise
Adonijah and all the guests who are with him hear it
As they finish feasting
When Joab hears the sound of the trumpet
"What does this uproar in the city mean?"
While he is still speaking
Jonathan the son of Abiathar the priest comes
Adonijah: "Come in, for you are a worthy man"
"You bring good news"
Jonathan: "No, for our lord King David has made Solomon king"
"The king has sent with him Zadok the priest"
"Nathan the prophet, and Benaiah the son of Jehoiada"
"The Cherethites and the Pelethites"
"They have had him ride on the king's mule"
"Zadok the priest and Nathan the prophet have anointed him king at Gihon"
"They have gone up from there rejoicing"
"So that the city is in an uproar"
"This is the noise that you have heard"
"Solomon sits on the royal throne"
"Moreover, the king's servants came to congratulate our lord King David"
"'May your God make the name of Solomon more famous than yours'"
"'"And make his throne greater than your throne"'"
"The king bowed himself on the bed"
"The king also said, 'Blessed be the Lord, the God of Israel'"
"'"Who has granted someone to sit on my throne this day"'"
"'"My own eyes seeing it"'"
All the guests of Adonijah tremble
They rise, and each goes his own way
Adonijah fears Solomon
He arises and goes and takes hold of the horns of the altar
It is told Solomon
"Behold, Adonijah fears King Solomon"
"Behold, he has laid hold of the horns of the altar"
"'Let King Solomon swear to me first that he will not put his servant to death'"
Solomon: "If he will show himself a worthy man"
"Not one of his hairs shall fall to the earth"
"But if wickedness is found in him, he shall die"
King Solomon sends, and they bring him down from the altar
He comes and pays homage to King Solomon
Solomon: "Go to your house"
When David's time to die draws near
He commands Solomon his son
"I am about to go the way of all the earth"
"Be strong, and show yourself a man"
"Keep the charge of the Lord your God"
"Walking in his ways and keeping his statutes"
"His commandments, his rules, and his testimonies"
"As it is written in the Law of Moses"
"That you may prosper in all that you do"
"And wherever you turn"
"That the Lord may establish his word that he spoke concerning me"
"'If your sons pay close attention to their way'"
"'"To walk before me in faithfulness with all their heart and with all their soul"'"
"'You shall not lack a man on the throne of Israel'"
"Moreover, you also know what Joab the son of Zeruiah did to me"
"What he did to the two commanders of the armies of Israel"
"To Abner the son of Ner, and to Amasa the son of Jether"
"Whom he killed, avenging in time of peace for blood shed in war"
"Putting the blood of war on the belt around his waist"
"And on the sandals on his feet"
"Act therefore according to your wisdom"
"Do not let his gray head go down to Sheol in peace"
"But deal loyally with the sons of Barzillai the Gileadite"
"Let them be among those who eat at your table"
"For with such loyalty they met me when I fled from Absalom"
"And there is also with you Shimei the son of Gera"
"The Benjaminite from Bahurim"
"Who cursed me with a grievous curse"
"On the day when I went to Mahanaim"
"But when he came down to meet me at the Jordan"
"I swore to him by the Lord, 'I will not put you to death with the sword'"
"Now therefore do not hold him guiltless"
"For you are a wise man"
"You will know what you ought to do to him"
"You shall bring his gray head down with blood to Sheol"
David sleeps with his fathers
He is buried in the city of David
The time that David reigns over Israel is forty years
He reigns seven years in Hebron
And thirty-three years in Jerusalem
Solomon sits on the throne of David his father
His kingdom is firmly established
Adonijah the son of Haggith comes to Bathsheba the mother of Solomon
"Do you come peacefully?"
"Peacefully"
"I have something to say to you"
"Say on"
"You know that the kingdom was mine"
"All Israel fully expected me to reign"
"However, the kingdom has turned about and become my brother's"
"For it was his from the Lord"
"And now I have one request to make of you; do not refuse me"
"Say on"
"Please ask King Solomon to give me Abishag the Shunammite as my wife"
"He will not refuse you"
"Very well; I will speak to the king on your behalf"
Bathsheba goes to King Solomon to speak to him on behalf of Adonijah
The king rises to meet her
He bows down to her
He sits on his throne
He has a seat brought for the king's mother
She sits on his right
"I have one small request to make of you; do not refuse me"
The king: "Make your request, my mother"
"For I will not refuse you"
"Let Abishag the Shunammite be given to Adonijah your brother as his wife"
King Solomon answers his mother
"Why do you ask Abishag the Shunammite for Adonijah?"
"Ask for him the kingdom also"
"For he is my older brother"
"Ask for him and for Abiathar the priest and for Joab the son of Zeruiah"
King Solomon swears by the Lord
"God do so to me and more also if this word does not cost Adonijah his life"
"Now therefore as the Lord lives"
"Who has established me and placed me on the throne of David my father"
"Who has made me a house, as he promised"
"Adonijah shall be put to death today"
King Solomon sends Benaiah the son of Jehoiada
He strikes him down, so that he dies
To Abiathar the priest the king says
"Go to Anathoth, to your estate"
"For you deserve death"
"But I will not at this time put you to death"
"Because you carried the ark of the Lord God before David my father"
"Because you shared in all my father's affliction"
Solomon removes Abiathar from being priest to the Lord
Thus fulfilling the word of the Lord that he had spoken concerning the house of Eli
When the news comes to Joab
(For Joab has supported Adonijah, although he has not supported Absalom)
Joab flees to the tent of the Lord
He catches hold of the horns of the altar
It is told King Solomon, "Joab has fled to the tent of the Lord"
"Behold, he is beside the altar"
Solomon sends Benaiah the son of Jehoiada
"Go, strike him down"
Benaiah comes to the tent of the Lord
"The king commands, 'Come out'"
"No, I will die here"
Benaiah brings the king word again
"Thus said Joab, and thus he answered me"
The king: "Do as he has said"
"Strike him down and bury him"
"That you may remove from me and from my father's house"
"The guilt for the blood that Joab shed without cause"
"The Lord will bring back his bloody deeds on his own head"
"Because, without the knowledge of my father David"
"He attacked and killed with the sword two men more righteous and better than himself"
"Abner the son of Ner, commander of the army of Israel"
"And Amasa the son of Jether, commander of the army of Judah"
"So shall their blood come back on the head of Joab"
"And on the head of his descendants forever"
"But for David and for his descendants and for his house and for his throne"
"There shall be peace from the Lord forevermore"
Benaiah the son of Jehoiada goes up
He strikes him down and puts him to death
He is buried in his own house in the wilderness
The king puts Benaiah the son of Jehoiada over the army in place of Joab
The king puts Zadok the priest in the place of Abiathar
The king sends and summons Shimei
"Build yourself a house in Jerusalem and dwell there"
"Do not go out from there to any place whatever"
"For on the day you go out and cross the brook Kidron"
"Know for certain that you shall die"
"Your blood shall be on your own head"
Shimei: "What you say is good"
"As my lord the king has said, so will your servant do"
Shimei dwells in Jerusalem many days
At the end of three years, two of Shimei's servants run away
To Achish, son of Maacah, king of Gath
It is told Shimei, "Behold, your servants are in Gath"
Shimei arises and saddles a donkey
He goes to Gath to Achish to seek his servants
Shimei goes and brings his servants from Gath
When Solomon is told that Shimei has gone from Jerusalem to Gath and returned
The king sends and summons Shimei
"Did I not make you swear by the Lord?"
"Did I not solemnly warn you, saying, 'Know for certain that on the day you go out'"
"'"And go to any place whatever, you shall die"?'"
"You said to me, 'What you say is good; I will obey'"
"Why then have you not kept your oath to the Lord"
"And the commandment with which I commanded you?"
"You know in your own heart all the harm that you did to David my father"
"The Lord will bring back your harm on your own head"
"But King Solomon shall be blessed"
"The throne of David shall be established before the Lord forever"
The king commands Benaiah the son of Jehoiada
He goes out and strikes him down, and he dies
The kingdom is established in the hand of Solomon
Solomon makes a marriage alliance with Pharaoh king of Egypt
He takes Pharaoh's daughter
He brings her into the city of David
Until he has finished building his own house
And the house of the Lord
And the wall around Jerusalem
The people are sacrificing at the high places
Because no house has yet been built for the name of the Lord
Solomon loves the Lord, walking in the statutes of David his father
Only, he sacrifices and makes offerings at the high places
The king goes to Gibeon to sacrifice there
For that is the great high place
Solomon used to offer a thousand burnt offerings on that altar
At Gibeon the Lord appears to Solomon in a dream by night
God says, "Ask what I shall give you"
Solomon: "You have shown great and steadfast love to your servant David"
"Because he walked before you in faithfulness, in righteousness"
"And in uprightness of heart toward you"
"You have kept for him this great and steadfast love"
"You have given him a son to sit on his throne this day"
"And now, O Lord my God, you have made your servant king"
"In place of David my father"
"Although I am but a little child"
"I do not know how to go out or come in"
"Your servant is in the midst of your people whom you have chosen"
"A great people, too many to be numbered or counted"
"Give your servant therefore an understanding mind to govern your people"
"That I may discern between good and evil"
"For who is able to govern this your great people?"
It pleases the Lord that Solomon has asked this
God: "Because you have asked this"
"Have not asked for yourself long life"
"Or riches or the life of your enemies"
"But have asked for yourself understanding to discern what is right"
"Behold, I now do according to your word"
"Behold, I give you a wise and discerning mind"
"So that none like you has been before you"
"And none like you shall arise after you"
"I give you also what you have not asked"
"Both riches and honor"
"So that no other king shall compare with you, all your days"
"And if you will walk in my ways"
"Keeping my statutes and my commandments, as your father David walked"
"Then I will lengthen your days"
Solomon awakes, and behold, it is a dream
He comes to Jerusalem
He stands before the ark of the covenant of the Lord
He offers up burnt offerings and peace offerings
He makes a feast for all his servants
Two prostitutes come to the king
They stand before him
The one woman says, "Oh, my lord"
"This woman and I live in the same house"
"I gave birth to a child while she was in the house"
"Then on the third day after I gave birth, this woman also gave birth"
"We were alone"
"There was no one else with us in the house; only we two were in the house"
"This woman's son died in the night"
"Because she lay on him"
"She arose at midnight"
"She took my son from beside me, while your servant slept"
"She laid him at her breast"
"And laid her dead son at my breast"
"When I rose in the morning to nurse my child"
"Behold, he was dead"
"But when I looked at him closely in the morning"
"Behold, he was not the child that I had borne"
The other woman: "No, the living child is mine"
"The dead child is yours"
The first: "No, the dead child is yours"
"The living child is mine"
Thus they speak before the king
The king: "The one says, 'This is my son that is alive, and your son is dead'"
"The other says, 'No; but your son is dead, and my son is the living one'"
The king: "Bring me a sword"
They bring a sword before the king
The king: "Divide the living child in two"
"Give half to the one and half to the other"
The woman whose son is alive says to the king
(Because her heart yearns for her son)
"Oh, my lord, give her the living child"
"By no means put him to death"
The other: "He shall be neither mine nor yours; divide him"
The king answers
"Give the living child to the first woman"
"Do not put him to death; she is his mother"
All Israel hears of the judgment that the king has rendered
They stand in awe of the king
Because they perceive that the wisdom of God is in him to do justice
King Solomon is king over all Israel
These are his high officials
Azariah the son of Zadok is the priest
Elihoreph and Ahijah the sons of Shisha are secretaries
Jehoshaphat the son of Ahilud is recorder
Benaiah the son of Jehoiada is in command of the army
Zadok and Abiathar are priests
Azariah the son of Nathan is over the officers
Zabud the son of Nathan is priest and king's friend
Ahishar is in charge of the palace
Adoniram the son of Abda is in charge of the forced labor
Solomon has twelve officers over all Israel
Who provide food for the king and his household
Each man has to make provision for one month in the year
(The twelve officers and their districts are listed)
Judah and Israel are as many as the sand by the sea
They eat and drink and are happy
Solomon rules over all the kingdoms
From the Euphrates to the land of the Philistines and to the border of Egypt
They bring tribute and serve Solomon all the days of his life
Solomon's provision for one day is
Thirty cors of fine flour
Sixty cors of meal
Ten fat oxen, and twenty pasture-fed cattle
A hundred sheep, besides deer, gazelles, roebucks, and fattened fowl
He has dominion over all the region west of the Euphrates
From Tiphsah to Gaza, over all the kings west of the Euphrates
He has peace on all sides around him
Judah and Israel dwell in safety
From Dan even to Beersheba
Every man under his vine and under his fig tree
All the days of Solomon
Solomon also has 40,000 stalls of horses for his chariots
And 12,000 horsemen
Those officers supply provisions for King Solomon
And for all who come to King Solomon's table
Each one in his month
They let nothing be lacking
Barley also and straw for the horses and swift steeds
They bring to the place where it is required
Each according to his duty
God gives Solomon wisdom and understanding beyond measure
And breadth of mind like the sand on the seashore
Solomon's wisdom surpasses the wisdom of all the people of the east
And all the wisdom of Egypt
He is wiser than all other men
Wiser than Ethan the Ezrahite
And Heman, Calcol, and Darda, the sons of Mahol
His fame is in all the surrounding nations
He also speaks 3,000 proverbs
His songs are 1,005
He speaks of trees, from the cedar in Lebanon to the hyssop that grows out of the wall
He speaks also of beasts, and of birds, and of reptiles, and of fish
People of all nations come to hear the wisdom of Solomon
From all the kings of the earth, who have heard of his wisdom
Hiram king of Tyre sends his servants to Solomon
When he hears that they have anointed him king in place of his father
For Hiram always loved David
Solomon sends word to Hiram
"You know that David my father could not build a house for the name of the Lord"
"Because of the warfare with which his enemies surrounded him"
"Until the Lord put them under the soles of his feet"
"But now the Lord my God has given me rest on every side"
"There is neither adversary nor misfortune"
"And so I intend to build a house for the name of the Lord my God"
"As the Lord said to David my father"
"'Your son, whom I will set on your throne in your place'"
"'Shall build the house for my name'"
"Now therefore command that cedars of Lebanon be cut for me"
"My servants will join your servants"
"I will pay you for your servants such wages as you set"
"For you know that there is no one among us who knows how to cut timber like the Sidonians"
When Hiram hears the words of Solomon, he rejoices greatly
"Blessed be the Lord this day"
"Who has given to David a wise son to be over this great people"
Hiram sends to Solomon
"I have heard the message that you have sent to me"
"I am ready to do all you desire in the matter of cedar and cypress timber"
"My servants shall bring it down to the sea from Lebanon"
"I will make it into rafts to go by sea to the place you direct"
"I will have them broken up there, and you shall receive it"
"And you shall meet my wishes by providing food for my household"
Hiram supplies Solomon with all the timber of cedar and cypress that he desires
Solomon gives Hiram 20,000 cors of wheat as food for his household
And 20,000 cors of beaten oil
Solomon gives this to Hiram year by year
The Lord gives Solomon wisdom, as he promised him
There is peace between Hiram and Solomon
The two of them make a treaty
King Solomon drafts forced labor out of all Israel
The draft numbers 30,000 men
He sends them to Lebanon, 10,000 a month in shifts
They are a month in Lebanon and two months at home
Adoniram is in charge of the draft
Solomon also has 70,000 burden-bearers
And 80,000 stonecutters in the hill country
Besides Solomon's 3,300 chief officers who are over the work
Who have charge of the people who carry on the work
At the king's command they quarry out great, costly stones
In order to lay the foundation of the house with dressed stones
Solomon's builders and Hiram's builders and the men of Gebal cut them
They prepare the timber and the stone to build the house
In the four hundred and eightieth year after the people of Israel came out of Egypt
In the fourth year of Solomon's reign over Israel
In the month of Ziv, which is the second month
He begins to build the house of the Lord
The house that King Solomon builds for the Lord is sixty cubits long
Twenty cubits wide, and thirty cubits high
The vestibule in front of the nave of the house is twenty cubits long
Equal to the width of the house
And ten cubits deep in front of the house
For the house he makes windows with recessed frames
He also builds a structure against the wall of the house
Running around the walls of the house, both the nave and the inner sanctuary
He makes side chambers all around
The lowest story is five cubits broad
The middle one is six cubits broad
The third is seven cubits broad
For around the outside of the house he makes offsets on the wall
In order that the supporting beams should not be inserted into the walls
When the house is built, it is with stone prepared at the quarry
So that neither hammer nor axe nor any tool of iron is heard in the house while it is being built
The entrance for the lowest story is on the south side of the house
One goes up by stairs to the middle story
And from the middle story to the third
He builds the house and finishes it
He makes the ceiling of the house of beams and planks of cedar
He builds the structure against the whole house, five cubits high
It is joined to the house with timbers of cedar
Now the word of the Lord comes to Solomon
"Concerning this house that you are building"
"If you will walk in my statutes"
"And obey my rules and keep all my commandments and walk in them"
"Then I will establish my word with you"
"Which I spoke to David your father"
"I will dwell among the children of Israel"
"I will not forsake my people Israel"
Solomon builds the house and finishes it
He lines the walls of the house on the inside with boards of cedar
From the floor of the house to the walls of the ceiling
He covers them on the inside with wood
He covers the floor of the house with boards of cypress
He builds twenty cubits of the rear of the house with boards of cedar
From the floor to the walls
He builds this within as an inner sanctuary, as the Most Holy Place
The house, that is, the nave in front of the inner sanctuary, is forty cubits long
The cedar within the house is carved in the form of gourds and open flowers
All is cedar; no stone is seen
The inner sanctuary he prepares in the innermost part of the house
To set there the ark of the covenant of the Lord
The inner sanctuary is twenty cubits long, twenty cubits wide, and twenty cubits high
He overlays it with pure gold
He also overlays an altar of cedar
Solomon overlays the inside of the house with pure gold
He draws chains of gold across, in front of the inner sanctuary
He overlays it with gold
The whole house he overlays with gold
Until all the house is finished
Also the whole altar that belongs to the inner sanctuary he overlays with gold
In the inner sanctuary he makes two cherubim of olivewood
Each ten cubits high
Five cubits is the length of one wing of the cherub
And five cubits the length of the other wing
Ten cubits from the tip of one wing to the tip of the other
The other cherub also measures ten cubits
Both cherubim have the same measure and the same form
The height of one cherub is ten cubits
And so is that of the other cherub
He puts the cherubim in the innermost part of the house
The wings of the cherubim are spread out
So that a wing of one touches the one wall
And a wing of the other cherub touches the other wall
Their other wings touch each other in the middle of the house
He overlays the cherubim with gold
Around all the walls of the house he carves engraved figures of cherubim
And palm trees and open flowers, in the inner and outer rooms
The floor of the house he overlays with gold in the inner and outer rooms
