For the entrance to the inner sanctuary he makes doors of olivewood
The lintel and the doorposts form a pentagon
He covers the two doors of olivewood with carvings of cherubim, palm trees, and open flowers
He overlays them with gold
He spreads gold on the cherubim and on the palm trees
So also he makes for the entrance to the nave doorposts of olivewood
In the form of a square
And two doors of cypress wood
The two leaves of the one door are folding
The two leaves of the other door are folding
On them he carves cherubim and palm trees and open flowers
He overlays them with gold evenly applied on the carved work
He builds the inner court with three courses of cut stone
And one course of cedar beams
In the fourth year the foundation of the house of the Lord is laid
In the month of Ziv
In the eleventh year, in the month of Bul, which is the eighth month
The house is finished in all its parts, and according to all its specifications
He is seven years in building it
Solomon builds his own house in thirteen years
And he finishes his entire house
He builds the House of the Forest of Lebanon
Its length is a hundred cubits and its breadth fifty cubits and its height thirty cubits
It is built on four rows of cedar pillars, with cedar beams on the pillars
It is roofed with cedar above the chambers that are on the forty-five pillars
Fifteen in each row
There are window frames in three rows
Window opposite window in three tiers
All the doorways and windows have square frames
Window is opposite window in three tiers
He makes the Hall of Pillars
Its length is fifty cubits, and its breadth thirty cubits
There is a porch in front with pillars, and a canopy in front of them
He makes the Hall of the Throne where he is to pronounce judgment
The Hall of Judgment
It is finished with cedar from floor to rafters
His own house where he is to dwell, in the other court back of the hall
Is of like workmanship
Solomon also makes a house like this hall for Pharaoh's daughter
Whom he has taken in marriage
All these are made of costly stones
Cut according to measure, sawed with saws, back and front
Even from the foundation to the coping
And from the outside to the great court
The foundation is of costly stones, huge stones
Stones of eight and ten cubits
Above are costly stones, cut according to measurement, and cedar
The great court has three courses of cut stone all around
And a course of cedar beams
So has the inner court of the house of the Lord
And the vestibule of the house
King Solomon sends and brings Hiram from Tyre
He is the son of a widow of the tribe of Naphtali
His father is a man of Tyre, a worker in bronze
He is full of wisdom, understanding, and skill for making any work in bronze
He comes to King Solomon and does all his work
He casts two pillars of bronze
Eighteen cubits is the height of one pillar
A line of twelve cubits measures its circumference
It is hollow, and its thickness is four fingers
The second pillar is the same
He also makes two capitals of cast bronze to set on the tops of the pillars
The height of the one capital is five cubits
The height of the other capital is five cubits
There are lattices of checker work with wreaths of chain work for the capitals
On the tops of the pillars, a lattice for the one capital and a lattice for the other
He makes pomegranates in two rows around the one latticework
To cover the capital that is on the top of the pillar
He does the same with the other capital
Now the capitals that are on the tops of the pillars in the vestibule are of lily-work
Four cubits
The capitals are on the two pillars
And also above the rounded projection which is beside the latticework
There are two hundred pomegranates, in two rows all around
And so with the other capital
He sets up the pillars at the vestibule of the temple
He sets up the pillar on the south and calls its name Jachin
He sets up the pillar on the north and calls its name Boaz
On the tops of the pillars is lily-work
Thus the work of the pillars is finished
He makes the sea of cast metal
It is round, ten cubits from brim to brim
And five cubits high
A line of thirty cubits measures its circumference
Under its brim are gourds, for ten cubits
Compassing the sea all around
The gourds are in two rows, cast with it when it is cast
It stands on twelve oxen
Three facing north, three facing west, three facing south, three facing east
The sea is set on them
All their rear parts are inward
Its thickness is a handbreadth
Its brim is made like the brim of a cup
Like the flower of a lily
It holds two thousand baths
He also makes the ten stands of bronze
Each stand is four cubits long, four cubits wide, and three cubits high
This is the construction of the stands
They have panels, and the panels are set in the frames
On the panels that are set in the frames are lions, oxen, and cherubim
On the frames, both above and below the lions and oxen
There are wreaths of beveled work
Moreover, each stand has four bronze wheels and axles of bronze
At the four corners are supports for a basin
The supports are cast with wreaths at the side of each
Its opening is within a crown that projects upward one cubit
Its opening is round, as a pedestal is made, a cubit and a half deep
At its opening there are carvings
And its panels are square, not round
The four wheels are underneath the panels
The axles of the wheels are of one piece with the stands
The height of a wheel is a cubit and a half
The wheels are made like a chariot wheel
Their axles, their rims, their spokes, and their hubs are all cast
There are four supports at the four corners of each stand
The supports are of one piece with the stands
On the top of the stand there is a round band half a cubit high
On the top of the stand its stays and its panels are of one piece with it
On the surfaces of its stays and on its panels, he carves cherubim, lions, and palm trees
According to the space of each, with wreaths all around
After this manner he makes the ten stands
All of them are cast alike, of the same measure and the same form
He makes ten basins of bronze
Each basin holds forty baths
Each basin measures four cubits
There is a basin for each of the ten stands
He sets the stands, five on the south side of the house
And five on the north side of the house
He sets the sea on the southeast corner of the house
Hiram also makes the pots, the shovels, and the basins
Hiram finishes all the work that he does for King Solomon on the house of the Lord
The two pillars
The two bowls of the capitals that are on the tops of the pillars
The two latticeworks to cover the two bowls of the capitals on the tops of the pillars
The four hundred pomegranates for the two latticeworks
Two rows of pomegranates for each latticework
To cover the two bowls of the capitals on the pillars
The ten stands, and the ten basins on the stands
The one sea, and the twelve oxen underneath the sea
Now the pots, the shovels, and the basins, all these vessels
That Hiram makes for King Solomon for the house of the Lord
Are of burnished bronze
In the plain of the Jordan the king casts them
In the clay ground between Succoth and Zarethan
Solomon leaves all the vessels unweighed
Because there are so many of them
The weight of the bronze is not ascertained
Solomon makes all the vessels that are in the house of the Lord
The golden altar
The golden table for the bread of the Presence
The lampstands of pure gold, five on the south side and five on the north
Before the inner sanctuary
The flowers, the lamps, and the tongs, of gold
The cups, snuffers, basins, dishes for incense, and fire pans, of pure gold
The sockets of gold, for the doors of the innermost part of the house, the Most Holy Place
And for the doors of the nave of the temple
Thus all the work that King Solomon does on the house of the Lord is finished
Solomon brings in the things that David his father has dedicated
The silver, the gold, and the vessels
He stores them in the treasuries of the house of the Lord
Solomon assembles the elders of Israel
And all the heads of the tribes, the leaders of the fathers' houses of the people of Israel
Before King Solomon in Jerusalem
To bring up the ark of the covenant of the Lord out of the city of David, which is Zion
All the men of Israel assemble to King Solomon at the feast in the month Ethanim
Which is the seventh month
All the elders of Israel come
The priests take up the ark
They bring up the ark of the Lord
The tent of meeting, and all the holy vessels that are in the tent
The priests and the Levites bring them up
King Solomon and all the congregation of Israel, who have assembled before him
Are with him before the ark
Sacrificing so many sheep and oxen that they cannot be counted or numbered
The priests bring the ark of the covenant of the Lord to its place
In the inner sanctuary of the house, in the Most Holy Place
Underneath the wings of the cherubim
For the cherubim spread out their wings over the place of the ark
The cherubim overshadow the ark and its poles
The poles are so long that the ends of the poles are seen from the Holy Place
Before the inner sanctuary
But they cannot be seen from outside
They are there to this day
There is nothing in the ark except the two tablets of stone
That Moses put there at Horeb
Where the Lord makes a covenant with the people of Israel
When they come out of the land of Egypt
When the priests come out of the Holy Place
A cloud fills the house of the Lord
The priests are not able to stand to minister because of the cloud
For the glory of the Lord fills the house of the Lord
Solomon says, "The Lord has said that he would dwell in thick darkness"
"I have indeed built you an exalted house"
"A place for you to dwell in forever"
The king turns around and blesses all the assembly of Israel
While all the assembly of Israel stands
"Blessed be the Lord, the God of Israel"
"Who with his hand has fulfilled what he promised with his mouth"
"To David my father, saying"
"'Since the day that I brought my people Israel out of Egypt'"
"'I chose no city out of all the tribes of Israel in which to build a house'"
"'That my name might be there'"
"'But I chose David to be over my people Israel'"
"Now it was in the heart of David my father to build a house"
"For the name of the Lord, the God of Israel"
"But the Lord said to David my father"
"'Whereas it was in your heart to build a house for my name'"
"'You did well that it was in your heart'"
"'Nevertheless, you shall not build the house'"
"'But your son who shall be born to you shall build the house for my name'"
"Now the Lord has fulfilled his promise that he made"
"For I have risen in the place of David my father"
"I sit on the throne of Israel, as the Lord promised"
"I have built the house for the name of the Lord, the God of Israel"
"There I have provided a place for the ark"
"In which is the covenant of the Lord"
"That he made with our fathers, when he brought them out of the land of Egypt"
Solomon stands before the altar of the Lord
In the presence of all the assembly of Israel
He spreads out his hands toward heaven
"O Lord, God of Israel, there is no God like you"
"In heaven above or on earth beneath"
"Keeping covenant and showing steadfast love to your servants"
"Who walk before you with all their heart"
(Solomon's prayer continues at length)
"But will God indeed dwell on the earth?"
"Behold, heaven and the highest heaven cannot contain you"
"How much less this house that I have built"
"Hear in heaven your dwelling place"
"When you hear, forgive"
(Solomon lists various situations where Israel will need God's forgiveness)
"If there is famine in the land, if there is pestilence"
"Or blight or mildew or locust or caterpillar"
"If their enemy besieges them in the land at their gates"
"Whatever plague, whatever sickness there is"
"Whatever prayer, whatever plea is made by any man"
"Or by all your people Israel"
"Each knowing the affliction of his own heart"
"And stretching out his hands toward this house"
"Then hear in heaven your dwelling place and forgive"
"Likewise, when a foreigner, who is not of your people Israel"
"Comes from a far country for your name's sake"
"When he comes and prays toward this house"
"Hear in heaven your dwelling place and do according to all"
"For which the foreigner calls to you"
"If your people go out to battle against their enemy"
"By whatever way you shall send them"
"And they pray to the Lord toward the city that you have chosen"
"And the house that I have built for your name"
"Then hear in heaven their prayer and their plea"
"And maintain their cause"
"If they sin against you—for there is no one who does not sin—"
"And you are angry with them and give them to an enemy"
"So that they are carried away captive to the land of the enemy"
"Far off or near"
"Yet if they turn their heart in the land to which they have been carried captive"
"And repent and plead with you in the land of their captors, saying"
"'We have sinned and have acted perversely and wickedly'"
"If they repent with all their heart and with all their soul"
"In the land of their enemies, who carried them captive"
"And pray to you toward their land, which you gave to their fathers"
"The city that you have chosen, and the house that I have built for your name"
"Then hear in heaven your dwelling place their prayer and their plea"
"And maintain their cause"
"And forgive your people who have sinned against you"
"For they are your people, and your heritage"
"Which you brought out of Egypt"
"From the midst of the iron furnace"
Solomon finishes offering all this prayer and plea to the Lord
He arises from before the altar of the Lord
Where he has knelt with hands outstretched toward heaven
He stands and blesses all the assembly of Israel with a loud voice
"Blessed be the Lord who has given rest to his people Israel"
"According to all that he promised"
"Not one word has failed of all his good promise"
"Which he spoke by Moses his servant"
"The Lord our God be with us, as he was with our fathers"
"May he not leave us or forsake us"
"That he may incline our hearts to him"
"To walk in all his ways and to keep his commandments"
"His statutes, and his rules, which he commanded our fathers"
"Let these words of mine, with which I have pleaded before the Lord"
"Be near to the Lord our God day and night"
"That he may maintain the cause of his servant and the cause of his people Israel"
"As each day requires"
"That all the peoples of the earth may know that the Lord is God"
"There is no other"
"Let your heart therefore be wholly true to the Lord our God"
"Walking in his statutes and keeping his commandments, as at this day"
The king, and all Israel with him, offer sacrifice before the Lord
Solomon offers as peace offerings to the Lord 22,000 oxen
And 120,000 sheep
So the king and all the people of Israel dedicate the house of the Lord
The same day the king consecrates the middle of the court
That is before the house of the Lord
For there he offers the burnt offering and the grain offering
And the fat pieces of the peace offerings
Because the bronze altar that is before the Lord is too small
To receive the burnt offering and the grain offering and the fat pieces
Solomon holds the feast at that time
And all Israel with him, a great assembly
From Lebo-hamath to the Brook of Egypt
Before the Lord our God, seven days
On the eighth day he sends the people away
They bless the king and go to their homes
Joyful and glad of heart for all the goodness that the Lord has shown to David
And to Israel his people
As soon as Solomon has finished building the house of the Lord
And the king's house and all that Solomon desires to build
The Lord appears to Solomon a second time
As he has appeared to him at Gibeon
The Lord says to him
"I have heard your prayer and your plea"
"Which you have made before me"
"I have consecrated this house that you have built"
"By putting my name there forever"
"My eyes and my heart will be there for all time"
"And as for you, if you will walk before me"
"As David your father walked"
"With integrity of heart and uprightness"
"Doing according to all that I have commanded you"
"And keeping my statutes and my rules"
"Then I will establish your royal throne over Israel forever"
"As I promised David your father, saying"
"'You shall not lack a man on the throne of Israel'"
"But if you turn aside from following me"
"You or your children"
"And do not keep my commandments and my statutes that I have set before you"
"But go and serve other gods and worship them"
"Then I will cut off Israel from the land that I have given them"
"And the house that I have consecrated for my name"
"I will cast out of my sight"
"And Israel will become a proverb and a byword among all peoples"
"And this house will become a heap of ruins"
"Everyone passing by it will be astonished and will hiss"
"And they will say, 'Why has the Lord done thus to this land and to this house?'"
"Then they will say, 'Because they abandoned the Lord their God'"
"'Who brought their fathers out of the land of Egypt'"
"'And laid hold on other gods and worshiped them and served them'"
"'Therefore the Lord has brought all this disaster on them'"
At the end of twenty years
In which Solomon has built the two houses, the house of the Lord and the king's house
Hiram king of Tyre has supplied Solomon with cedar and cypress timber
And gold, as much as he desires
King Solomon gives to Hiram twenty cities in the land of Galilee
Hiram comes from Tyre to see the cities that Solomon has given him
They do not please him
"What kind of cities are these that you have given me, my brother?"
They are called the land of Cabul to this day
Hiram has sent to the king 120 talents of gold
This is the account of the forced labor
That King Solomon drafts to build the house of the Lord
And his own house and the Millo and the wall of Jerusalem
And Hazor and Megiddo and Gezer
(Pharaoh king of Egypt has gone up and captured Gezer
He burns it with fire
He kills the Canaanites who dwell in the city
He gives it as dowry to his daughter, Solomon's wife)
Solomon rebuilds Gezer
And Lower Beth-horon
And Baalath and Tamar in the wilderness, in the land of Judah
And all the store cities that Solomon has
And the cities for his chariots
And the cities for his horsemen
And whatever Solomon desires to build
In Jerusalem, in Lebanon, and in all the land of his dominion
All the people who are left of the Amorites, the Hittites, the Perizzites
The Hivites, and the Jebusites, who are not of the people of Israel
Their descendants who are left after them in the land
Whom the people of Israel are unable to devote to destruction
These Solomon drafts to be slaves
And so they are to this day
But of the people of Israel Solomon makes no slaves
They are the soldiers
They are his officials, his commanders, his captains
His chariot commanders and his horsemen
These are the chief officers who are over Solomon's work
550 who have charge of the people who carry on the work
Pharaoh's daughter goes up from the city of David
To her own house that Solomon has built for her
Then he builds the Millo
Three times a year Solomon offers burnt offerings and peace offerings
On the altar that he builds to the Lord
Making offerings with it before the Lord
So he finishes the house
King Solomon builds a fleet of ships at Ezion-geber
Which is near Eloth on the shore of the Red Sea, in the land of Edom
Hiram sends with the fleet his servants, seamen who are familiar with the sea
Together with the servants of Solomon
They go to Ophir
They bring from there gold, 420 talents
They bring it to King Solomon
Now when the queen of Sheba hears of the fame of Solomon
Concerning the name of the Lord
She comes to test him with hard questions
She comes to Jerusalem with a very great retinue
With camels bearing spices and very much gold and precious stones
When she comes to Solomon
She tells him all that is on her mind
Solomon answers all her questions
There is nothing hidden from the king that he cannot explain to her
When the queen of Sheba has seen all the wisdom of Solomon
The house that he has built
The food of his table, the seating of his officials
The attendance of his servants, their clothing
His cupbearers, and his burnt offerings that he offers at the house of the Lord
There is no more breath in her
She says to the king
"The report was true that I heard in my own land"
"Of your words and of your wisdom"
"But I did not believe the reports until I came"
"And my own eyes had seen it"
"And behold, the half was not told me"
"Your wisdom and prosperity surpass the report that I heard"
"Happy are your men! Happy are your servants"
"Who continually stand before you and hear your wisdom"
"Blessed be the Lord your God, who has delighted in you"
"And set you on the throne of Israel"
"Because the Lord loved Israel forever"
"He has made you king, that you may execute justice and righteousness"
She gives the king 120 talents of gold
A very great quantity of spices and precious stones
Never again comes such an abundance of spices
As these that the queen of Sheba gives to King Solomon
Moreover, the fleet of Hiram, which brings gold from Ophir
Brings from Ophir a very great amount of almug wood and precious stones
The king makes of the almug wood supports for the house of the Lord
And for the king's house, also lyres and harps for the singers
No such almug wood has come or been seen to this day
King Solomon gives to the queen of Sheba all that she desires
Whatever she asks besides what is given her by the bounty of King Solomon
She turns and goes back to her own land with her servants
Now the weight of gold that comes to Solomon in one year
Is 666 talents of gold
Besides that which comes from the explorers
And from the business of the merchants
And from all the kings of the west and from the governors of the land
King Solomon makes 200 large shields of beaten gold
600 shekels of gold go into each shield
He makes 300 shields of beaten gold
Three minas of gold go into each shield
The king puts them in the House of the Forest of Lebanon
The king also makes a great ivory throne
He overlays it with the finest gold
The throne has six steps
The throne has a round top
On each side of the seat are armrests
Two lions standing beside the armrests
Twelve lions stand there, one on each end of a step on the six steps
Nothing like it has ever been made in any kingdom
All King Solomon's drinking vessels are of gold
All the vessels of the House of the Forest of Lebanon are of pure gold
None is of silver; silver is not considered as anything in the days of Solomon
For the king has a fleet of ships of Tarshish at sea with the fleet of Hiram
Once every three years the fleet of ships of Tarshish comes
Bringing gold, silver, ivory, apes, and peacocks
Thus King Solomon excels all the kings of the earth
In riches and in wisdom
The whole earth seeks the presence of Solomon
To hear his wisdom, which God has put into his mind
Every one of them brings his present
Articles of silver and gold, garments, myrrh, spices, horses, and mules
So much year by year
Solomon gathers together chariots and horsemen
He has 1,400 chariots and 12,000 horsemen
Whom he stations in the chariot cities and with the king in Jerusalem
The king makes silver as common in Jerusalem as stone
He makes cedar as plentiful as the sycamore of the Shephelah
Solomon's import of horses is from Egypt and Kue
The king's traders receive them from Kue at a price
A chariot is imported from Egypt for 600 shekels of silver
A horse for 150
Likewise through them these are exported to all the kings of the Hittites
And the kings of Syria
Now King Solomon loves many foreign women
Along with the daughter of Pharaoh
Moabite, Ammonite, Edomite, Sidonian, and Hittite women
From the nations concerning which the Lord has said to the people of Israel
"You shall not enter into marriage with them"
"Neither shall they with you"
"For surely they will turn away your heart after their gods"
Solomon clings to these in love
He has 700 wives, who are princesses
And 300 concubines
His wives turn away his heart
When Solomon is old his wives turn away his heart after other gods
His heart is not wholly true to the Lord his God
As was the heart of David his father
Solomon goes after Ashtoreth the goddess of the Sidonians
And after Milcom the abomination of the Ammonites
Solomon does what is evil in the sight of the Lord
He does not wholly follow the Lord, as David his father has done
Then Solomon builds a high place for Chemosh the abomination of Moab
And for Molech the abomination of the Ammonites
On the mountain east of Jerusalem
He does the same for all his foreign wives
Who make offerings and sacrifice to their gods
The Lord is angry with Solomon
Because his heart has turned away from the Lord, the God of Israel
Who has appeared to him twice
And has commanded him concerning this thing
That he should not go after other gods
He has not kept what the Lord commanded
Therefore the Lord says to Solomon
"Since this has been your practice"
"And you have not kept my covenant and my statutes that I have commanded you"
"I will surely tear the kingdom from you"
"And will give it to your servant"
"Yet for the sake of David your father I will not do it in your days"
"But I will tear it out of the hand of your son"
"However, I will not tear away all the kingdom"
"But I will give one tribe to your son"
"For the sake of David my servant and for the sake of Jerusalem that I have chosen"
The Lord raises up an adversary against Solomon
Hadad the Edomite
He is of the royal house in Edom
(When David is in Edom, and Joab the commander of the army goes up
To bury the slain
He strikes down every male in Edom
For Joab and all Israel remain there six months
Until he has cut off every male in Edom
But Hadad flees to Egypt
Together with certain Edomites of his father's servants, Hadad still being a little child
They set out from Midian and come to Paran
They take men with them from Paran and come to Egypt
To Pharaoh king of Egypt
Who gives him a house and assigns him an allowance of food
And gives him land
Hadad finds great favor in the sight of Pharaoh
So that he gives him in marriage the sister of his own wife
The sister of Tahpenes the queen
The sister of Tahpenes bears him Genubath his son
Tahpenes weans him in Pharaoh's house
Genubath is in Pharaoh's house among the sons of Pharaoh
When Hadad hears in Egypt that David sleeps with his fathers
And that Joab the commander of the army is dead
Hadad says to Pharaoh, "Let me depart, that I may go to my own country"
Pharaoh: "What have you lacked with me that you are now seeking to go?"
"Nothing; only let me depart")
God also raises up as an adversary to him Rezon the son of Eliada
Who has fled from his master Hadadezer king of Zobah
He gathers men about him and becomes leader of a marauding band
After the killing by David
They go to Damascus and dwell there
They make him king in Damascus
He is an adversary of Israel all the days of Solomon
Doing harm as Hadad does
He loathes Israel and reigns over Syria
Jeroboam the son of Nebat, an Ephraimite of Zeredah
A servant of Solomon, whose mother's name is Zeruah, a widow
Also lifts up his hand against the king
This is the reason why he lifts up his hand against the king
Solomon builds the Millo
He closes up the breach of the city of David his father
The man Jeroboam is very able
Solomon sees that the young man is industrious
He gives him charge over all the forced labor of the house of Joseph
At that time, when Jeroboam goes out of Jerusalem
The prophet Ahijah the Shilonite finds him on the road
Ahijah has dressed himself in a new garment
The two of them are alone in the open country
Ahijah lays hold of the new garment that is on him
He tears it into twelve pieces
He says to Jeroboam
"Take for yourself ten pieces"
"For thus says the Lord, the God of Israel"
"'Behold, I am about to tear the kingdom from the hand of Solomon'"
"'I will give you ten tribes'"
"'But he shall have one tribe'"
"'For the sake of my servant David'"
"'And for the sake of Jerusalem, the city that I have chosen'"
"'Out of all the tribes of Israel'"
"'Because they have forsaken me'"
"'And worshiped Ashtoreth the goddess of the Sidonians'"
"'Chemosh the god of Moab, and Milcom the god of the Ammonites'"
"'And they have not walked in my ways'"
"'Doing what is right in my sight and keeping my statutes and my rules'"
"'As David his father did'"
"'Nevertheless, I will not take the whole kingdom out of his hand'"
"'But I will make him ruler all the days of his life'"
"'For the sake of David my servant whom I chose'"
"'Who kept my commandments and my statutes'"
"'But I will take the kingdom out of his son's hand'"
"'And I will give it to you, ten tribes'"
"'Yet to his son I will give one tribe'"
"'That David my servant may always have a lamp before me in Jerusalem'"
"'The city where I have chosen to put my name'"
"'And I will take you, and you shall reign over all that your soul desires'"
"'You shall be king over Israel'"
"'And if you will listen to all that I command you'"
"'And will walk in my ways, and do what is right in my eyes'"
"'By keeping my statutes and my commandments, as David my servant did'"
"'I will be with you and will build you a sure house'"
"'As I built for David, and I will give Israel to you'"
"'And I will afflict the offspring of David because of this'"
"'But not forever'"
Solomon seeks therefore to kill Jeroboam
Jeroboam arises and flees into Egypt
To Shishak king of Egypt
He is in Egypt until the death of Solomon
Now the rest of the acts of Solomon
And all that he did, and his wisdom
Are they not written in the Book of the Acts of Solomon?
The time that Solomon reigns in Jerusalem over all Israel is forty years
Solomon sleeps with his fathers
He is buried in the city of David his father
Rehoboam his son reigns in his place
Rehoboam goes to Shechem
For all Israel has come to Shechem to make him king
When Jeroboam the son of Nebat hears of it
(For he is still in Egypt, where he has fled from King Solomon)
Jeroboam returns from Egypt
They send and call him
Jeroboam and all the assembly of Israel come
They say to Rehoboam
"Your father made our yoke heavy"
"Now therefore lighten the hard service of your father"
"And his heavy yoke on us, and we will serve you"
He says to them, "Go away for three days, then come again to me"
The people go away
King Rehoboam takes counsel with the old men
Who have stood before Solomon his father while he yet lived
"How do you advise me to answer this people?"
They say to him
"If you will be a servant to this people today and serve them"
"And speak good words to them when you answer them"
"Then they will be your servants forever"
He abandons the counsel that the old men give him
He takes counsel with the young men who have grown up with him
Who stand before him
"What do you advise that we answer this people"
"Who have said to me, 'Lighten the yoke that your father put on us'?"
The young men who have grown up with him say to him
"Thus shall you speak to this people who said to you"
"'Your father made our yoke heavy, but you lighten it for us'"
"Thus shall you say to them"
"'My little finger is thicker than my father's thighs'"
"'And now, whereas my father laid on you a heavy yoke'"
"'I will add to your yoke'"
"'My father disciplined you with whips'"
"'But I will discipline you with scorpions'"
Jeroboam and all the people come to Rehoboam the third day
As the king says, "Come to me again the third day"
The king answers the people harshly
He abandons the counsel that the old men have given him
He speaks to them according to the counsel of the young men
"My father made your yoke heavy, but I will add to your yoke"
"My father disciplined you with whips, but I will discipline you with scorpions"
The king does not listen to the people
For it is a turn of affairs brought about by the Lord
That he might fulfill his word
Which the Lord spoke by Ahijah the Shilonite to Jeroboam the son of Nebat
When all Israel sees that the king does not listen to them
The people answer the king
"What portion do we have in David?"
"We have no inheritance in the son of Jesse"
"To your tents, O Israel"
"Look now to your own house, David"
Israel goes to their tents
Rehoboam reigns over the people of Israel who dwell in the cities of Judah
King Rehoboam sends Adoram, who is taskmaster over the forced labor
All Israel stones him to death with stones
King Rehoboam makes haste to mount his chariot to flee to Jerusalem
Israel has been in rebellion against the house of David to this day
When all Israel hears that Jeroboam has returned
They send and call him to the assembly
They make him king over all Israel
There is none that follows the house of David but the tribe of Judah only
When Rehoboam comes to Jerusalem
He assembles all the house of Judah and the tribe of Benjamin
180,000 chosen warriors, to fight against the house of Israel
To restore the kingdom to Rehoboam the son of Solomon
The word of God comes to Shemaiah the man of God
"Say to Rehoboam the son of Solomon, king of Judah"
"And to all the house of Judah and Benjamin, and to the rest of the people"
"'Thus says the Lord, You shall not go up or fight against your relatives'"
"'The people of Israel. Every man return to his home'"
"'For this thing is from me'"
They listen to the word of the Lord
They go home again, according to the word of the Lord
Jeroboam builds Shechem in the hill country of Ephraim
He dwells there
He goes out from there and builds Penuel
Jeroboam says in his heart
"Now the kingdom will turn back to the house of David"
"If this people go up to offer sacrifices in the temple of the Lord at Jerusalem"
"Then the heart of this people will turn again to their lord"
"To Rehoboam king of Judah"
"They will kill me and return to Rehoboam king of Judah"
The king takes counsel
He makes two calves of gold
He says to the people, "You have gone up to Jerusalem long enough"
"Behold your gods, O Israel, who brought you up out of the land of Egypt"
He sets one in Bethel
The other he puts in Dan
This thing becomes a sin
The people go as far as Dan to be before one
He also makes temples on high places
He appoints priests from among all the people
Who are not of the Levites
Jeroboam appoints a feast on the fifteenth day of the eighth month
Like the feast that is in Judah
He offers sacrifices on the altar
So he does in Bethel, sacrificing to the calves that he makes
He places in Bethel the priests of the high places that he has made
He goes up to the altar that he has made in Bethel
On the fifteenth day in the eighth month
In the month that he has devised from his own heart
He institutes a feast for the people of Israel
He goes up to the altar to make offerings
Behold, a man of God comes out of Judah by the word of the Lord to Bethel
Jeroboam is standing by the altar to make offerings
The man cries against the altar by the word of the Lord
"O altar, altar, thus says the Lord"
"'Behold, a son shall be born to the house of David, Josiah by name'"
"'He shall sacrifice on you the priests of the high places'"
"'Who make offerings on you'"
"'And human bones shall be burned on you'"
He gives a sign the same day
"This is the sign that the Lord has spoken"
"'Behold, the altar shall be torn down'"
"'And the ashes that are on it shall be poured out'"
When the king hears the saying of the man of God
Which he cries against the altar at Bethel
Jeroboam stretches out his hand from the altar
"Seize him"
His hand, which he stretches out against him, dries up
So that he cannot draw it back to himself
The altar also is torn down
The ashes are poured out from the altar
According to the sign that the man of God has given by the word of the Lord
The king says to the man of God
"Entreat now the favor of the Lord your God"
"And pray for me, that my hand may be restored to me"
The man of God entreats the Lord
The king's hand is restored to him
It becomes as it was before
The king says to the man of God
"Come home with me, and refresh yourself"
"I will give you a reward"
The man of God says to the king
"If you give me half your house, I will not go in with you"
"I will not eat bread or drink water in this place"
"For so was it commanded me by the word of the Lord, saying"
"'You shall neither eat bread nor drink water'"
"'Nor return by the way that you came'"
He goes another way
He does not return by the way that he came to Bethel
An old prophet dwells in Bethel
His sons come and tell him all that the man of God has done that day in Bethel
They tell their father the words that he has spoken to the king
Their father says to them, "Which way did he go?"
His sons show him the way that the man of God who came from Judah has gone
He says to his sons, "Saddle the donkey for me"
They saddle the donkey for him
He rides after him
He finds him sitting under an oak
"Are you the man of God who came from Judah?"
"I am"
"Come home with me and eat bread"
"I may not return with you, or go in with you"
"I will not eat bread or drink water with you in this place"
"For it was said to me by the word of the Lord"
"'You shall neither eat bread nor drink water there'"
"'Nor return by the way that you came'"
"I also am a prophet as you are"
"And an angel spoke to me by the word of the Lord, saying"
"'Bring him back with you into your house'"
"'That he may eat bread and drink water'"
He lies to him
The man of God goes back with him
He eats bread in his house and drinks water
As they sit at the table
The word of the Lord comes to the prophet who has brought him back
He cries to the man of God who came from Judah
"Thus says the Lord"
"'Because you have disobeyed the word of the Lord'"
"'And have not kept the command that the Lord your God commanded you'"
"'But have come back and have eaten bread and drunk water'"
"'In the place of which he said to you'"
"'"Eat no bread and drink no water"'"
"'Your body shall not come to the tomb of your fathers'"
After he has eaten bread and drunk
He saddles the donkey for the prophet whom he has brought back
He goes away
A lion meets him on the road
The lion kills him
His body is thrown in the road
The donkey stands beside it
The lion also stands beside the body
Behold, men pass by and see the body thrown in the road
And the lion standing by the body
They come and tell it in the city where the old prophet dwells
When the prophet who brought him back from the way hears of it
"It is the man of God who disobeyed the word of the Lord"
"Therefore the Lord has given him to the lion"
"Which has torn him and killed him"
"According to the word that the Lord spoke to him"
He says to his sons, "Saddle the donkey for me"
They saddle it
He goes and finds his body thrown in the road
The donkey and the lion standing beside the body
The lion has not eaten the body or torn the donkey
The prophet takes up the body of the man of God
He lays it on the donkey
He brings it back to the city to mourn and to bury him
He lays the body in his own grave
They mourn over him, saying, "Alas, my brother"
After he has buried him, he says to his sons
"When I die, bury me in the grave in which the man of God is buried"
"Lay my bones beside his bones"
"For the saying that he called out by the word of the Lord"
"Against the altar in Bethel and against all the houses of the high places"
"That are in the cities of Samaria, shall surely come to pass"
After this thing Jeroboam does not turn from his evil way
He again makes priests for the high places from among all the people
Any who will, he consecrates to be priests of the high places
This thing becomes sin to the house of Jeroboam
So as to cut it off and to destroy it from the face of the earth
At that time Abijah the son of Jeroboam falls sick
Jeroboam says to his wife
"Arise, and disguise yourself"
"That it not be known that you are the wife of Jeroboam"
"And go to Shiloh"
"Behold, Ahijah the prophet is there"
"Who said of me that I should be king over this people"
"Take with you ten loaves, some cakes, and a jar of honey"
"Go to him. He will tell you what shall happen to the child"
Jeroboam's wife does so
She arises and goes to Shiloh
She comes to the house of Ahijah
Ahijah cannot see, for his eyes are dim because of his age
The Lord says to Ahijah
"Behold, the wife of Jeroboam is coming to inquire of you concerning her son"
"For he is sick"
"Thus and thus shall you say to her"
When she comes, she pretends to be another woman
When Ahijah hears the sound of her feet, as she comes in at the door
"Come in, wife of Jeroboam. Why do you pretend to be another?"
"For I am charged with unbearable news for you"
"Go, tell Jeroboam, 'Thus says the Lord, the God of Israel'"
"'I exalted you from among the people'"
"'I made you leader over my people Israel'"
"'I tore the kingdom away from the house of David'"
"'I gave it to you'"
"'Yet you have not been like my servant David'"
"'Who kept my commandments'"
"'And followed me with all his heart'"
"'Doing only that which was right in my eyes'"
"'But you have done evil above all who were before you'"
"'You have gone and made for yourself other gods and metal images'"
"'Provoking me to anger, and have cast me behind your back'"
"'Therefore behold, I will bring harm upon the house of Jeroboam'"
"'I will cut off from Jeroboam every male'"
"'Both bond and free in Israel'"
"'I will burn up the house of Jeroboam'"
"'As a man burns up dung until it is all gone'"
"'Anyone belonging to Jeroboam who dies in the city'"
"'The dogs shall eat'"
"'And anyone who dies in the open country'"
"'The birds of the heavens shall eat'"
"'For the Lord has spoken it'"
"'Arise therefore, go to your house'"
"'When your feet enter the city, the child shall die'"
"'All Israel shall mourn for him and bury him'"
"'For he only of Jeroboam shall come to the grave'"
"'Because in him there is found something pleasing to the Lord'"
"'The God of Israel, in the house of Jeroboam'"
"'Moreover, the Lord will raise up for himself a king over Israel'"
"'Who shall cut off the house of Jeroboam today'"
"'And henceforth, the Lord will strike Israel'"
"'As a reed is shaken in the water'"
"'He will root up Israel out of this good land'"
"'That he gave to their fathers'"
"'He will scatter them beyond the Euphrates'"
"'Because they have made their Asherim'"
"'Provoking the Lord to anger'"
"'He will give Israel up because of the sins of Jeroboam'"
"'Which he sinned and made Israel to sin'"
Jeroboam's wife arises and departs
She comes to Tirzah
As she comes to the threshold of the house, the child dies
All Israel buries him and mourns for him
According to the word of the Lord
Which he spoke by his servant Ahijah the prophet
Now the rest of the acts of Jeroboam, how he warred and how he reigned
Behold, they are written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Israel
The time that Jeroboam reigns is twenty-two years
He sleeps with his fathers
Nadab his son reigns in his place
Rehoboam the son of Solomon reigns in Judah
Rehoboam is forty-one years old when he begins to reign
He reigns seventeen years in Jerusalem
The city that the Lord has chosen out of all the tribes of Israel
To put his name there
His mother's name is Naamah the Ammonite
Judah does what is evil in the sight of the Lord
They provoke him to jealousy with their sins that they commit
More than all that their fathers have done
For they also build for themselves high places and pillars and Asherim
On every high hill and under every green tree
There are also male cult prostitutes in the land
They do according to all the abominations of the nations
That the Lord drives out before the people of Israel
In the fifth year of King Rehoboam
Shishak king of Egypt comes up against Jerusalem
He takes away the treasures of the house of the Lord
And the treasures of the king's house
He takes away everything
He also takes away all the shields of gold that Solomon has made
King Rehoboam makes in their place shields of bronze
He commits them to the hands of the officers of the guard
Who keep the door of the king's house
As often as the king goes into the house of the Lord
The guard carries them and brings them back to the guardroom
Now the rest of the acts of Rehoboam and all that he did
Are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Judah?
There is war between Rehoboam and Jeroboam continually
Rehoboam sleeps with his fathers
He is buried with his fathers in the city of David
His mother's name is Naamah the Ammonite
Abijam his son reigns in his place
In the eighteenth year of King Jeroboam the son of Nebat
Abijam begins to reign over Judah
He reigns for three years in Jerusalem
His mother's name is Maacah the daughter of Abishalom
He walks in all the sins that his father did before him
His heart is not wholly true to the Lord his God
As the heart of David his father
Nevertheless, for David's sake the Lord his God gives him a lamp in Jerusalem
Setting up his son after him
And establishing Jerusalem
Because David did what was right in the eyes of the Lord
And did not turn aside from anything that he commanded him all the days of his life
Except in the matter of Uriah the Hittite
There is war between Abijam and Jeroboam
Now the rest of the acts of Abijam and all that he did
Are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Judah?
There is war between Abijam and Jeroboam
Abijam sleeps with his fathers
They bury him in the city of David
Asa his son reigns in his place
In the twentieth year of Jeroboam king of Israel
Asa begins to reign over Judah
He reigns forty-one years in Jerusalem
His mother's name is Maacah the daughter of Abishalom
Asa does what is right in the eyes of the Lord
As David his father has done
He puts away the male cult prostitutes out of the land
He removes all the idols that his fathers have made
He also removes Maacah his mother from being queen mother
Because she has made an abominable image for Asherah
Asa cuts down her image
He burns it at the brook Kidron
The high places are not taken away
Nevertheless, the heart of Asa is wholly true to the Lord all his days
He brings into the house of the Lord the sacred gifts of his father
And his own sacred gifts, silver, and gold, and vessels
There is war between Asa and Baasha king of Israel all their days
Baasha king of Israel goes up against Judah
He builds Ramah, that he may permit no one to go out or come in to Asa king of Judah
Asa takes all the silver and the gold that are left in the treasures of the house of the Lord
And the treasures of the king's house
He gives them into the hands of his servants
King Asa sends them to Ben-hadad the son of Tabrimmon
The son of Hezion, king of Syria, who dwells in Damascus
"Let there be a covenant between me and you"
"As there was between my father and your father"
"Behold, I am sending to you a present of silver and gold"
"Go, break your covenant with Baasha king of Israel"
"That he may withdraw from me"
Ben-hadad listens to King Asa
He sends the commanders of his armies against the cities of Israel
He conquers Ijon, Dan, Abel-beth-maacah, and all Chinneroth
With all the land of Naphtali
When Baasha hears of it, he stops building Ramah
He dwells in Tirzah
King Asa makes a proclamation to all Judah, none is exempt
They carry away the stones of Ramah and its timber
With which Baasha has been building
With them King Asa builds Geba of Benjamin and Mizpah
Now the rest of all the acts of Asa
All his might, and all that he did, and the cities that he built
Are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Judah?
In his old age he is diseased in his feet
Asa sleeps with his fathers
He is buried with his fathers in the city of David his father
Jehoshaphat his son reigns in his place
Nadab the son of Jeroboam begins to reign over Israel in the second year of Asa
He reigns over Israel two years
He does what is evil in the sight of the Lord
He walks in the way of his father
And in his sin which he made Israel to sin
Baasha the son of Ahijah, of the house of Issachar, conspires against him
Baasha strikes him down at Gibbethon, which belongs to the Philistines
For Nadab and all Israel are laying siege to Gibbethon
Baasha kills him in the third year of Asa king of Judah
He reigns in his place
As soon as he is king, he kills all the house of Jeroboam
He leaves to the house of Jeroboam not one that breathes
Until he has destroyed it
According to the word of the Lord that he spoke by his servant Ahijah the Shilonite
It is for the sins of Jeroboam that he sinned
And that he made Israel to sin
And because of the anger to which he provoked the Lord, the God of Israel
Now the rest of the acts of Nadab and all that he did
Are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Israel?
There is war between Asa and Baasha king of Israel all their days
In the third year of Asa king of Judah
Baasha the son of Ahijah begins to reign over all Israel at Tirzah
He reigns twenty-four years
He does what is evil in the sight of the Lord
He walks in the way of Jeroboam and in his sin which he made Israel to sin
The word of the Lord comes to Jehu the son of Hanani against Baasha
"Since I exalted you out of the dust"
"And made you leader over my people Israel"
"And you have walked in the way of Jeroboam"
"And have made my people Israel to sin"
"Provoking me to anger with their sins"
"Behold, I will utterly sweep away Baasha and his house"
"I will make your house like the house of Jeroboam the son of Nebat"
"Anyone belonging to Baasha who dies in the city the dogs shall eat"
"And anyone of his who dies in the field the birds of the heavens shall eat"
Now the rest of the acts of Baasha and what he did, and his might
Are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Israel?
Baasha sleeps with his fathers
He is buried at Tirzah
Elah his son reigns in his place
Moreover, the word of the Lord comes by the prophet Jehu the son of Hanani
Against Baasha and his house
Both because of all the evil that he did in the sight of the Lord
Provoking him to anger with the work of his hands
In being like the house of Jeroboam
And also because he destroyed it
In the twenty-sixth year of Asa king of Judah
Elah the son of Baasha begins to reign over Israel in Tirzah
He reigns two years
His servant Zimri, commander of half his chariots, conspires against him
When he is at Tirzah, drinking himself drunk in the house of Arza
Who is over the household in Tirzah
Zimri comes in and strikes him down and kills him
In the twenty-seventh year of Asa king of Judah
He reigns in his place
When he begins to reign, as soon as he has seated himself on his throne
He strikes down all the house of Baasha
He does not leave him a single male of his relatives or his friends
Thus Zimri destroys all the house of Baasha
According to the word of the Lord, which he spoke against Baasha by Jehu the prophet
For all the sins of Baasha and the sins of Elah his son
That they sinned and that they made Israel to sin
Provoking the Lord God of Israel to anger with their idols
Now the rest of the acts of Elah and all that he did
Are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Israel?
In the twenty-seventh year of Asa king of Judah
Zimri reigns seven days in Tirzah
Now the troops are encamped against Gibbethon, which belongs to the Philistines
The troops who are encamped hear it said
"Zimri has conspired, and he has killed the king"
Therefore all Israel makes Omri, the commander of the army, king over Israel
That day in the camp
Omri goes up from Gibbethon, and all Israel with him
They besiege Tirzah
When Zimri sees that the city is taken
He goes into the citadel of the king's house
He burns the king's house over him with fire
And he dies
Because of his sins that he committed
Doing evil in the sight of the Lord
Walking in the way of Jeroboam
And for his sin which he committed, making Israel to sin
Now the rest of the acts of Zimri, and the conspiracy that he made
Are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Israel?
Then the people of Israel are divided into two parts
Half of the people follow Tibni the son of Ginath, to make him king
And half follow Omri
The people who follow Omri overcome the people who follow Tibni
Tibni dies
Omri becomes king
In the thirty-first year of Asa king of Judah
Omri begins to reign over Israel
He reigns for twelve years
Six years he reigns in Tirzah
He buys the hill of Samaria from Shemer for two talents of silver
He fortifies the hill
He calls the name of the city that he builds Samaria
After the name of Shemer, the owner of the hill
Omri does what is evil in the sight of the Lord
He does more evil than all who were before him
He walks in all the way of Jeroboam the son of Nebat
And in the sins that he made Israel to sin
Provoking the Lord, the God of Israel, to anger by their idols
Now the rest of the acts of Omri that he did, and the might that he showed
Are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Israel?
Omri sleeps with his fathers
He is buried in Samaria
Ahab his son reigns in his place
In the thirty-eighth year of Asa king of Judah
Ahab the son of Omri begins to reign over Israel
Ahab the son of Omri reigns over Israel in Samaria twenty-two years
Ahab the son of Omri does evil in the sight of the Lord
More than all who were before him
As if it had been a light thing for him to walk in the sins of Jeroboam
He takes for his wife Jezebel the daughter of Ethbaal king of the Sidonians
He goes and serves Baal and worships him
He erects an altar for Baal in the house of Baal
Which he builds in Samaria
Ahab makes an Asherah
Ahab does more to provoke the Lord, the God of Israel, to anger
Than all the kings of Israel who were before him
In his days Hiel of Bethel builds Jericho
He lays its foundation at the cost of Abiram his firstborn
He sets up its gates at the cost of his youngest son Segub
According to the word of the Lord
Which he spoke by Joshua the son of Nun
Elijah the Tishbite, of Tishbe in Gilead, says to Ahab
"As the Lord, the God of Israel, lives, before whom I stand"
"There shall be neither dew nor rain these years"
"Except by my word"
The word of the Lord comes to him
"Depart from here and turn eastward"
"Hide yourself by the brook Cherith, which is east of the Jordan"
"You shall drink from the brook"
"I have commanded the ravens to feed you there"
He goes and does according to the word of the Lord
He goes and dwells by the brook Cherith that is east of the Jordan
The ravens bring him bread and meat in the morning
And bread and meat in the evening
He drinks from the brook
After a while the brook dries up
Because there is no rain in the land
The word of the Lord comes to him
"Arise, go to Zarephath, which belongs to Sidon, and dwell there"
"Behold, I have commanded a widow there to feed you"
He arises and goes to Zarephath
When he comes to the gate of the city
Behold, a widow is there gathering sticks
He calls to her
"Bring me a little water in a vessel, that I may drink"
As she is going to bring it
He calls to her, "Bring me a morsel of bread in your hand"
"As the Lord your God lives, I have nothing baked"
"Only a handful of flour in a jar and a little oil in a jug"
"And now I am gathering a couple of sticks"
"That I may go in and prepare it for myself and my son"
"That we may eat it and die"
Elijah says to her, "Do not fear"
"Go and do as you have said"
"But first make me a little cake of it and bring it to me"
"And afterward make something for yourself and your son"
"For thus says the Lord, the God of Israel"
"'The jar of flour shall not be spent'"
"'And the jug of oil shall not be empty'"
"'Until the day that the Lord sends rain upon the earth'"
She goes and does as Elijah says
She and he and her household eat for many days
The jar of flour is not spent
Neither does the jug of oil become empty
According to the word of the Lord that he spoke by Elijah
After this the son of the woman, the mistress of the house, becomes ill
His illness is so severe that there is no breath left in him
She says to Elijah
"What have you against me, O man of God?"
"You have come to me to bring my sin to remembrance"
"And to cause the death of my son"
"Give me your son"
He takes him from her arms
He carries him up into the upper chamber where he lodges
He lays him on his own bed
He cries to the Lord
"O Lord my God, have you brought calamity even upon the widow"
"With whom I sojourn, by killing her son?"
He stretches himself upon the child three times
He cries to the Lord
"O Lord my God, let this child's life come into him again"
The Lord listens to the voice of Elijah
The life of the child comes into him again, and he revives
Elijah takes the child and brings him down from the upper chamber into the house
He gives him to his mother
Elijah says, "See, your son lives"
The woman says to Elijah
"Now I know that you are a man of God"
"And that the word of the Lord in your mouth is truth"
After many days the word of the Lord comes to Elijah, in the third year
"Go, show yourself to Ahab, and I will send rain upon the earth"
Elijah goes to show himself to Ahab
Now the famine is severe in Samaria
Ahab calls Obadiah, who is over the household
(Now Obadiah fears the Lord greatly
When Jezebel cut off the prophets of the Lord
Obadiah took a hundred prophets and hid them by fifties in a cave
And fed them with bread and water)
Ahab says to Obadiah
"Go through the land to all the springs of water and to all the valleys"
"Perhaps we may find grass and save the horses and mules alive"
"And not lose some of the animals"
They divide the land between them to pass through it
Ahab goes in one direction by himself
Obadiah goes in another direction by himself
As Obadiah is on the way, behold, Elijah meets him
Obadiah recognizes him
He falls on his face
"Is it you, my lord Elijah?"
"It is I. Go, tell your lord, 'Behold, Elijah is here'"
"How have I sinned, that you would give your servant into the hand of Ahab"
"To kill me?"
"As the Lord your God lives, there is no nation or kingdom"
"Where my lord has not sent to seek you"
"And when they would say, 'He is not here,'"
"He would take an oath of the kingdom or nation"
"That they had not found you"
"And now you say, 'Go, tell your lord, "Behold, Elijah is here"'"
"As soon as I have gone from you, the Spirit of the Lord will carry you"
"I know not where"
"And so, when I come and tell Ahab and he cannot find you"
"He will kill me"
"Although I your servant have feared the Lord from my youth"
"Has it not been told my lord what I did when Jezebel killed the prophets?"
"How I hid a hundred men of the Lord's prophets by fifties in a cave"
"And fed them with bread and water?"
"And now you say, 'Go, tell your lord, "Behold, Elijah is here"'"
"He will kill me"
Elijah says, "As the Lord of hosts lives, before whom I stand"
"I will surely show myself to him today"
Obadiah goes to meet Ahab
He tells him
Ahab goes to meet Elijah
When Ahab sees Elijah, Ahab says to him
"Is it you, you troubler of Israel?"
"I have not troubled Israel, but you have, and your father's house"
"Because you have abandoned the commandments of the Lord"
"And followed the Baals"
"Now therefore send and gather all Israel to me at Mount Carmel"
"And the 450 prophets of Baal and the 400 prophets of Asherah"
"Who eat at Jezebel's table"
Ahab sends to all the people of Israel
He gathers the prophets together at Mount Carmel
Elijah comes near to all the people
"How long will you go limping between two different opinions?"
"If the Lord is God, follow him"
"But if Baal, then follow him"
The people do not answer him a word
Elijah says to the people
"I, even I only, am left a prophet of the Lord"
"But Baal's prophets are 450 men"
"Let two bulls be given to us"
"Let them choose one bull for themselves"
"Cut it in pieces and lay it on the wood, but put no fire to it"
"I will prepare the other bull and lay it on the wood"
"And put no fire to it"
"Then you call upon the name of your god"
"And I will call upon the name of the Lord"
"And the God who answers by fire, he is God"
All the people answer, "It is well spoken"
Elijah says to the prophets of Baal
"Choose for yourselves one bull and prepare it first"
"For you are many"
"And call upon the name of your god, but put no fire to it"
They take the bull that is given them
They prepare it
They call upon the name of Baal from morning until noon
"O Baal, answer us"
There is no voice, and no one answers
They limp around the altar that they have made
At noon Elijah mocks them
"Cry aloud, for he is a god"
"Either he is musing, or he is relieving himself"
"Or he is on a journey, or perhaps he is asleep and must be awakened"
They cry aloud
They cut themselves after their custom with swords and lances
Until the blood gushes out upon them
As midday passes, they rave on until the time of the offering of the oblation
There is no voice. No one answers; no one pays attention
Elijah says to all the people, "Come near to me"
All the people come near to him
He repairs the altar of the Lord that has been thrown down
Elijah takes twelve stones
According to the number of the tribes of the sons of Jacob
To whom the word of the Lord came, saying, "Israel shall be your name"
With the stones he builds an altar in the name of the Lord
He makes a trench about the altar, as great as would contain two seahs of seed
He puts the wood in order
He cuts the bull in pieces and lays it on the wood
"Fill four jars with water and pour it on the burnt offering and on the wood"
"Do it a second time"
They do it a second time
"Do it a third time"
They do it a third time
The water runs around the altar
He fills the trench also with water
At the time of the offering of the oblation
Elijah the prophet comes near
"O Lord, God of Abraham, Isaac, and Israel"
"Let it be known this day that you are God in Israel"
"And that I am your servant"
"And that I have done all these things at your word"
"Answer me, O Lord, answer me"
"That this people may know that you, O Lord, are God"
"And that you have turned their hearts back"
The fire of the Lord falls
It consumes the burnt offering and the wood and the stones and the dust
It licks up the water that is in the trench
When all the people see it, they fall on their faces
"The Lord, he is God; the Lord, he is God"
Elijah says to them, "Seize the prophets of Baal; let not one of them escape"
They seize them
Elijah brings them down to the brook Kishon
He slaughters them there
Elijah says to Ahab, "Go up, eat and drink, for there is a sound of the rushing of rain"
Ahab goes up to eat and to drink
Elijah goes up to the top of Mount Carmel
He bows himself down on the earth
He puts his face between his knees
He says to his servant, "Go up now, look toward the sea"
He goes up and looks
"There is nothing"
He says, "Go again," seven times
At the seventh time he says, "Behold, a little cloud like a man's hand"
"Is rising from the sea"
"Go up, say to Ahab, 'Prepare your chariot and go down'"
"'Lest the rain stop you'"
In a little while the heavens grow black with clouds and wind
There is a great rain
Ahab rides and goes to Jezreel
The hand of the Lord is on Elijah
He gathered up his garment and runs before Ahab to the entrance of Jezreel
Ahab tells Jezebel all that Elijah has done
How he has killed all the prophets with the sword
Jezebel sends a messenger to Elijah
"So may the gods do to me and more also"
"If I do not make your life as the life of one of them by this time tomorrow"
He is afraid
He arises and runs for his life
He comes to Beersheba, which belongs to Judah
He leaves his servant there
He himself goes a day's journey into the wilderness
He comes and sits down under a broom tree
He asks that he might die
"It is enough; now, O Lord, take away my life"
"For I am no better than my fathers"
He lies down and sleeps under a broom tree
Behold, an angel touches him
"Arise and eat"
He looks, and behold, there is at his head a cake baked on hot stones
And a jar of water
He eats and drinks
He lies down again
The angel of the Lord comes a second time
He touches him
"Arise and eat, for the journey is too great for you"
He arises and eats and drinks
He goes in the strength of that food forty days and forty nights
To Horeb, the mount of God
There he comes to a cave and lodges in it
Behold, the word of the Lord comes to him
"What are you doing here, Elijah?"
"I have been very jealous for the Lord, the God of hosts"
"For the people of Israel have forsaken your covenant"
"Thrown down your altars, and killed your prophets with the sword"
"I, even I only, am left, and they seek my life, to take it away"
"Go out and stand on the mount before the Lord"
Behold, the Lord passes by
A great and strong wind tears the mountains
And breaks in pieces the rocks before the Lord
But the Lord is not in the wind
After the wind an earthquake
But the Lord is not in the earthquake
After the earthquake a fire
But the Lord is not in the fire
After the fire the sound of a low whisper
When Elijah hears it, he wraps his face in his cloak
He goes out and stands at the entrance of the cave
Behold, there comes a voice to him
"What are you doing here, Elijah?"
"I have been very jealous for the Lord, the God of hosts"
"For the people of Israel have forsaken your covenant"
"Thrown down your altars, and killed your prophets with the sword"
"I, even I only, am left, and they seek my life, to take it away"
The Lord says to him
"Go, return on your way to the wilderness of Damascus"
"When you arrive, you shall anoint Hazael to be king over Syria"
"Also you shall anoint Jehu the son of Nimshi to be king over Israel"
"And Elisha the son of Shaphat of Abel-meholah you shall anoint to be prophet"
"In your place"
"And the one who escapes from the sword of Hazael shall Jehu put to death"
"And the one who escapes from the sword of Jehu shall Elisha put to death"
"Yet I will leave seven thousand in Israel"
"All the knees that have not bowed to Baal"
"And every mouth that has not kissed him"
He departs from there
He finds Elisha the son of Shaphat
Who is plowing with twelve yoke of oxen in front of him
He is with the twelfth
Elijah passes by him and casts his cloak upon him
He leaves the oxen and runs after Elijah
"Let me kiss my father and my mother, and then I will follow you"
"Go back again, for what have I done to you?"
He returns from following him
He takes the yoke of oxen and sacrifices them
He boils their flesh with the yokes of the oxen
He gives it to the people, and they eat
He arises and goes after Elijah
He assists him
Ben-hadad king of Syria gathers all his army
Thirty-two kings are with him, and horses and chariots
He goes up and besieges Samaria and fights against it
He sends messengers into the city to Ahab king of Israel
"Thus says Ben-hadad: 'Your silver and your gold are mine'"
"'Your best wives and children also are mine'"
The king of Israel answers, "As you say, my lord, O king"
"I am yours, and all that I have"
The messengers come again
"Thus says Ben-hadad: 'I sent to you, saying'"
"'Deliver to me your silver and your gold, your wives and your children'"
"'Nevertheless I will send my servants to you tomorrow about this time'"
"'And they shall search your house and the houses of your servants'"
"'And lay hands on whatever pleases them and take it away'"
The king of Israel calls all the elders of the land
"Mark, now, and see how this man is seeking trouble"
"For he sent to me for my wives and my children and for my silver and my gold"
"And I did not refuse him"
All the elders and all the people say to him
"Do not listen or consent"
So he says to the messengers of Ben-hadad
"Tell my lord the king, 'All that you first demanded of your servant I will do'"
"'But this thing I cannot do'"
The messengers depart and bring him word again
Ben-hadad sends to him
"The gods do so to me and more also"
"If the dust of Samaria shall suffice for handfuls for all the people who follow me"
The king of Israel answers
"Tell him, 'Let not him who straps on his armor boast himself as he who takes it off'"
When Ben-hadad hears this message as he is drinking
He and the kings in the booths
He says to his men, "Take your positions"
They take their positions against the city
Behold, a prophet comes near to Ahab king of Israel
"Thus says the Lord, 'Have you seen all this great multitude?'"
"'Behold, I will give it into your hand this day'"
"'And you shall know that I am the Lord'"
Ahab says, "By whom?"
"Thus says the Lord, 'By the servants of the governors of the districts'"
"Who shall begin the battle?"
"You"
He musters the servants of the governors of the districts
They are 232
After them he musters all the people of Israel, seven thousand
They go out at noon
Ben-hadad is drinking himself drunk in the booths
He and the thirty-two kings who help him
The servants of the governors of the districts go out first
Ben-hadad sends out scouts
They tell him, "Men are coming out from Samaria"
"If they have come out for peace, take them alive"
"If they have come out for war, take them alive"
These men of the governors of the districts go out of the city
The army that follows them
Each strikes down his man
The Syrians flee
Israel pursues them
Ben-hadad king of Syria escapes on a horse with horsemen
The king of Israel goes out and strikes the horses and chariots
He strikes the Syrians with a great blow
The prophet comes near to the king of Israel
"Come, strengthen yourself, and consider well what you have to do"
"For in the spring the king of Syria will come up against you"
The servants of the king of Syria say to him
"Their gods are gods of the hills"
"That is why they were stronger than we"
"But let us fight against them in the plain"
"And surely we shall be stronger than they"
"Also do this: remove the kings, each from his post"
"And put commanders in their places"
"And muster an army like the army that you have lost"
"Horse for horse, and chariot for chariot"
"Then we will fight against them in the plain"
"And surely we shall be stronger than they"
He listens to their voice and does so
In the spring, Ben-hadad musters the Syrians
He goes up to Aphek to fight against Israel
The people of Israel are mustered and provisioned
They go against them
The people of Israel encamp before them like two little flocks of goats
But the Syrians fill the country
A man of God comes near
He says to the king of Israel
"Thus says the Lord, 'Because the Syrians have said'"
"'The Lord is a god of the hills but he is not a god of the valleys'"
"'Therefore I will give all this great multitude into your hand'"
"'And you shall know that I am the Lord'"
They encamp opposite one another seven days
On the seventh day the battle is joined
The people of Israel strike down of the Syrians 100,000 foot soldiers in one day
The rest flee into the city of Aphek
The wall falls upon 27,000 men who are left
Ben-hadad flees and enters an inner chamber in the city
His servants say to him
"Behold now, we have heard that the kings of the house of Israel are merciful kings"
"Let us put sackcloth around our waists and ropes on our heads"
"And go out to the king of Israel"
"Perhaps he will spare your life"
They tie sackcloth around their waists and put ropes on their heads
They go to the king of Israel
"Your servant Ben-hadad says, 'Please, let me live'"
He says, "Does he still live? He is my brother"
The men are watching for a sign
They quickly take it up from him
"Yes, your brother Ben-hadad"
He says, "Go and bring him"
Ben-hadad comes out to him
He causes him to come up into the chariot
Ben-hadad says to him
"The cities that my father took from your father I will restore"
"And you may establish bazaars for yourself in Damascus"
"As my father did in Samaria"
Ahab says, "I will let you go on these terms"
He makes a covenant with him and lets him go
A certain man of the sons of the prophets says to his fellow
By the word of the Lord, "Strike me, please"
The man refuses to strike him
He says to him, "Because you have not obeyed the voice of the Lord"
"Behold, as soon as you have gone from me, a lion shall strike you down"
As soon as he had departed from him, a lion meets him and strikes him down
He finds another man
"Strike me, please"
The man strikes him, striking and wounding him
The prophet departs and waits for the king by the way
He disguises himself with a bandage over his eyes
As the king passes, he cries to the king
"Your servant went out into the midst of the battle"
"And behold, a soldier turned and brought a man to me"
"And said, 'Guard this man'"
"'If by any means he is missing, your life shall be for his life'"
"'Or else you shall pay a talent of silver'"
"As your servant was busy here and there, he was gone"
The king of Israel says to him
"So shall your judgment be; you yourself have decided it"
He hurries to take the bandage away from his eyes
The king of Israel recognizes him as one of the prophets
He says to him, "Thus says the Lord"
"'Because you have let go out of your hand the man whom I had devoted to destruction'"
"'Therefore your life shall be for his life, and your people for his people'"
The king of Israel goes to his house vexed and sullen
He comes to Samaria
Now Naboth the Jezreelite has a vineyard in Jezreel
Beside the palace of Ahab king of Samaria
Ahab speaks to Naboth
"Give me your vineyard, that I may have it for a vegetable garden"
"Because it is near my house"
"I will give you a better vineyard for it"
"Or, if it seems good to you, I will give you its value in money"
Naboth says to Ahab
"The Lord forbid that I should give you the inheritance of my fathers"
Ahab goes into his house vexed and sullen
Because of what Naboth the Jezreelite has said to him
He lies down on his bed and turns away his face
He will eat no food
Jezebel his wife comes to him
"Why is your spirit so vexed that you eat no food?"
"Because I spoke to Naboth the Jezreelite"
"And said to him, 'Give me your vineyard for money'"
"'Or else, if it please you, I will give you another vineyard for it'"
"And he answered, 'I will not give you my vineyard'"
Jezebel his wife says to him
"Do you now govern Israel?"
"Arise and eat bread and let your heart be cheerful"
"I will give you the vineyard of Naboth the Jezreelite"
She writes letters in Ahab's name
She seals them with his seal
She sends the letters to the elders and the leaders who live with Naboth in his city
She writes in the letters
"Proclaim a fast, and set Naboth at the head of the people"
"And set two worthless men opposite him"
"And let them bring a charge against him, saying"
"'You have cursed God and the king'"
"Then take him out and stone him to death"
The men of his city, the elders and the leaders who live in his city, do as Jezebel has sent word to them
As it is written in the letters that she has sent to them
They proclaim a fast
They set Naboth at the head of the people
The two worthless men come in
They sit opposite him
The worthless men bring a charge against Naboth in the presence of the people
"Naboth cursed God and the king"
They take him outside the city
They stone him to death with stones
They send to Jezebel, "Naboth has been stoned; he is dead"
As soon as Jezebel hears that Naboth has been stoned and is dead
Jezebel says to Ahab
"Arise, take possession of the vineyard of Naboth the Jezreelite"
"Which he refused to give you for money"
"For Naboth is not alive, but dead"
As soon as Ahab hears that Naboth is dead
Ahab arises to go down to the vineyard of Naboth the Jezreelite
To take possession of it
The word of the Lord comes to Elijah the Tishbite
"Arise, go down to meet Ahab king of Israel, who is in Samaria"
"Behold, he is in the vineyard of Naboth, where he has gone to take possession"
"You shall say to him, 'Thus says the Lord'"
"'Have you killed and also taken possession?'"
"And you shall say to him, 'Thus says the Lord'"
"'In the place where dogs licked up the blood of Naboth'"
"'Shall dogs lick your own blood'"
Ahab says to Elijah, "Have you found me, O my enemy?"
"I have found you"
"Because you have sold yourself to do what is evil in the sight of the Lord"
"'Behold, I will bring disaster upon you'"
"'I will utterly burn you up'"
"'And will cut off from Ahab every male, bond or free, in Israel'"
"'And I will make your house like the house of Jeroboam the son of Nebat'"
"'And like the house of Baasha the son of Ahijah'"
"'For the anger to which you have provoked me'"
"'And because you have made Israel to sin'"
"And of Jezebel the Lord also has spoken, saying"
"'The dogs shall eat Jezebel within the walls of Jezreel'"
"'Anyone belonging to Ahab who dies in the city the dogs shall eat'"
"'And anyone of his who dies in the open country the birds of the heavens shall eat'"
There is none who sells himself to do what is evil in the sight of the Lord like Ahab
Whom Jezebel his wife incites
He acts very abominably in going after idols
As the Amorites had done, whom the Lord cast out before the people of Israel
When Ahab hears those words, he tears his clothes
He puts sackcloth on his flesh and fasts
He lies in sackcloth and goes about dejectedly
The word of the Lord comes to Elijah the Tishbite
"Have you seen how Ahab has humbled himself before me?"
"Because he has humbled himself before me"
"I will not bring the disaster in his days"
"But in his son's days I will bring the disaster upon his house"
For three years Syria and Israel continue without war
In the third year Jehoshaphat the king of Judah comes down to the king of Israel
The king of Israel says to his servants
"Do you know that Ramoth-gilead belongs to us"
"And we keep quiet and do not take it out of the hand of the king of Syria?"
He says to Jehoshaphat
"Will you go with me to battle at Ramoth-gilead?"
Jehoshaphat says to the king of Israel, "I am as you are"
"My people as your people, my horses as your horses"
Jehoshaphat says to the king of Israel
"Inquire first for the word of the Lord"
The king of Israel gathers the prophets together, about four hundred men
"Shall I go to battle against Ramoth-gilead, or shall I refrain?"
They say, "Go up, for the Lord will give it into the hand of the king"
Jehoshaphat says, "Is there not here another prophet of the Lord"
"Of whom we may inquire?"
The king of Israel says to Jehoshaphat
"There is yet one man by whom we may inquire of the Lord, Micaiah the son of Imlah"
"But I hate him, for he never prophesies good concerning me, but evil"
Jehoshaphat says, "Let not the king say so"
The king of Israel calls an officer
