"Bring quickly Micaiah the son of Imlah"
Now the king of Israel and Jehoshaphat the king of Judah are sitting on their thrones
Arrayed in their robes, at the threshing floor at the entrance of the gate of Samaria
All the prophets are prophesying before them
Zedekiah the son of Chenaanah makes for himself horns of iron
"Thus says the Lord, 'With these you shall push the Syrians until they are destroyed'"
All the prophets prophesy so
"Go up to Ramoth-gilead and triumph; the Lord will give it into the hand of the king"
The messenger who goes to summon Micaiah says to him
"Behold, the words of the prophets with one accord are favorable to the king"
"Let your word be like the word of one of them, and speak favorably"
Micaiah says, "As the Lord lives, what the Lord says to me, that I will speak"
When he has come to the king
The king says to him, "Micaiah, shall we go to Ramoth-gilead to battle, or shall we refrain?"
He answers him, "Go up and triumph; the Lord will give it into the hand of the king"
The king says to him, "How many times shall I make you swear"
"That you speak to me nothing but the truth in the name of the Lord?"
"I saw all Israel scattered on the mountains"
"As sheep that have no shepherd"
"And the Lord said, 'These have no master'"
"'Let each return to his home in peace'"
The king of Israel says to Jehoshaphat
"Did I not tell you that he would not prophesy good concerning me, but evil?"
Micaiah says, "Therefore hear the word of the Lord"
"I saw the Lord sitting on his throne"
"And all the host of heaven standing beside him on his right hand and on his left"
"And the Lord said, 'Who will entice Ahab'"
"'That he may go up and fall at Ramoth-gilead?'"
"One said one thing, and another said another"
"Then a spirit came forward and stood before the Lord, saying"
"'I will entice him'"
"'How?' the Lord asked him"
"'I will go out and will be a lying spirit in the mouth of all his prophets'"
"He said, 'You are to entice him, and you shall succeed'"
"'Go out and do so'"
"Now therefore behold, the Lord has put a lying spirit in the mouth of all these your prophets"
"The Lord has declared disaster for you"
Zedekiah the son of Chenaanah comes near
He strikes Micaiah on the cheek
"How did the Spirit of the Lord go from me to speak to you?"
Micaiah says, "Behold, you shall see on that day when you go into an inner chamber to hide yourself"
The king of Israel says, "Seize Micaiah and take him back to Amon the governor of the city"
"And to Joash the king's son"
"And say, 'Thus says the king, "Put this fellow in prison'"
"'And feed him with meager rations of bread and water'"
"'Until I come in peace'"
Micaiah says, "If you return in peace, the Lord has not spoken by me"
He says, "Hear, all you peoples"
The king of Israel and Jehoshaphat the king of Judah go up to Ramoth-gilead
The king of Israel says to Jehoshaphat
"I will disguise myself and go into battle, but you wear your robes"
The king of Israel disguises himself and goes into battle
Now the king of Syria has commanded the thirty-two captains of his chariots
"Fight with neither small nor great, but only with the king of Israel"
As soon as the captains of the chariots see Jehoshaphat
They say, "It is surely the king of Israel"
They turn to fight against him
Jehoshaphat cries out
When the captains of the chariots see that it is not the king of Israel
They turn back from pursuing him
A certain man draws his bow at random
He strikes the king of Israel between the scale armor and the breastplate
He says to the driver of his chariot, "Turn around and carry me out of the battle"
"For I am wounded"
The battle grows hot that day
The king is propped up in his chariot facing the Syrians
He dies at evening
The blood of the wound flows into the bottom of the chariot
About sunset a cry goes through the army
"Every man to his city, and every man to his country"
The king dies and is brought to Samaria
They bury the king in Samaria
They wash the chariot by the pool of Samaria
The dogs lick up his blood
The prostitutes wash themselves in it
According to the word of the Lord that he had spoken
Now the rest of the acts of Ahab and all that he did
And the ivory house that he built
And all the cities that he built, are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Israel?
Ahab sleeps with his fathers
Ahaziah his son reigns in his place
Jehoshaphat the son of Asa begins to reign over Judah in the fourth year of Ahab king of Israel
Jehoshaphat is thirty-five years old when he begins to reign
He reigns twenty-five years in Jerusalem
His mother's name is Azubah the daughter of Shilhi
He walks in all the way of Asa his father
He does not turn aside from it, doing what is right in the sight of the Lord
Yet the high places are not taken away
The people still sacrifice and make offerings on the high places
Jehoshaphat also makes peace with the king of Israel
Now the rest of the acts of Jehoshaphat and his might that he showed
And how he warred, are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Judah?
The remnant of the male cult prostitutes who remain in the days of his father Asa
He exterminated from the land
There is no king in Edom; a deputy is king
Jehoshaphat makes ships of Tarshish to go to Ophir for gold
But they do not go, for the ships are wrecked at Ezion-geber
Ahaziah the son of Ahab says to Jehoshaphat
"Let my servants go with your servants in the ships"
Jehoshaphat is not willing
Jehoshaphat sleeps with his fathers
He is buried with his fathers in the city of David his father
Jehoram his son reigns in his place
Ahaziah the son of Ahab begins to reign over Israel in Samaria
In the seventeenth year of Jehoshaphat king of Judah
He reigns two years over Israel
He does what is evil in the sight of the Lord
He walks in the way of his father and in the way of his mother
And in the way of Jeroboam the son of Nebat, who made Israel to sin
He serves Baal and worships him
He provokes the Lord, the God of Israel, to anger in every way that his father had done
Ahaziah falls through the lattice in his upper chamber in Samaria
He lies injured
He sends messengers, telling them
"Go, inquire of Baal-zebub, the god of Ekron, whether I shall recover from this injury"
The angel of the Lord says to Elijah the Tishbite
"Arise, go up to meet the messengers of the king of Samaria"
"And say to them, 'Is it because there is no God in Israel'"
"'That you are going to inquire of Baal-zebub, the god of Ekron?'"
"Now therefore thus says the Lord"
"'You shall not come down from the bed to which you have gone up'"
"'But you shall surely die'"
So Elijah goes
The messengers return to the king
He says to them, "Why have you returned?"
They say to him, "There came a man to meet us"
"And he said to us, 'Go back to the king who sent you'"
"'And say to him, "Thus says the Lord"'"
"'"Is it because there is no God in Israel that you are sending to inquire of Baal-zebub, the god of Ekron?"'"
"'"Therefore you shall not come down from the bed to which you have gone up, but you shall surely die"'"
He says to them, "What kind of man was he who came to meet you and told you these things?"
They answer him, "He wore a garment of hair, with a belt of leather about his waist"
He says, "It is Elijah the Tishbite"
The king sends to him a captain of fifty men with his fifty
He goes up to Elijah, who is sitting on the top of a hill
He says to him, "O man of God, the king says, 'Come down'"
Elijah answers the captain of fifty, "If I am a man of God"
"Let fire come down from heaven and consume you and your fifty"
Fire comes down from heaven and consumes him and his fifty
Again the king sends to him another captain of fifty men with his fifty
He goes up and says to him, "O man of God, this is the king's order, 'Come down quickly'"
Elijah answers them, "If I am a man of God"
"Let fire come down from heaven and consume you and your fifty"
The fire of God comes down from heaven and consumes him and his fifty
Again the king sends the captain of a third fifty with his fifty
The third captain of fifty goes up and comes and falls on his knees before Elijah
He entreats him, "O man of God, please let my life and the life of these fifty servants of yours be precious in your sight"
"Behold, fire came down from heaven and consumed the two former captains of fifty men with their fifties"
"But now let my life be precious in your sight"
The angel of the Lord says to Elijah, "Go down with him; do not be afraid of him"
He arises and goes down with him to the king
He says to him, "Thus says the Lord"
"'Because you have sent messengers to inquire of Baal-zebub, the god of Ekron'"
"'Is it because there is no God in Israel to inquire of his word?'"
"'Therefore you shall not come down from the bed to which you have gone up'"
"'But you shall surely die'"
He dies according to the word of the Lord that Elijah has spoken
Jehoram becomes king in his place in the second year of Jehoram the son of Jehoshaphat, king of Judah
Because Ahaziah has no son
Now the rest of the acts of Ahaziah that he did, are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Israel?
Now when the Lord is about to take Elijah up to heaven by a whirlwind
Elijah and Elisha are on their way from Gilgal
Elijah says to Elisha, "Please stay here, for the Lord has sent me as far as Bethel"
Elisha says, "As the Lord lives, and as you yourself live, I will not leave you"
They go down to Bethel
The sons of the prophets who are in Bethel come out to Elisha
"Do you know that today the Lord will take away your master from over you?"
He says, "Yes, I know it; keep quiet"
Elijah says to him, "Elisha, please stay here, for the Lord has sent me to Jericho"
"As the Lord lives, and as you yourself live, I will not leave you"
They come to Jericho
The sons of the prophets who are at Jericho draw near to Elisha
"Do you know that today the Lord will take away your master from over you?"
He answers, "Yes, I know it; keep quiet"
Elijah says to him, "Please stay here, for the Lord has sent me to the Jordan"
"As the Lord lives, and as you yourself live, I will not leave you"
The two of them go on
Fifty men of the sons of the prophets also go and stand at some distance from them
As they both are standing by the Jordan
Elijah takes his cloak and rolls it up
He strikes the water
The water is parted to the one side and to the other
Till the two of them cross on dry ground
When they have crossed, Elijah says to Elisha
"Ask what I shall do for you, before I am taken from you"
Elisha says, "Please let there be a double portion of your spirit on me"
"You have asked a hard thing"
"Yet, if you see me as I am being taken from you, it shall be so for you"
"But if you do not see me, it shall not be so"
As they still go on and talk
Behold, chariots of fire and horses of fire separate the two of them
Elijah goes up by a whirlwind into heaven
Elisha sees it and cries out, "My father, my father!"
"The chariots of Israel and its horsemen!"
He sees him no more
He takes hold of his own clothes and tears them in two pieces
He takes up the cloak of Elijah that has fallen from him
He goes back and stands on the bank of the Jordan
He takes the cloak of Elijah that has fallen from him
He strikes the water, saying, "Where is the Lord, the God of Elijah?"
When he has struck the water
The water is parted to the one side and to the other
Elisha goes over
Now when the sons of the prophets who are at Jericho see him opposite them
They say, "The spirit of Elijah rests on Elisha"
They come to meet him and bow to the ground before him
They say to him, "Behold now, there are with your servants fifty strong men"
"Please let them go and seek your master"
"It may be that the Spirit of the Lord has caught him up"
"And cast him upon some mountain or into some valley"
He says, "You shall not send"
When they urge him till he is ashamed, he says, "Send"
They send therefore fifty men
For three days they seek him but do not find him
They come back to him while he is staying at Jericho
He says to them, "Did I not say to you, 'Do not go'?"
Men of Jericho complain to Elisha that the water is bad and the land unfruitful
Elisha heals the spring with salt in a new bowl
Elisha goes up to Bethel
Young boys mock him: "Go up, you baldhead"
Elisha curses them in the name of the Lord
Two she-bears come out of the woods and tear forty-two of the boys
Elisha goes to Mount Carmel, then returns to Samaria
Jehoram son of Ahab becomes king over Israel
He does evil in the Lord's sight but removes the pillar of Baal his father had made
Mesha king of Moab rebels against Israel after Ahab's death
Jehoram musters all Israel and sends to Jehoshaphat king of Judah for alliance
Israel, Judah, and Edom march seven days through wilderness without water
Jehoram despairs, but Jehoshaphat asks for a prophet of the Lord
They go to Elisha
Elisha rebukes Jehoram but respects Jehoshaphat
Elisha calls for a musician
The hand of the Lord comes upon Elisha as the musician plays
Elisha prophesies water without wind or rain, and victory over Moab
Water flows from the direction of Edom, filling the valley
Moabites see the water red as blood and think the kings have slain each other
Moabites come to plunder but Israel rises and strikes them
Israel pursues Moabites into their land, destroying cities
King of Moab offers his firstborn son as burnt offering on the wall
Great wrath comes upon Israel; they withdraw to their own land
A widow of a prophet cries to Elisha: her creditor will take her two children as slaves
Elisha asks what she has; she has only a jar of oil
Elisha tells her to borrow many vessels and pour oil
The oil multiplies until all vessels are filled
She sells the oil, pays her debt, and lives on the rest
Elisha passes through Shunem regularly
A wealthy Shunammite woman urges him to eat with her
She persuades her husband to build Elisha a small upper room
Elisha wishes to repay her kindness
Gehazi notes she has no son and her husband is old
Elisha promises she will embrace a son
She protests, "Do not lie to your servant"
The woman conceives and bears a son in due season
When the child is grown, he goes to his father among the reapers
The child cries out, "My head, my head!"
A servant carries him to his mother
The child sits on her lap until noon, then dies
She lays him on Elisha's bed and shuts the door
She calls her husband to send her a servant and a donkey to go to Elisha
Her husband questions why she goes today
She says, "All is well," and goes to Mount Carmel
Elisha sees her coming and sends Gehazi to meet her
She says all is well but goes straight to Elisha and grasps his feet
"Did I ask my lord for a son? Did I not say, 'Do not deceive me'?"
Elisha sends Gehazi ahead with his staff to lay on the child's face
The woman refuses to leave without Elisha
Gehazi goes ahead and lays the staff on the child, but no sound or sign of life
Gehazi returns: "The child has not awakened"
Elisha enters the house and finds the child dead on his bed
Elisha prays to the Lord
He lies upon the child, mouth to mouth, eyes to eyes, hands to hands
The child's flesh grows warm
Elisha walks back and forth, then stretches himself upon him again
The child sneezes seven times and opens his eyes
Elisha calls Gehazi to summon the Shunammite
She comes, falls at his feet, bows to the ground, and takes up her son
Elisha returns to Gilgal during a famine
Sons of the prophets are sitting before him
Elisha tells his servant to set on the large pot and make stew
One goes to the field to gather herbs and finds wild gourds
He shreds them into the pot of stew, not knowing what they are
They pour out for the men to eat
As they eat, they cry out, "O man of God, there is death in the pot!"
Elisha calls for flour and throws it into the pot
There is no harm in the pot
A man comes from Baal-shalishah bringing bread of firstfruits and fresh grain
Elisha says to give it to the men to eat
His servant protests: "How can I set this before a hundred men?"
Elisha repeats the command, adding that the Lord says they will eat and have some left
They eat and have some left over, according to the Lord's word
Naaman, commander of the Syrian army, is a great and mighty man of valor
But he is a leper
Syrian raiders have carried away a young Israelite girl who serves Naaman's wife
She says to her mistress, "Would that my lord were with the prophet who is in Samaria!"
"He would cure him of his leprosy"
Naaman tells his king what the girl said
The king of Syria sends Naaman with a letter to the king of Israel
Naaman goes, taking silver, gold, and garments
The letter says, "I have sent Naaman my servant to you, that you may cure him of his leprosy"
The king of Israel tears his clothes in distress
"Am I God, to kill and to make alive, that this man sends word to cure a man of his leprosy?"
Elisha hears the king has torn his clothes
He sends word: "Why have you torn your clothes? Let him come to me"
Naaman comes with his horses and chariots and stands at Elisha's door
Elisha sends a messenger: "Go and wash in the Jordan seven times"
"Your flesh shall be restored, and you shall be clean"
Naaman is angry and goes away
"I thought he would surely come out and stand and call upon the name of the Lord his God"
"Are not Abana and Pharpar, the rivers of Damascus, better than all the waters of Israel?"
His servants approach him
"My father, it is a great word the prophet has spoken to you; will you not do it?"
"Has he actually said to you, 'Wash, and be clean'?"
Naaman goes down and dips himself seven times in the Jordan
His flesh is restored like the flesh of a little child
He is clean
Naaman returns to Elisha with all his company
He stands before him and declares, "Now I know that there is no God in all the earth but in Israel"
"Please accept a present from your servant"
Elisha refuses: "As the Lord lives, before whom I stand, I will receive none"
Naaman urges him, but he refuses
Naaman asks for two mule-loads of earth
"For from now on your servant will not offer burnt offering or sacrifice to any god but the Lord"
He asks pardon: when his master leans on his arm in the house of Rimmon and bows
"When I bow myself in the house of Rimmon, may the Lord pardon your servant"
Elisha says, "Go in peace"
Naaman departs
Gehazi, Elisha's servant, thinks, "My master has spared this Naaman, in not accepting what he brought"
"As the Lord lives, I will run after him and get something from him"
Gehazi pursues Naaman
Naaman sees someone running after him and alights from the chariot
"Is all well?"
Gehazi says all is well, but Elisha has sent him
"Two young men of the sons of the prophets have just come to me from the hill country of Ephraim"
"Please give them a talent of silver and two changes of clothing"
Naaman urges him to accept two talents
He binds two talents in two bags with two changes of clothing
He lays them on two of his servants who carry them before Gehazi
When Gehazi comes to the hill, he takes them and hides them in the house
He dismisses the men
Gehazi enters and stands before Elisha
"Where have you been, Gehazi?"
"Your servant went nowhere"
"Did not my heart go when the man turned from his chariot to meet you?"
"Was it a time to accept money and garments, olive orchards and vineyards, sheep and oxen, male servants and female servants?"
"Therefore the leprosy of Naaman shall cling to you and to your descendants forever"
Gehazi goes out from his presence a leper, as white as snow
The sons of the prophets say to Elisha, "The place where we dwell under your charge is too small for us"
"Let us go to the Jordan and each of us get there a log, and let us make a place for us to dwell there"
Elisha agrees, and at their urging, goes with them
They come to the Jordan and cut down trees
As one is felling a log, his axe head falls into the water
He cries out, "Alas, my master! It was borrowed"
Elisha asks where it fell, and the man shows him the place
Elisha cuts off a stick and throws it there
The iron floats
"Take it up"
He reaches out his hand and takes it
The king of Syria is warring against Israel
He takes counsel with his servants about where to encamp
Elisha warns the king of Israel: "Beware that you do not pass this place"
"For the Syrians are going down there"
The king of Israel sends to the place Elisha told him
Elisha saves him there more than once or twice
The mind of the king of Syria is greatly troubled
He calls his servants and demands to know who is betraying him to Israel
One of his servants tells him, "Elisha the prophet tells the king of Israel the words you speak in your bedroom"
The king commands, "Go and see where he is, that I may send and seize him"
Word comes that Elisha is in Dothan
The king sends horses and chariots and a great army by night
They surround the city
Elisha's servant rises early and goes out
He sees the army with horses and chariots all around the city
"Alas, my master! What shall we do?"
"Do not be afraid, for those who are with us are more than those who are with them"
Elisha prays, "O Lord, please open his eyes that he may see"
The Lord opens the young man's eyes
He sees the mountain full of horses and chariots of fire all around Elisha
The Syrians come down against Elisha
Elisha prays, "Please strike this people with blindness"
The Lord strikes them with blindness
Elisha tells them, "This is not the way, and this is not the city"
"Follow me, and I will bring you to the man whom you seek"
He leads them to Samaria
When they enter Samaria, Elisha prays, "O Lord, open the eyes of these men, that they may see"
The Lord opens their eyes
They see they are in the midst of Samaria
The king of Israel sees them and asks Elisha, "My father, shall I strike them down?"
"You shall not strike them down"
"Would you strike down those whom you have taken captive with your sword and with your bow?"
"Set bread and water before them, that they may eat and drink and go to their master"
He prepares a great feast for them
When they have eaten and drunk, he sends them away to their master
The Syrians do not come again on raids into the land of Israel
Afterward Ben-hadad king of Syria musters his entire army
He goes up and besieges Samaria
There is a great famine in Samaria as they besiege it
A donkey's head is sold for eighty shekels of silver
A fourth of a kab of dove's dung for five shekels of silver
As the king of Israel is passing by on the wall
A woman cries to him, "Help, my lord, O king!"
"If the Lord will not help you, how shall I help you?"
"From the threshing floor, or from the winepress?"
"What is your trouble?"
"This woman said to me, 'Give your son, that we may eat him today'"
"'And we will eat my son tomorrow'"
"So we boiled my son and ate him"
"And on the next day I said to her, 'Give your son, that we may eat him'"
"But she has hidden her son"
When the king hears the woman's words, he tears his clothes
As he passes by on the wall, the people see he is wearing sackcloth beneath
"May God do so to me and more also, if the head of Elisha the son of Shaphat remains on his shoulders today"
Elisha is sitting in his house, and the elders are sitting with him
The king sends a man ahead
Before the messenger arrives, Elisha says to the elders
"Do you see how this murderer has sent to take off my head?"
"Look, when the messenger comes, shut the door and hold the door fast against him"
"Is not the sound of his master's feet behind him?"
While Elisha is still speaking with them, the messenger comes down to him
The king says, "This trouble is from the Lord!"
"Why should I wait for the Lord any longer?"
Elisha says, "Hear the word of the Lord"
"Thus says the Lord, 'Tomorrow about this time a seah of fine flour shall be sold for a shekel'"
"'And two seahs of barley for a shekel, at the gate of Samaria'"
The captain on whose hand the king leans answers Elisha
"If the Lord himself should make windows in heaven, could this thing be?"
"You shall see it with your own eyes, but you shall not eat of it"
Four men who are lepers are at the entrance to the gate
They say to one another, "Why are we sitting here until we die?"
"If we say, 'Let us enter the city,' the famine is in the city, and we shall die there"
"If we sit here, we die also"
"So now come, let us go over to the camp of the Syrians"
"If they spare our lives we shall live, and if they kill us we shall but die"
They arise at twilight to go to the camp of the Syrians
When they come to the edge of the camp, no one is there
The Lord has made the army of the Syrians hear the sound of chariots and horses
The sound of a great army
They say to one another, "The king of Israel has hired against us the kings of the Hittites and the kings of Egypt to come against us"
They flee in the twilight, abandoning tents, horses, donkeys, and the camp as it is
They flee for their lives
The lepers come to the edge of the camp
They enter a tent, eat and drink
They carry off silver, gold, and clothing and hide them
They return and enter another tent and carry off things from it and hide them
They say to one another, "We are not doing right"
"This day is a day of good news"
"If we are silent and wait until the morning light, punishment will overtake us"
"Now therefore come; let us go and tell the king's household"
They come and call to the gatekeepers of the city
They tell them, "We came to the camp of the Syrians"
"And behold, there was no one to be seen or heard there"
"Nothing but the horses tied and the donkeys tied and the tents as they were"
The gatekeepers call out and tell it within the king's household
The king rises in the night
He says to his servants, "I will tell you what the Syrians have done to us"
"They know that we are hungry"
"Therefore they have gone out of the camp to hide themselves in the open country"
"Thinking, 'When they come out of the city, we shall take them alive'"
"'And get into the city'"
One of his servants answers
"Let some men take five of the remaining horses"
"Seeing that those who are left here will fare like the whole multitude of Israel who have already perished"
"Let us send and see"
They take two horsemen
The king sends them after the army of the Syrians, saying, "Go and see"
They go after them as far as the Jordan
All the way is littered with garments and equipment the Syrians have thrown away in their haste
The messengers return and tell the king
The people go out and plunder the camp of the Syrians
A seah of fine flour is sold for a shekel
Two seahs of barley for a shekel, according to the word of the Lord
The king appoints the captain on whose hand he leans to have charge of the gate
The people trample him in the gate
He dies, as Elisha had said when the king came down to him
It happens as Elisha told him: "Two seahs of barley for a shekel, and a seah of fine flour for a shekel"
"Shall be at the gate of Samaria tomorrow about this time"
The captain had answered, "If the Lord himself should make windows in heaven, could such a thing be?"
Elisha had said, "You shall see it with your own eyes, but you shall not eat of it"
It happens to him, for the people trample him in the gate and he dies
Elisha has said to the woman whose son he restored to life
"Arise, and depart with your household, and sojourn wherever you can"
"For the Lord has called for a famine, and it will come upon the land for seven years"
The woman arises and does according to Elisha's word
She and her household sojourn in the land of the Philistines seven years
At the end of seven years, the woman returns from the land of the Philistines
She goes to appeal to the king for her house and her land
The king is talking with Gehazi the servant of Elisha
"Tell me all the great things that Elisha has done"
While Gehazi is telling the king how Elisha restored the dead to life
The woman whose son Elisha restored to life appeals to the king
Gehazi says, "My lord, O king, here is the woman, and here is her son whom Elisha restored to life"
The king questions the woman, and she tells him
The king appoints an official for her
"Restore all that was hers, together with all the produce of the fields from the day that she left the land until now"
Elisha comes to Damascus
Ben-hadad the king of Syria is sick
It is told him, "The man of God has come here"
The king says to Hazael, "Take a present with you and go to meet the man of God"
"And inquire of the Lord through him, saying, 'Shall I recover from this sickness?'"
Hazael goes to meet Elisha
He takes a present with him, all kinds of goods of Damascus, forty camel loads
He comes and stands before him
"Your son Ben-hadad king of Syria has sent me to you, saying, 'Shall I recover from this sickness?'"
Elisha says to him, "Go, say to him, 'You shall certainly recover'"
"But the Lord has shown me that he shall certainly die"
Elisha fixes his gaze and stares at Hazael until he is ashamed
The man of God weeps
Hazael asks, "Why does my lord weep?"
"Because I know the evil that you will do to the people of Israel"
"You will set on fire their fortresses"
"You will kill their young men with the sword"
"Dash in pieces their little ones"
"And rip open their pregnant women"
Hazael says, "What is your servant, who is but a dog, that he should do this great thing?"
"The Lord has shown me that you are to be king over Syria"
Hazael departs from Elisha and comes to his master
Ben-hadad asks him, "What did Elisha say to you?"
"He told me that you would certainly recover"
On the following day Hazael takes the bed cloth and dips it in water
He spreads it over Ben-hadad's face
Ben-hadad dies
Hazael becomes king in his place
In the fifth year of Joram son of Ahab king of Israel
Jehoram the son of Jehoshaphat king of Judah begins to reign
He is thirty-two years old when he becomes king
He reigns eight years in Jerusalem
He walks in the way of the kings of Israel, as the house of Ahab had done
For the daughter of Ahab is his wife
He does what is evil in the sight of the Lord
Yet the Lord is not willing to destroy Judah, for the sake of David his servant
Since he promised to give a lamp to him and to his sons forever
In his days Edom revolts from the rule of Judah
They set up a king of their own
Jehoram passes over to Zair with all his chariots
He rises by night and strikes the Edomites who have surrounded him
And the captains of the chariots
His army flees home
So Edom revolts from the rule of Judah to this day
Libnah also revolts at the same time
Now the rest of the acts of Jehoram and all that he did, are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Judah?
Jehoram sleeps with his fathers
He is buried with his fathers in the city of David
Ahaziah his son reigns in his place
In the twelfth year of Joram the son of Ahab, king of Israel
Ahaziah the son of Jehoram, king of Judah, begins to reign
Ahaziah is twenty-two years old when he begins to reign
He reigns one year in Jerusalem
His mother's name is Athaliah; she is a granddaughter of Omri king of Israel
He walks in the way of the house of Ahab
He does what is evil in the sight of the Lord, as the house of Ahab had done
For he is son-in-law to the house of Ahab
He goes with Joram the son of Ahab to wage war against Hazael king of Syria at Ramoth-gilead
The Syrians wound Joram
King Joram returns to be healed in Jezreel of the wounds that the Syrians have given him at Ramah
When he fights against Hazael king of Syria
Ahaziah the son of Jehoram king of Judah goes down to see Joram son of Ahab in Jezreel
Because he is wounded
Elisha the prophet calls one of the sons of the prophets
"Tie up your garments, and take this flask of oil in your hand, and go to Ramoth-gilead"
"When you arrive, look there for Jehu the son of Jehoshaphat, son of Nimshi"
"Go in and have him rise from among his fellows, and lead him to an inner chamber"
"Then take the flask of oil and pour it on his head and say"
"'Thus says the Lord, I anoint you king over Israel'"
"Then open the door and flee; do not linger"
The young man, the servant of the prophet, goes to Ramoth-gilead
When he comes, the commanders of the army are in council
He says, "I have a word for you, O commander"
Jehu asks, "To which of us all?"
"To you, O commander"
Jehu rises and goes into the house
The young man pours the oil on his head
"Thus says the Lord, the God of Israel, I anoint you king over the people of the Lord, over Israel"
"You shall strike down the house of Ahab your master"
"So that I may avenge on Jezebel the blood of my servants the prophets"
"And the blood of all the servants of the Lord"
"For the whole house of Ahab shall perish"
"I will cut off from Ahab every male, bond or free, in Israel"
"I will make the house of Ahab like the house of Jeroboam the son of Nebat"
"And like the house of Baasha the son of Ahijah"
"The dogs shall eat Jezebel in the territory of Jezreel, and none shall bury her"
Then he opens the door and flees
Jehu comes out to the servants of his master
They say to him, "Is all well? Why did this mad fellow come to you?"
"You know the fellow and his talk"
"That is not true; tell us now"
"Thus and so he spoke to me, saying, 'Thus says the Lord, I anoint you king over Israel'"
Then they hurry and each takes his garment and puts it under him on the bare steps
They blow the trumpet and proclaim, "Jehu is king"
Jehu the son of Jehoshaphat the son of Nimshi conspires against Joram
Now Joram with all Israel has been on guard at Ramoth-gilead against Hazael king of Syria
But King Joram has returned to be healed in Jezreel of the wounds that the Syrians have given him
When he fights with Hazael king of Syria
Jehu says, "If this is your decision, then let no one slip out of the city to go and tell the news in Jezreel"
Jehu mounts his chariot and goes to Jezreel
For Joram is lying there
Ahaziah king of Judah has come down to visit Joram
The watchman standing on the tower in Jezreel spies the company of Jehu as he comes
"I see a company"
Joram says, "Take a horseman and send to meet them, and let him say, 'Is it peace?'"
A man on horseback goes to meet him
"Thus says the king, 'Is it peace?'"
"What do you have to do with peace? Turn around and ride behind me"
The watchman reports, "The messenger reached them, but he is not coming back"
He sends out a second horseman
He comes to them and says, "Thus the king has said, 'Is it peace?'"
"What do you have to do with peace? Turn around and ride behind me"
The watchman reports, "He reached them, but he is not coming back"
"And the driving is like the driving of Jehu the son of Nimshi, for he drives furiously"
Joram says, "Make ready"
They make ready his chariot
Joram king of Israel and Ahaziah king of Judah set out
Each in his chariot
They set out to meet Jehu
They meet him at the property of Naboth the Jezreelite
When Joram sees Jehu, he says, "Is it peace, Jehu?"
"What peace can there be, so long as the whorings and the sorceries of your mother Jezebel are so many?"
Joram reins about and flees
He says to Ahaziah, "Treachery, O Ahaziah!"
Jehu draws his bow with his full strength
He shoots Joram between the shoulders
The arrow pierces his heart
Jehu sinks in his chariot
Jehu says to Bidkar his aide, "Take him up and throw him on the plot of ground belonging to Naboth the Jezreelite"
"For remember, when you and I rode side by side behind Ahab his father"
"How the Lord made this pronouncement against him"
"'As surely as I saw yesterday the blood of Naboth and the blood of his sons, declares the Lord'"
"'I will repay you on this plot of ground, in accordance with the word of the Lord'"
They take him up and throw him on the plot of ground, in accordance with the word of the Lord
When Ahaziah the king of Judah sees this, he flees in the direction of Beth-haggan
Jehu pursues him
"Shoot him also"
They shoot him in the chariot at the ascent of Gur, which is by Ibleam
He flees to Megiddo and dies there
His servants carry him in a chariot to Jerusalem
They bury him in his tomb with his fathers in the city of David
In the eleventh year of Joram the son of Ahab, Ahaziah begins to reign over Judah
When Jehu comes to Jezreel, Jezebel hears of it
She paints her eyes and adorns her head
She looks out of the window
As Jehu enters the gate, she says, "Is it peace, you Zimri, murderer of your master?"
Jehu looks up to the window
"Who is on my side? Who?"
Two or three eunuchs look out at him
"Throw her down"
They throw her down
Some of her blood spatters on the wall and on the horses
They trample on her
Jehu goes in and eats and drinks
"See now to this cursed woman and bury her, for she is a king's daughter"
They go to bury her
They find no more of her than the skull and the feet and the palms of her hands
They come back and tell him
"This is the word of the Lord, which he spoke by his servant Elijah the Tishbite"
"'In the territory of Jezreel the dogs shall eat the flesh of Jezebel'"
"'And the corpse of Jezebel shall be as dung on the face of the field in the territory of Jezreel'"
"'So that no one can say, This is Jezebel'"
Ahab has seventy sons in Samaria
Jehu writes letters and sends them to Samaria
To the rulers of the city, to the elders, and to the guardians of the sons of Ahab
"Now then, as soon as this letter reaches you, seeing your master's sons are with you"
"And there are with you chariots and horses, fortified cities, and weapons"
"Select the best and fittest of your master's sons and set him on his father's throne and fight for your master's house"
They are exceedingly afraid
"Behold, the two kings could not stand before him. How then can we stand?"
The steward of the palace, and he who is over the city, together with the elders and the guardians, send to Jehu
"We are your servants, and we will do all that you tell us"
"We will not make anyone king. Do whatever is good in your eyes"
He writes to them a second letter
"If you are on my side, and if you are ready to obey me, take the heads of your master's sons and come to me at Jezreel tomorrow at this time"
Now the king's sons, seventy persons, are with the great men of the city, who are bringing them up
When the letter comes to them, they take the king's sons and slaughter them, seventy persons
They put their heads in baskets and send them to him at Jezreel
When the messenger comes and tells him, "They have brought the heads of the king's sons"
He says, "Lay them in two heaps at the entrance of the gate until the morning"
In the morning, when he goes out, he stands and says to all the people
"You are innocent. It was I who conspired against my master and killed him"
"But who struck down all these?"
"Know then that there shall fall to the earth nothing of the word of the Lord"
"Which the Lord spoke concerning the house of Ahab"
"For the Lord has done what he said by his servant Elijah"
Jehu strikes down all who remain of the house of Ahab in Jezreel
All his great men and his close friends and his priests
Until he leaves him none remaining
He sets out and goes to Samaria
On the way, when he is at Beth-eked of the Shepherds
Jehu meets the relatives of Ahaziah king of Judah
"Who are you?"
"We are the relatives of Ahaziah, and we came down to visit the royal princes and the sons of the queen mother"
"Take them alive"
They take them alive and slaughter them at the pit of Beth-eked, forty-two persons
He spares none of them
When he departs from there, he meets Jehonadab the son of Rechab coming to meet him
He greets him and says to him, "Is your heart true to my heart as mine is to yours?"
Jehonadab answers, "It is"
Jehu says, "If it is, give me your hand"
Jehonadab gives him his hand
Jehu takes him up with him into the chariot
"Come with me, and see my zeal for the Lord"
They have him ride in his chariot
When he comes to Samaria, he strikes down all who remain to Ahab in Samaria
Till he has wiped them out, according to the word of the Lord that he spoke to Elijah
Jehu assembles all the people
"Ahab served Baal a little, but Jehu will serve him much"
"Now therefore call to me all the prophets of Baal, all his worshipers and all his priests"
"Let none be missing, for I have a great sacrifice to offer to Baal"
"Whoever is missing shall not live"
Jehu does it with cunning in order to destroy the worshipers of Baal
Jehu orders, "Sanctify a solemn assembly for Baal"
They proclaim it
Jehu sends throughout all Israel
All the worshipers of Baal come, so that there is not a man left who does not come
They enter the house of Baal
The house of Baal is filled from one end to the other
He says to him who is in charge of the wardrobe, "Bring out the vestments for all the worshipers of Baal"
He brings out the vestments for them
Jehu goes into the house of Baal with Jehonadab the son of Rechab
He says to the worshipers of Baal, "Search, and see that there is no servant of the Lord here among you"
"But only the worshipers of Baal"
They go in to offer sacrifices and burnt offerings
Jehu has stationed eighty men outside
"The man who allows any of those whom I give into your hands to escape shall forfeit his life"
As soon as he has made an end of offering the burnt offering
Jehu says to the guard and to the officers, "Go in and strike them down; let not a man escape"
They strike them down with the edge of the sword
The guard and the officers cast them out
They go into the inner room of the house of Baal
They bring out the pillar that is in the house of Baal and burn it
They demolish the pillar of Baal
They demolish the house of Baal
They make it a latrine to this day
Thus Jehu wipes out Baal from Israel
But Jehu does not turn aside from the sins of Jeroboam the son of Nebat
Which he makes Israel to sin
The golden calves that are in Bethel and in Dan
The Lord says to Jehu, "Because you have done well in carrying out what is right in my eyes"
"And have done to the house of Ahab according to all that was in my heart"
"Your sons of the fourth generation shall sit on the throne of Israel"
But Jehu is not careful to walk in the law of the Lord, the God of Israel, with all his heart
He does not turn from the sins of Jeroboam, which he makes Israel to sin
In those days the Lord begins to cut off parts of Israel
Hazael defeats them throughout the territory of Israel
From the Jordan eastward, all the land of Gilead, the Gadites, the Reubenites, and the Manassites
From Aroer, which is by the Valley of the Arnon, that is, Gilead and Bashan
Now the rest of the acts of Jehu and all that he did and all his might, are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Israel?
Jehu sleeps with his fathers
They bury him in Samaria
Jehoahaz his son reigns in his place
The time that Jehu reigns over Israel in Samaria is twenty-eight years
When Athaliah the mother of Ahaziah sees that her son is dead
She arises and destroys all the royal family
But Jehosheba, the daughter of King Joram, sister of Ahaziah, takes Joash the son of Ahaziah
She steals him away from among the king's sons who are being put to death
She puts him and his nurse in a bedroom
Thus they hide him from Athaliah, so that he is not put to death
He remains with her six years, hidden in the house of the Lord
While Athaliah reigns over the land
In the seventh year Jehoiada sends and brings the captains of the Carites and of the guards
He has them come to him in the house of the Lord
He makes a covenant with them and puts them under oath in the house of the Lord
He shows them the king's son
He commands them, "This is the thing that you shall do"
"One third of you, those who come off duty on the Sabbath and guard the king's house"
"Another third being at the gate Sur and a third at the gate behind the guards"
"Shall guard the palace"
"And the two divisions of you, which come on duty in force on the Sabbath and guard the house of the Lord on behalf of the king"
"Shall surround the king, each with his weapons in his hand"
"And whoever approaches the ranks is to be put to death"
"Be with the king when he goes out and when he comes in"
The captains do according to all that Jehoiada the priest commands
Each brings his men who are to go off duty on the Sabbath, with those who are to come on duty on the Sabbath
They come to Jehoiada the priest
The priest gives to the captains the spears and shields that have been King David's
Which are in the house of the Lord
The guards stand, every man with his weapons in his hand
From the south side of the house to the north side of the house, around the altar and the house on behalf of the king
He brings out the king's son and puts the crown on him and gives him the testimony
They proclaim him king and anoint him
They clap their hands and say, "Long live the king!"
When Athaliah hears the noise of the guard and of the people
She goes into the house of the Lord to the people
She looks, and there is the king standing by the pillar, according to the custom
With the captains and the trumpeters beside the king
All the people of the land rejoicing and blowing trumpets
Athaliah tears her clothes and cries, "Treason! Treason!"
Jehoiada the priest commands the captains who are set over the army
"Bring her out between the ranks, and put to death with the sword anyone who follows her"
For the priest says, "Let her not be put to death in the house of the Lord"
They lay hands on her
She goes through the horses' entrance to the king's house
She is put to death there
Jehoiada makes a covenant between the Lord and the king and people
That they should be the Lord's people
Also between the king and the people
All the people of the land go to the house of Baal and tear it down
His altars and his images they break in pieces
They kill Mattan the priest of Baal before the altars
The priest posts watchmen over the house of the Lord
He takes the captains, the Carites, the guards, and all the people of the land
They bring the king down from the house of the Lord
Marching through the gate of the guards to the king's house
He takes his seat on the throne of the kings
All the people of the land rejoice
The city is quiet after Athaliah has been put to death with the sword at the king's house
Jehoash is seven years old when he begins to reign
In the seventh year of Jehu, Jehoash begins to reign
He reigns forty years in Jerusalem
His mother's name is Zibiah of Beersheba
Jehoash does what is right in the eyes of the Lord all his days
Because Jehoiada the priest instructs him
Nevertheless, the high places are not taken away
The people continue to sacrifice and make offerings on the high places
Jehoash says to the priests, "All the money of the holy things that is brought into the house of the Lord"
"The money for which each man is assessed, the money from the assessment of persons"
"And the money that a man's heart prompts him to bring into the house of the Lord"
"Let the priests take, each from his donor, and let them repair the house wherever any need of repairs is discovered"
By the twenty-third year of King Jehoash, the priests have made no repairs on the house
King Jehoash summons Jehoiada the priest and the other priests
"Why are you not repairing the house? Now therefore take no more money from your donors"
"But hand it over for the repair of the house"
The priests agree that they should take no more money from the people
And that they should not repair the house
Jehoiada the priest takes a chest and bores a hole in the lid
He sets it beside the altar on the right side as one enters the house of the Lord
The priests who guard the threshold put in it all the money that is brought into the house of the Lord
Whenever they see that there is much money in the chest
The king's secretary and the high priest come up and they count and tie up in bags the money that is found in the house of the Lord
They give the money that is weighed out into the hands of the workmen who have the oversight of the house of the Lord
They pay it out to the carpenters and the builders who work on the house of the Lord
And to the masons and the stonecutters
As well as to buy timber and quarried stone for making repairs on the house of the Lord
And for any outlay for the repairs of the house
But there are not made for the house of the Lord basins of silver, snuffers, bowls, trumpets, or any vessels of gold, or of silver
From the money that is brought into the house of the Lord
For that is given to the workmen who are repairing the house of the Lord with it
They do not ask for an accounting from the men into whose hand they deliver the money to pay out to the workmen
For they deal honestly
The money from the guilt offerings and the money from the sin offerings is not brought into the house of the Lord
It belongs to the priests
At that time Hazael king of Syria goes up and fights against Gath and takes it
Hazael sets his face to go up against Jerusalem
Jehoash king of Judah takes all the sacred gifts that Jehoshaphat and Jehoram and Ahaziah his fathers, the kings of Judah, have dedicated
And his own sacred gifts, and all the gold that is found in the treasuries of the house of the Lord and of the king's house
He sends these to Hazael king of Syria
Hazael withdraws from Jerusalem
Now the rest of the acts of Joash and all that he did, are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Judah?
His servants arise and make a conspiracy
They strike down Joash in the house of Millo, on the way that goes down to Silla
It is Jozacar the son of Shimeath and Jehozabad the son of Shomer, his servants, who strike him down
So that he dies
They bury him with his fathers in the city of David
Amaziah his son reigns in his place
In the twenty-third year of Joash the son of Ahaziah, king of Judah
Jehoahaz the son of Jehu begins to reign over Israel in Samaria
He reigns seventeen years
He does what is evil in the sight of the Lord
He follows the sins of Jeroboam the son of Nebat, which he makes Israel to sin
He does not depart from them
The anger of the Lord is kindled against Israel
He gives them continually into the hand of Hazael king of Syria
And into the hand of Ben-hadad the son of Hazael
Jehoahaz entreats the favor of the Lord
The Lord listens to him
For he sees the oppression of Israel, how the king of Syria oppresses them
Therefore the Lord gives Israel a savior, so that they escape from the hand of the Syrians
The people of Israel dwell in their homes as formerly
Nevertheless, they do not depart from the sins of the house of Jeroboam, which he makes Israel to sin
They walk in them
The Asherah also remains in Samaria
For there is not left to Jehoahaz an army of more than fifty horsemen and ten chariots and ten thousand footmen
For the king of Syria has destroyed them and made them like the dust at threshing
Now the rest of the acts of Jehoahaz and all that he did, and his might, are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Israel?
Jehoahaz sleeps with his fathers
They bury him in Samaria
Joash his son reigns in his place
In the thirty-seventh year of Joash king of Judah
Jehoash the son of Jehoahaz begins to reign over Israel in Samaria
He reigns sixteen years
He does what is evil in the sight of the Lord
He does not depart from all the sins of Jeroboam the son of Nebat, which he makes Israel to sin
He walks in them
Now the rest of the acts of Joash and all that he did, and the might with which he fought against Amaziah king of Judah
Are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Israel?
Joash sleeps with his fathers
Jeroboam sits on his throne
Joash is buried in Samaria with the kings of Israel
Elisha becomes sick with the illness of which he is to die
Joash king of Israel goes down to him and weeps before him
"My father, my father! The chariots of Israel and its horsemen!"
Elisha says to him, "Take a bow and arrows"
He takes a bow and arrows
Then he says to the king of Israel, "Draw the bow"
He draws it
Elisha lays his hands on the king's hands
He says, "Open the window eastward"
He opens it
Elisha says, "Shoot"
He shoots
"The Lord's arrow of victory, the arrow of victory over Syria!"
"For you shall fight the Syrians in Aphek until you have made an end of them"
"Take the arrows"
He takes them
He says to the king of Israel, "Strike the ground with them"
He strikes three times and stops
The man of God is angry with him
"You should have struck five or six times"
"Then you would have struck down Syria until you had made an end of it"
"But now you will strike down Syria only three times"
Elisha dies
They bury him
Now bands of Moabites used to invade the land in the spring of the year
As a man is being buried, behold, a marauding band is seen
The man is thrown into the grave of Elisha
As soon as the man touches the bones of Elisha, he revives
He stands on his feet
Hazael king of Syria oppresses Israel all the days of Jehoahaz
But the Lord is gracious to them and has compassion on them
He turns toward them, because of his covenant with Abraham, Isaac, and Jacob
He is not willing to destroy them
He has not cast them from his presence until now
When Hazael king of Syria dies, Ben-hadad his son becomes king in his place
Jehoash the son of Jehoahaz takes again from Ben-hadad the son of Hazael the cities that he had taken from Jehoahaz his father in war
Three times Joash defeats him and recovers the cities of Israel
In the second year of Joash the son of Joahaz, king of Israel
Amaziah the son of Joash, king of Judah, begins to reign
He is twenty-five years old when he begins to reign
He reigns twenty-nine years in Jerusalem
His mother's name is Jehoaddin of Jerusalem
He does what is right in the eyes of the Lord
Yet not like David his father
He does in all things as Joash his father had done
But the high places are not removed
The people still sacrifice and make offerings on the high places
As soon as the royal power is firmly in his hand
He strikes down his servants who have struck down the king his father
But he does not put to death the children of the murderers
According to what is written in the Book of the Law of Moses, where the Lord commands
"Fathers shall not be put to death because of their children"
"Nor shall children be put to death because of their fathers"
"But each one shall die for his own sin"
He strikes down ten thousand Edomites in the Valley of Salt
He takes Sela by storm
He calls it Joktheel, which is its name to this day
Amaziah sends messengers to Jehoash the son of Jehoahaz, son of Jehu, king of Israel
"Come, let us look one another in the face"
Jehoash king of Israel sends word to Amaziah king of Judah
"A thistle on Lebanon sent to a cedar on Lebanon, saying"
"'Give your daughter to my son for a wife'"
"And a wild beast of Lebanon passed by and trampled down the thistle"
"You have indeed struck down Edom, and your heart has lifted you up"
"Be content with your glory, and stay at home"
"For why should you provoke trouble so that you fall, you and Judah with you?"
Amaziah will not listen
Jehoash king of Israel goes up
He and Amaziah king of Judah face one another in battle at Beth-shemesh, which belongs to Judah
Judah is defeated by Israel
Every man flees to his home
Jehoash king of Israel captures Amaziah king of Judah, the son of Jehoash, son of Ahaziah, at Beth-shemesh
He comes to Jerusalem and breaks down the wall of Jerusalem for four hundred cubits
From the Ephraim Gate to the Corner Gate
He seizes all the gold and silver, and all the vessels that are found in the house of the Lord and in the treasuries of the king's house
Also hostages
He returns to Samaria
Now the rest of the acts of Jehoash that he did, and his might, and how he fought with Amaziah king of Judah
Are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Israel?
Jehoash sleeps with his fathers
He is buried in Samaria with the kings of Israel
Jeroboam his son reigns in his place
Amaziah the son of Joash, king of Judah, lives fifteen years after the death of Jehoash son of Jehoahaz, king of Israel
Now the rest of the deeds of Amaziah, are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Judah?
They make a conspiracy against him in Jerusalem
He flees to Lachish
They send after him to Lachish and put him to death there
They bring him on horses
He is buried in Jerusalem with his fathers in the city of David
All the people of Judah take Azariah, who is sixteen years old
They make him king instead of his father Amaziah
He builds Elath and restores it to Judah
After the king sleeps with his fathers
In the fifteenth year of Amaziah the son of Joash, king of Judah
Jeroboam the son of Joash, king of Israel, begins to reign in Samaria
He reigns forty-one years
He does what is evil in the sight of the Lord
He does not depart from all the sins of Jeroboam the son of Nebat, which he makes Israel to sin
He restores the border of Israel from Lebo-hamath as far as the Sea of the Arabah
According to the word of the Lord, the God of Israel
Which he spoke by his servant Jonah the son of Amittai, the prophet, who is from Gath-hepher
For the Lord sees that the affliction of Israel is very bitter
For there is none left, bond or free, and there is none to help Israel
The Lord has not said that he will blot out the name of Israel from under heaven
So he saves them by the hand of Jeroboam the son of Joash
Now the rest of the acts of Jeroboam and all that he did, and his might
How he fought, and how he restored Damascus and Hamath to Judah in Israel
Are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Israel?
Jeroboam sleeps with his fathers, the kings of Israel
Zechariah his son reigns in his place
In the twenty-seventh year of Jeroboam king of Israel
Azariah the son of Amaziah, king of Judah, begins to reign
He is sixteen years old when he begins to reign
He reigns fifty-two years in Jerusalem
His mother's name is Jecoliah of Jerusalem
He does what is right in the eyes of the Lord, according to all that his father Amaziah had done
Nevertheless, the high places are not taken away
The people still sacrifice and make offerings on the high places
The Lord touches the king, so that he is a leper to the day of his death
He lives in a separate house
Jotham the king's son is over the household, governing the people of the land
Now the rest of the acts of Azariah, and all that he did, are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Judah?
Azariah sleeps with his fathers
They bury him with his fathers in the city of David
Jotham his son reigns in his place
In the thirty-eighth year of Azariah king of Judah
Zechariah the son of Jeroboam reigns over Israel in Samaria six months
He does what is evil in the sight of the Lord, as his fathers had done
He does not depart from the sins of Jeroboam the son of Nebat, which he makes Israel to sin
Shallum the son of Jabesh conspires against him
He strikes him down at Ibleam and puts him to death
He reigns in his place
Now the rest of the deeds of Zechariah, behold, they are written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Israel
This is the promise of the Lord that he gave to Jehu
"Your sons shall sit on the throne of Israel to the fourth generation"
And so it comes to pass
Shallum the son of Jabesh begins to reign in the thirty-ninth year of Uzziah king of Judah
He reigns one month in Samaria
Menahem the son of Gadi comes up from Tirzah
He comes to Samaria and strikes down Shallum the son of Jabesh in Samaria
He puts him to death and reigns in his place
Now the rest of the deeds of Shallum, and the conspiracy that he made
Behold, they are written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Israel
At that time Menahem sacks Tiphsah and all who are in it and its territory from Tirzah on
Because they do not open it to him
Therefore he sacks it, and he rips open all the women in it who are pregnant
In the thirty-ninth year of Azariah king of Judah
Menahem the son of Gadi begins to reign over Israel
He reigns ten years in Samaria
He does what is evil in the sight of the Lord
He does not depart all his days from the sins of Jeroboam the son of Nebat, which he makes Israel to sin
Pul the king of Assyria comes against the land
Menahem gives Pul a thousand talents of silver
That he may help him to confirm his hold on the royal power
Menahem exacts the money from Israel, from all the wealthy men
Fifty shekels of silver from every man, to give to the king of Assyria
The king of Assyria turns back
He does not stay there in the land
Now the rest of the deeds of Menahem and all that he did, are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Israel?
Menahem sleeps with his fathers
Pekahiah his son reigns in his place
In the fiftieth year of Azariah king of Judah
Pekahiah the son of Menahem begins to reign over Israel in Samaria
He reigns two years
He does what is evil in the sight of the Lord
He does not turn away from the sins of Jeroboam the son of Nebat, which he makes Israel to sin
Pekah the son of Remaliah, his captain, conspires against him with fifty men of the people of Gilead
He strikes him down in Samaria, in the citadel of the king's house with Argob and Arieh
He puts him to death and reigns in his place
Now the rest of the deeds of Pekahiah and all that he did
Behold, they are written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Israel
In the fifty-second year of Azariah king of Judah
Pekah the son of Remaliah begins to reign over Israel in Samaria
He reigns twenty years
He does what is evil in the sight of the Lord
He does not depart from the sins of Jeroboam the son of Nebat, which he makes Israel to sin
In the days of Pekah king of Israel
Tiglath-pileser king of Assyria comes
He captures Ijon, Abel-beth-maacah, Janoah, Kedesh, Hazor, Gilead, and Galilee
All the land of Naphtali
He carries the people captive to Assyria
Hoshea the son of Elah makes a conspiracy against Pekah the son of Remaliah
He strikes him down and puts him to death
He reigns in his place, in the twentieth year of Jotham the son of Uzziah
Now the rest of the acts of Pekah and all that he did
Behold, they are written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Israel
In the second year of Pekah the son of Remaliah, king of Israel
Jotham the son of Uzziah, king of Judah, begins to reign
He is twenty-five years old when he begins to reign
He reigns sixteen years in Jerusalem
His mother's name is Jerusha the daughter of Zadok
He does what is right in the eyes of the Lord, according to all that his father Uzziah had done
Nevertheless, the high places are not removed
The people still sacrifice and make offerings on the high places
He builds the upper gate of the house of the Lord
Now the rest of the acts of Jotham and all that he did, are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Judah?
In those days the Lord begins to send Rezin the king of Syria and Pekah the son of Remaliah against Judah
Jotham sleeps with his fathers
He is buried with his fathers in the city of David his father
Ahaz his son reigns in his place
In the seventeenth year of Pekah the son of Remaliah
Ahaz the son of Jotham, king of Judah, begins to reign
Ahaz is twenty years old when he begins to reign
He reigns sixteen years in Jerusalem
He does not do what is right in the eyes of the Lord his God, as his father David had done
He walks in the way of the kings of Israel
He even burns his son as an offering, according to the despicable practices of the nations
Whom the Lord drove out before the people of Israel
He sacrifices and makes offerings on the high places and on the hills and under every green tree
Rezin king of Syria and Pekah the son of Remaliah, king of Israel, come up to wage war on Jerusalem
They besiege Ahaz but cannot conquer him
At that time Rezin the king of Syria recovers Elath for Syria
He drives the men of Judah from Elath
The Edomites come to Elath, where they dwell to this day
Ahaz sends messengers to Tiglath-pileser king of Assyria
"I am your servant and your son. Come up and rescue me from the hand of the king of Syria"
"And from the hand of the king of Israel, who are attacking me"
Ahaz also takes the silver and gold that is found in the house of the Lord
And in the treasures of the king's house
He sends a present to the king of Assyria
The king of Assyria listens to him
The king of Assyria marches up against Damascus and takes it
Carrying its people captive to Kir
He puts Rezin to death
King Ahaz goes to Damascus to meet Tiglath-pileser king of Assyria
When he sees the altar that is at Damascus
King Ahaz sends to Uriah the priest a model of the altar, and its pattern, exact in all its details
Uriah the priest builds the altar
In accordance with all that King Ahaz has sent from Damascus
Uriah the priest makes it, before King Ahaz arrives from Damascus
When the king comes from Damascus, the king views the altar
The king approaches the altar and goes up on it
He burns his burnt offering and his grain offering
He pours his drink offering and throws the blood of his peace offerings on the altar
The bronze altar that is before the Lord he removes from the front of the house
From the place between his altar and the house of the Lord
He puts it on the north side of his altar
King Ahaz commands Uriah the priest
"On the great altar burn the morning burnt offering and the evening grain offering"
"And the king's burnt offering and his grain offering, with the burnt offering of all the people of the land"
"And their grain offering and their drink offering"
"And throw on it all the blood of the burnt offering and all the blood of the sacrifice"
"But the bronze altar shall be for me to inquire by"
Uriah the priest does all this, as King Ahaz commands
King Ahaz cuts off the frames of the stands
He removes the basin from them
He takes down the sea from off the bronze oxen that are under it
He puts it on a stone pedestal
The covered way for the Sabbath that has been built inside the house
And the outer entrance for the king he removes from the house of the Lord
Because of the king of Assyria
Now the rest of the acts of Ahaz that he did, are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Judah?
Ahaz sleeps with his fathers
He is buried with his fathers in the city of David
Hezekiah his son reigns in his place
In the twelfth year of Ahaz king of Judah
Hoshea the son of Elah begins to reign in Samaria over Israel
He reigns nine years
He does what is evil in the sight of the Lord
Yet not as the kings of Israel who are before him
Shalmaneser king of Assyria comes up against him
Hoshea becomes his vassal and pays him tribute
The king of Assyria finds treachery in Hoshea
For he has sent messengers to So, king of Egypt
He offers no tribute to the king of Assyria, as he had done year by year
Therefore the king of Assyria shuts him up and binds him in prison
The king of Assyria invades all the land
He comes to Samaria
He besieges it for three years
In the ninth year of Hoshea, the king of Assyria captures Samaria
He carries Israel away to Assyria
He places them in Halah, and on the Habor, the river of Gozan, and in the cities of the Medes
This occurs because the people of Israel have sinned against the Lord their God
Who brought them up out of the land of Egypt from under the hand of Pharaoh king of Egypt
They fear other gods
They walk in the customs of the nations whom the Lord drove out before the people of Israel
And in the customs that the kings of Israel have practiced
The people of Israel do secretly against the Lord their God things that are not right
They build for themselves high places in all their towns
From watchtower to fortified city
They set up for themselves pillars and Asherim on every high hill and under every green tree
There they make offerings on all the high places, as the nations do whom the Lord carries away before them
They do wicked things, provoking the Lord to anger
They serve idols, of which the Lord has said to them, "You shall not do this"
Yet the Lord warns Israel and Judah by every prophet and every seer
"Turn from your evil ways and keep my commandments and my statutes"
"In accordance with all the Law that I commanded your fathers"
"And that I sent to you by my servants the prophets"
They do not listen but are stubborn, as their fathers had been
Who do not believe in the Lord their God
They despise his statutes and his covenant that he makes with their fathers
And the warnings that he gives them
They go after false idols and become false
They follow the nations that are around them
Concerning whom the Lord has commanded them that they should not do like them
They forsake all the commandments of the Lord their God
They make for themselves metal images of two calves
They make an Asherah
They worship all the host of heaven
They serve Baal
They burn their sons and their daughters as offerings
They use divination and omens
They sell themselves to do evil in the sight of the Lord, provoking him to anger
Therefore the Lord is very angry with Israel
He removes them out of his sight
None is left but the tribe of Judah only
Judah also does not keep the commandments of the Lord their God
They walk in the customs that Israel has practiced
The Lord rejects all the descendants of Israel
He afflicts them and gives them into the hand of plunderers
Until he has cast them out of his sight
When he has torn Israel from the house of David
They make Jeroboam the son of Nebat king
Jeroboam drives Israel from following the Lord
He makes them commit great sin
The people of Israel walk in all the sins that Jeroboam does
They do not depart from them
Until the Lord removes Israel out of his sight, as he has spoken by all his servants the prophets
So Israel is exiled from their own land to Assyria to this day
The king of Assyria brings people from Babylon, Cuthah, Avva, Hamath, and Sepharvaim
He places them in the cities of Samaria instead of the people of Israel
They take possession of Samaria and dwell in its cities
When they first dwell there, they do not fear the Lord
Therefore the Lord sends lions among them, which kill some of them
The king of Assyria is told
"The nations that you have carried away and placed in the cities of Samaria do not know the law of the god of the land"
"Therefore he has sent lions among them, and behold, they are killing them"
"Because they do not know the law of the god of the land"
The king of Assyria commands
"Send there one of the priests whom you carried away from there"
"Let him go and dwell there and teach them the law of the god of the land"
One of the priests whom they have carried away from Samaria comes and dwells in Bethel
He teaches them how they should fear the Lord
But every nation still makes gods of its own
They put them in the shrines of the high places that the Samaritans have made
Every nation in the cities in which they dwell
The men of Babylon make Succoth-benoth
The men of Cuth make Nergal
The men of Hamath make Ashima
The Avvites make Nibhaz and Tartak
The Sepharvites burn their children in the fire to Adrammelech and Anammelech
The gods of Sepharvaim
They also fear the Lord
They appoint from among themselves all sorts of people as priests of the high places
Who sacrifice for them in the shrines of the high places
So they fear the Lord but also serve their own gods
After the manner of the nations from among whom they have been carried away
To this day they do according to the former manner
They do not fear the Lord
They do not follow the statutes or the rules or the law or the commandment that the Lord commanded the children of Jacob
Whom he named Israel
The Lord makes a covenant with them and commands them
"You shall not fear other gods or bow yourselves to them or serve them or sacrifice to them"
"But you shall fear the Lord, who brought you out of the land of Egypt with great power and with an outstretched arm"
"You shall bow yourselves to him, and to him you shall sacrifice"
"And the statutes and the rules and the law and the commandment that he wrote for you"
"You shall always be careful to do"
"You shall not fear other gods"
"And you shall not forget the covenant that I have made with you"
"You shall not fear other gods"
"But you shall fear the Lord your God"
"And he will deliver you out of the hand of all your enemies"
However, they do not listen
They do according to their former manner
So these nations fear the Lord and also serve their carved images
Their children do likewise, and their children's children
As their fathers did, so they do to this day
In the third year of Hoshea son of Elah, king of Israel
Hezekiah the son of Ahaz, king of Judah, begins to reign
He is twenty-five years old when he begins to reign
He reigns twenty-nine years in Jerusalem
His mother's name is Abi the daughter of Zechariah
He does what is right in the eyes of the Lord, according to all that David his father has done
He removes the high places and breaks the pillars and cuts down the Asherah
He breaks in pieces the bronze serpent that Moses has made
For until those days the people of Israel have made offerings to it
It is called Nehushtan
He trusts in the Lord, the God of Israel
So that there is none like him among all the kings of Judah after him
Nor among those who are before him
He holds fast to the Lord
He does not depart from following him
He keeps the commandments that the Lord commanded Moses
The Lord is with him
Wherever he goes out, he prospers
He rebels against the king of Assyria and will not serve him
He strikes down the Philistines as far as Gaza and its territory
From watchtower to fortified city
In the fourth year of King Hezekiah, which is the seventh year of Hoshea son of Elah, king of Israel
Shalmaneser king of Assyria comes up against Samaria and besieges it
At the end of three years they take it
In the sixth year of Hezekiah, which is the ninth year of Hoshea king of Israel, Samaria is taken
The king of Assyria carries the Israelites away to Assyria
He puts them in Halah, and on the Habor, the river of Gozan, and in the cities of the Medes
Because they do not obey the voice of the Lord their God
But transgress his covenant, even all that Moses the servant of the Lord commanded
They neither listen nor obey
In the fourteenth year of King Hezekiah
Sennacherib king of Assyria comes up against all the fortified cities of Judah and takes them
Hezekiah king of Judah sends to the king of Assyria at Lachish
"I have done wrong; withdraw from me. Whatever you impose on me I will bear"
The king of Assyria requires of Hezekiah king of Judah three hundred talents of silver and thirty talents of gold
Hezekiah gives him all the silver that is found in the house of the Lord
And in the treasuries of the king's house
At that time Hezekiah strips the gold from the doors of the temple of the Lord
And from the doorposts that Hezekiah king of Judah has overlaid
He gives it to the king of Assyria
The king of Assyria sends the Tartan, the Rab-saris, and the Rabshakeh with a great army from Lachish to King Hezekiah at Jerusalem
They go up and come to Jerusalem
When they arrive, they come and stand by the conduit of the upper pool
Which is on the highway to the Washer's Field
When they call for the king
There come out to them Eliakim the son of Hilkiah, who is over the household
And Shebnah the secretary, and Joah the son of Asaph, the recorder
The Rabshakeh says to them
"Say to Hezekiah, 'Thus says the great king, the king of Assyria'"
"'What is this confidence that you have?'"
"'Do you think that mere words are strategy and power for war?'"
"'In whom do you now trust, that you have rebelled against me?'"
"'Behold, you are trusting now in Egypt, that broken reed of a staff'"
"'Which will pierce the hand of any man who leans on it'"
"'Such is Pharaoh king of Egypt to all who trust in him'"
"'But if you say to me, "We trust in the Lord our God"'"
"'Is it not he whose high places and altars Hezekiah has removed'"
"'Saying to Judah and to Jerusalem, "You shall worship before this altar in Jerusalem"?'"
"'Come now, make a wager with my master the king of Assyria'"
"'I will give you two thousand horses, if you are able on your part to set riders on them'"
"'How then can you repulse a single captain among the least of my master's servants'"
"'When you trust in Egypt for chariots and for horsemen?'"
"'Moreover, is it without the Lord that I have come up against this place to destroy it?'"
"'The Lord said to me, "Go up against this land and destroy it"'"
Eliakim the son of Hilkiah, and Shebnah, and Joah, say to the Rabshakeh
"Please speak to your servants in Aramaic, for we understand it"
"Do not speak to us in the language of Judah within the hearing of the people who are on the wall"
The Rabshakeh says to them
"Has my master sent me to speak these words to your master and to you"
"And not to the men sitting on the wall"
"Who are doomed with you to eat their own dung and to drink their own urine?"
The Rabshakeh stands and calls out in a loud voice in the language of Judah
"Hear the word of the great king, the king of Assyria!"
"Thus says the king: 'Do not let Hezekiah deceive you'"
"'For he will not be able to deliver you out of my hand'"
"'Do not let Hezekiah make you trust in the Lord by saying'"
"'"The Lord will surely deliver us, and this city will not be given into the hand of the king of Assyria"'"
"'Do not listen to Hezekiah'"
"'For thus says the king of Assyria'"
"'"Make your peace with me and come out to me'"
"'"Then each one of you will eat of his own vine, and each one of his own fig tree'"
"'"And each one of you will drink the water of his own cistern'"
"'"Until I come and take you away to a land like your own land'"
"'"A land of grain and wine, a land of bread and vineyards'"
"'"A land of olive trees and honey, that you may live, and not die'"
"'"And do not listen to Hezekiah when he misleads you by saying, 'The Lord will deliver us'"'"
"'Has any of the gods of the nations ever delivered his land out of the hand of the king of Assyria?'"
"'Where are the gods of Hamath and Arpad?'"
"'Where are the gods of Sepharvaim, Hena, and Ivvah?'"
"'Have they delivered Samaria out of my hand?'"
"'Who among all the gods of the lands have delivered their lands out of my hand'"
"'That the Lord should deliver Jerusalem out of my hand?'"
The people are silent and answer him not a word
For the king's command is, "Do not answer him"
Eliakim the son of Hilkiah, who is over the household, and Shebna the secretary, and Joah the son of Asaph, the recorder, come to Hezekiah
With their clothes torn
They tell him the words of the Rabshakeh
As soon as King Hezekiah hears it, he tears his clothes
He covers himself with sackcloth and goes into the house of the Lord
He sends Eliakim, who is over the household, and Shebna the secretary, and the senior priests
Covered with sackcloth, to the prophet Isaiah the son of Amoz
They say to him, "Thus says Hezekiah"
