"'This day is a day of distress, of rebuke, and of disgrace'"
"'Children have come to the point of birth, and there is no strength to bring them forth'"
"'It may be that the Lord your God will hear all the words of the Rabshakeh'"
"'Whom his master the king of Assyria has sent to mock the living God'"
"'And will rebuke the words that the Lord your God has heard'"
"'Therefore lift up your prayer for the remnant that is left'"
When the servants of King Hezekiah come to Isaiah
Isaiah says to them, "Say to your master"
"'Thus says the Lord: Do not be afraid because of the words that you have heard'"
"'With which the young men of the king of Assyria have reviled me'"
"'Behold, I will put a spirit in him, so that he shall hear a rumor and return to his own land'"
"'And I will make him fall by the sword in his own land'"
The Rabshakeh returns and finds the king of Assyria fighting against Libnah
For he hears that the king has left Lachish
Now the king hears concerning Tirhakah king of Cush
"Behold, he has set out to fight against you"
He sends messengers again to Hezekiah
"Thus shall you speak to Hezekiah king of Judah"
"'Do not let your God in whom you trust deceive you by promising that Jerusalem will not be given into the hand of the king of Assyria'"
"'Behold, you have heard what the kings of Assyria have done to all lands'"
"'Devoting them to destruction'"
"'And shall you be delivered?'"
"'Have the gods of the nations delivered them'"
"'The nations that my fathers destroyed, Gozan, Haran, Rezeph, and the people of Eden who were in Telassar?'"
"'Where is the king of Hamath, the king of Arpad, the king of the city of Sepharvaim, the king of Hena, or the king of Ivvah?'"
Hezekiah receives the letter from the hand of the messengers and reads it
Hezekiah goes up to the house of the Lord
He spreads it before the Lord
Hezekiah prays before the Lord
"O Lord, the God of Israel, enthroned above the cherubim"
"You are the God, you alone, of all the kingdoms of the earth"
"You have made heaven and earth"
"Incline your ear, O Lord, and hear"
"Open your eyes, O Lord, and see"
"And hear the words of Sennacherib, which he has sent to mock the living God"
"Truly, O Lord, the kings of Assyria have laid waste the nations and their lands"
"And have cast their gods into the fire"
"For they were not gods, but the work of men's hands, wood and stone"
"Therefore they were destroyed"
"So now, O Lord our God, save us, please, from his hand"
"That all the kingdoms of the earth may know that you, O Lord, are God alone"
Isaiah the son of Amoz sends to Hezekiah
"Thus says the Lord, the God of Israel"
"'Your prayer to me about Sennacherib king of Assyria I have heard'"
"This is the word that the Lord has spoken concerning him"
"'She despises you, she scorns you, the virgin daughter of Zion'"
"'She wags her head behind you, the daughter of Jerusalem'"
"'Whom have you mocked and reviled?'"
"'Against whom have you raised your voice and lifted your eyes to the heights?'"
"'Against the Holy One of Israel!'"
"'By your messengers you have mocked the Lord'"
"'And you have said, "With my many chariots I have gone up the heights of the mountains'"
"'"To the far recesses of Lebanon'"
"'"I felled its tallest cedars, its choicest cypresses'"
"'"I entered its farthest lodging place, its most fruitful forest'"
"'"I dug wells and drank foreign waters'"
"'"I dried up with the sole of my foot all the streams of Egypt"'"
"'Have you not heard that I determined it long ago?'"
"'I planned from days of old what now I bring to pass'"
"'That you should turn fortified cities into heaps of ruins'"
"'While their inhabitants, shorn of strength, are dismayed and confounded'"
"'And have become like plants of the field and like tender grass'"
"'Like grass on the housetops, blighted before it is grown'"
"'But I know your sitting down and your going out and coming in'"
"'And your raging against me'"
"'Because you have raged against me and your complacency has come into my ears'"
"'I will put my hook in your nose and my bit in your mouth'"
"'And I will turn you back on the way by which you came'"
"'And this shall be the sign for you: this year you shall eat what grows of itself'"
"'And in the second year what springs of the same'"
"'Then in the third year sow and reap and plant vineyards, and eat their fruit'"
"'And the surviving remnant of the house of Judah shall again take root downward and bear fruit upward'"
"'For out of Jerusalem shall go a remnant, and out of Mount Zion a band of survivors'"
"'The zeal of the Lord will do this'"
"'Therefore thus says the Lord concerning the king of Assyria'"
"'He shall not come into this city or shoot an arrow there'"
"'Or come before it with a shield or cast up a siege mound against it'"
"'By the way that he came, by the same he shall return'"
"'And he shall not come into this city, declares the Lord'"
"'For I will defend this city to save it, for my own sake and for the sake of my servant David'"
That very night the angel of the Lord goes out
He strikes down 185,000 in the camp of the Assyrians
When people arise early in the morning, behold, these are all dead bodies
Sennacherib king of Assyria departs and goes home
He dwells at Nineveh
As he is worshiping in the house of Nisroch his god
Adrammelech and Sharezer, his sons, strike him down with the sword
They escape into the land of Ararat
Esarhaddon his son reigns in his place
In those days Hezekiah becomes sick and is at the point of death
Isaiah the prophet the son of Amoz comes to him
"Thus says the Lord, 'Set your house in order, for you shall die; you shall not recover'"
Hezekiah turns his face to the wall and prays to the Lord
"Now, O Lord, please remember how I have walked before you in faithfulness and with a whole heart"
"And have done what is good in your sight"
Hezekiah weeps bitterly
Before Isaiah has gone out of the middle court, the word of the Lord comes to him
"Turn back, and say to Hezekiah the leader of my people"
"'Thus says the Lord, the God of David your father'"
"'"I have heard your prayer; I have seen your tears'"
"'"Behold, I will heal you. On the third day you shall go up to the house of the Lord'"
"'"And I will add fifteen years to your life'"
"'"I will deliver you and this city out of the hand of the king of Assyria'"
"'"And I will defend this city for my own sake and for my servant David's sake"'"
Isaiah says, "Bring a cake of figs"
They take and lay it on the boil
He recovers
Hezekiah says to Isaiah, "What shall be the sign that the Lord will heal me"
"And that I shall go up to the house of the Lord on the third day?"
Isaiah says, "This shall be the sign to you from the Lord, that the Lord will do the thing that he has promised"
"Shall the shadow go forward ten steps, or go back ten steps?"
Hezekiah answers, "It is an easy thing for the shadow to lengthen ten steps"
"Rather let the shadow go back ten steps"
Isaiah the prophet calls to the Lord
He brings the shadow back ten steps, by which it has gone down on the steps of Ahaz
At that time Merodach-baladan the son of Baladan, king of Babylon, sends envoys with letters and a present to Hezekiah
For he hears that Hezekiah has been sick
Hezekiah welcomes them
He shows them all his treasure house, the silver, the gold, the spices, the precious oil, his armory
All that is found in his storehouses
There is nothing in his house or in all his realm that Hezekiah does not show them
Isaiah the prophet comes to King Hezekiah
"What did these men say? And from where did they come to you?"
Hezekiah says, "They have come from a far country, from Babylon"
"What have they seen in your house?"
"They have seen all that is in my house"
"There is nothing in my storehouses that I did not show them"
Isaiah says to Hezekiah, "Hear the word of the Lord"
"'Behold, the days are coming, when all that is in your house'"
"'And that which your fathers have stored up till this day, shall be carried to Babylon'"
"'Nothing shall be left, says the Lord'"
"'And some of your own sons, who shall be born to you, shall be taken away'"
"'And they shall be eunuchs in the palace of the king of Babylon'"
Hezekiah says to Isaiah, "The word of the Lord that you have spoken is good"
For he thinks, "Why not, if there will be peace and security in my days?"
The rest of the deeds of Hezekiah and all his might and how he made the pool and the conduit
And brought water into the city, are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Judah?
Hezekiah sleeps with his fathers
Manasseh his son reigns in his place
Manasseh is twelve years old when he begins to reign
He reigns fifty-five years in Jerusalem
His mother's name is Hephzibah
He does what is evil in the sight of the Lord
According to the despicable practices of the nations whom the Lord drove out before the people of Israel
He rebuilds the high places that Hezekiah his father has destroyed
He erects altars for Baal and makes an Asherah, as Ahab king of Israel had done
He worships all the host of heaven and serves them
He builds altars in the house of the Lord
Of which the Lord has said, "In Jerusalem will I put my name"
He builds altars for all the host of heaven in the two courts of the house of the Lord
He burns his son as an offering
He practices soothsaying and augury
He deals with mediums and with necromancers
He does much evil in the sight of the Lord, provoking him to anger
The carved image of Asherah that he has made he sets in the house
Of which the Lord said to David and to Solomon his son
"In this house, and in Jerusalem, which I have chosen out of all the tribes of Israel"
"I will put my name forever"
"And I will not cause the feet of Israel to wander anymore out of the land that I gave to their fathers"
"If only they will be careful to do according to all that I have commanded them"
"And according to all the Law that my servant Moses commanded them"
They do not listen
Manasseh misleads them to do more evil than the nations had done whom the Lord destroyed before the people of Israel
The Lord says by his servants the prophets
"Because Manasseh king of Judah has committed these abominations"
"And has done things more evil than all that the Amorites did, who were before him"
"And has made Judah also to sin with his idols"
"Therefore thus says the Lord, the God of Israel"
"'Behold, I am bringing upon Jerusalem and Judah such disaster'"
"'That the ears of everyone who hears of it will tingle'"
"'And I will stretch over Jerusalem the measuring line of Samaria'"
"'And the plumb line of the house of Ahab'"
"'And I will wipe Jerusalem as one wipes a dish, wiping it and turning it upside down'"
"'And I will forsake the remnant of my heritage'"
"'And give them into the hand of their enemies'"
"'And they shall become a prey and a spoil to all their enemies'"
"'Because they have done what is evil in my sight'"
"'And have provoked me to anger, since the day their fathers came out of Egypt, even to this day'"
Moreover, Manasseh sheds very much innocent blood
Till he has filled Jerusalem from one end to another
Besides the sin that he makes Judah to sin
So that they do what is evil in the sight of the Lord
Now the rest of the acts of Manasseh and all that he did, and the sin that he committed
Are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Judah?
Manasseh sleeps with his fathers
He is buried in the garden of his house, in the garden of Uzza
Amon his son reigns in his place
Amon is twenty-two years old when he begins to reign
He reigns two years in Jerusalem
His mother's name is Meshullemeth the daughter of Haruz of Jotbah
He does what is evil in the sight of the Lord, as Manasseh his father had done
He walks in all the way in which his father walked
He serves the idols that his father served and worships them
He forsakes the Lord, the God of his fathers
He does not walk in the way of the Lord
The servants of Amon conspire against him
They put the king to death in his house
But the people of the land strike down all those who have conspired against King Amon
The people of the land make Josiah his son king in his place
Now the rest of the acts of Amon that he did, are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Judah?
He is buried in his tomb in the garden of Uzza
Josiah his son reigns in his place
Josiah is eight years old when he begins to reign
He reigns thirty-one years in Jerusalem
His mother's name is Jedidah the daughter of Adaiah of Bozkath
He does what is right in the eyes of the Lord
He walks in all the way of David his father
He does not turn aside to the right or to the left
In the eighteenth year of King Josiah, the king sends Shaphan the son of Azaliah, son of Meshullam, the secretary, to the house of the Lord
"Go up to Hilkiah the high priest, that he may count the money that has been brought into the house of the Lord"
"Which the keepers of the threshold have collected from the people"
"And let it be given into the hand of the workmen who have the oversight of the house of the Lord"
"And let them give it to the workmen who are at the house of the Lord, repairing the house"
"That is, to the carpenters, and to the builders, and to the masons"
"And let them use it for buying timber and quarried stone to repair the house"
"But no accounting shall be asked from them for the money that is delivered into their hand"
"For they deal honestly"
Hilkiah the high priest says to Shaphan the secretary
"I have found the Book of the Law in the house of the Lord"
Hilkiah gives the book to Shaphan, and he reads it
Shaphan the secretary comes to the king and reports to the king
"Your servants have emptied out the money that was found in the house"
"And have delivered it into the hand of the workmen who have the oversight of the house of the Lord"
Shaphan the secretary tells the king, "Hilkiah the priest has given me a book"
Shaphan reads it before the king
When the king hears the words of the Book of the Law, he tears his clothes
The king commands Hilkiah the priest, and Ahikam the son of Shaphan, and Achbor the son of Micaiah, and Shaphan the secretary, and Asaiah the king's servant
"Go, inquire of the Lord for me, and for the people, and for all Judah"
"Concerning the words of this book that has been found"
"For great is the wrath of the Lord that is kindled against us"
"Because our fathers have not obeyed the words of this book"
"To do according to all that is written concerning us"
Hilkiah the priest, and Ahikam, and Achbor, and Shaphan, and Asaiah go to Huldah the prophetess
The wife of Shallum the son of Tikvah, son of Harhas, keeper of the wardrobe
Now she dwells in Jerusalem in the Second Quarter
They speak to her
She says to them, "Thus says the Lord, the God of Israel"
"'Tell the man who sent you to me'"
"'Thus says the Lord, Behold, I will bring disaster upon this place and upon its inhabitants'"
"'All the words of the book that the king of Judah has read'"
"'Because they have forsaken me and have made offerings to other gods'"
"'That they might provoke me to anger with all the work of their hands'"
"'Therefore my wrath will be kindled against this place, and it will not be quenched'"
"'But to the king of Judah, who sent you to inquire of the Lord, thus shall you say to him'"
"'Thus says the Lord, the God of Israel: Regarding the words that you have heard'"
"'"Because your heart was penitent, and you humbled yourself before the Lord'"
"'"When you heard how I spoke against this place and against its inhabitants'"
"'"That they should become a desolation and a curse'"
"'"And you have torn your clothes and wept before me, I also have heard you, declares the Lord'"
"'"Therefore, behold, I will gather you to your fathers'"
"'"And you shall be gathered to your grave in peace'"
"'"And your eyes shall not see all the disaster that I will bring upon this place"'"
They bring back word to the king
The king sends, and all the elders of Judah and Jerusalem are gathered to him
The king goes up to the house of the Lord
And with him all the men of Judah and all the inhabitants of Jerusalem and the priests and the prophets
All the people, both small and great
He reads in their hearing all the words of the Book of the Covenant that has been found in the house of the Lord
The king stands by the pillar and makes a covenant before the Lord
To walk after the Lord and to keep his commandments and his testimonies and his statutes with all his heart and all his soul
To perform the words of this covenant that are written in this book
All the people join in the covenant
The king commands Hilkiah the high priest and the priests of the second order and the keepers of the threshold
To bring out of the temple of the Lord all the vessels made for Baal, for Asherah, and for all the host of heaven
He burns them outside Jerusalem in the fields of the Kidron
He carries their ashes to Bethel
He deposes the priests whom the kings of Judah have ordained to make offerings in the high places
At the cities of Judah and around Jerusalem
Those also who make offerings to Baal, to the sun and the moon and the constellations and all the host of the heavens
He brings out the Asherah from the house of the Lord, outside Jerusalem, to the brook Kidron
He burns it at the brook Kidron and beats it to dust
He casts the dust of it upon the graves of the common people
He breaks down the houses of the male cult prostitutes who are in the house of the Lord
Where the women weave hangings for the Asherah
He brings all the priests out of the cities of Judah
He defiles the high places where the priests have made offerings, from Geba to Beersheba
He breaks down the high places of the gates that are at the entrance of the gate of Joshua the governor of the city
Which are on one's left at the gate of the city
However, the priests of the high places do not come up to the altar of the Lord in Jerusalem
But they eat unleavened bread among their brothers
He defiles Topheth, which is in the Valley of the Son of Hinnom
That no one might burn his son or his daughter as an offering to Molech
He removes the horses that the kings of Judah have dedicated to the sun
At the entrance to the house of the Lord, by the chamber of Nathan-melech the chamberlain, which is in the precincts
He burns the chariots of the sun with fire
The altars on the roof of the upper chamber of Ahaz, which the kings of Judah have made
And the altars that Manasseh has made in the two courts of the house of the Lord
The king breaks down and beats them down from there
He casts their dust into the brook Kidron
The king defiles the high places that are east of Jerusalem
To the south of the mount of corruption, which Solomon the king of Israel has built for Ashtoreth the abomination of the Sidonians
And for Chemosh the abomination of Moab, and for Milcom the abomination of the Ammonites
He breaks in pieces the pillars and cuts down the Asherim
He fills their places with the bones of men
Moreover, the altar at Bethel, the high place erected by Jeroboam the son of Nebat, who makes Israel to sin
That altar and the high place he pulls down
He burns the high place and crushes it to dust
He burns the Asherah
As Josiah turns, he sees the tombs there on the mount
He sends and takes the bones out of the tombs
He burns them on the altar and defiles it
According to the word of the Lord that the man of God proclaimed, who had predicted these things
"What is that monument that I see?"
The men of the city tell him, "It is the tomb of the man of God who came from Judah"
"And predicted these things that you have done against the altar at Bethel"
"Let him be; let no man move his bones"
So they let his bones alone, with the bones of the prophet who came out of Samaria
Josiah also removes all the shrines of the high places that are in the cities of Samaria
Which kings of Israel have made, provoking the Lord to anger
He does to them according to all that he has done at Bethel
He sacrifices all the priests of the high places who are there, on the altars
He burns human bones on them
Then he returns to Jerusalem
The king commands all the people, "Keep the Passover to the Lord your God, as it is written in this Book of the Covenant"
For no such Passover has been kept since the days of the judges who judged Israel
Or during all the days of the kings of Israel or of the kings of Judah
But in the eighteenth year of King Josiah this Passover is kept to the Lord in Jerusalem
Moreover, Josiah puts away the mediums and the necromancers and the household gods and the idols
And all the abominations that are seen in the land of Judah and in Jerusalem
That he may establish the words of the law that are written in the book that Hilkiah the priest finds in the house of the Lord
Before him there is no king like him, who turns to the Lord with all his heart and with all his soul and with all his might
According to all the Law of Moses
Nor does any like him arise after him
Still the Lord does not turn from the burning of his great wrath
By which his anger is kindled against Judah, because of all the provocations with which Manasseh has provoked him
The Lord says, "I will remove Judah also out of my sight, as I have removed Israel"
"And I will cast off this city that I have chosen, Jerusalem, and the house of which I said, 'My name shall be there'"
Now the rest of the acts of Josiah and all that he did, are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Judah?
In his days Pharaoh Neco king of Egypt goes up to the king of Assyria to the river Euphrates
King Josiah goes to meet him
Pharaoh Neco kills him at Megiddo, as soon as he sees him
His servants carry him dead in a chariot from Megiddo
They bring him to Jerusalem and bury him in his own tomb
The people of the land take Jehoahaz the son of Josiah
They anoint him and make him king in his father's place
Jehoahaz is twenty-three years old when he begins to reign
He reigns three months in Jerusalem
His mother's name is Hamutal the daughter of Jeremiah of Libnah
He does what is evil in the sight of the Lord, according to all that his fathers had done
Pharaoh Neco puts him in bonds at Riblah in the land of Hamath
That he might not reign in Jerusalem
He laid on the land a tribute of a hundred talents of silver and a talent of gold
Pharaoh Neco makes Eliakim the son of Josiah king in the place of Josiah his father
He changes his name to Jehoiakim
He takes Jehoahaz away, and he comes to Egypt and dies there
Jehoiakim gives the silver and the gold to Pharaoh
He taxes the land to give the money according to the command of Pharaoh
He exacts the silver and the gold of the people of the land, from everyone according to his assessment, to give it to Pharaoh Neco
Jehoiakim is twenty-five years old when he begins to reign
He reigns eleven years in Jerusalem
His mother's name is Zebidah the daughter of Pedaiah of Rumah
He does what is evil in the sight of the Lord, according to all that his fathers had done
In his days, Nebuchadnezzar king of Babylon comes up
Jehoiakim becomes his servant for three years
Then he turns and rebels against him
The Lord sends against him bands of the Chaldeans and bands of the Syrians and bands of the Moabites and bands of the Ammonites
He sends them against Judah to destroy it
According to the word of the Lord that he spoke by his servants the prophets
Surely this comes upon Judah at the command of the Lord
To remove them out of his sight, for the sins of Manasseh, according to all that he has done
And also for the innocent blood that he has shed
For he fills Jerusalem with innocent blood
The Lord is not willing to pardon
Now the rest of the deeds of Jehoiakim and all that he did, are they not written in the Book of the Chronicles of the Kings of Judah?
Jehoiakim sleeps with his fathers
Jehoiachin his son reigns in his place
The king of Egypt does not come again out of his land
For the king of Babylon has taken all that belonged to the king of Egypt from the Brook of Egypt to the river Euphrates
Jehoiachin is eighteen years old when he becomes king
He reigns three months in Jerusalem
His mother's name is Nehushta the daughter of Elnathan of Jerusalem
He does what is evil in the sight of the Lord, according to all that his father had done
At that time the servants of Nebuchadnezzar king of Babylon come up to Jerusalem
The city is besieged
Nebuchadnezzar king of Babylon comes to the city while his servants are besieging it
Jehoiachin king of Judah gives himself up to the king of Babylon
Himself and his mother and his servants and his officials and his palace officials
The king of Babylon takes him prisoner in the eighth year of his reign
He carries off all the treasures of the house of the Lord
And the treasures of the king's house
He cuts in pieces all the vessels of gold in the temple of the Lord, which Solomon king of Israel has made
As the Lord had foretold
He carries away all Jerusalem and all the officials and all the mighty men of valor, 10,000 captives
And all the craftsmen and the smiths
None remain, except the poorest people of the land
He carries away Jehoiachin to Babylon
The king's mother, the king's wives, his officials, and the chief men of the land
He takes them into captivity from Jerusalem to Babylon
The king of Babylon brings captive to Babylon all the men of valor, 7,000
And the craftsmen and the metal workers, 1,000
All of them strong and fit for war
The king of Babylon makes Mattaniah, Jehoiachin's uncle, king in his place
He changes his name to Zedekiah
Zedekiah is twenty-one years old when he becomes king
He reigns eleven years in Jerusalem
His mother's name is Hamutal the daughter of Jeremiah of Libnah
He does what is evil in the sight of the Lord, according to all that Jehoiakim had done
For because of the anger of the Lord it comes to the point in Jerusalem and Judah that he casts them out from his presence
Zedekiah rebels against the king of Babylon
In the ninth year of his reign, in the tenth month, on the tenth day of the month
Nebuchadnezzar king of Babylon comes with all his army against Jerusalem
He lays siege to it
They build siegeworks all around it
The city is besieged till the eleventh year of King Zedekiah
On the ninth day of the fourth month the famine is so severe in the city
That there is no food for the people of the land
A breach is made in the city
All the men of war flee by night by the way of the gate between the two walls
By the king's garden, though the Chaldeans are around the city
They go in the direction of the Arabah
The army of the Chaldeans pursues the king
They overtake him in the plains of Jericho
All his army is scattered from him
They capture the king
They bring him up to the king of Babylon at Riblah
They pass sentence on him
They slaughter the sons of Zedekiah before his eyes
They put out the eyes of Zedekiah
They bind him in chains
They bring him to Babylon
In the fifth month, on the seventh day of the month
That is the nineteenth year of King Nebuchadnezzar, king of Babylon
Nebuzaradan, the captain of the bodyguard, a servant of the king of Babylon, comes to Jerusalem
He burns the house of the Lord and the king's house and all the houses of Jerusalem
Every great house he burns down
All the army of the Chaldeans, who are with the captain of the guard, break down the walls around Jerusalem
Nebuzaradan the captain of the guard carries into exile the rest of the people who are left in the city
And the deserters who have deserted to the king of Babylon
Together with the rest of the multitude
The captain of the guard leaves some of the poorest of the land to be vinedressers and plowmen
The pillars of bronze that are in the house of the Lord, and the stands and the bronze sea that are in the house of the Lord
The Chaldeans break in pieces and carry the bronze to Babylon
They take away the pots and the shovels and the snuffers and the dishes for incense
And all the vessels of bronze used in the temple service
The fire pans also and the bowls
What is of gold the captain of the guard takes away as gold
And what is of silver, as silver
As for the two pillars, the one sea, and the stands that Solomon has made for the house of the Lord
The bronze of all these vessels is beyond weight
The height of the one pillar is eighteen cubits
And on it is a capital of bronze
The height of the capital is three cubits
A latticework and pomegranates, all of bronze, are on the capital all around
The second pillar has the same, with the latticework
The captain of the guard takes Seraiah the chief priest and Zephaniah the second priest
And the three keepers of the threshold
From the city he takes an officer who has been in command of the men of war
And five men of the king's council who are found in the city
And the secretary of the commander of the army who musters the people of the land
And sixty men of the people of the land who are found in the city
Nebuzaradan the captain of the guard takes them
He brings them to the king of Babylon at Riblah
The king of Babylon strikes them down and puts them to death at Riblah in the land of Hamath
So Judah is taken into exile out of its land
Nebuchadnezzar king of Babylon appoints Gedaliah the son of Ahikam, son of Shaphan, governor over the people who remain in the land of Judah
Whom he has left
When all the captains of the forces in the open country and their men hear that the king of Babylon has appointed Gedaliah governor
They come with their men to Gedaliah at Mizpah
Namely, Ishmael the son of Nethaniah, and Johanan the son of Kareah, and Seraiah the son of Tanhumeth the Netophathite, and Jaazaniah the son of the Maacathite
Gedaliah swears to them and their men
"Do not be afraid because of the Chaldean officials. Live in the land and serve the king of Babylon, and it shall be well with you"
But in the seventh month, Ishmael the son of Nethaniah, son of Elishama, of the royal family, comes with ten men
They strike down Gedaliah so that he dies
Along with the Jews and the Chaldeans who are with him at Mizpah
Then all the people, both small and great, and the captains of the forces arise
They go to Egypt, for they are afraid of the Chaldeans
In the thirty-seventh year of the exile of Jehoiachin king of Judah
In the twelfth month, on the twenty-seventh day of the month
Evil-merodach king of Babylon, in the year that he begins to reign, graciously frees Jehoiachin king of Judah from prison
He speaks kindly to him
He sets his throne above the throne of the kings who are with him in Babylon
So Jehoiachin puts off his prison garments
Every day of his life he dines regularly at the king's table
For his allowance, a regular allowance is given him by the king
As long as he lives
Isaiah son of Amoz sees concerning Judah and Jerusalem in the days of Uzziah, Jotham, Ahaz, and Hezekiah, kings of Judah
Isaiah sees the Lord sitting upon a throne, high and lifted up
The train of his robe fills the temple
Seraphim stand above him, each with six wings
One calls to another: "Holy, holy, holy is the Lord of hosts"
"The whole earth is full of his glory"
The foundations of the thresholds shake at the voice
The house is filled with smoke
Isaiah says, "Woe is me! For I am lost"
"For I am a man of unclean lips, and I dwell in the midst of a people of unclean lips"
"For my eyes have seen the King, the Lord of hosts"
One of the seraphim flies to him, having in his hand a burning coal
He has taken it with tongs from the altar
He touches Isaiah's mouth with it
"Behold, this has touched your lips; your guilt is taken away, and your sin atoned for"
Isaiah hears the voice of the Lord saying, "Whom shall I send, and who will go for us?"
"Here I am! Send me"
The Lord says, "Go, and say to this people"
"'Keep on hearing, but do not understand; keep on seeing, but do not perceive'"
"'Make the heart of this people dull, and their ears heavy, and blind their eyes'"
"'Lest they see with their eyes, and hear with their ears'"
"'And understand with their hearts, and turn and be healed'"
Isaiah asks, "How long, O Lord?"
"Until cities lie waste without inhabitant, and houses without people"
"And the land is a desolate waste"
"And the Lord removes people far away, and the forsaken places are many in the midst of the land"
In the year that King Ahaz dies, Isaiah receives this oracle
In the year that the commander in chief, sent by Sargon king of Assyria, comes to Ashdod and fights against it and takes it
The Lord speaks by Isaiah, telling him to loose the sackcloth from his waist and take off his sandals from his feet
Isaiah does so, walking naked and barefoot
The Lord says, "As my servant Isaiah has walked naked and barefoot for three years"
"As a sign and a portent against Egypt and Cush"
"So shall the king of Assyria lead away the Egyptian captives and the Cushite exiles"
"Both the young and the old, naked and barefoot, with buttocks uncovered"
"The nakedness of Egypt"
Isaiah sees a wilderness oracle: a vision of Babylon fallen
"Fallen, fallen is Babylon; and all the carved images of her gods he has shattered to the ground"
Isaiah sees the oracle concerning the valley of vision
He sees chariots with horsemen, and Kir uncovering the shield
Isaiah sees an oracle concerning Tyre
The Lord will lay waste the earth and make it desolate
He will twist its surface and scatter its inhabitants
The earth is utterly broken, the earth is split apart, the earth is violently shaken
The earth staggers like a drunkard
Isaiah prophesies: the Lord will swallow up death forever
He will wipe away tears from all faces
The reproach of his people he will take away from all the earth
It will be said on that day, "Behold, this is our God; we have waited for him"
"Let us be glad and rejoice in his salvation"
Isaiah speaks of a people walking in darkness who have seen a great light
Those dwelling in a land of deep darkness, on them has light shone
For to us a child is born, to us a son is given
The government shall be upon his shoulder
His name shall be called Wonderful Counselor, Mighty God, Everlasting Father, Prince of Peace
Of the increase of his government and of peace there will be no end
On the throne of David and over his kingdom, to establish it and to uphold it
With justice and with righteousness from this time forth and forevermore
Isaiah speaks of a shoot from the stump of Jesse
A branch from his roots shall bear fruit
The Spirit of the Lord shall rest upon him
The spirit of wisdom and understanding, the spirit of counsel and might
The spirit of knowledge and the fear of the Lord
He shall not judge by what his eyes see, or decide disputes by what his ears hear
With righteousness he shall judge the poor
He shall strike the earth with the rod of his mouth
With the breath of his lips he shall kill the wicked
The wolf shall dwell with the lamb, the leopard shall lie down with the young goat
The calf and the lion and the fattened calf together
A little child shall lead them
The nursing child shall play over the hole of the cobra
The weaned child shall put his hand on the adder's den
They shall not hurt or destroy in all my holy mountain
For the earth shall be full of the knowledge of the Lord as the waters cover the sea
In that day the Lord will extend his hand a second time to recover the remnant of his people
He will raise a signal for the nations and will assemble the banished of Israel
He will gather the dispersed of Judah from the four corners of the earth
Isaiah sees the day of the Lord coming, cruel, with wrath and fierce anger
To make the land a desolation and to destroy its sinners from it
The stars of the heavens and their constellations will not give their light
The sun will be dark at its rising, and the moon will not shed its light
Behold, the Lord will empty the earth and make it desolate
He will twist its surface and scatter its inhabitants
Isaiah speaks of new heavens and a new earth
The former things shall not be remembered or come into mind
But be glad and rejoice forever in that which he creates
For behold, he creates Jerusalem to be a joy, and her people to be a gladness
No more shall be heard in it the sound of weeping and the cry of distress
No more shall there be an infant who lives but a few days
Or an old man who does not fill out his days
They shall build houses and inhabit them
They shall plant vineyards and eat their fruit
The wolf and the lamb shall graze together
The lion shall eat straw like the ox
They shall not hurt or destroy in all my holy mountain
Jeremiah son of Hilkiah, of the priests in Anathoth, receives the word of the Lord
In the thirteenth year of Josiah son of Amon, king of Judah
The word of the Lord comes to Jeremiah: "Before I formed you in the womb I knew you"
"Before you were born I consecrated you"
"I appointed you a prophet to the nations"
Jeremiah says, "Ah, Lord God! Behold, I do not know how to speak, for I am only a youth"
The Lord says, "Do not say, 'I am only a youth'"
"For to all to whom I send you, you shall go"
"And whatever I command you, you shall speak"
The Lord puts out his hand and touches Jeremiah's mouth
"Behold, I have put my words in your mouth"
"See, I have set you this day over nations and over kingdoms"
"To pluck up and to break down, to destroy and to overthrow"
"To build and to plant"
The word of the Lord comes to Jeremiah: "What do you see?"
"I see an almond branch"
"You have seen well, for I am watching over my word to perform it"
The word of the Lord comes to him a second time: "What do you see?"
"I see a boiling pot, facing away from the north"
"Out of the north disaster shall be let loose upon all the inhabitants of the land"
"For behold, I am calling all the tribes of the kingdoms of the north"
"They shall come and every one shall set his throne at the entrance of the gates of Jerusalem"
Jeremiah prophesies the destruction of Jerusalem
The Lord tells him to go and proclaim in the hearing of Jerusalem
Jeremiah goes to the house of the potter
He sees the potter working at his wheel
The vessel he is making of clay is spoiled in the potter's hand
He reworks it into another vessel, as it seems good to the potter to do
The word of the Lord comes to Jeremiah
"O house of Israel, can I not do with you as this potter has done?"
"Behold, like the clay in the potter's hand, so are you in my hand, O house of Israel"
The Lord tells Jeremiah to go and buy a potter's earthenware flask
To take some of the elders of the people and some of the elders of the priests
To go out to the Valley of the Son of Hinnom at the entry of the Potsherd Gate
To proclaim there the words the Lord tells him
Jeremiah does so and prophesies disaster
Then he breaks the flask in the sight of the men who go with him
"Thus says the Lord of hosts: So will I break this people and this city"
"As one breaks a potter's vessel, so that it can never be mended"
Pashhur the priest, who is chief officer in the house of the Lord, hears Jeremiah prophesying these things
Pashhur strikes Jeremiah the prophet and puts him in the stocks
The stocks are in the upper Benjamin Gate of the house of the Lord
The next day, when Pashhur releases Jeremiah from the stocks
Jeremiah says to him, "The Lord does not call your name Pashhur, but Terror on Every Side"
"For thus says the Lord: Behold, I will make you a terror to yourself and to all your friends"
"They shall fall by the sword of their enemies while you look on"
"And I will give all Judah into the hand of the king of Babylon"
"He shall carry them captive to Babylon, and shall strike them down with the sword"
King Zedekiah sends Pashhur and Zephaniah the priest to Jeremiah
"Inquire of the Lord for us, for Nebuchadnezzar king of Babylon is making war against us"
"Perhaps the Lord will deal with us according to all his wonderful deeds"
"And will make him withdraw from us"
Jeremiah says to them, "Thus you shall say to Zedekiah"
"'Thus says the Lord, the God of Israel: Behold, I will turn back the weapons of war that are in your hands'"
"'With which you are fighting against the king of Babylon and against the Chaldeans'"
"'Who are besieging you outside the walls'"
"'I will gather them into the midst of this city'"
"'I myself will fight against you with outstretched hand and strong arm'"
"'In anger and in fury and in great wrath'"
The word that comes to Jeremiah from the Lord, when Nebuchadnezzar king of Babylon and all his army fight against Jerusalem
And against all its cities
"Thus says the Lord, the God of Israel: Go and speak to Zedekiah king of Judah"
"'Behold, I am giving this city into the hand of the king of Babylon, and he shall burn it with fire'"
"'You shall not escape from his hand but shall surely be captured and delivered into his hand'"
"'You shall see the king of Babylon eye to eye and speak with him face to face'"
"'And you shall go to Babylon'"
The Lord tells Jeremiah to take a scroll and write on it all the words he has spoken
Concerning Israel and Judah and all the nations
From the day he spoke to him in the days of Josiah until this day
Jeremiah summons Baruch the son of Neriah
Baruch writes on a scroll at the dictation of Jeremiah all the words of the Lord
Jeremiah orders Baruch, "I am banned from going to the house of the Lord"
"So you are to go and read from the scroll that you have written at my dictation"
"The words of the Lord, in the hearing of the people"
In the fifth year of Jehoiakim, in the ninth month
All the people in Jerusalem and all the people who come from the cities of Judah proclaim a fast before the Lord
Baruch reads the words of Jeremiah from the scroll in the house of the Lord
In the chamber of Gemariah the son of Shaphan the secretary, in the upper court
At the entry of the New Gate of the Lord's house, in the hearing of all the people
Micaiah the son of Gemariah hears all the words of the Lord from the scroll
He goes down to the king's house, into the secretary's chamber
All the officials are sitting there
Micaiah tells them all the words he has heard
The officials send Jehudi to Baruch, saying, "Take in your hand the scroll that you read"
"And come"
Baruch takes the scroll in his hand and comes to them
They say to him, "Sit down and read it"
Baruch reads it to them
When they hear all the words, they turn to one another in fear
They say to Baruch, "We must report all these words to the king"
They ask Baruch, "Tell us, please, how did you write all these words? Was it at his dictation?"
Baruch answers them, "He dictated all these words to me, while I wrote them with ink on the scroll"
The officials say to Baruch, "Go and hide, you and Jeremiah, and let no one know where you are"
They go into the court to the king, having put the scroll in the chamber of Elishama the secretary
They report all the words to the king
The king sends Jehudi to get the scroll
Jehudi takes it from the chamber of Elishama the secretary
He reads it to the king and all the officials who stand beside the king
It is the ninth month, and the king is sitting in the winter house
A fire is burning in the fire pot before him
As Jehudi reads three or four columns, the king cuts them off with a knife
He throws them into the fire in the fire pot, until the entire scroll is consumed
Yet neither the king nor any of his servants who hear all these words is afraid
Nor do they tear their garments
Even when Elnathan and Delaiah and Gemariah urge the king not to burn the scroll, he will not listen to them
The king commands Jerahmeel the king's son and Seraiah and Shelemiah to seize Baruch the secretary and Jeremiah the prophet
But the Lord hides them
The word of the Lord comes to Jeremiah after the king has burned the scroll
"Take another scroll and write on it all the former words that were in the first scroll"
"Which Jehoiakim the king of Judah has burned"
Jeremiah takes another scroll and gives it to Baruch the secretary, the son of Neriah
Baruch writes on it at the dictation of Jeremiah all the words of the scroll that Jehoiakim king of Judah has burned in the fire
And many similar words are added to them
Zedekiah sends Jehucal and Zephaniah the priest to Jeremiah
"Please pray for us to the Lord our God"
Now Jeremiah is still going in and out among the people
For he has not yet been put in prison
The army of Pharaoh has come out of Egypt
When the Chaldeans who are besieging Jerusalem hear news of them, they withdraw from Jerusalem
The word of the Lord comes to Jeremiah
"Thus says the Lord, God of Israel: Thus shall you say to the king of Judah who sent you to me to inquire of me"
"'Behold, Pharaoh's army that came to help you is about to return to Egypt'"
"'And the Chaldeans shall come back and fight against this city'"
"'They shall capture it and burn it with fire'"
When the Chaldean army withdraws from Jerusalem at the approach of Pharaoh's army
Jeremiah sets out from Jerusalem to go to the land of Benjamin to receive his portion there among the people
When he is at the Benjamin Gate, a sentry arrests him
"You are deserting to the Chaldeans"
Jeremiah says, "It is a lie; I am not deserting to the Chaldeans"
The sentry will not listen to him
He seizes Jeremiah and brings him to the officials
The officials are enraged at Jeremiah
They strike him and imprison him in the house of Jonathan the secretary
For it has been made a prison
Jeremiah remains many days in the dungeon cells
King Zedekiah sends for him and receives him
The king questions him secretly in his house
"Is there any word from the Lord?"
Jeremiah says, "There is"
"You shall be delivered into the hand of the king of Babylon"
Jeremiah also says to King Zedekiah, "What wrong have I done to you or your servants or this people"
"That you have put me in prison?"
"Where are your prophets who prophesied to you, saying, 'The king of Babylon will not come against you'"
"'And against this land'?"
"Please hear me, my lord the king: let my humble plea come before you"
"Do not send me back to the house of Jonathan the secretary, lest I die there"
King Zedekiah gives orders, and they commit Jeremiah to the court of the guard
They give him a loaf of bread daily from the bakers' street, until all the bread of the city is gone
Jeremiah remains in the court of the guard
Shephatiah, Gedaliah, Jucal, and Pashhur hear the words that Jeremiah is saying to all the people
"Thus says the Lord: He who stays in this city shall die by the sword, by famine, and by pestilence"
"But he who goes out to the Chaldeans shall live"
"He shall have his life as a prize of war, and live"
The officials say to the king, "Let this man be put to death"
"For he is weakening the hands of the soldiers who are left in this city"
"And the hands of all the people, by speaking such words to them"
"For this man is not seeking the welfare of this people, but their harm"
King Zedekiah says, "Behold, he is in your hands"
"For the king can do nothing against you"
They take Jeremiah and cast him into the cistern of Malchiah, the king's son
Which is in the court of the guard
They let Jeremiah down by ropes
There is no water in the cistern, but only mud
Jeremiah sinks in the mud
Ebed-melech the Ethiopian, a eunuch in the king's house, hears that they have put Jeremiah into the cistern
The king is sitting in the Benjamin Gate
Ebed-melech goes from the king's house and says to the king
"My lord the king, these men have done evil in all that they did to Jeremiah the prophet"
"By casting him into the cistern, and he will die there of hunger"
"For there is no bread left in the city"
The king commands Ebed-melech the Ethiopian
"Take thirty men with you from here, and lift Jeremiah the prophet out of the cistern before he dies"
Ebed-melech takes the men with him
He goes to the house of the king, to a wardrobe in the storehouse
He takes from there old rags and worn-out clothes
He lets them down by ropes into the cistern to Jeremiah
Ebed-melech the Ethiopian says to Jeremiah
"Put the rags and clothes between your armpits and the ropes"
Jeremiah does so
They draw Jeremiah up with the ropes and lift him out of the cistern
Jeremiah remains in the court of the guard
King Zedekiah sends for Jeremiah and receives him at the third entrance of the temple of the Lord
The king says to Jeremiah, "I will ask you a question; hide nothing from me"
Jeremiah says to Zedekiah, "If I tell you, will you not surely put me to death?"
"And if I give you counsel, you will not listen to me"
King Zedekiah swears secretly to Jeremiah, "As the Lord lives, who made our souls"
"I will not put you to death or deliver you into the hand of these men who seek your life"
Jeremiah says to Zedekiah, "Thus says the Lord, the God of hosts, the God of Israel"
"'If you will surrender to the officials of the king of Babylon'"
"'Then your life shall be spared, and this city shall not be burned with fire'"
"'And you and your house shall live'"
"'But if you do not surrender to the officials of the king of Babylon'"
"'Then this city shall be given into the hand of the Chaldeans, and they shall burn it with fire'"
"'And you shall not escape from their hand'"
King Zedekiah says to Jeremiah, "I am afraid of the Judeans who have deserted to the Chaldeans"
"Lest I be handed over to them and they abuse me"
Jeremiah says, "You shall not be given to them"
"Obey now the voice of the Lord in what I say to you, and it shall be well with you"
"And your life shall be spared"
"But if you refuse to surrender, this is the vision which the Lord has shown to me"
Zedekiah says to Jeremiah, "Let no one know of these words, and you shall not die"
When the city is broken into, all the officials of the king of Babylon come and sit in the middle gate
Nergal-sharezer, Samgar-nebo, Sarsechim the Rabsaris, Nergal-sharezer the Rabmag, with all the rest of the officers of the king of Babylon
When Zedekiah king of Judah and all the soldiers see them, they flee
They go out of the city at night by way of the king's garden through the gate between the two walls
They go toward the Arabah
The army of the Chaldeans pursues them
They overtake Zedekiah in the plains of Jericho
When they have taken him, they bring him up to Nebuchadnezzar king of Babylon, at Riblah
The king of Babylon passes sentence on him
The king of Babylon slaughters the sons of Zedekiah at Riblah before his eyes
The king of Babylon also slaughters all the nobles of Judah
He puts out the eyes of Zedekiah
He binds him in chains to take him to Babylon
The Chaldeans burn the king's house and the house of the people
They break down the walls of Jerusalem
Nebuzaradan, the captain of the guard, carries into exile to Babylon the rest of the people who are left in the city
Those who have deserted to him, and the people who remain
Nebuzaradan the captain of the guard leaves in the land of Judah some of the poor people who own nothing
He gives them vineyards and fields at the same time
Nebuchadnezzar king of Babylon gives command concerning Jeremiah through Nebuzaradan, the captain of the guard
"Take him, look after him well, and do him no harm"
"But deal with him as he tells you"
Nebuzaradan the captain of the guard, Nebushazban the Rabsaris, Nergal-sharezer the Rabmag send
And all the chief officers of the king of Babylon send
They take Jeremiah from the court of the guard
They entrust him to Gedaliah the son of Ahikam, son of Shaphan, that he should take him home
Jeremiah dwells among the people
The word of the Lord comes to Jeremiah while he is shut up in the court of the guard
"Go, and say to Ebed-melech the Ethiopian"
"'Thus says the Lord of hosts, the God of Israel: Behold, I will fulfill my words against this city for harm and not for good'"
"'And they shall be accomplished before you on that day'"
"'But I will deliver you on that day, declares the Lord'"
"'And you shall not be given into the hand of the men of whom you are afraid'"
"'For I will surely save you, and you shall not fall by the sword'"
"'But you shall have your life as a prize of war, because you have put your trust in me, declares the Lord'"
The word that comes to Jeremiah from the Lord after Nebuzaradan the captain of the guard releases him from Ramah
He had taken him bound in chains along with all the captives of Jerusalem and Judah who are being exiled to Babylon
The captain of the guard takes Jeremiah and says to him
"The Lord your God pronounced this disaster against this place"
"The Lord has brought it about, and has done as he said"
"Because you sinned against the Lord and did not obey his voice, this thing has come upon you"
"Now, behold, I release you today from the chains on your hands"
"If it seems good to you to come with me to Babylon, come"
"And I will look after you well"
"But if it seems wrong to you to come with me to Babylon, do not come"
"See, the whole land is before you; go wherever you think it good and right to go"
Jeremiah goes to Gedaliah the son of Ahikam at Mizpah
He dwells with him among the people who are left in the land
When all the captains of the forces in the open country and their men hear that the king of Babylon has appointed Gedaliah governor in the land
They come with their men to Gedaliah at Mizpah
Gedaliah swears to them and their men
"Do not be afraid to serve the Chaldeans"
"Dwell in the land and serve the king of Babylon, and it shall be well with you"
"As for me, I will dwell at Mizpah, to represent you before the Chaldeans who will come to us"
"But as for you, gather wine and summer fruits and oil, and store them in your vessels"
"And dwell in your cities that you have taken"
Likewise, when all the Judeans who are in Moab and among the Ammonites hear that the king of Babylon has left a remnant in Judah
And has appointed over them Gedaliah the son of Ahikam, son of Shaphan
All the Judeans return from all the places to which they have been driven
They come to the land of Judah, to Gedaliah at Mizpah
They gather wine and summer fruits in great abundance
Johanan the son of Kareah and all the leaders of the forces in the open country come to Gedaliah at Mizpah
They say to him, "Do you know that Baalis the king of the Ammonites has sent Ishmael the son of Nethaniah to take your life?"
But Gedaliah the son of Ahikam will not believe them
Johanan the son of Kareah speaks secretly to Gedaliah at Mizpah
"Please let me go and strike down Ishmael the son of Nethaniah, and no one will know it"
"Why should he take your life, so that all the Judeans who are gathered about you would be scattered"
"And the remnant of Judah would perish?"
Gedaliah the son of Ahikam says to Johanan the son of Kareah
"You shall not do this thing, for you are speaking falsely of Ishmael"
In the seventh month, Ishmael the son of Nethaniah, son of Elishama, of the royal family, comes with ten men to Gedaliah at Mizpah
As they eat bread together there at Mizpah
Ishmael the son of Nethaniah and the ten men with him rise up
They strike down Gedaliah the son of Ahikam, son of Shaphan, with the sword
They kill him, whom the king of Babylon has appointed governor in the land
Ishmael also strikes down all the Judeans who are with Gedaliah at Mizpah
And the Chaldean soldiers who happen to be there
On the day after the murder of Gedaliah, before anyone knows of it
Eighty men arrive from Shechem and Shiloh and Samaria
With their beards shaved and their clothes torn, and their bodies gashed
Bringing grain offerings and incense to present at the temple of the Lord
Ishmael the son of Nethaniah comes out from Mizpah to meet them, weeping as he comes
As he meets them, he says to them, "Come in to Gedaliah the son of Ahikam"
When they come into the city, Ishmael the son of Nethaniah and the men with him slaughter them
They cast them into a cistern
But there are ten men among them who say to Ishmael
"Do not put us to death, for we have stores of wheat, barley, oil, and honey hidden in the fields"
So he does not put them to death with their companions
Now the cistern into which Ishmael casts all the bodies of the men whom he has struck down is the large cistern that King Asa has made
For defense against Baasha king of Israel
Ishmael the son of Nethaniah fills it with the slain
Ishmael takes captive all the rest of the people who are in Mizpah
The king's daughters and all the people who are left at Mizpah
Whom Nebuzaradan, the captain of the guard, has committed to Gedaliah the son of Ahikam
Ishmael the son of Nethaniah takes them captive
He sets out to cross over to the Ammonites
When Johanan the son of Kareah and all the leaders of the forces with him hear of all the evil that Ishmael has done
They take all their men and go to fight against Ishmael
They come upon him at the great pool that is in Gibeon
When all the people who are with Ishmael see Johanan and all the leaders of the forces with him
They are glad
All the people whom Ishmael has carried away captive from Mizpah turn around
They come back and go to Johanan the son of Kareah
But Ishmael the son of Nethaniah escapes from Johanan with eight men
He goes to the Ammonites
Johanan the son of Kareah and all the leaders of the forces with him take from Mizpah all the rest of the people whom he has recovered from Ishmael
After he has struck down Gedaliah the son of Ahikam
Soldiers, women, children, and eunuchs, whom Johanan brings back from Gibeon
They set out and stay at Geruth Chimham near Bethlehem
Intending to go to Egypt
Because of the Chaldeans
For they are afraid of them, because Ishmael has struck down Gedaliah whom the king of Babylon has made governor over the land
All the commanders of the forces, and Johanan and Jezaniah, and all the people from the least to the greatest, come near
They say to Jeremiah the prophet, "Let our plea for mercy come before you"
"And pray to the Lord your God for us, for all this remnant"
"Because we are left with but a few, as your eyes see us"
"That the Lord your God may show us the way we should go, and the thing that we should do"
Jeremiah the prophet says to them, "I have heard you"
"Behold, I will pray to the Lord your God according to your request"
"And whatever the Lord answers you, I will tell you"
"I will keep nothing back from you"
They say to Jeremiah, "May the Lord be a true and faithful witness against us"
"If we do not act according to all the word with which the Lord your God sends you to us"
"Whether it is good or bad, we will obey the voice of the Lord our God to whom we are sending you"
"That it may be well with us when we obey the voice of the Lord our God"
At the end of ten days the word of the Lord comes to Jeremiah
He summons Johanan the son of Kareah and all the commanders of the forces who are with him
And all the people from the least to the greatest
He says to them, "Thus says the Lord, the God of Israel, to whom you sent me"
"'To present your plea for mercy before him'"
"'If you will remain in this land, then I will build you up and not pull you down'"
"'I will plant you, and not pluck you up'"
"'For I relent of the disaster that I did to you'"
"'Do not fear the king of Babylon, of whom you are afraid'"
"'Do not fear him, declares the Lord, for I am with you, to save you and to deliver you from his hand'"
"'I will grant you mercy, that he may have mercy on you and let you remain in your own land'"
"'But if you say, "We will not remain in this land," disobeying the voice of the Lord your God'"
"'And saying, "No, we will go to the land of Egypt, where we shall not see war"'"
"'"Or hear the sound of the trumpet or be hungry for bread, and we will dwell there"'"
"'Then hear the word of the Lord, O remnant of Judah'"
"'Thus says the Lord of hosts, the God of Israel'"
"'"If you set your faces to enter Egypt and go to live there"'"
"'"Then the sword that you fear shall overtake you there in the land of Egypt"'"
"'"And the famine of which you are afraid shall follow close after you to Egypt"'"
"'"And there you shall die"'"
Johanan and all the commanders of the forces and all the people do not obey the voice of the Lord, to remain in the land of Judah
Johanan and all the commanders of the forces take all the remnant of Judah who have returned to live in the land of Judah
From all the nations to which they have been driven
The men, the women, the children, the king's daughters
And every person whom Nebuzaradan the captain of the guard has left with Gedaliah
Also Jeremiah the prophet and Baruch the son of Neriah
They come into the land of Egypt, for they do not obey the voice of the Lord
They arrive at Tahpanhes
The word of the Lord comes to Jeremiah in Tahpanhes
"Take in your hands large stones and hide them in the mortar in the pavement that is at the entrance to Pharaoh's palace in Tahpanhes"
"In the sight of the men of Judah"
"And say to them, 'Thus says the Lord of hosts, the God of Israel'"
"'Behold, I will send and take Nebuchadnezzar the king of Babylon, my servant'"
"'And I will set his throne above these stones that I have hidden'"
"'And he will spread his royal canopy over them'"
Jeremiah does so
Ezekiel the son of Buzi, the priest, receives visions of God by the Chebar canal in the land of the Chaldeans
He is among the exiles
In the thirtieth year, in the fourth month, on the fifth day of the month
As he is among the exiles by the Chebar canal
The heavens open
He sees visions of God
The hand of the Lord is upon him there
He looks, and behold, a stormy wind comes out of the north
A great cloud, with brightness around it, and fire flashing forth continually
In the midst of the fire, as it were gleaming metal
From the midst of it comes the likeness of four living creatures
They have a human likeness
Each has four faces, and each of them has four wings
Their legs are straight, and the soles of their feet are like the sole of a calf's foot
They sparkle like burnished bronze
Under their wings on their four sides they have human hands
The four of them have their faces and their wings thus
Their wings touch one another
Each one of them goes straight forward, without turning as they go
As for the likeness of their faces, each has a human face
The four have the face of a lion on the right side
The four have the face of an ox on the left side
The four have the face of an eagle
Such are their faces
Their wings are spread out above
Each creature has two wings, each of which touches the wing of another
While two cover their bodies
Each goes straight forward
Wherever the spirit would go, they go, without turning as they go
As for the likeness of the living creatures, their appearance is like burning coals of fire
Like the appearance of torches moving to and fro among the living creatures
The fire is bright, and out of the fire goes forth lightning
The living creatures dart to and fro, like the appearance of a flash of lightning
Ezekiel looks at the living creatures
He beholds a wheel on the earth beside the living creatures, one for each of the four of them
As for the appearance of the wheels and their construction
Their appearance is like the gleaming of beryl
The four have the same likeness, their appearance and construction being as it were a wheel within a wheel
When they go, they go in any of their four directions without turning as they go
Their rims are tall and awesome
The rims of all four are full of eyes all around
When the living creatures go, the wheels go beside them
When the living creatures rise from the earth, the wheels rise
Wherever the spirit wants to go, they go
The spirit of the living creatures is in the wheels
Over the heads of the living creatures there is the likeness of an expanse
Shining like awe-inspiring crystal, spread out above their heads
Under the expanse their wings are stretched out straight, one toward another
Each creature has two wings covering its body
When they go, Ezekiel hears the sound of their wings
Like the sound of many waters, like the sound of the Almighty
A sound of tumult like the sound of an army
When they stand still, they let down their wings
There comes a voice from above the expanse over their heads
When they stand still, they let down their wings
Above the expanse over their heads there is the likeness of a throne
In appearance like sapphire
Seated above the likeness of a throne is a likeness with a human appearance
Ezekiel sees from what has the appearance of his waist and upward
Something like the appearance of fire enclosed all around
From what has the appearance of his waist and downward
He sees something like the appearance of fire
There is brightness around him
Like the appearance of the bow that is in the cloud on the day of rain
So is the appearance of the brightness all around
Such is the appearance of the likeness of the glory of the Lord
When Ezekiel sees it, he falls on his face
He hears the voice of one speaking
The voice says to him, "Son of man, stand on your feet, and I will speak with you"
As he speaks to him, the Spirit enters into Ezekiel
The Spirit sets him on his feet
Ezekiel hears him speaking to him
The Lord says, "Son of man, I send you to the people of Israel"
"To nations of rebels, who have rebelled against me"
"They and their fathers have transgressed against me to this very day"
"The descendants also are impudent and stubborn"
"I send you to them, and you shall say to them, 'Thus says the Lord God'"
"And whether they hear or refuse to hear, for they are a rebellious house"
"They will know that a prophet has been among them"
"And you, son of man, be not afraid of them, nor be afraid of their words"
"Though briers and thorns are with you and you sit on scorpions"
"Be not afraid of their words, nor be dismayed at their looks"
"For they are a rebellious house"
"You shall speak my words to them, whether they hear or refuse to hear"
"For they are a rebellious house"
"But you, son of man, hear what I say to you"
"Be not rebellious like that rebellious house"
"Open your mouth and eat what I give you"
Ezekiel looks, and behold, a hand is stretched out to him
Behold, a scroll of a book is in it
The Lord spreads it before him
It has writing on the front and on the back
There are written on it words of lamentation and mourning and woe
The Lord says, "Son of man, eat whatever you find here"
"Eat this scroll, and go, speak to the house of Israel"
Ezekiel opens his mouth, and the Lord gives him the scroll to eat
He says to him, "Son of man, feed your belly with this scroll that I give you"
"And fill your stomach with it"
Ezekiel eats it, and it is in his mouth as sweet as honey
The Spirit lifts Ezekiel up
He hears behind him the voice of a great earthquake
"Blessed be the glory of the Lord from its place!"
He hears the sound of the wings of the living creatures as they touch one another
And the sound of the wheels beside them, and the sound of a great earthquake
The Spirit lifts him up and takes him away
He goes in bitterness in the heat of his spirit
The hand of the Lord is strong upon him
He comes to the exiles at Tel-abib, who are dwelling by the Chebar canal
He sits where they are dwelling
He sits there overwhelmed among them seven days
At the end of seven days, the word of the Lord comes to him
"Son of man, I have made you a watchman for the house of Israel"
"Whenever you hear a word from my mouth, you shall give them warning from me"
The hand of the Lord is upon Ezekiel there
He says to him, "Arise, go out into the valley, and there I will speak with you"
Ezekiel arises and goes out into the valley
Behold, the glory of the Lord stands there, like the glory that he had seen by the Chebar canal
He falls on his face
The Spirit enters into him and sets him on his feet
The Lord speaks with him
"Go, shut yourself within your house"
"And you, O son of man, behold, cords will be placed upon you"
"And you shall be bound with them, so that you cannot go out among the people"
"And I will make your tongue cling to the roof of your mouth"
"So that you shall be mute and unable to reprove them"
"For they are a rebellious house"
"But when I speak with you, I will open your mouth"
"And you shall say to them, 'Thus says the Lord God'"
"'He who will hear, let him hear; and he who will refuse to hear, let him refuse'"
"'For they are a rebellious house'"
The Lord says to Ezekiel, "And you, O son of man, take a brick"
"And lay it before you, and engrave on it a city, even Jerusalem"
"And put siegeworks against it, and build a siege wall against it"
"And cast up a mound against it"
"Set camps also against it, and plant battering rams against it all around"
"And you, take an iron griddle, and place it as an iron wall between you and the city"
"And set your face toward it, and let it be in a state of siege"
"And press the siege against it"
"This is a sign for the house of Israel"
Ezekiel does so
The Lord tells Ezekiel to lie on his left side for 390 days, bearing the punishment of the house of Israel
Then to lie on his right side for 40 days, bearing the punishment of the house of Judah
Ezekiel does so
The Lord tells him what he shall eat and drink during these days
And that he shall bake his bread over human dung
Ezekiel says, "Ah, Lord God! Behold, I have never defiled myself"
The Lord allows him to use cow's dung instead
The Lord tells Ezekiel to take a sharp sword and use it as a barber's razor
To pass it over his head and his beard
Then to take balances for weighing and divide the hair
A third part he is to burn in the fire in the midst of the city
A third part he is to strike with the sword all around the city
A third part he is to scatter to the wind
And the Lord will unsheathe the sword after them
Ezekiel is to take a small number of hairs and bind them in the skirts of his robe
And of these again he is to take some and throw them into the midst of the fire
And burn them in the fire
From there a fire will come out into all the house of Israel
This is Jerusalem that the Lord has set in the center of the nations
With countries all around her
The word of the Lord comes to Ezekiel
"Son of man, set your face toward the mountains of Israel, and prophesy against them"
Ezekiel prophesies against the mountains
In the sixth year, in the sixth month, on the fifth day of the month
As Ezekiel sits in his house, with the elders of Judah sitting before him
The hand of the Lord God falls upon him there
He looks, and behold, a form that has the appearance of a man
Below what appears to be his waist is fire
Above his waist is something like the appearance of brightness, like gleaming metal
He puts out the form of a hand and takes Ezekiel by a lock of his head
The Spirit lifts him up between earth and heaven
Brings him in visions of God to Jerusalem
To the entrance of the gateway of the inner court that faces north
Where is the seat of the image of jealousy, which provokes to jealousy
Behold, the glory of the God of Israel is there
Like the vision that Ezekiel had seen in the valley
The Lord says to him, "Son of man, lift up your eyes now toward the north"
Ezekiel lifts up his eyes toward the north
Behold, north of the altar gate, in the entrance, is this image of jealousy
"Son of man, do you see what they are doing?"
"The great abominations that the house of Israel are committing here"
"To drive me far from my sanctuary?"
"But you will see still greater abominations"
The Lord brings him to the entrance of the court
Ezekiel looks, and behold, there is a hole in the wall
"Son of man, dig in the wall"
Ezekiel digs in the wall
Behold, there is an entrance
"Go in, and see the vile abominations that they are committing here"
Ezekiel goes in and looks
Behold, there is every form of creeping things and loathsome beasts
And all the idols of the house of Israel, carved on the wall all around
Before them stand seventy men of the elders of the house of Israel
With Jaazaniah the son of Shaphan standing among them
Each has his censer in his hand
The smoke of the cloud of incense goes up
"Son of man, have you seen what the elders of the house of Israel are doing in the dark?"
"Each in his room of pictures?"
"For they say, 'The Lord does not see us, the Lord has forsaken the land'"
"You will see still greater abominations that they commit"
The Lord brings him to the entrance of the north gate of the house of the Lord
Behold, there sit women weeping for Tammuz
"Have you seen this, O son of man?"
"You will see still greater abominations than these"
He brings him into the inner court of the house of the Lord
Behold, at the entrance of the temple of the Lord
Between the porch and the altar
Are about twenty-five men, with their backs to the temple of the Lord
And their faces toward the east, worshiping the sun toward the east
"Have you seen this, O son of man?"
"Is it too light a thing for the house of Judah to commit the abominations that they commit here?"
"That they should fill the land with violence and provoke me still further to anger?"
"Behold, they put the branch to their nose"
"Therefore I will act in wrath"
"My eye will not spare, nor will I have pity"
"And though they cry in my ears with a loud voice, I will not hear them"
He cries in Ezekiel's ears with a loud voice
"Bring near the executioners of the city, each with his destroying weapon in his hand"
Behold, six men come from the direction of the upper gate, which faces north
Each with his weapon for slaughter in his hand
Among them is a man clothed in linen, with a writing case at his waist
They go in and stand beside the bronze altar
Now the glory of the God of Israel has gone up from the cherub on which it rested
To the threshold of the house
The Lord calls to the man clothed in linen, who has the writing case at his waist
"Pass through the city, through Jerusalem"
"And put a mark on the foreheads of the men who sigh and groan over all the abominations that are committed in it"
To the others he says in Ezekiel's hearing
"Pass through the city after him, and strike"
"Your eye shall not spare, and you shall show no pity"
"Kill old men outright, young men and maidens, little children and women"
"But touch no one on whom is the mark"
"And begin at my sanctuary"
They begin with the elders who are before the house
"Defile the house, and fill the courts with the slain. Go out"
They go out and strike in the city
While they are striking, and Ezekiel is left alone
He falls upon his face and cries out
"Ah, Lord God! Will you destroy all the remnant of Israel in the outpouring of your wrath on Jerusalem?"
"The guilt of the house of Israel and Judah is exceedingly great"
"The land is full of blood, and the city full of injustice"
"For they say, 'The Lord has forsaken the land, and the Lord does not see'"
"As for me, my eye will not spare, nor will I have pity"
"I will bring their deeds upon their heads"
Behold, the man clothed in linen, with the writing case at his waist, brings back word
"I have done as you commanded me"
Ezekiel looks, and behold, on the expanse that is over the heads of the cherubim
There appears above them something like a sapphire, in appearance like a throne
The Lord says to the man clothed in linen
"Go in among the whirling wheels underneath the cherubim"
"Fill your hands with burning coals from between the cherubim, and scatter them over the city"
He goes in before Ezekiel's eyes
Now the cherubim are standing on the south side of the house, when the man goes in
A cloud fills the inner court
The glory of the Lord goes up from the cherub to the threshold of the house
The house is filled with the cloud
The court is filled with the brightness of the glory of the Lord
The sound of the wings of the cherubim is heard as far as the outer court
Like the voice of God Almighty when he speaks
When the Lord commands the man clothed in linen
"Take fire from between the whirling wheels, from between the cherubim"
He goes in and stands beside a wheel
A cherub stretches out his hand from between the cherubim to the fire
That is between the cherubim, and takes some of it
And puts it into the hands of the man clothed in linen, who takes it and goes out
The cherubim appear to have the form of a human hand under their wings
Ezekiel looks, and behold, there are four wheels beside the cherubim
One beside each cherub
The appearance of the wheels is like sparkling beryl
As for their appearance, the four have the same likeness
As if a wheel were within a wheel
When they go, they go in any of their four directions without turning as they go
Their whole body, their rims, and their spokes, their wings, and the wheels are full of eyes all around
The wheels that the four of them have
As for the wheels, they are called in Ezekiel's hearing "the whirling wheels"
Each one has four faces
The first face is the face of the cherub
The second face is a human face
The third face is the face of a lion
The fourth is the face of an eagle
The cherubim mount up
These are the living creatures that Ezekiel saw by the Chebar canal
When the cherubim go, the wheels go beside them
When the cherubim lift up their wings to mount up from the earth
The wheels do not turn from beside them
When they stand still, these stand still
When they mount up, these mount up with them
For the spirit of the living creatures is in them
The glory of the Lord goes out from the threshold of the house
It stands over the cherubim
The cherubim lift up their wings and mount up from the earth before Ezekiel's eyes as they go out
With the wheels beside them
They stand at the entrance of the east gate of the house of the Lord
The glory of the God of Israel is over them
These are the living creatures that Ezekiel saw underneath the God of Israel by the Chebar canal
He knows that they are cherubim
Each has four faces, and each four wings
And underneath their wings the likeness of human hands
As for the likeness of their faces, they are the same faces whose appearance Ezekiel had seen by the Chebar canal
Each one of them goes straight forward
The Spirit lifts Ezekiel up and brings him to the east gate of the house of the Lord
Which faces east
Behold, at the entrance of the gateway there are twenty-five men
Among them Ezekiel sees Jaazaniah the son of Azzur, and Pelatiah the son of Benaiah
Princes of the people
The Lord says to him, "Son of man, these are the men who devise iniquity"
"And who give wicked counsel in this city"
"Who say, 'The time is not near to build houses'"
"'This city is the cauldron, and we are the meat'"
"Therefore prophesy against them, prophesy, O son of man"
The Spirit of the Lord falls upon Ezekiel
He says to him, "Say, Thus says the Lord"
"'So you think, O house of Israel'"
"'For I know the things that come into your mind'"
"'You have multiplied your slain in this city'"
"'And have filled its streets with the slain'"
"'Therefore thus says the Lord God'"
"'"Your slain whom you have laid in the midst of it, they are the meat'"
"'"And this city is the cauldron'"
"'"But you shall be brought out of the midst of it'"
As Ezekiel is prophesying, Pelatiah the son of Benaiah dies
Ezekiel falls on his face and cries out with a loud voice
